# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 9

In response to your letter, in which you write about your state of mind and the difficulties you are encountering in your avodah and in your general conduct—

It is well known that the yetzer hara’s primary tactic is not necessarily to cause a person to stumble in a specific sin, but rather to bring a person to a state of sadness and despondency. By doing so, the yetzer hara prevents the person from serving Hashem with joy and with a full heart. As the Alter Rebbe explains in Tanya, this is the "trap" that the yetzer hara sets for the person, for sadness is the greatest obstacle to true avodah.

Therefore, you must strengthen your bitul and your hiskashrus to the Rebbe, and realize that these thoughts of discouragement are merely external distractions. The path to success is through persistence and consistency—davening with kavanah, setting fixed times for learning Torah, and engaging in acts of kindness—regardless of how you feel at any given moment. 

Do not be misled by your own subjective feelings. The Ribono shel Olam desires the heart, and your sincere efforts, even when they feel dry or difficult, are precious in His eyes. Continue with your avodah, and in time, you will surely see the fruits of your labor.

## 2723

By the Grace of Hashem
Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Peace and Blessing!

In connection with the various rumors that have reached me—which surprise me greatly—I am writing these lines, despite my many preoccupations.

It has been conveyed to me (and I hope that, in the end, these reports will prove to be incorrect) that your family is opposed to arranging your daughter’s wedding in accordance with the requirement of the Shulchan Aruch, which mandates that there must be a *mechitza* between men and women during the wedding.

I wish to explain to you the situation as I see it. It is as follows:

When a wedding is arranged with a *mechitza* as our holy Torah requires, the Torah rules that we may recite "Shehasimcha Bime'ono"—meaning that when we invoke the Name of Hashem, we do so in a way that draws down joy into the world, and first and foremost, upon the *chassan* and *kallah*.

It is surely unnecessary to describe what has transpired in the world in recent years in general, and among Jews in particular. If in all times one had to turn to the Ribono shel Olam for blessing and success—and even more so for a healthy and happy life—in our generation this is far more necessary. The only One who can safeguard this is the Master of the entire world, the Holy One, Blessed be He.

At the time when Rabbi... (may he live and be well) asked for my opinion regarding this *shidduch*, and when your inquiry regarding it reached me, I felt it my duty and privilege to ensure that when your daughter and Rabbi... (may they live and be well) begin their life together, it should be in a manner that allows one to expect the maximum blessings from Hashem. They should have a healthy, happy home, which, as stated, has the approval of our holy Torah when one can recite at the wedding **"Shehasimcha Bime'ono."** Since the Torah rules this way, and not otherwise, it is self-understood that no one can change it. Therefore, I was surprised that parents who do everything to ensure their children are happy—in matters that depend solely on them—would actually exert effort **not** to allow there to be *simcha* at their daughter’s wedding, which, by definition, would then be lacking in their lives, G-d forbid.

One marries in order to build a home for decades. Is it right for parents to risk that which affects their daughter for decades, just so that for the few hours the wedding lasts, they can please people who do not know the laws of the Shulchan Aruch, or who do not concern themselves with the Shulchan Aruch, or those frivolous individuals for whom it is acceptable to risk a matter of decades for a momentary, imagined pleasure? It surprises me where parents find the latitude to take such a responsibility upon themselves.

It is not my business to send police to force people to act according to my opinion; it is not my business to coerce people in general to act according to my view; and it is not my business to speak harsh words. Therefore, I wish to conclude my letter by speaking only of the positive. When I gave my consent to this *shidduch*, I was certain that the parents on their side would also do everything within their power to ensure that their daughter and future son-in-law would be as secure as possible for the decades they will be together. It is self-understood that the fact that her friends might or might not be pleased should not take precedence over the holy Torah being pleased with such an arrangement at the wedding. Taking this into account, I gave my consent to this *shidduch*. As stated earlier, if one truly wants the holy Torah to rule that one may recite **"Shehasimcha Bime'ono"** at the wedding, and through that to be happy for the rest of one's life, the Shulchan Aruch\* states that the wedding must be with a *mechitza*.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

P.S.

I am conveying to Rabbi... (may he live and be well) that he should no longer involve himself in the question of the *mechitza*. If it turns out that the parents have broad shoulders and can gamble with the happy life of their daughter (may she live and be well) on their own responsibility, contrary to what is written in the Shulchan Aruch, I unfortunately cannot do anything about that.

I also know that there have been many weddings, even among the pious, that were unfortunately held without a *mechitza*, but I also know the troubles that unfortunately came later. May Hashem bless you that you should always be able to report only good news, both in material and spiritual matters.

***

\*) *Bach* and *Beis Shmuel*—in *Shulchan Aruch, Even HaEzer*, Chapter 62, subsection 11; and the *Levush* wrote (in *Minhagim*, end of *Orach Chaim*) that it is like "white geese"—in our many sins, we see that at this time, this is not the case.

## 2424

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter informing me that your son, Yosef Yitzchak—may he live—turned three years old on the 23rd of Nissan.

While it is possible to find grounds to permit the haircut during the days of Sefirah—and all the more so given that it has been permitted to do so during Chol Hamoed (see Shaarei Teshuvah, Orach Chaim, siman 531)—nevertheless, and especially in light of what is written in Pri Etz Chaim regarding the explanation of cutting hair during the days of Sefirah, in my opinion, it is advisable to perform the haircut on Lag B'Omer. This is especially pertinent as it is the custom of the Jewish people to cut the hair of young children on this day. May Hashem grant him success, that together with his wife—may they live—you should raise all your children—may they live—to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with peace of mind.

With blessings.

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 349; completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

## 2725

2 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you ask about a point that troubled you regarding a letter of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, which was printed in *Bitaon Chabad*.

I was in doubt as to whether to answer this letter at all, because aside from the question you have regarding the Rebbe, I found nothing in your letter about your studies in Chassidus or in the revealed Torah. Yet, starting with a question is not the way to study any part of Torah. Only after one has studied the relevant area of Torah for some time and acquired some knowledge is there room to raise questions—or, more accurately, not questions, but requests for clarification of matters that are not understood at first glance.

Nevertheless, I wish to judge you favorably, assuming that your intent is surely for the good. A sign of this is that you are apparently involved in and assisting with the printing of books on the inner dimension of Torah—the Zohar, Tikkunei Zohar, and so on. Therefore, I have provided the following explanation.

**The Question:**

In the letter of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, printed in *Bitaon Chabad*, issue 4, page 37, he explains the difference between the study methods of a Chassid and a *misnaged*. Both study with *iyun* (depth) and both seek out errors and exert themselves to correct them. The difference is only this: Chassidim know that what is stated in the book is good and true, and the error lies within themselves and their own reasoning; the *misnaged*, however, proves that his own knowledge and *pilpul* are the truth, and the error lies in the book, etc.

You expressed astonishment at this explanation, asking how it is possible to say that the great *misnagdim* studied in the manner described above.

**The Answer:**

To understand this, we must first preface an explanation of a more piercing and wondrous matter, found in the *Pardes* of the Ramak, and cited in a *maamar* (apparently by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*). The *maamar* states: To understand...

It is explained in *Pardes* that anyone who does not study [the wisdom of Kabbalah] is an *epikores*.

The *maamar* explains the meaning: Even if he is not yet an *epikores*, if he is by nature an investigator, he will inevitably end up as an *epikores*. For according to the investigations of the philosophers, it is impossible in any way for the world and its minute details to be created from the Simple Unity, and for there to be Divine Providence over them, without there being any change in His Essence, etc. He will eventually arrive at heretical views, because only on the foundations of the teachings of Kabbalah can all the above be resolved in accordance with our holy faith. This is the intent of the *Pardes*.

— Apparently, this refers to what is written in *Pardes*, *Shaar* 1, Chapter 9. There it says *kofer* (for the distinctions between these, see Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, Chapter 3). However, beyond the fact that this *maamar* does not delve into the distinctions between a *kofer*, *min*, and *epikores*, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe—as well as the *Nesi'im* before and after him—delivered his *maamarim* in "Yiddish and not in the Holy Tongue" (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 25, 101a), and the transcriber did not always render the language into the Holy Tongue with grammatical precision. —

The same applies to our subject:

Even if at the beginning of his study the *misnaged* is not in the state described in the aforementioned letter, if he is a person of strong intellect, he will eventually end up that way. For the rule of Torah is well known: "It is not in heaven," but was given to human beings, and each person must exert himself to understand it **with his own intellect**. And one who has been granted the authority to rule—the judge has nothing but what his own eyes of intellect see. As is known regarding the "Oven of Achnai" (*Bava Metzia* 59b), the debate in the Heavenly Academy (*Bava Metzia* 86a), "My children have defeated Me," and so on.

Consequently, one whom Hashem has graced with intellect and who is diligent in this—when he approaches the study of Torah, and the study is conducted according to the rules of Torah (which include the aforementioned principles), his premise and approach are that the matter has been given over to his complete discretion. Since the Holy One, blessed be He, asks only according to the capacity of each person, he must study according to his own intellect, and however he understands it, the matter has been given to his discretion to decide. That is to say, his knowledge and *pilpul* are the truth. And if he finds a contradiction to this in a book, it does not obligate him, based on the above.

It is known from our Sages that Scripture equates three of the lightest of the world with three of the heaviest of the world, to tell you that Yerubaal in his generation is like Moshe in his generation, etc. (*Rosh Hashanah* 25b).

One of the primary differences between a Chassid and a *misnaged* is this: The foundation of the Chassid’s worldview is that his soul (as well as the souls of his peers) is a spark and a branch of a more general soul—the soul of his Rebbe. As a result, both in physical matters and in spiritual matters, there is a strong bond between them. What happens to one is connected in a significant measure to the other, as mentioned—whether in physical matters or spiritual matters, which naturally includes the study of Torah and the performance of *mitzvos*.

— And with this, one can understand the well-known saying of the *Nesi'im* of Chassidus: "The righteous shall live by his faith" (*Tzaddik be'emunaso yichyeh*)—do not read *yichyeh* (shall live), but *yechayeh* (shall give life); the *Tzaddik* gives life through his faith and his *avodah* to those souls who belong to him and are connected to him. —

From this, it is also understood that a private soul is not the final arbiter even in its own understanding of Torah, since it is only a detail of the whole. There are many other details that can clarify the manner of understanding of this private soul, and certainly the general soul can understand it and illuminate it with additional intellect—at which point the private soul itself will understand with its own intellect better and more deeply.

Just as in understanding additional details in a *sugya*, one adds to the understanding of the other details of the *sugya*, so too it is with the intellect and the one who is intellectualizing: when more intellectual details are added, it will also add to the understanding of other intellectual details.

This very knowledge—that even though it is his obligation to exert himself in the study of Torah and the performance of *mitzvos*, and he does not fulfill his obligation by having another private soul, or even a general soul, engage in the above, for he is commanded himself—nevertheless, alongside this, and even though the Torah was given to human beings, he himself is only one detail and his understanding is only the understanding of one detail of the intellectual, and consequently he is liable to err, and the other details have the ability to correct and complete his understanding, and certainly the understanding of the general soul will clarify the entire intellect with a light of great wisdom.

This very knowledge changes his approach even at the beginning of study, as mentioned in the letter of the Rebbe, my father-in-law: he is certain that what is stated in the book is good and true—since it has been publicized among the Jewish people and confirmed by many, many details—and the error is in himself and his own reasoning, because he is only one detail, and the other details, whose help he is obligated to seek as mentioned, will surely correct his error.

***

I have only touched upon the core of the matter, for it is difficult to explain at length in writing, especially since you do not state the extent of your understanding in the revealed Torah, nor what you have studied and in what manner regarding the inner dimension of Torah, which is called the "Tree of Life," in which there is no "question from the side of evil" and no "dispute from the spirit of impurity"—as is brought in *Ra'aya Mehemna* (*Zohar* III, 124b), and explained at length in *Iggeres HaKodesh* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, section 26.

And this is to note and illuminate: the Rebbe, my father-in-law, in his aforementioned letter, is speaking about a person whose description is *misnaged*, and not an *olam’sher* (a worldly person) or the like, which is also precise, and this also assists in understanding the content of his letter, as is understood.

And just as in the general acceptance of the entire Torah by the Jewish people as a whole, the precedence of "we will do" to "we will hear" was necessary—for only then does "the integrity of the upright guide them," and were it not for this, then regarding that it is said, "the perversity of the treacherous shall destroy them," as explained by our Sages (*Shabbos* 88b)—so too is it in the acceptance of each and every part of the *Pardes* of Torah: the beginning must be the precedence of "we will do" to "we will hear," and only then does one receive this part and "the integrity of the upright guide them."

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 2,606

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to read at the end of your letter that your son, Yosef Yitzchak, may he live and be well, is beginning to learn in cheder at the beginning of the month of Iyar. It is well known what the Midrash Tanchuma states regarding the verse, "In the fourth year, all its fruit shall be holy, a praise [hillulim] to Hashem" — see also the beginning of the Laws of Talmud Torah by our Alter Rebbe. May it be the will of Hashem that he grows from "five years old for Scripture" to "ten years old," and so on, in accordance with the ruling of our holy Torah, and that you and your wife, may you live and be well, derive much Chassidishe nachas from all your children, may they live and be well.

With blessings.

## 2727

B.H., 3 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and pious individual, who engages in communal needs, Moreinu HaRav Shmuel Menachem, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 25 Nissan, in which you inform me that your son, Reuven Shlomo, may he live, has begun to study Chumash. May it be the will of Hashem that from the study of Mikra he will grow to reach the age of ten for Mishnah, and so on, and may you and your wife, may you live, derive from him much Chassidishe nachas, together with a good livelihood and peace of mind.

I enjoyed reading what you wrote regarding the activities of the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Jerusalem during the past Purim. Certainly, you should continue this good practice of reporting on such matters in the future, and the more detailed one is in this regard, the more praiseworthy it is. It is surprising that until now I have not received reports of their good activities from Purim until the present, especially regarding participation in the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad gathering, which surely took place to the appropriate extent, and I await good news.

From reading your reports, I am left with the impression that when the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad visit synagogues and gatherings, they do not have a detailed plan in advance, but rather rely on the situation as they find it upon arrival, and so on. While it is certainly impossible to determine every minute detail before arriving on site, there must be a sufficiently detailed plan so that there will be no confusion, disorder, and the like. One must be especially careful wherever one goes, since they are viewed as an example of what a young Chabad Chassid is. When a deficiency is found, there is room for concern that it will be attributed to the entire group rather than to the specific individual, and a word to the wise is sufficient. As our Sages have already said, "For example, I, who take..." (Yoma 86a).

With blessings that you should always merit to share good news in a revealed and abundant manner, both regarding yourself and regarding your colleagues in your holy work.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2828

B"H, 4 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter of 27 Nissan has just been received. May Hashem grant each of us success to see, very soon, the fulfillment of the request that every Jew makes three times daily: "And let there be no hope for the slanderers," and to serve Hashem through the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos with hiddur. [This includes] putting forth the greatest possible effort to expand and grow our holy institutions, especially those connected to the Nesi’ei Chabad—the Rebbe Rashab and my father-in-law, the Rebbe—may their merits protect us. Anyone who accepts upon himself the yoke of Heaven and engages energetically, for his own sake, in all of the above, will have all distractions and confusions removed from him. As is well known, the parable regarding this is that whoever devotes himself—even beyond the constraints of logic and intellect—to the service of the Nesi’im, then his livelihood, the livelihood of his household, his sustenance, and the tranquility of his soul and body are provided by the Nesi’im, as explained in several of the Rebbe’s sichos.

May Hashem bless you with long, good days and years, and may you add strength to your avodah in the vineyard of Chabad, which will draw down additional blessing and success in your communal activities and in your personal affairs.

With blessings for success.

## 2829

B"H, 4 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, involved in communal needs,
Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live, HaKohen,

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of the 8th of Iyar, in which you write regarding the farbrengen of the festival of Pesach and the content of your remarks at that time. May it be the will of Hashem that you continue to exert your influence upon your surroundings, to draw their hearts closer to Torah and mitzvos, and to the "light of Torah"—which is the pnimiyus haTorah. It is understood that this also adds to the pnimiyus of vitality in physical matters, for in the case of a Jewish person, physicality and spirituality go hand in hand. Consequently, this also adds to the externality of the vitality of the body. As it is known that "a man’s wife is as his own body," this adds an increase in health also regarding one's wife, and may Hashem grant you success in bringing good tidings in this regard as well.

I trust that you are also receiving the kuntresim as you requested, and surely you will have a "good eye" regarding others, to merit them with the content of these kuntresim as well.

With blessings for long and good years, and to increase strength in raising the pride of the Jewish people, with proper health and peace of mind.

#### ***2829***

**Rabbi Yitzchak:** Huberman; another letter to him appears above in Vol. 6, 1732.

## 2731

B"H, 4 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, who engages in communal needs,
Rabbi Zalman Tuvia, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

Your letter from 24 Nisan has just been received. You will surely increase your strength in your holy work for the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, as much as possible. You have already seen tangibly that when one simply engages in these institutions, our Nasi, my father-in-law the Rebbe, arouses Heavenly mercy, and extraordinary success is bestowed upon the places where they are involved. However, since "there is no opening even as small as the eye of a needle," then [there is no result], and so on. When you apply yourself to the avodah as required, the work will be successful. One should not be discouraged by the fact that other schools have furniture, etc.; with appropriate effort, this too will be added little by little, provided that in the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch schools, the internal matters are well-ordered. Without a doubt, this involvement will also draw down an increase in blessing and success in your personal affairs, and those of your wife and children, may they live. I look forward to hearing good news.

With a blessing for success in all of the above.

## 2732

B"H, 4 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter from Rosh Chodesh Iyar has just been received, in which you write that, given the time and the situation, you have succeeded in your shlichus in the country of... It is surprising that you do not provide more details. In any event, you surely know and have heard of the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to shluchim: "to gather gashmius and to sow — to plant — ruchniyus," from which it is understood that the one is dependent upon the other.

Regarding what you write, that doctors are advising to remove the tonsils of... *shiy* and that you are waiting for the doctor’s call to perform the surgery: surely, before proceeding, you will ask for his opinion once again, since this depends on the atmospheric conditions at the time and day they say the tonsils should be removed—in addition to the fact that many doctors are not as firmly in favor of removing tonsils as they were in years past. However it may be, may it be the will of Hashem that it be at a good and auspicious time, and may you raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to maasim tovim.

Concerning the matters of your parnassah: in general, one must strive with all one's might that even one's gashmius parnassah be connected with work in the vineyard of Chabad. Beyond the fact that this is closer to the hearts of anash—whether they are aware of it or not, and consequently the work is more successful—it is also understood from a ruchniyus perspective, for our holy Nasi is the one who bestows upon his students and upon anash in general all the influences they require. This is similar to what was said regarding Moshe Rabbeinu, "From where shall I have meat, etc.," which was not at his level at all, as explained in Likutei Torah; consequently, the influence of the meat had to be mediated through the seventy elders, but even so, it was only through Moshe Rabbeinu.

When parnassah is connected to the vineyard of Chabad, the ruchniyus and gashmius aspects assist one another. As for what you write, that your involvement until now in the vineyard of Chabad is detrimental to your health, etc.—surely it can be arranged in a way that avoids extremes. That is to say, if you must travel, it does not have to be all year round or for the majority of the year, but on the other hand, you should not withdraw your hand from it entirely. May Hashem provide you with your parnassah and the parnassah of your household, may they live, with peace of mind, and may you increase your strength both in quantity in the dissemination of the wellsprings outward, and in the study of Nigleh and Chassidus for yourself as well.

With blessings.

## 2733

B"H, 4 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your *pidyon nefesh* requesting a blessing for you and your family, *shichyu*. When I visit the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zi"e*, I will read the *pidyon nefesh*, and he will surely arouse great mercy for everyone you mentioned in the *pidyon nefesh* according to their needs.

It is surely unnecessary to point out that in order to receive the blessings of Hashem, each person in their own area of need, one must create the appropriate *keilim* for this, which are the matters of Torah and *mitzvos*. Since the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* demands this of every Jew, it is certain that He—*Baruch Hu*—has given the ability and the strength to fulfill it. It depends only on the good will of each individual. It is understood that the notion that America is "different" is a viewpoint of *kefirah*, *r"l*. Whoever believes that *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* is the Creator of the entire world and is the Master of the **entire** world—and among Jews, who are believers the children of believers, there is no doubt about this—even if one forgets this for a short time, the *nefesh elokis* that exists within every Jew reminds them of it. When one listens to Hashem, one overcomes the deceptions of the *yetzer hara* and conducts oneself as a Jew should conduct oneself; only then can one be certain to be successful, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*. May Hashem help you to have true *nachas* from all your children and grandchildren, and to receive this in good health, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

P.S.
Surely you recite *Tehillim* every day after *davening*, and also give *tzedakah* a few times a week, at the very least a few cents, and may Hashem grant you success.

***

**That America is different:** See below, letter 2939, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 2734

B"H, 4 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have just received your *pan* regarding your wife, the Rabbanit [Name], *tichyeh*. When I am at the *tziyun hakadosh* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*, I will mention her for a speedy recovery. May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings in this regard.

Surely, for one such as yourself, it is superfluous to point out the words of our Sages that the measure of Hashem is "measure for measure." When one increases the health of those he influences—that is, his environment and his community—in spiritual matters, by drawing their hearts ever closer to our Father in Heaven, Hashem in turn increases his own physical and spiritual health (for in a Jewish person, these go together and are interdependent) as is necessary for him and his wife, for "one's wife is as one's own self."

This is in addition to the fact that this matter has great value in its own right, as explained in the words of our Sages, "the reward of a mitzvah is a mitzvah." The very ability to perform a mitzvah in actuality is the greatest reward that a created being can receive through the free kindness of Hashem, who enables a person—fashioned from material—to fulfill the will of the King of Kings, Hashem, in His glory and essence.

With respect and with blessings to hear good news regarding all the above.

## 2735

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent in the service of Hashem,
Rabbi Schneur Zalman Eliezer, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 23 Nissan, in which you comment on what is written in the Tanya regarding "Train a child" (in parentheses), and that the mitzvah of *chinuch* (education/training) is also a *mitzvah aseh* (positive commandment), as stated in *Orach Chaim*, section 343.

Regarding the aforementioned **"also a *mitzvah aseh*,"** one can interpret the words "also a *mitzvah aseh*" in two ways:

Either the emphasis is on the words "*mitzvah aseh*," meaning, and all the more so in a *mitzvah lo saaseh* (negative commandment)—which is indeed the position of the Alter Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch*, section 343.

Or, the emphasis is on the word "also," referring back to what was stated previously: just as love is the root and foundation for *mitzvos asei*, so too is the mitzvah of *chinuch* a *mitzvah aseh* (for it is **irrelevant** here whether the mitzvah of *chinuch* is a *mitzvah lo saaseh* or not). In that case, the word "also" is understood more simply. For according to the first interpretation, it would have sufficed to say "also in a *mitzvah aseh*." But from the conclusion of the introduction—"but its essence is from the love with which he was trained, etc."—it is understood that the parenthetical statement intends to emphasize that in love, there is also the mitzvah of *chinuch*.

And with this, it is further clarified that, generally, parenthetical statements are understood to add something that is not as essential to the understanding of the matter. This is the case here as well, for the verse "Train a child" does not necessarily mean only before he becomes an adult obligated in *mitzvos*. On the contrary (see *Kiddushin* 30a), "from the time he can speak... from the age of eighteen, etc." (Incidentally, it should be noted that in the Laws of Torah Study, Chapter 1, Paragraph 9, the Alter Rebbe seemingly rides two horses at once. But this is not the place to elaborate.) The parenthetical statement adds that the verse can also be interpreted according to its literal meaning, at the time when there is a mitzvah of *chinuch*—namely, at the actual age of *chinuch*.

Furthermore, it should be noted in continuation of the above that, seemingly, it begins with the roots of the service of Hashem—love and fear—and concludes only with love (and this is not unrelated to the above, for fear is also a *mitzvah aseh*). This can be explained according to what is explained in many places: that fear is also included in love. And not only in "hidden love," as explained in Tanya, Chapter 18, but in any love whatsoever; for because of love, one fears to rebel against His will, as is also stated here, that love is the foundation and root for the fulfillment of all *mitzvos asei*, in which fear is also included.

Regarding your comment on the difference of opinion among the Tosafists as to whether *chinuch* applies to *mitzvos lo saaseh*, you should certainly consult the *Bach* on *Orach Chaim*, section 343.

Regarding what you noted in the list of corrections, possibly regarding my correction concerning the "four elements" (that it should be "four" [arba'ah]—note also the Rambam's *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, Chapter 4), and you add that accordingly, one should also correct Chapter 7, and similarly from one to another on page 15.

Indeed, that is the case, and they are among the omissions in the list of corrections due to the haste in preparing the printing. Just as some matters were added between the publication of the Tanya in the regular format and the pocket format, and several other corrections remained that were not included in the latter either—but there is still a vision for the appointed time.

You mention in your letter the original manuscript of the Tanya from the first edition. I would appreciate it if you could inform me as soon as possible with more details about it, as well as the possibility of obtaining it for a period of time. Thank you in advance.

With blessing,

## 2736

B"H, 7 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, R' Yosef, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

It is with pleasure that I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 4 Iyar, along with the enclosed checks for Kolel Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, which are being sent to their destination at this time. I was also pleased by your promptness in sending the aforementioned without waiting for the rest.

How wondrous are the words of our Alter Rebbe regarding the matter of the Akeidah—an event that serves as an example and symbol not only for the Children of Israel but also for the nations of the world and the general public. The simple interpretation of the matter is that an elderly father brings his only son to be bound for sacrifice in accordance with the command of the Holy One, Blessed be He. But our Alter Rebbe comes and delves deeper to explain that this is not the inner essence of the matter. In his holy words: "The Akeidah itself is not considered such a great trial in relation to the stature of Avraham Avinu, peace be upon him, especially since Hashem spoke to him, 'Take now your son, etc.' Rather, it is that Avraham Avinu, peace be upon him, performed it with wondrous alacrity to show his joy and desire, etc. And from him, our Sages of blessed memory learned regarding the fulfillment of all mitzvos in general, and specifically the act of tzedakah, which surpasses them all" (see Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 21). From this, the virtue of alacrity is understood—that it is even greater, more vast, and more wondrous than the virtue of the Akeidah itself. For one such as you, further elaboration is surely unnecessary.

You surely received my previous letter in due time.

With blessings for success in all your affairs.

## 2737

B.H., 7 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

A few weeks ago, Hashem showed His kindness in that what happened to you can be called by the name **miracle**. Normally, this should evoke gratitude to Hashem, who is the Healer of all flesh and performs wonders. And this gratitude must be expressed in the way that **Hashem** desires, and His will has been clearly stated to all Jews, without distinction between man and woman, in His holy Torah. Therefore, I hoped that this would awaken in you a desire to wear a full sheitel; for through this, one sanctifies the Name of Hashem **in public**. And if it seems that this is difficult, then the expression of gratitude to Hashem Yisbarach is all the greater, and consequently, one should do it with even more joy.

I also hoped that your gratitude to Hashem would express itself regarding others as well, according to how He—blessed be He—demands in His holy Torah: to influence your surroundings so that they should be more Jewish, especially in matters that are done in public, meaning, where many people see it.

Therefore, I was very surprised by the report that reached me, that the **miracle** which happened to you was accepted as a normal occurrence. And not only did it not bring about gratitude and recognition of the kindness of Hashem to become warmer and closer to Yiddishkeit yourself, but one even uses the influence one has over those close to them so that they should oppose the Shulchan Aruch—that when one is about to marry off a daughter, which is a foundation for her entire life, one should want to do the opposite of what Hashem Yisbarach says in His Shulchan Aruch. And fearing that the bride herself might want to act as the Shulchan Aruch commands, one seeks to influence the parents so that they should act contrary to the Shulchan Aruch. And this is the gratitude after the miracle that Hashem performed!

I want to hope that this report is not correct and that something is not accurate. But since the report has reached me, and everything is surely by Divine Providence, I find it my duty to write the above lines. I hope that I will receive good news from you, that you have already begun wearing a full sheitel, at the very least from today onward, according to the custom of kosher Jewish daughters, and also that you are using your influence to impact your environment in general, and those close to you in particular, that they should conduct themselves as the Shulchan Aruch directs. May Hashem Yisbarach bless you.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

May Hashem grant you the merit to share good news.

With blessings of *mazal tov*.

2741

8 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious, engaged in communal needs, Rabbi Nissan Nemanov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 2 Iyar, and thank you for the good news that the students’ examinations showed that they are learning quite well, and surely this applies to matters of yiras shamayim as well. May Hashem grant him success, and may He grant them success, so that through an opening that is, in relative terms, as small as the eye of a needle, there will be opened from Above an opening as wide as the entrance to the Ulam—which, even in the higher realms, is considered an "opening as wide as the entrance to the Ulam."

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the absolute necessity to begin in good time and with energy to ensure that students come to learn during the vacation days, and perhaps even before that. The same applies to the students of Beis Rivkah; if you can encourage them in this, you will surely do so, even though I have written to them directly as well. Do not take this matter lightly, for beyond the well-known saying of the Baal Shem Tov—that for the sake of one good deed, whether in the physical or spiritual realm, for one person, it is worth the soul descending below for seventy or eighty years (and the depth of this matter is explained by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in Tanya, end of Chapter 25, and this unification above is eternal, forever and ever)—surely, when you exert the appropriate energy, a significant portion of those who come for the vacation will continue afterward in the ways of Torah and mitzvos, and some of them even in their studies within the walls of Tomchei Temimim. I look forward to good news regarding all of the above, and especially regarding this matter.

I cannot refrain from expressing my great astonishment and wonder, which is as follows:

It is understood based on what is brought in many places in Chassidic discourse, and specifically regarding the wonderment of Moshe Rabbeinu, "Whence should I have meat?"—that this was not on his level at all. Nevertheless, even though his argument was strong—the proof being that they said to him, "Gather for Me seventy men," etc.—the influence of the meat still came through him (even though he was also an intermediary in the matter). From this, it is understood that all the influence upon those who are connected and the Chassidim must be bound in some way with their Nasi, etc. It is necessarily derived from this that in our generation, which has merited that the Rebbe, our leader and shepherd, is its guide, all matters must be connected in some way with him. This is certainly true for Anash, the Temimim, and their families, may they live, and even more so for matters connected to Torah and mitzvos, and especially in general matters, and specifically in matters connected to faith, as it is written, "And they believed in Hashem and in Moshe His servant." It is stated in the Mechilta that whoever believes in the faithful shepherd is as if he believes in the word of Him who spoke and the world came into being. Therefore, my astonishment is great when I learn that specifically regarding the "food of faith" (matzah), a portion of Anash chose to obtain it from elsewhere, at a time when it was possible to receive it through the office established by the Rebbe, whose righteous deeds endure forever, and consequently, it remains his office even now.

There are surely some excuses for this, and perhaps even strong ones—that it might have been expensive, or that it was not baked quite as well, or that there was some friction between the aforementioned seller and Anash, or as others have said, that this is only for their families, whereas they themselves (as if it were possible to distinguish in faith between the "great in Israel" and the "small in Israel," especially regarding the Festival of Matzos, which is the *katnus* [infancy] of Abba, and the analogy for this is an infant eating grain). But after all this, I am astonished: is it worth risking another matter of connection with the Rebbe? And even if it were only a *safek sfeika* [a double doubt], for matters that are themselves not free of doubt, to receive Shmurah Matzah—the "food of faith"—from elsewhere?

Since I do not wish to specify by name who acted as described, I am writing these words to you, as you and those you influence surely took Shmurah specifically from the bakery connected with the office. Consequently, it will be easier for you to explain these matters at a farbrengen, as Hashem grants you the ability. Surely, the saying of the Rebbe is known even in France: "Our *zivoris* [inferior grain] is better than their *idiss* [superior grain]." May Hashem grant us merit and grant success to each and every one to draw down the influences of Pesach for the entire year, openly, in daily life.

With blessing.

## 2842

8 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, a man of many accomplishments, who works to strengthen the observance of Torah and mitzvos, etc., Rabbi Chananya Yom Tov Lipa, may he live.

Shalom u’vrachah!

I received with pleasure your books, *Taharas Yom Tov*—five volumes—as well as the news that you are in the process of printing the sixth volume of your works.

They are based on the sefer *Yesod Yosef*, which discusses the matter of guarding the *bris*, and the *tikkun* for the *pegam* (blemish), *chas v’shalom*, in this regard, etc.

Although it has not been the custom among *anash* to publish books specifically to explain the cause of this sin, nor even to speak of it in public or in a publicized manner—and there is a reason for this, based on the words of the Tzemach Tzedek, that the very thought and fear of the sin can, by nature, cause *keri* just like improper thoughts (Responsa Tzemach Tzedek, *Shaar HaMiluim*, siman 62; see there)—nevertheless, in this country, where a great breach has been made regarding this sin in certain circles, and they view the matter as a wide-open field—and furthermore, some physicians, "false healers" who permit what is forbidden, instruct those who come to them to engage in it and treat it as a routine matter, mocking those who abstain and explaining that it is not only permitted, but, *rachmana litzlan*, a mitzvah—and unfortunately, there is no one who speaks out, protests, or exposes this disgrace, nor does anyone explain the destruction of the body and its powers and the loss of life that results from it, in addition to the impurity of the soul and its descent, which, in the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, is a sin more severe and greater than the sin of forbidden relations in terms of the magnitude and abundance of the impurity and *kelipos* that it generates and increases to a very great degree (*Tanya*, end of Chapter 7; see there, and in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Shelach*, at the beginning, specifically the words "to a very great degree").

Therefore, there is room to say that one should publish and publicize the magnitude of the sin and the *pegam*, and even to speak about it specifically, if only to save the souls of the *bochurim* of Israel from falling, etc. And primarily, to strengthen and increase through this the attention of the *melamdim*, the *Roshei Yeshiva* and *Rabbanim* shlita to the situation, for to a known and significant extent, it depends on them to rectify this rampant situation. It is fitting for this measure that "the collar hangs around their necks," and whoever has the power to protest, etc.

May the desire of Hashem succeed in his hand, to bring merit to the many and to awaken them to "do justice" (*ihu rachamei*—it is mercy) for the oppressed—the *nitzotzos* of *kedushah* that are oppressed by the evil deeds of people (the Mitteler Rebbe in his *Siddur* on the verse "He does justice for the oppressed"; see there)—until Hashem gathers the outcasts of His people, Israel, through *mitzvos*, speedily in our days.

With blessings for success.

Since your book also deals with the laws of *mikvaos*, I am enclosing a copy of the list of instructions from the Rebbe Rashab, the father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—*ztzukulleh"h nbg"m zya*—from the time of the construction of the *mikveh* in his city.

Because of the importance of the matter, I have added some notes in the margins of your books.

**Vol. 1, p. 1a: To the head of the *goyah*.** To note and illuminate from our Sages' statement, "There is no erection except for the sake of knowledge" (*Yevamos* 53b), for there is a connection and attachment of the organ to the brain in the head. The reason is known: there are fine nerves through which the thread in the organ is connected to the brain, and they become one, to the point that they are considered as one organ. See the sefer *Torah Or* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, in the *Hosafos* at the end of *Parshas Vayechi*, where he discusses this at length.

**Ibid., based on this:** To note from the sefer *Or HaShanim* (by Rabbi A. L. Epstein, a *gaon* and *mekubal*, *Av Beis Din* of Königsberg), who counted the act of *z.l.* among the negative commandments derived from "You shall not commit adultery." For the time being, I have not found another who holds this view.

**Vol. 2, p. 74d: The reason it is not written in the Torah regarding the sin of *z.l.*** (See above regarding the sefer *Or HaShanim*). In *Tanya*, end of Chapter 7, he writes the reason: because through this sin, it is possible to elevate the *chiyus* that descended into the *kelipos* through proper *teshuvah*, etc., which is not the case with other prohibitions in the Torah. See *Panim LaTorah*.

**Ibid., p. 88f: Regarding the punishment of *gilgul*.** It is surprising that after the teachings of the Arizal and his students were revealed, he did not quote from there. Especially since there is a specific *shaar* for this—in the *Shemonah Shearim* of the Arizal—which is *Shaar HaGilgulim*, in addition to what is brought in many places in the writings of the Arizal. See the introduction of Rav Chaim Vital to *Shaar HaHakdamos*, near the end.

**Vol. 3, at the beginning: *Tikkunei HaChet*.** See *Tanya* Chapter 7; *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 3; and Chapter 9 there.

**Ibid., p. 111a: Removing the ring from the *lulav* on *Hoshana Rabbah* after saying *Hallel*.** This requires study. Our custom is to remove it **before** saying *Hallel*. This is also the case in the *Bach*, *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* 654; see there for the reason. This is also written in *Darchei Chaim V'Shalom* 891.

**Vol. 4, at the beginning: "He should occupy himself with the secrets of the Torah, and it is a *tikkun*, etc."** From this there is another reason (an additional one, as the verse says "and also to call") for what the Arizal wrote, that specifically in these final generations it is permitted and a **mitzvah** to reveal this wisdom (Kabbalah). Rav Chaim Vital already elaborated on this in the aforementioned introduction, and he writes: Everything depends on engaging in this wisdom, and our prevention from engaging in it causes the delay and hindrance of the building of the *Beis HaMikdash*, etc. And all this evil is because... one does not engage in it... for there is no pleasure for the Holy One, Blessed be He, in all that He created in His world except when His children below engage in the secrets of the Torah, etc. For in the literal aspects of the Torah, etc., man was not created except to learn the wisdom of Kabbalah, etc. He brings and explains the words of the *Zohar*, Vol. 1, 26a and 27a; 118a; Vol. 2, 207a; and more; see there where he elaborates.

**Ibid., p. 87 and onwards:** See regarding all this in the Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Even HaEzer*, siman 39; and *Shaar HaMiluim*, siman 45.

In his *Chiddushim* to *Berachos* 3:5 (5a).

**Vol. 5, at the beginning: On the verse "And Yosef came."** See *Derech Mitzvosecha* by the Tzemach Tzedek, Vol. 2, p. 277b and onwards, where he elaborates on all this.

**Ibid., p. 190t: *S.N.A. S.K.A.*** See regarding this the Responsa *Tzafnas Paneach* by the Rogatchover Gaon, Rabbi Yosef Rosen, siman 25.

**Ibid., at the end, p. 182b: "He was perfect, etc., even for a thought, and it requires study where this is hinted."** It can be said that it is based on the *Zohar Chadash* 230, beginning of side a: "His inside like his outside, in all internal and external limbs, etc., 'You shall be perfect,' etc."

And see there, 165b, that he learns from this verse regarding Noach, "a righteous man, perfect in his generations."

## 2,745

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you write regarding your state of mind, which is not as it should be, and the lack of vitality in your learning, etc., and you conclude that you do not know how to advise yourself.

Now, you do not need to devise your own counsel, for the advice already counseled by our holy Torah regarding all the above is well known: "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him." Success in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus—and that the learning should be with the proper vitality—depends on this. However, just as one requires *siyata d'shmaya* for everything, and this is included in that, you must observe the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzuklaleh-h nbg"m zya*: the well-known *shiurim* in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*. Furthermore, it is appropriate that every weekday, before the morning *tefillah*, you give a few coins to *tzedakah*, as this is a *segulah* for the *tefillah* to be accepted. Surely you have studied with *iyun* and are fulfilling what is written in *Likutei Torah* in the *maamar* beginning with the words "Under the fact that you did not serve," etc.

With blessings for success in all the above.

**Secretary**

## 2847

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs, R' Avraham, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters dated 3, 9, 12, and 26 Nissan. I trust that my telegrams for the holiday of Pesach, as well as for the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad conference, were received in time. You will surely write in appropriate detail regarding how the conference went, the quality and quantity of the participants, and most importantly, regarding the practical outcomes that emerged from it...

It distresses me that, apparently, the reason for the temporary delay in granting the license to import the seforim is not known in your camp, for if it were, it would be easy to appeal it. Verbally, they stated the reason—almost officially—that Kehot seforim compete with the seforim printed in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily. It is understood that this has no basis, as it is the opposite of reality. Since my hope is strong that they will approve the contract, a list has been sent, as per your request, of Kehot publications as a proposal for a new shipment.

...to instill in Anash the idea that we are all parts of one complete entity. When one person wants to make a "Shabbos for himself," the result is not that he receives a larger portion of the Leviathan and Shor HaBar, or greater honor in this physical world—and certainly not in this material world. On the contrary, it is impossible for one part of a complete entity to be as it should be, and in a state of increase, at the same time that it is striving to snatch away from another part, or at the very least, not allowing it to occupy the place that belongs to it. Such an approach leads to damage, both because of the mistaken calculation mentioned above, and because of the haste and secrecy, which are not desirable at all. See also Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 31...

With blessings for proper health for you and all your household, may they live—awaiting good news regarding all the above.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2747*

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Your urgent letter of the 25th of the month, in which you write regarding the situation concerning matters of *shechitah* and *bedikah*, has just been received. I have already received a question about this... In truth, the entire question is pointless when one asks the same thing many times over. For, either way, if you wish to hear someone's opinion, the answer given the first time is sufficient; and if you do not wish to hear it, what is the benefit of asking repeatedly? Nevertheless, out of respect, I am enclosing a copy of my response to the aforementioned, from which my position on this matter can also be understood. I will repeat once more: if you stand with true firmness, you will succeed.

In general, it is incomprehensible what the laws of *tzedakah* have to do with the laws of *shechitah*; one should not mix one with the other. However, desire misleads the intellect. If, *chas v'shalom*, you do not conduct yourselves with firmness in this—just as, in my opinion, you are not conducting yourselves with firmness in matters of the rabbinate—then one can derive a *binyan av* (a foundational principle) from one matter to the other. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success, together with all *anash*—may they live—to conduct yourselves with the firmness that our holy *Nesi'im* demanded. As they say: "When one does so, one walks on an iron bridge," and it is upon their own responsibility.

With respect and blessings for both material and spiritual matters.

## 2848

[13 Iyar 5714]

...In continuation of the matter regarding the Genizah letters: although time does not permit me to go into the necessary length and detail, I will nevertheless respond to a few points, which are as follows:

The overwhelming majority of the Genizah letters and manuscripts were written on parchment, not paper. By "overwhelming majority," I do not mean just over half, but far more than three-quarters.

Regarding the letters printed in the collection *HaTamim*: it is understood that the typesetter was not given the Genizah letters themselves, but rather copies. These had been prepared several years prior by a *yungerman*—may Hashem avenge his blood—in Riga, who was a *yirei shamayim* but not meticulous, particularly in matters that did not hold much significance for Chassidim, such as dates and the like.

Regarding the style of the letters: the claim that "they were all written in exactly the same style" is astounding. This premise is entirely refuted from the outset, as among the writings there are: stories, testaments, *pidyon nefesh* (P"N), receipts, etc., and it is impossible for all of these to be in the same style, let alone to add the word "exactly." Perhaps the intent is to refer only to the actual letters among them. Even then, the claimant is incorrect, because some of the letters were printed decades before the discovery of this Genizah and are also found among the Genizah letters. If so, it is understood that, on the contrary, those who say the entire Genizah is a forgery cannot maintain that the style is identical between the letters that were printed—whose authenticity is beyond doubt—and those that they claim were forged in both content and language. It is self-evident that there is a similarity between them, especially between Chassidim and their Rebbes, as they strive in the style of their letters and their conduct in general to emulate their Rebbe. The witticism regarding this is already known, based on the words of our Sages (Sotah 11a): "Follow Hashem your G-d—is it possible for a person to follow the *Shechinah*? ... Rather, a student follows his teacher." A characteristic example of this is the well-known fact that copyists of manuscripts and *maamarim* of *Chassidus* throughout the generations strove to imitate the Rebbe’s handwriting, to the point that often, even without examining the body of the *maamar*, one can recognize the handwriting itself, whether it was a copyist from the generation of the Mitteler Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, etc.

Regarding the observation that many errors were found: I have already written (in my letter from Adar I, 5714) that if the hypothesis is correct—that the letters were copied from the original manuscripts for the officials of the Tsarist government, and consequently the work was done in haste and not necessarily by expert copyists, and furthermore, as mentioned above, Chassidim never concerned themselves with dates—then it is no wonder that the vast majority of the errors occurred. This is all the more true for one copying a manuscript today; before proofreading, there is a high percentage of errors, especially if copying a cursive manuscript where one letter runs into the next, etc. This is even more so if the copyist attempts to decipher abbreviations and does so in haste, which increases not only the number of errors but also the nature of the errors (let someone who is not an expert try to copy, without taking much time, an original manuscript from that era, such as a letter from the Baal Shem Tov or the Rav, the Chassid, R. Menachem Mendel of Horodok, which were printed in the collection *HaTamim* (issues 1 and 2), and then examine the errors they make!). This is especially true since, in the case at hand, according to the aforementioned hypothesis, there was no concern from the outset for the accuracy of the copy.

According to the aforementioned hypothesis, that the copying from the original manuscripts was done for government officials with the goal of deceiving them into believing these were the originals, it is understood why their external appearance had to be that of original letters, and why almost every single one had the official’s address in Russian on the back of the page. Why is the percentage of letters with substantive content so small, especially letters regarding Torah, etc.? This question is answered in a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the Genizah letters in *HaTamim*, issue 1. He writes at the end of his letter: "There are such things as matters of *Kabbalah Ma'asit*, combinations of Divine Names, and similar deep matters in *Kabbalah* that cannot be transmitted except through..." [This section was omitted in *Igros Baal HaTanya U'Bnei Doro*, as was the **primary** section of the Rebbe’s letter in which he writes his father’s opinion after reviewing "all the manuscripts and reading all the stories and writings; he praised them highly and revealed his holy opinion that all the writings and letters are only copies, etc., but the content of the writings and letters is true. And if one finds any contradiction, they are of little value compared to the wonder of their content and are nothing but the errors of the copyists."]

Consequently, it is no wonder that the percentage of substantive letters is small compared to the other letters, since, as mentioned, they were not submitted to be printed in *HaTamim*.

Anyone who has the slightest knowledge of the conduct of the Chassidic leaders of those generations knows that they did not write down their teachings. On the contrary, they were careful not to write them down for various reasons, and only in exceptional cases, when it was impossible to provide an answer orally, did they resort to writing, and even then, only in extreme brevity. Anyone who questions why there is a very small percentage of Torah teachings among the writings of one of the leaders and Rebbes of past generations simply demonstrates that he has **no** understanding of their conduct. Furthermore, even in the time of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his father, the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory, who answered their followers regarding matters of the *nigleh* of Torah and the teachings of *Chassidus* **much** more than the Chabad leaders before them—and certainly more than the Rebbes in the generation of the Baal Shem Tov and the Maggid—whose archives were preserved and it is **clear** that it is their handwriting or a copy from an original manuscript, even then, the percentage of letters regarding Torah, etc., is small. This is understandable, because the needs of the people are many, etc.; there were far more people asking about material matters or seeking a blessing, etc., than those asking about Torah, *nigleh*, and *Chassidus*. Most of the latter would ask them orally when they traveled to the Rebbes for the *regalim* and *moadim* and would then enter for *yechidus*, as these questions were not urgent matters that could not wait a few weeks or months for a resolution.

Regarding the fact that some of the letters are signed with the mother’s name, as in a *pidyon nefesh*, and not the father’s name: anyone with knowledge of the customs of Chassidim when writing to their Rebbe knows that they very often sign with the mother’s name, even in letters, and not only in a *pidyon nefesh*.

The assumption that if one can prove a single letter is a forgery, it is absolute proof that the entire Genizah is a forgery—this premise is clearly refuted from the outset. If so, one could prove the forgery of all our books, Heaven forbid, on the basis that printing errors are found in them and that additions from later periods are found, etc. It is well known that in the *Shas* there are additions from the *Rabbanan Savorai*, and similarly in many subsequent books.

On the contrary, if one finds among the letters even one that was known through **secret** tradition, Rebbe to Rebbe, this is not something that just anyone could forge and invent out of thin air; it must be that they copied from the original manuscripts those who knew of this secret tradition. It makes no difference whether it is combinations of Names, deep *Kabbalistic* matters, adjurations of angels, etc., as with all the things and categories enumerated by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his aforementioned letter. It is astonishing that the "forger" remains hidden, and was not known before this, nor is he known now. To me, this is most wondrous, because to forge letters—even just those that were printed, and certainly those that were not, which, as explained in the aforementioned letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, his father, the Rebbe Rashab, studied many times and praised highly—one must be not only a talented forger but also possess significant knowledge in matters of *Kabbalah* and *Chassidus*, in addition to an intimate knowledge of the relationships between the Rebbes and their families mentioned in the letters. It is a great wonder that a person with such talents did not publish anything in the years before the discovery of the Genizah, nor after. It is already known that in past generations, when the authorship of a book was questioned, they would explain who should be suspected of authoring the book or writing based on his knowledge. It is unnecessary to mention that regarding the *Zohar*, they mentioned the name of R. Moshe de Leon. Regarding several *teshuvos* of the *Rishonim*, they confused the Ramban, the Rashba, and the Ritba with one another, etc. The same is true in recent generations regarding the *She'eilot U'Teshuvot Besamim Rosh*, the tombstones found in Crimea, the *Yerushalmi Seder Kodashim*, etc., etc. To elaborate on such a simple matter is superfluous.

There was a custom in the past not to print books—whoever the author might be—without *haskamos* (approbations). The reason is simple: every human being is liable to err, and self-love and faith in one's own intellect cover all faults and errors. Even the greatest of Israel, the true *chad-bedra* (Sanhedrin 7b), would consult and ask for the opinions of others before issuing a final ruling.

In our wretched generation, there is no longer a need for *haskamos*; anyone who wishes says that he, too, is capable of being a sole judge, certainly in his own field, and if it is not his field, he makes assumptions and on their basis establishes the matter. The printer prints, and the reader decides that there is nothing more to be said after the printing is done.

The Rebbe of Munkacs—author of *Minchas Elazar* and others—whose way was stormy and who did not refrain from sharp expressions, etc., writes with known caution regarding the Genizah letters in general: "The hands of strangers, the forgers, have dominated them," "Beware and be careful not to believe them," "These letters are suspected of being forgeries" (*Divrei Torah*, 5th edition, 69).

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, announced his father’s decision, after they had examined all the Genizah writings (except for **individual** letters that came to others) **over the course of several months**, that the content of the writings and letters is true and the contradictions that may be found are of little value compared to the wonder of their content.

And they are the **only ones who saw the part of these Genizah writings whose content was: matters of *Kabbalah*, various epithets for the Names of the Holy One, blessed be He, names of angels and their songs, combinations of Names and their adjurations, and more.**

And yet, the author of *Igros Baal HaTanya U'Bnei Doro* writes: **"All of them** (the researchers into the authenticity of the writings) did not descend to a general and fundamental examination of the content of the writings. And I have reached the conclusion that all (!!!) of the Genizah letters that have been published are forgeries. And some of them were printed and disseminated even with the approval of the great men of Israel who were mistaken in this."

And who is the naive reader who would cast doubt on such simple certainty?

**M. Schneerson**

## 2849

B"H, 13 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with the needs of the community, Moreinu HaRav Dovid, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Emor. I was pleased to hear that my letter brought you satisfaction, even though I wrote the matter exactly as it is, without embellishment, simply to bring you satisfaction...

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the distribution of the matzah shemurah, and that you had a generous eye for others to enable them to merit it as well. Had I known in advance, I would have sent more, but one does not cry over the past, and everything depends on mazal. May it be the will of Hashem that by next year, all the matters that we currently accept through emunah—and which are consequently supported by the "food of faith" (*michla d'mehemanusa*)—will then be settled in the intellect and da'as, and you will use the power of emunah for even loftier matters. This is similar to what is explained in many places in Chassidus: that there are many levels in emunah. When a person elevates himself through the power of his intellect, he grasps with his intellect what yesterday was for him only a matter of emunah. Nevertheless, there remain for him many matters that, for the time being, his intellect is too limited to grasp, and he believes in them with simple emunah. This is similar to what is also seen now: for a young child, many things are matters of emunah, which an adult understands and knows. Consequently, it is understood that for one who is even greater than that adult, things that the adult requires emunah for are understood by the intellect.

I was pleased by what you wrote, that you are continuing with the printing of *Likutei Maamarei Razal* in various periodicals. I am certain you will send these excerpts here as well, and I thank you in advance...

With blessings for the proper success and for nachas from your children, may they live.

## 2551

B"H, Pesach Sheni, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

This is especially true since the name is a factor, as your honor—may he live and be well—is named after his grandfather, who was named after our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe.
