## 2552

B"H, 14 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Iyar, in which you write that you are having difficulty understanding the study of the *nigleh* and, in your opinion, this is because the *maggid shiur* is not accustomed to explaining in *Lashon HaKodesh*. Now, it is known that our Sages have ruled: "If you have not labored and found, do not believe; if you have labored and not found, do not believe."

In my opinion, this applies to you as well. For when a Jewish person has the desire to study Torah—especially if the study is with *yiras shamayim*—the *yetzer hara* rises up against this with various strange tactics. It is understood that he strives to explain to the person that these matters do not depend on him at all, but rather on someone else, and consequently, it is impossible to do anything about it, since he, for his part, has already done what is required of him. If, *chas v'shalom*, this temptation is accepted, it is liable to cause great damage, not only in the study of Torah but also in the performance of *mitzvos*, even practical *mitzvos*. For as mentioned above, the *yetzer* comes and proves with various strange arguments that, regarding the performance of *mitzvos* as well, the situation is the same. Just as in any war, it is easier to win at the beginning than after the enemy has already strengthened himself. As the *Zohar HaKadosh* (Vol. III, p. 87b) states regarding the verse "You shall rise before the aged" (*mipnei seivah takum*), that the *yetzer hara* grows old within him, and therefore the advice of the Torah is **"mipnei"** (before/because of) the *seivah* (the aged one), you shall rise. So too in your case: as soon as possible, you must nullify the aforementioned claims of the *yetzer hara* and crush them, as the ways to do this are explained in the *Tanya Kadisha* in the explanation of the statement of our Sages: "A person should always incite the *yetzer tov* against the *yetzer hara*." Then you will succeed both in the study of Torah and in the performance of *mitzvos* and in *yiras shamayim*, which is his true treasure.

It is possible that because the *Rosh Yeshiva* and the students are not accustomed to each other, there are some difficulties in mutual understanding, but this is considered nothing and naught compared to the happiness that comes to a Jewish person through the study of our holy Torah, the wisdom and will of *Hashem*. And "according to the effort is the reward."

It is possible that among your peers there are also those who think that the obstacle to Torah study and the necessary diligence is due to the aforementioned reason or something similar. It would be good for you to explain to them everything written here, and you will surely find the appropriate words required.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

## 2593

2593

By the Grace of Hashem, 15 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...And a primary matter, which is in addition to what was conveyed to him by the esteemed Chossid, etc., Rabbi Chaim Mordechai Avraham Hodakov, may he live, via telephone: I do not understand his conduct at all regarding what was reported to me concerning the lack of eating, speech, etc., etc.

Surely he has some reason for this, but since "a woman’s tear is readily available" and "women are of light mind," and furthermore, changing to better conduct is not achieved through coercion—Hashem does not desire [service through] speech and whips. This is in addition to the directive of the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, and our Alter Rebbe, etc., regarding the necessity of maintaining the health of the body, as is also explained in the maamar of the most recent 10th of Shevat. Elaboration on this is superfluous. It is already known what is brought in Chassidus regarding the fact that Yaakov could have chosen even non-kosher animals for the offering, even though this is in the context of offering sacrifices; for before the giving of the Torah there were many paths, but after the standing at Har Sinai, what is forbidden is forbidden, and there is no room for ruling that it is permitted (except for a prophet who heard a command from Hashem against this, as a temporary instruction—and it is understood that I do not suspect him of this). I await good news that from here on, there will be peace in their home, and that they will increase in the health of the body and the health of the soul, and may Hashem grant them success.

With blessings—awaiting good news.

## 2554

15 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chassid, a man of action, engaged in communal needs, energetic and prolific, etc., Rabbi Tzvi Hirsch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I have received the sheets of the commentary on the Torah by the Ramban, along with the notes of your honor, and I thank you for the trouble of sending them to me. I enjoyed reading through the pages and seeing how much work and wisdom you invested in these notes. Following custom, I am appending here a few notes of my own regarding the opening of the Ramban’s commentary.

Also enclosed are some notes on your pamphlet, "Proposal for the Correction of Eiruvin." The interpretation of our Sages on the verse "And Vahev in Sufah" is already well-known.

On this occasion, I wish to express my blessings to your honor for a proper and successful journey, and that you may utilize your influence while in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, to raise the pride of Israel, the elder, with majesty and a high hand.

With respect and blessing.

***

**Notes on the pamphlet of the Ramban’s Torah commentary, etc.**

**Line 3. The Aleph — "And the awesome."** One should note: See *Devarim 10:17*. And see *Yoma 69b*.

**Ibid. "I will begin" and the note thereon.** In the introduction to the *Yad*, he also uses the future tense: "**I will divide** the laws... **I will divide** it." Generally, it is somewhat puzzling to say that the book was written before the introduction. And the contradiction between the years—in *Hilchos Shemitah V'Yovel* (10:5) it says 1007 years after the Destruction, and in the introduction, 1008—is something that has already been noted, and in any case requires clarification, given that in *Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh* (11:16) it says 1009 years after the Destruction (as it should be).

One should add to this that in *Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh* itself, it is slightly implied that they were written in the year 1000 after the Destruction (9:5).

All of the above is understood based on what is known: that the Rambam wrote the *Sefer HaYad*, corrected it, and corrected it again, etc. (see *Rambam*, Shulsinger edition, end of volume 5). It is understood that he did not change every manuscript in the second edition, only the laws that required correction, especially since copies of the first edition had already spread, as cited in the *Igros HaRambam*, by his son, etc.

Therefore, it is possible that chapter 7 of *Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh* was written in the first edition in the year 1000, and the chapter was included as is in subsequent editions. Chapter 11 underwent changes or corrections later on, and its final editing was in the year 1009.

The introduction was written after the Rambam was already able to determine not only the number of books, but also the laws and mitzvos contained in each and every book, as he details at the end of the introduction—meaning that all the "material" was already prepared for him, but *before* the writing of the book itself, as he concludes: "**And now I will begin** to explain the judgments of every mitzvah," etc.

Based on the above, it is also understood that there is room for all the opinions regarding the year the Rambam *began* working on his book *Mishneh Torah* (cited in *Sdei Chemed* and *Kesef Mishneh*. The earliest of them is the year 1000, as mentioned above).

**Ibid. "With awe... with trembling."** One should note: From the language of the Gemara, *Berachos 22a*. And what the Ramban adds here, "**with fear**," requires study, because according to the teachings of the *Sod* (Kabbalah), these four expressions are precise and correspond to the four letters of the Name *Havayah* (*Likutei HaShas* of the Arizal to tractate *Moed Katan*. By the way: there is an obvious omission there in all the printings I have seen, the content of which is an explanation of the matter of "trembling," which is in the external limbs, in the secret of the *Heh* in the Name, the external garment, etc. The copyist skipped from the third "in the Name" to the fourth "in the Name." Woe to the ear that hears, and woe to the one who noted this!). He could have also preserved the end of the rhyme (a *kamatz* vowel) by changing the order and writing "with trembling... with awe." Perhaps it can be said that "**with fear**" corresponds to the *kotzo shel yud* (the tip of the *yud*), which in several matters is hinted at separately and is not included in the *yud* itself. Just as in the saying of our Sages, "Five names were called for it" (*Bereishis Rabbah* 14:9), even though in the *Zohar* (I, 79b) they are included in four names. And in *Berachos*, he only counted four things, similar to the aforementioned *Zohar*, that "fear" is included in "awe." But this is not the place to elaborate.

**Ibid. Line 4. "Forgiveness... pardon and atonement."** Note the *Yerushalmi*, end of *Yoma*. *Acharonim* on *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim* 607. *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe there, section 7, and in his *Siddur*.

**Ibid. Line 5. "With bowing. With kneeling. With prostration."** Note: From the language of the Gemara, *Berachos 34b*.

**Ibid. Line 6. "The egg of an ant."** For now, I have not found this elsewhere. It requires study and clarification; perhaps it was corrupted by copyists, and it should be "**the egg of a louse**," which is the smallest living creature in the world (*Shabbos 107b*), and corresponds to the "upper sphere"—the most important creation in the world. Note the *Rambam*, *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah* 2:7. *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*—by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe—chapter 7 (83a).

***

**Notes on the pamphlet "Proposal for the Correction of Eiruvin"**

**Page 1. Section 2. The opinion of Rashi.** So ruled our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch*, 345:11, and elsewhere. In *Responsa Beis Av*, second series, section 6, in the indices, he counts thirty *Rishonim* who hold like Rashi.

**Ibid. 11.** The reason that the number 600,000—also including Eretz Yisrael—is because they were commanded regarding Shabbos at Marah (see *Tosafos* s.v. *Et HaTechumin*, *Shabbos 87b*), and they still had the status of *Bnei Noach* (as is known, the opinion of several *Rishonim* on this). And even afterwards, at the Giving of the Torah, the matters of Shabbos were defined "as He commanded you"—at Marah.

**Page 2. Section 3. According to all, a *Reshus HaRabim* by Torah law.** This requires study and clarification. For it seems to me that all streets end, *ultimately*, with bridges and tunnels blocked by *tzuras hapesach* or also a partition and "shranken" (barriers) to collect taxes and the like. See *Aruch HaShulchan* of Rabbi A. of Butchatch, 345.

**Page 3. The definition of a sea and a river.** (The difference in writing a *Get* and the like). Seemingly, one could say if its waters are stagnant and remain in their place (even if there are waves), or if they are flowing (*Mikvaos* 5:4; *Makkos 4a*; *Yevamos 121a*). And further, see *Responsa Tzafnas Paneach* of the Rogatchover Gaon, 59-60. But in truth, it seems to me that in every place it is according to its nature. And in *Hilchos Eiruvin*, it depends on what is seen in practice, if (at least sometimes) it raises a sandbar and solidifies. This is something to say. And with this, it is explained why in the *Rishonim* and *Acharonim* several laws and distinctions are detailed regarding the aforementioned concerns, in different rivers, in *ukim*, etc.—even though they are not explained in the *Shas*.

Based on this, one must clarify all parts of the perimeter of Manhattan brought here. One should study the books cited in this regard in *Orchos Chayim* (the new one), 343.

**Page 3. The concern that perhaps the sea will raise a sandbar according to one opinion.** This requires study, for the *Rema* rules this way (see *Yad Malachi*, *Klalei HaRema* 18). And the Alter Rebbe copied it as a halachic ruling, 363:36.

**Ibid. The opinion of the Chasam Sofer.** The opinion of the Alter Rebbe (ibid.) is that it is good to be concerned for the words of the one who forbids.

**Page 4. Section 8. That it is possible to see from the top of the high buildings, etc.** It does not seem correct to me at all to say that by building a tower with its top in the heavens in the middle of a very large area, the entire area *will turn* from a *Reshus HaRabim* *by Torah law* to a *Reshus HaYachid*. And one cannot say that everything *capable* of seeing the perimeter by means of a building and the like is a *Reshus HaYachid* by Torah law, for if so, the question of the *Shas* that "the ocean surrounds it" (*Eiruvin 22b*, according to the explanation brought in the pamphlet that the perimeter is required) remains in its place, as is told regarding Solomon (*Yerushalmi*, cited in *Tosafos* s.v. *KeKadur*, *Avodah Zarah 41a*).

And it must be said that according to the above, it is necessary that he see it while standing on the surface of the land. And in *Bechoros* (54a) it says it is 16 *mil*.

And perhaps in the case at hand it is more than that, for there it must be that the eye has dominion over it to guard and count, whereas here it is not so with the perimeter of partitions.

Note the above from *Pesachim* (94a): "He can enter with horses and mules," etc. See also regarding the measure of a nearby place (*Moed Katan 22a*), in our days when they travel by train, by airplane, and the like—there is discussion about this in the books cited in *Sefer Kol Bo*—by Rabbi Grunwald—Part 1, p. 350.

**Page 5. End of section 11.** One should study *Biur Halacha* to the *Mishnah Berurah*, 358:9.

**Ibid. Section 12.** See *Biur Halacha* to the *Mishnah Berurah*, 358:9.

**Ibid. 3.** It is a subject of dispute—see the books cited in the glosses of the *Maharsham* in *Orchos Chayim* (the new one), 358.

***

Regarding the matter that it is a mitzvah to correct *eiruvin*—see *Eiruvin 28a*. *Tur Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim* 366:13.

*Shitah Mekubetzes* to *Beitzah* (16b). *Responsa HaRosh*, rule 21. *Rashbetz* (Part 2, 37). *Chasam Sofer*, *Orach Chayim* 99.

*Responsa Beis Av*, second series, section 1.

One should note that the entire latter book discusses matters of *eiruvin*, and there is discussion there on several details brought in this pamphlet.

## 2555

B"H, 15 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you write about what you have been going through. You complain about your current situation, as you are teaching *tinokos shel beis raban* (young children), and you believe that because of this, you have regressed in your own learning. Consequently, you wish to either travel to Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—or be assigned a higher-level class to teach.

In general, matters such as these fall under the administration of the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch institutions in Morocco. I have therefore forwarded your request to them, and they will be in contact with you.

However, what surprises me most is your distress regarding your current occupation, and your concluding remark that you are in great pain because of it, claiming that this engagement has caused you to fall behind in your studies. Yet, it is a well-known and famous teaching of the Baal Shem Tov—which we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—that it is worth the descent of the *neshamah* to this world below, to be here in a physical body for seventy or eighty years, just to do a favor for a fellow Jew—man or woman—even once in one's lifetime, whether in material or spiritual matters. The *neshamah* is truly a "part of Elokus from above," hewn from beneath the Throne of Glory; yet, the *Shechinah* says it is worth descending from its place of honor, from the highest heights to the deepest depths, just to perform one act of kindness.

And here, Hashem has granted you the merit and success to bring the hearts of fellow Jews closer to our Father in Heaven every single day. Through this, you have a share in the "joy of Hashem in His works" and the "joy of Yisrael in their Maker." Yet, you claim that one can fall behind in the study of Torah because of this, and you are in great distress. When the matter is so clear and simple, one must wonder where these arguments come from; it seems that you are in doubt, and you mistakenly believe these to be the arguments of the *yetzer tov*.

Abandon this line of thinking entirely. Dedicate yourself to your holy work of teaching Torah to the children of Yisrael—for one who teaches, starting from the *aleph-beis* and so on, cannot know what is considered greater before Hashem. Furthermore, as our Sages of blessed memory said, "Do not sit and weigh the *mitzvos* of the Torah..." as it is written, "The path of life, **lest you weigh it**." It is understood that this work must be done with joy for having merited such a task. Then, you will also succeed in your personal matters, which will make your mind and heart—in the words of the Alter Rebbe—a thousand times more refined, and you will ascend in your study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

***

**Teaching of the Baal Shem Tov:** See also above, Letter 2551, and the references in the notes there.

**In the words of the Alter Rebbe:** Torah Or, at the beginning.

## 2596

B"H, 15 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 9 Iyar: It is well known that the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, which is the foundation of our holy Torah, is that all matters in the world occur through Divine Providence from Him, may He be blessed. He is the One who oversees every single one of the Bnei Yisrael—not only in a general sense, but in every detail and every minute detail of daily life. Consequently, regarding every individual, the verse states, "Hashem is with me, I will not fear." Even if at times one loses sight of this, it is merely a tactic of the yetzer hara, which seeks to frighten a Yid, chas v'shalom, from our Father in Heaven through foolish arguments, as our Sages have said regarding this. For the truth is as stated above: every single Yid is a child of our Father in Heaven, and it is impossible to separate a father from his son or daughter.

The conclusion to be drawn from this is that there is no room for fear, chas v'shalom, at all, since "Hashem is your shadow at your right hand," and He, may He be blessed, watches over and oversees each and every one of us. It is my hope that these few lines, though small in quantity, will suffice to ensure that you remain strong in your trust in Hashem in your daily life, and that you will engage in your affairs with confidence and joy.

May Hashem cause the days of her pregnancy to be completed properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child in its proper time, in a good and easy manner.

With blessings,

P.S.
It would be appropriate to check the mezuzos in your home, as it is likely that there are some that need to be replaced, and likewise to check your tefillin.

## 2557

B"H, 15 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos: as an aside, it is surprising that you exert yourself to be only—as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, used to say—one of the "tzaros Chassidim" (Chassidim of troubles), meaning that you write only in times of trouble, G-d forbid, and were it not for that, all vision would be sealed from you.

Regarding your question: a long time ago I already urged you and wrote to you about the absolute necessity of being in *kiruv hada'as* (closeness of mind) with *baalei batim*, especially those who, if it seems that one suffers from them, it is not due to a lack of *yiras shamayim* on their part, but at most only due to a lack of knowledge. Consequently, it is *kal v'chomer* that one must draw them close in appropriate ways, especially regarding [the matter you mentioned]... I am not at all pleased with the relationship between you. Since you are the younger one, and Hashem has merited you to study in the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva and to receive many instructions from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, regarding conduct in general, and regarding the matter of *ahavas Yisrael* in this in particular, the initiative and the first steps—and perhaps even more than that—must come from your side. There is no issue here of diminishing one’s stature or insulting the honor of Torah, etc., etc., as is understood. The story of the wise man is already well-known—I believe it is brought in the sefer *Mivchar HaPeninim* by Bedersi—explaining why the wise go to the wealthy, and not the wealthy to the wise: the reason is that the wealthy, when they are not wise, do not know the value of wisdom and what they are lacking. The wise, however, recognize the value that exists in wealth and that it should be utilized. The same applies to the matter at hand...

With blessings for success in all of the above.

With blessings and regards to all *anash*, awaiting good news.

## 2598

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished Torah scholar, etc., R' Dan Hakohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I have received your letter of 11 Iyar. As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about when I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, at a time of favor. It is surprising, however, that you do not mention in your letter whether you are writing on their behalf—based on the teaching of our Sages that a person’s agent is like the person himself—or whether you are writing on your own initiative, out of the principle of *ahavas Yisrael*, which is a great principle of the Torah. As our Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya—who is the authority on the hidden dimensions of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the authority on the revealed dimensions of Torah—both state, this is the vessel for "loving Hashem your G-d." The mitzvah of loving Hashem is the root for the fulfillment of all positive mitzvos, within which is also included the mitzvah of fearing Hashem, which is the root for the fulfillment of all negative mitzvos. Thus, *ahavas Yisrael* is the root for all mitzvos in general. I am certain that when you have good news regarding those mentioned in your letter, you will inform me. Thank you in advance.

Regarding the end of your letter concerning a fee for your efforts: the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself. In return for all the above, you should increase your efforts in drawing the hearts of Jewish men and women closer to our Father in Heaven, through the influence of the "right hand that draws near," and through *ahavas Yisrael*. If you do this with the appropriate *mesiras nefesh* and dedication, you will surely succeed, and that will be my reward.

You surely have fixed times for study, including the inner dimensions of the Torah. Since you have established a connection with me through correspondence, I trust that you will set a *shiur* for studying Chabad *seforim*, beginning with the holy Tanya.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. In your letter, you mention that those you are writing about are in the city of Djerba; I assume you mean the city of Djerba and the holy community there. I am interested to know about any study of the inner dimensions of the Torah—is it taking place there, and in what manner?

## 2599

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the beginning of the week, in which you write that you have begun working on a *Shabbos* gathering organized by *anash* of Lubavitch.

For when one does a favor—whatever favor it may be—for another, our Sages of blessed memory say regarding this: "The poor person does more for the householder than the householder does for the poor person." And when the favor is a spiritual one, where one brings others closer to our Father in Heaven, to Torah and *mitzvos*, the benefit that one receives oneself through this is far, far greater. This is especially expressed in the blessing of Hashem, that He helps the one who performs this spiritual favor so that they themselves can conduct their life according to the demands of our holy Torah without obstacles, and that they should also ascend from strength to strength in their private matters.

May Hashem help you to work on the aforementioned *Shabbos* gathering with the dedication expected of a Jewish daughter. May you be successful in seeing good results from your work in this, and may you be able to report good news regarding this, as well as regarding your success in your studies and your deeds in general.

With blessings for success,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. My request: convey a greeting to those who are working with you, and also share with them the content of what is written above, and wish them all blessing and success.

## 2660

2660

B”H, 16 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Iyar, in which you write that in the past you studied at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim... and subsequently became lax in your studies and spent part of your time working at various jobs in Kfar Chabad, and you ask my opinion on what you should do in the coming months.

In my opinion, you should enter the Yeshiva as soon as possible and study there with *mesiras nefesh* and diligence. This will be good preparation in general, and also regarding the matter of entering the vocational school. For it is understood that priority in admission to this school is given to those *avreichim* who demonstrate that their intellect rules over their desires, and that they are capable of fulfilling the task assigned to them as required. Those who do as they please are not suited for the discipline and conduct of *kabbalas ol* and the principle of "we will do" preceding "we will hear."

I trust that you recite the daily *Tehillim* after morning *davening*, and that you also have a set time for studying *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*. May Hashem grant you success.

Awaiting good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2662

B"H, Lag B'Omer, 5714
Brooklyn

To the Administration of the Beis Rivkah School and Seminary
Yeres, France
May Hashem keep them alive

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the preparation of a memorial book for the supporters of the aforementioned institutions, and I, too, participate in this with a willing heart.

It is my prayer that this memorial book will correspond to what is stated: "Then those who fear Hashem spoke to one another... and a book of remembrance was written before Him for those who fear Hashem and for those who contemplate His name." This verse encompasses the three garments of the soul, which are the three modes of human action: thought, speech, and deed.

Deed is the essential thing, for any matter connected to actual deed has continuity and permanence. This is all the more true regarding matters of goodness, truth, and holiness, the entirety of which is that they are eternal.

This is especially true of a matter connected to education on the foundation of holiness, and above all, the "Beis Rivkah" educational institution. Its goal is not only to educate the daughters of Yisrael so that they are worthy of their name—daughters of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah, who built the house of Yisrael—but it is also an institution that trains educators; educators in a manner of "producing fruit and fruit of fruit," ever-increasing and ever-brightening.

May it be the will of Hashem that all those inscribed in this memorial book have their remembrance and their contribution come before Hashem for good, for grace, for kindness, for mercy, and for a good life and peace, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings.

#### ***2662***

Published in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 22, p. 429.

## 2663

B"H, 18 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 13 Iyar, which was received on the bright day of Hod sheb'Hod, the Hillula of the Rashbi, which opened the channel of influence regarding the concept of "and upon Him is his desire" — in both interpretations, whereby through his opening, every single Jew has the ability and power to attain this (see the introduction to the Lag B'Omer 5710 Kuntres, Kuntres 78). And according to what is known regarding the connection between the Rashbi, Achiyah HaShiloni, the Baal Shem Tov, and the Alter Rebbe, this is especially relevant to each and every one of us who are connected to the Alter Rebbe through his successors, the Nesi'im of Chabad throughout the generations, up to and including the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory.

In it, you write regarding the discussion you had concerning the administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, where the previous administration stated that the work was difficult for them, etc.

It is understood that based on the aforementioned, regarding the concept of Lag B'Omer—whose essence extends throughout the entire year—and according to the message of the Baal Shem Tov in the name of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, that his coming depends on the spreading of his wellsprings outward, it is a great wonder that those who have merited to stand at the helm of such work would say that the work is difficult for them, etc., at a time when this is the purpose of the entire Seder Hishtalshelus and the creation of the world as such, specifically as explained in Tanya, Chapter 36. It is understood that it is the duty and privilege of every member to assist the administration in its work to the best of their ability; but to shirk such a great privilege, and to fail to strive in this with added courage, is, on the face of it, contrary to reason. It is understood that the meaning of this letter is not to intervene in the aforementioned, nor even to offer a suggestion, for any work, in order to be as it should be and performed with hiddur, must be done with a joyous heart and not merely by way of kabbalas ol. Rather, it is to awaken [you] to the inner nature of your work as I see it ought to be, and to the attitude that such work should inspire. May the Ribono shel Olam bless and grant success to all members of the administration, past and future, to add courage to their work with joy, which in itself will diminish the concealments and obstructions, and success will ascend higher and higher.

With blessings to draw closer, at the very least little by little, to the opening of Rabbi Shimon, the master of the Hillula, who is bound in a single bond with the Holy One, blessed be He, and because of this, "and upon Him is his desire."

## 2665

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., our teacher Rabbi Yisrael Yehuda, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Iyar, in which you write that you returned home yesterday: It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your activities in bringing the hearts of our fellow Jews closer to our Father in Heaven while you were in the army reserves. For it is well known—the ruling of the Baal Shem Tov that we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—that in everything a Jewish person sees or hears, there is a lesson for his avodah of his Creator. This is certainly true when a Jew finds himself in a new environment for a period of time, where he must surely utilize this opportunity in his avodah of his Creator, appropriate to the new environment and conditions.

After all, "Love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle of the Torah and a vessel for the mitzvah of "Love Hashem your G-d," which is the foundation for all positive mitzvos, including the mitzvah of the fear of Hashem, and fear is the foundation for all negative mitzvos. It follows that "Love your fellow as yourself" is a vessel, a preparation, and a cause for the fulfillment of all the mitzvos. This is simple to understand, and there is nothing that can stand before the will. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for true health, both materially and spiritually.

## 2656

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to the questions in your letter:

1) Regarding your study of the end of Chapter 1 of Tanya concerning the source of the souls of the nations who are not Jewish, and your question regarding the souls of the righteous among the nations of the world (*Chasidei Umos HaOlam*):

The souls of the *Chasidei Umos HaOlam* are drawn from *Noga*, as explained in several places in *Chassidus*, including in the printed *Likutei Biurim* on *Kuntres HaHispaalus*, page 47, column 4. See also *Zohar* Vol. III, 95b and onward.

2) How is it with a *ger* (convert) who has converted; does his soul remain as it was during his non-Jewish state?

Heaven forbid to say such a thing. It is obvious that a soul of *kedushah* is drawn to him. This is also one of the interpretations of the expression of our Sages, "A *ger* who has converted is like a newborn child." See the introduction to the *Zohar*, page 13, bottom of column 1 and top of column 2, regarding the source of the souls of converts.

You are surely aware of the *takanah* that applies to every person: to recite daily, after *davening*, the portion of *Tehillim* as divided for the days of the month, and likewise to study the *Chumash* portion of the week with the commentary of *Rashi*. Keep these *takanos*, as they are also a *segulah* for success in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of *Chassidus*.

With blessings,

Secretary

## 2657

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, etc., our teacher and rabbi, R. Aharon, may he live, Hakohen.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through your brother, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who is occupied with communal needs and conducts his business with integrity, our teacher and rabbi, R. Yaakov, may he live, Hakohen. However, he did not write me any details about you, and I hope that you will inform me of this as well.

May Hashem, blessed be He, grant you success, such that you will have only good news to share regarding yourself, and also regarding your influence upon your surroundings to bring Jews closer to our Father in Heaven, each according to his own way. For Torah and mitzvos are **equal** for all Jews, yet one must have an appropriate starting point for each person. If one is a merchant, he must have specific, set times for learning, and his primary avodah is in matters connected to business—giving tzedakah, and being careful to avoid *hasagas gevul* (encroachment on others' livelihood), theft, etc.

And those who hold a position of *keli kodesh*, such as a Rav, a shochet, a melamed, or yeshiva students, must also give tzedakah and be careful to avoid *hasagas gevul*, theft, etc.

Their primary work, however, is to be diligent in learning Torah and the avodah of tefillah, and there are other similar distinctions among various classes of people. Yet, as stated earlier, all Jews are equally obligated in all mitzvos, without any excuse that one mitzvah is desired while another is difficult, seeking to fulfill one's obligation through a different one instead.

From this, it is understood that one who possesses the power of speech, or is otherwise gifted with influence over acquaintances and friends, his avodah must be to dedicate himself to propaganda—to make them into Jews who learn Torah and fulfill mitzvos.

And since this is demanded of a Jew, it is certain that Hashem, blessed be He, grants the *kochos* to be able to carry it out, and rewards this with *bracha* and *hatzlachah* in that which you yourself and your family, may they live, are in need. May Hashem, blessed be He, grant you the merit to report good news regarding all of the above.

With a blessing for success.

#### ***2657***

**R. Aharon:** Katz. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 5, 1510, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 2658

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It is a well-known ruling of the Mishnah that "a single judge may not judge alone," which, in my opinion, refers to the Holy One, Blessed be He, and not to any human being, whoever he may be. I believe that if Rav Ashi, who was a wealthy man, a great leader in Israel, and the singular authority of his generation, would ask every butcher in his city for their opinion whenever he had to rule on a question regarding an animal, then all the more so, someone who is not the singular authority of his generation should be willing to hear the opinion of another Jew. He should not twist and distort things to act as a sole judge in a matter that affects hundreds of Jewish children, and in a matter that is connected to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and the Rebbes before him—may the merit of the righteous protect us. Consequently, one may find himself connected to the Rebbes, or, Heaven forbid, the opposite.

...It is already a well-known saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that while it is a known ruling of the Mishnah that everyone must be judged favorably, one must be careful not to destroy matters of holiness by doing so.

I await a prompt response regarding all of the above.

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***2658***

**Rav Ashi:** Sanhedrin 7b.

## 2699

B”H, 21 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, scion of noble ancestors,
Rabbi Avraham Yehuda, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding your question as to which of Anash in your vicinity are qualified and capable of the work of organizing the *bichlach* (booklets): this must be determined on the spot, as my acquaintance with them is only through correspondence, and therefore I do not know them in relation to this matter. It is surely unnecessary to point out to someone like yourself that since these manuscripts have gone through many adventures, one must certainly be careful with them—even during the aforementioned work—so that the hands of strangers do not touch them. And the Ribono shel Olam does not perform a miracle for nothing; that is, the *sitra d’le’oza* (the side of impurity), where the concept is "for free, without mitzvos," and not even a "stranger" [is permitted], as explained in the *Hemshech* of 5631, *Vehecherim*—that is, a stranger in this matter; see there in the *maamar* beginning *Vehecherim*.

In particular, this is a matter of interest, as we are now publishing the *drushim* of the holy Rabbi, etc., R’ Hillel of Paritch on Sefer Shemos, which is found here as an organized booklet in the format of *Pelech HaRimon* on Sefer Bereishis. If among the *maamarim* in the *bichlach* you write about there are also these *maamarim* on Sefer Shemos, it is possible they contain additions, etc., even though the booklet in my possession here is generally organized for printing. Moreover, it has already undergone censorship review in the past, as is evident from the various corrections within it...

As you requested, I will mention you and all those you wrote about when I am at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*. May the Almighty grant each of us the merit to report good news, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing,

#### ***2699***

**Rabbi Avraham Yehuda:** Chen. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 8, 2339, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

**In organizing the bichlach:** From the estate of his father, R’ D.T. See above, ibid.

## B'ater

B'H, 21 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote in your letter, it is surely unnecessary to remind you once again of the mitzvah in our holy Torah to safeguard one’s physical health, as is also explained in the maamar of 10 Shevat of this year and in many other places. Such a simple matter requires no further proof. Consequently, the manner of your learning or your contemplation of Torah subjects should certainly be arranged in a way that does not negatively impact your health. Do not deceive yourself into saying that concerns for your health stem from the yetzer hara; although that is sometimes the case, in general, the commandment "Know Him in all your ways" implies that it is a great principle for the body to be healthy and whole. Therefore, when you feel fatigue in your learning or when reviewing your studies in your thoughts, you should either switch to a different type of study or take a break for rest. Beyond the fact that this is a mitzvah, as mentioned above, in the context of Torah study itself, this is a preparation so that learning will be possible afterward—and in many matters, the preparation for a mitzvah is considered like the mitzvah itself.

I trust that you were called to the Torah near your birthday, and that you gave to tzedakah on your birthday before the morning and afternoon prayers. May all of the above bring you an increase in blessing and success in your personal affairs and in your activities in the vineyard of Chabad.

With blessings for success and with regards to all of anash, may they live.

## 2711

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and refined, engaged in communal needs,
R' Yosef, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your notification that on the 3rd of Iyar your son Yitzchak, may he live, turned three years old: May it be the will of Hashem that you and your wife, may you live, raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with proper health and tranquility of soul and body.

With blessings for success in your holy avodah and for good tidings in all the above.

P.S.
Regarding what you write about performing the haircut: I have already written my opinion on this. Even though according to the revealed Torah it is permissible—and even more so according to what is explained in Shaarei Teshuvah to Orach Chaim, siman 531—nevertheless, we rely on the custom of Yisrael to perform the haircut of young children in Meron on Lag B'Omer, as is brought in many places. It is obvious that not all those who have their hair cut then were born on that specific day by design; nevertheless, we attach this matter to a meritorious day. This can be explained based on what is brought in the writings of the Arizal and in Pri Etz Chaim, etc., regarding the connection between hair cutting and the days of Sefirah specifically, from which the hiddur of a haircut on Lag B'Omer is understood (though it requires some study, as it is brought in certain places that the Arizal would not have his hair cut even on Lag B'Omer). Therefore, it seems to me that the haircut should be performed on Lag B'Omer, and may it be at a good and successful time.

#### ***2711***

**R' Yosef:** Goldberg.

**I have already written:** Above, 2704, and in the references noted there.

## 2772

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter from 3 Iyar has just been received, as well as the one preceding it... And since it is in the hands of Anash to distribute Chabad seforim on a large scale in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), and the demand for them has also grown, and the prices—given the circumstances—are not high, and even to the physical eye success is visible here that is beyond the natural way—yet you sit with folded arms! In almost every single letter, you content yourself with the notification that business is weak and the debt remains where it is, even though you immediately conclude that there is reason for a blessing to take effect.

Yet now, in dozens of places in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), there are Anash, or those of the lineage of Anash, or even the youth of Aguch, or at the very least those with whom you have been in contact recently. It is obvious that through a commission—that is, by way of brokerage or the like—they would publicize and also serve as intermediaries for the sale of the seforim and kuntreisim to wider circles, provided that the prices are not raised more than is necessary and that they work on the aforementioned with the necessary energy and in an orderly fashion. There is also a very great spiritual matter in this: that the seforim and kuntreisim will reach those to whom, until now, there was no possibility of them reaching or being studied by.

It is understood that since you are the distributor, you must take the lead in all the aforementioned work. But on the other hand, I am confident that Anash, both young and old, will assist in all of this. Distribution is one of the primary branches of the avodah of Anash in every single place, and further elaboration is superfluous. Without wishing to repeat all of this, it would be good and worthwhile for you to publicize my words or even propose them at the upcoming meeting of Aguch and Tzeirei Aguch, for "in the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

With blessings for proper health for you and your entire household (may they live), and awaiting good tidings in all of the above.

#### ***2772***

**Chabad seforim... in Eretz Yisrael:** See also above, letter 2747.

## 2773

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Iyar, in which you write about your situation and the various difficulties in obtaining a position.

Regarding your attributing this to your religious observance—that because of it, the non-observant are persecuting you—it is already well-known from *Birkas Hamazon* that it is from the Torah that it is specifically Hashem who sustains and provides for all. Consequently, you are also included in this, and what can a human being do to you when Hashem wishes to provide for you? It is therefore understood that if there are difficulties in livelihood, it depends on your own actions and not on the will of a person who has no power to save. When one increases their study of Torah and observance of mitzvos, Hashem increases His blessings, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "Whoever adds, they add to him." Although all of the above is simple, I have put it in writing because it seems from your letter that you sometimes entertain the thought that others have control over you regarding your livelihood.

Regarding [name] *tichyeh*, it was necessary to clarify early on her conduct regarding the laws of *taharas hamishpachah*, and primarily regarding the *mikveh*—that it should be a *mikveh* that is *kasher* and *b'hiddur*, using rainwater or spring water, but certainly not city water, which passes through various pipes, water meters, etc. When you are careful with the above as required, your family situation will surely also improve, and may Hashem grant you the merit to succeed and to bring good tidings regarding all of the above.

It is surprising that you do not mention your *shiurim* in the study of *Toras Hachassidus*, in addition to your study of the *nigleh* of Torah.

With blessings, and awaiting good tidings.

## 2714

2714

B.H., 21 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Iyar:

1) Regarding your involvement in registration, outreach, etc.: It is understood that this must be done with the consent of the Yeshiva administration. Certainly, a way must be found to arrange these matters so that they do not distract or interfere with your studies in Nigleh and Chassidus. Even if, on rare occasions, the timing does not align, you will surely make up for any incidental loss in your Nigleh and Chassidus studies during your free time.

2) Regarding what you wrote about traveling to the United States to study here: There is still much to accomplish and much in which to improve at your Yeshiva in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). You should study with dedication, self-sacrifice, and the appropriate diligence, without distracting yourself with thoughts of traveling, etc., for the time being.

3) Regarding what you wrote about your lack of diligence in your Nigleh studies: It is well known how much our Rebbeim, the Nesi'im, emphasized diligence in the study of Nigleh. Our Sages have already said, "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him." Consequently, the matter is in your own hands; if you truly desire it, you will study with diligence and also succeed. It is understood that after a break in this, all beginnings are difficult, but over time it will become easier for you, provided that you make a personal effort in this regard. The same applies to the study of Chassidus, which can certainly also be improved. In consultation with your Rosh Yeshiva and Mashpia, you should divide your review time so that you do not have to study one subject for hours on end, but rather alternate. At least initially, this will stimulate your desire to learn, and it is already known from our Sages that "a person should always study in the place where his heart desires."

I trust that you are keeping the three daily study portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—that were established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for every person. You should also take a tractate in the distribution of Shas, and from time to time, give a few coins to Tzedakah. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2715

21 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 4th... I have attached my notes herewith. It is understood that this does not constitute an endorsement, as that is not my practice in such matters. It is also understood that if the points which, in my opinion, could lead to a stumbling block are not removed from the publication, then there is no permission to mention that I have seen the manuscript, so that it should not be interpreted that I, too, share in the responsibility for that stumbling block.

With blessings.

**Notes:**

By way of introduction:
a) In books written in the vernacular—that is, intended also for the simple person—one must omit all matters that, according to the understanding of a simple person, would evoke in him a feeling of disrespect for matters of Torah and mitzvos.
b) One must omit all matters that require broad or deep explanation, which in any case cannot be presented in this book.
c) One must omit all matters that, to simple readers, would be interpreted as meaning that there are two Torahs or several Torahs among the Jewish people—that is, all matters of dispute, etc.
d) One must separate the wheat from the chaff—that is, not to mix in entirely secular matters, since the reader equates them with the other matters in the book.
e) One must omit all matters that are dependent on a political party—that is, matters that the various parties in Israel debate and are divided over. In accordance with all the above, I provide the order of the pages.

**Page 2:** Omit the lines that speak of "custom overriding law," etc., for the common practice in America is to nullify dozens of laws from the Shulchan Aruch because of the custom they have adopted. It is obvious that they will not study the books that explain why and what the customs are—about which they said, "Custom is an acronym for *Gehinnom*" (Sdei Chemed, Klalim, Ma'areches Minhag).

**Page 4 and following:** Wherever the Name of the Creator is written in Yiddish, and the same applies to English, it should be written as "G-t," and not in full, for according to the opinion of several Acharonim, the holiness of the Name applies to it.

**Page 7:** *Drei shtern* (three stars). The common practice is not to distinguish between large and small [stars], etc., and therefore one should write "when it becomes night" and the like.

**Page 8:** Kiddush on milk. Although one can find a basis for this, it is a highly questionable matter. In *Birkei Yosef* and *Shaarei Teshuvah*—and cited in *Mishnah Berurah* in Siman 272—they ruled explicitly that one should not perform Kiddush and Havdalah on milk.

**Page 10:** See Siman 285, that the mitzvah is to finish the *hasbarah* (explanation of the parsha) on Erev Shabbos, and only in cases of duress is it done on Shabbos.

**On the same page:** There are Shabbosos at the end of the summer when two chapters are recited on one Shabbos.

**Page 11:** Omit the matter regarding Havdalah on milk, and also add in the order of Havdalah that one recites *Hinei Keil Yeshuati*.

**Page 13:** The prohibition of *hotza'ah* (carrying) applies also from a *karmelis* and not only from a *reshus harabim*. Also, what he explains regarding the method of making an *eruv* should be omitted, because the laws of *eruvin* are extremely complex and not as the reader will understand from what is written. The same applies regarding *eruvei techumin*; since it is not so relevant to this book, it should be omitted, as one must also include the houses outside the city, etc., and many details therein.

**Page 14:** What is written, that Shammai the Elder is *Beis Shammai*, is not understood, for the discussion concerns Hillel and Shammai themselves, not their students.

**Page 15:** That Shabbos is for all people—this is the opposite of the law that a gentile who observes Shabbos is liable for death, and therefore it should be omitted. Likewise, the story of "we have a spice, and its name is Shabbos," which a simple person will not understand.

**Pages 16, 17, and 18:** One must omit the entire matter of the Sambation, since its location is subject to a great dispute, and not as he writes simply that it is in the south of the land of Ethiopia. Also, regarding the stories of the travels of R. Gershon, many dispute them, especially in what he concludes, "Do not kindle fire," and interprets it according to the interpretation of the Karaites.

**Page 20:** Delete the word "exact" (*genoye*), because our *molad* is the mean *molad*, not the true one. For the *Maftir* of Shabbos Rosh Chodesh, one begins "And on the Shabbos day," and not "And on your new moons." Also, omit the word "pious" (*frume*), since this is a custom brought in the Shulchan Aruch.

**Page 21:** *Kiddush Levanah* should not be called a mere custom, and it should not be mixed with the *Baraisa* that one recites a blessing over the sun, moon, and stars, for that is not the *Kiddush Levanah* of every month according to most commentators. Also, what is written at the bottom of the page there, that every three years a leap month is added, is incorrect, as is known by the mnemonic: *Guchadzat*.

**Page 22:** What is written regarding the matters of *Kiddush Hachamah*—that it returns to its original place and from there takes its light and heat—is **incorrect**. Likewise, what is written that the beginning of the *tekufah* is on the fourth night of the month of Nissan is also incorrect, for it is on the fourth day of the week, not the fourth day of the month. Also, this is not the place from which it takes its light, etc., as is explained in *Hilchos Kiddush Hachodesh* by the Rambam and others.

**Page 22/2:** Regarding what he explains about the month of *Bul*—that the grasses are dry or that heavy rains fall—this is a self-contradiction.

**Page 23/3:** It should be omitted entirely, because its interpretation is a matter of great dispute.

**Page 24:** In the explanation of the labors prohibited on Yom Tov, this requires a long explanation regarding the distinctions between the labors, as is explained in the commentators of the Shas and *Nosei Keilim*, regarding why some labors were permitted and some prohibited. It is not the purpose of this book to clarify this.

**Page 25:** That in Eretz Yisrael there is no second day of Yom Tov, etc.—this will confuse the simple reader and lead to disrespect, and as the Sages feared, in a book printed in Yiddish or English, one should not bring this up at all, since it does not concern all lands, and one should omit the entire distinction of the customs of Eretz Yisrael in this regard.

**Page 26:** What is written that *Eruv Tavshilin* is a decree of the Geonim is a great wonder, for it is found in the Mishnah. Also, one should omit the differences in custom regarding the wearing of Tefillin on Chol Hamoed for the reasons mentioned above.

**Page 27:** That on *Isru Chag* one does not recite *Lamnatzeach B'neginos* is a great wonder; it appears it should be *Lamnatzeach Ya'ancha*.

**Page 28:** The explanation of *chametz*—that it is a matter that has something "fermented" (*chamutzi*)—is, aside from being incorrect, liable to lead to many corruptions and stumbling blocks. The same applies to what is written regarding fruit juices and raisin wine.

**Page 30:** At the end, that *Sefiras HaOmer* was given for the Jewish people living in Eretz Yisrael is puzzling, especially according to the opinion of the *poskim* that even now in the Diaspora it is *d'oraisa*.

**Page 31:** That on Shabbos Chol Hamoed one reads six *aliyos* in the first scroll is puzzling.

**Page 32:** His explanation of Lag B'Omer—that it depends on the war of Bar Kochba, etc.—is the opposite of the Shas, even though it is found in the books of the *Maskilim*.

**Page 35:** Omit the story of R. Chaim Brisker, and likewise the story of R. Levi Yitzchak—zt"l—on page 36, for the reasons mentioned above.

**Page 39:** Omit the differences in custom regarding trees on the holiday of Shavuos, as above.

**Page 41:** It seems that it has already been abolished in **all** communities to recite *Yatziv Pitgam* **within** the Haftorah.

**Page 42:** Omit the entire matter of "a Moabite, but not a Moabitess" (regarding David).

**Page 45:** Omit it, for it is not the role of this book to weaken the matter of reciting *Tikkun Leil Shavuos*.

**Page 50:** Regarding what he copied **from books that preceded him**, that R. Amnon ruled on his own judgment regarding how they would punish him—this requires study as to whether it is true, for it is forbidden to judge oneself. It is known that many matters in the chain of tradition are questionable and not true, as is brought in several places.

**Pages 51 and 52:** That Gedaliah was killed by the family of Tzidkiyahu the Kohen, and also that in Rashi on Shabbos the custom of *Kaparos* with "slaughtering" is mentioned, is a wonder. On page 52, one should omit the opinion of those who are concerned about "ways of the Amorite" regarding the custom of *Kaparos*, as above in the introduction.

**Page 53:** To pray Mincha *ald nach* (after) 12:00. There are those who say that such prayer is void, and in any case, it should be half an hour after that. Also, omit on this page the opinion of those who are against reciting *Kol Nidrei*, since it has now been accepted by all Ashkenazic Jews. Also, what is written to say "for a good year" on the night of Yom Kippur is a great wonder.

**Page 55:** Omit the story of R. Dovid Lelever, for since in the entire United States the practice has been accepted to go to the synagogue on Yom Kippur, one should not provide leniency through stories such as these. For this reason, one should also omit the story that precedes it.

**Page 59:** The *na'anuim* (shaking of the Lulav) should also be upward and downward, and not only to the four directions.

**Page 61:** Omit Rashi's explanation that *Regel* is a separate matter, that one does not sit in the Sukkah—this applies primarily to Eretz Yisrael, where there is no *safeka d'yoma* (doubt of the day).

**Page 64:** What is written that Chanukah is always until the second day of Teves is not accurate, because Kislev is sometimes 29 and sometimes 30 days.

**Page 66:** One should not mix the interpretation of the *Nun-Gimel-Hei-Shin* (the dreidel) brought in the books of the great men of previous generations with the acronyms of Yiddish and English.

**Page 70:** Regarding the planting of trees on Tu B'Shvat, one should not mix this with the customs of the Shulchan Aruch, etc., and it should be omitted from a book that is supposed to be equal for all.

**Page 73:** *Machatzis Hashekel* should be given *lechatchilah* at least on Taanis Esther, and not on Purim. Also, omit on the aforementioned page the citation from the Sages that "a person is obligated to become intoxicated," etc.

**Page 74:** Regarding Shushan Purim: in many places in Eretz Yisrael, this law applies even now, and not only in Jerusalem.

P.S.
In order to make it easier to find the location of my notes, they have been marked in pencil on the copy of the manuscript, which can be easily removed.

***2715***

**In Nun-Gimel-Hei-Shin:** *A great miracle happened there.*

## 2716

B.H., 21 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

It is already known that our Sages of blessed memory ruled that "a drink is great, for it brings [people] closer," especially regarding boys and girls, concerning whom they said, "Always let the right hand draw near [and the left hand push away]."

## 2777

B.H., 23 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you describe your situation and ask for my opinion as to whether you should study at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod or at a vocational school, given that you are fourteen and a half years old.

In general, in order to succeed in learning, there must be the element of kabbalas ol and discipline. As our Sages relate, it was specifically through the fact that the Jewish people said "we will do" (naaseh) before "we will hear" (nishma) that they merited receiving the Torah. From this, we learn the order for undertaking any form of study. Therefore, you should study at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod with mesiras nefesh, diligence, and persistence, and then you will certainly succeed, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages: "You have labored and you have found"—both in the study of the revealed Torah and in the study of Chassidus, as well as in the performance of mitzvos with hidur. In time, when you see that you are able to overcome your yetzer in the study of Hashem’s Torah, then it will be possible to also consider your placement in a vocational school, but not before you see for yourself, and demonstrate to others, that the mind rules over the heart in the aforementioned matters.

I trust that every day after Shacharis you recite the daily portion of Tehillim as divided for the days of the month, and from time to time give a coin to tzedakah, and the Ribono shel Olam will grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2778

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 20 Iyar. Regarding your question as to what I intend for the good deeds you should perform:

This is a simple matter, addressed in many places in our holy seforim, and first and foremost in the ruling of Rabbi Akiva that "Love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle of the Torah. Consequently, just as one is obligated to exert oneself in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos, one must also endeavor to influence others in this direction. This is done by establishing public study sessions (it is understood that the study must be on a subject accessible to the many, such as the Kitzur Shulchan Aruch, Ein Yaakov, Chumash, and the like), arranging for a chapter of Tehillim to be recited after davening in the shul, and encouraging the fulfillment of practical mitzvos, etc., etc. It is understood that the methods of this outreach vary from place to place, but the variation is only in the methods, not in the goal of the outreach, which is to bring the hearts of Bnei Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven by spurring them on in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos. "You have labored — and you have found."

As you requested, I will mention you and your entire family, may they live, when I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and may Hashem grant you success in all of the above.

May it be the will of Hashem that from now on, you see *hashgacha pratis* only in matters of revealed and manifest good.

## 2881

B"H, 28 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent in communal needs,
Rabbi Yehoshua [Schneur Zalman] shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 19 Iyar. It is astonishing to me that after seeing—both you and all of Anash—such extraordinary success regarding the yeshiva, in the reality of the building and its acquisition, etc., you are still filled with doubts at every step. As you put it in your letter, you have no clear picture of how to approach the avodah. This, after you have been engaged in this for several years and have achieved success beyond what you initially imagined, in addition to the fact that the children of the... have also joined you, etc., etc.

All the more so—and *kal v’chomer*—if in your previous country, where the matter was bound up with *mesiras nefesh*, you engaged in chinuch without setting conditions for the Creator, may He be blessed, that He must show miracles at every step, or else it is impossible to continue the avodah—how much more so in your current country, where even through the natural order there is the possibility to continue the matter, and certainly, He does not withhold miracles. It only requires a bit of *hisbonenus* and opening one’s eyes, at least to a small degree...

I was pleased to hear that during your visit to Sydney, you met with several avreichim who were students of Oholei Torah in the past. Surely, you will continue to maintain contact with them through correspondence and will also endeavor to have them return to the yeshiva, at least for a period of time.

Regarding what you wrote, that the Feiglin family shlita kept the checks sent from here for the yeshiva as a memento, and deposited their equivalent—with an additional sum—into the bank on behalf of the yeshiva: if the yeshiva administration has given its consent to this, then *yashar cheilam*.

I await good news regarding all of the above, and with a blessing for success in your holy work and in your personal matters, for you and your entire family shlita, and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
Surely you gathered for a farbrengen during the days of the festival of Pesach and Lag B’Omer, and you will do so as well on the festival of Shavuos. I would appreciate it if you would provide details regarding this.

## 2783

B"H, 28 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

In response to your letter of 33 Omer and the information received via telephone.

It is a wonder to me, for although you have seen in your personal life—and all the more so in the lives of others—the wonders of Hashem, and at times, even when no solution was apparent, the situation changed for the good to such an extent that one wondered and felt regret for having been in a state of *marah shechorah* (melancholy) previously. And the saying of the wise is well-known, that the past teaches the future; consequently, one must be strong in *bitachon* that "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good," and in the course of time, one merits a higher level, that "this too is for the good" (that this itself is a *tovah*, and not merely a cause for good, as is known the distinction between the statement that "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good" (*Berachos 60b*) and the statement of "this too is for the good" (*Taanis 21a*))...

Awaiting good tidings and signing with a blessing to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 2824

B"H, 29 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 5 Bamidbar, in which you write that you wish to become a Lubavitcher Chossid and that your friend also desires this, and you wish to know the conditions and what must be done.

The conditions are to study the teachings of Chassidus, and according to our Sages, "The primary thing is not the study, but the deed"—to conduct oneself according to its guidance and customs. And naturally, just as in the receiving of the Torah, which was merited specifically through the precedence of "we will do" (*naaseh*) to "we will hear" (*nishma*), so too it is with any part of the *Pardes* of Torah; here as well, there must be the precedence of *naaseh* to *nishma*. It is already known what our Sages have ruled: "If one says, 'I have not labored and yet I have found,' do not believe him; [but if he says,] 'I have labored and I have found,' believe him." And if you truly desire this, then "he who comes to purify himself is assisted."

I trust that you are studying Tanya even now, and that you also recite every day after Shacharis the daily portion of Tehillim—as the Tehillim is divided according to the days of the month—and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for Torah study with fear of Heaven,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2885

B.H., 29 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter of 16 Iyar has been received, in which you write that it is difficult to establish a school or a cheder for Charedim, and therefore the children are studying in places that are contrary to the religion of Yisrael.

I was alarmed to read such news, at a time when everyone is aware of the mesiras nefesh that Yidden have always had to ensure their children receive an education that is not only not contrary to the religion of Yisrael—which might imply that one could settle for a neutral education—but they have invested efforts to the point of mesiras nefesh to ensure that the education be specifically in the spirit of the religion of Yisrael. This is especially true given that you write that you are the Rav of the village, for the responsibility of a Rav is not merely to pasken shailos when one comes to ask, but the main thing is to influence the kehillah so that they know that they need to ask shailos. In other words, they should know that the neshamah of every Yid stood at Har Sinai and accepted the Torah with the preface of "naaseh" before "nishma," and received from the mouth of the Gevurah the command of "Anochi Hashem Elokecha," which includes all 248 mitzvos asei, and the command of "Lo yihyeh lecha elokim acherim," which includes all 365 mitzvos lo saaseh. May Hashem grant you success in this work, especially during these days of preparation for Matan Torah, when all the matters that occurred at Matan Torah are aroused each year during these days.

With blessings.

## 2886

B”H, 29 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

2) Regarding the desire to send girls to study at the Beis Rivkah in Paris: one must clarify the situation—both regarding the provider and the recipient—such as whether the candidates are disciplined, etc. It is understood that the supervision at Beis Rivkah in Paris is not as full as it is in the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva; on the other hand, the responsibility regarding girls is greater than it is regarding bochurim. In any case, this is a matter of—when there is a benefit to traveling specifically to France because it is impossible to provide her with an appropriate education in her current location. Because of the second point, the time is certainly limited to specific periods; please let me know which those are.

With a blessing for success in your holy work and in your personal matters—for you and for your family, may they live.
