## 2787

B"H, 29 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, who is G-d-fearing and involved in communal needs,
Rabbi Gershon, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Tiferes shebeYesod, accompanied by the Pidyon Nefesh which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—may Hashem grant you success and may you have good news to report regarding it.

Regarding what you wrote about the maamar explaining the passage in Tanya, Chapter 23: There are several maamarim on this opening, and it appears that one of them is by the Tzemach Tzedek, one is by the Chassid Rabbi Hillel of Paritch, and others are by the children or grandchildren of the Tzemach Tzedek. It is difficult to determine to whom each belongs, as in general, they are all founded upon the maamar of the Tzemach Tzedek.

Regarding the custom of studying Maseches Sotah during the days of Sefirah: The reason can be explained based on what is elucidated in Zohar Vol. III, 97a, regarding the connection between them. This is also brought in Chassidic discourse, explaining that the Omer is barley, which is the same as the Minchas Sotah.

Regarding your observation about the number of pages—that Maseches Shevuos also has a number of pages corresponding to Maseches Sotah: The custom of studying Maseches Shevuos during the days of Sefirah is indeed found in certain books—it is brought in the name of the author of Imrei Esh in the Sefer Zichron Yehuda, which is cited in Likutei Maharich regarding the order of customs for the days of the Omer. However, what I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is that one studies Maseches Sotah.

With a blessing for true health, and as is the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 2828

B"H, 29 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may Hashem protect them, Tel Aviv.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 17 Iyar with pleasure and delight, along with a copy of the speeches delivered at the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad gathering in Kfar Chabad. I derived much pleasure both from their content and from the fact that the work is gradually becoming organized. Surely, you will continue to progress from strength to strength, and in the ways of the world, this will also add to the success of the work. The third point—which is the most essential—is that since the speakers emphasized the necessity of expanding the activities, my hope is strong that you will implement this in practice, increasing your work in all the branches, both in quantity and quality. May it be the will of Hashem that this, too, will fulfill the concept that an opening the size of a needle’s eye from below (which can be interpreted to mean that even in the context of the "below," it is like a needle’s eye) will thereby open from above like the entrance to a hall (which can be interpreted to mean that even in the context of the "above," it is the entrance to a hall). The time has already come not to be satisfied with plowing and sowing alone, but to do everything possible to ensure that we also reach the stage of reaping and gathering the fruits. My intention in this is that although at the beginning of outreach in a new place or environment, there must be a general preparation for receiving the new matter—which is akin to polishing the *ohr makif*—the ultimate goal is that the matters should penetrate into their *pnimiyus*. Regarding your outreach—namely, establishing a regular *shiur* in Torah in general and in *Chassidus* in particular—it should be done in such a way that between one visit and the next, you know what is happening in that place or environment, etc. It is also understood that one should not neglect the work of the first stage for this reason, for there are many places and environments that you have not yet entered, and they are in need of the work of *ohr makif* to polish the *keli* from the outside, at the very least.

2) It is surprising that you do not mention in your letter your participation in the registration, especially since in my telegram I specifically highlighted your names in the instructions.

3) Enclosed is a copy of my letter of response to an individual regarding his question, which is worth publishing in the next issue of the bulletin, as it seems from the questions received here that this letter has aroused astonishment and questions in various circles.

4) Furthermore, if the bulletin appears before the festival of Shavuos, it would be worthwhile to publish the excerpt from *Shabbos Mevarchim* Sivan of last year, as it is relevant to the day.

I await good news regarding your activities on the auspicious day of Lag B’Omer, and regarding your preparations for good deeds during the time of the giving of our Torah. I conclude with a blessing for extraordinary success in your holy work.

## 2829

29 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, a man of stature and renown,
Rabbi Avraham Yaakov, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received with pleasure the regards sent through the esteemed Chassid, a man of stature and renown, Rabbi Leib Zalmanov, as well as his gift, your book *Eshel Avraham* on Maseches Nashim, Part II. May Hashem grant you success in increasing and glorifying Torah.

It is a wondrous thing, as is brought down regarding the study of children, that although it is "breath without sin," it is nonetheless the beginning of study from the lowest levels of learning (Rambam, *Hilchos Talmud Torah* 2:7; *Yad Malachi*, *Klalei* 4). Conversely, regarding study that does not change a halachic ruling but merely adds beauty and splendor to the learning (*Chullin* 66b), this is the highest level of study. This also aligns with the well-known principle that every Jew has a share in the Torah. From this, it is understood that even an *am ha’aretz* is obligated in the mitzvah of Talmud Torah, even if it be only the recitation of a single verse, through which he fulfills his obligation. On the other hand, even the greatest of the great, if there was a brief moment in which he could have engaged in Torah study and did not, the verse speaks of him, as the Sages say in *Sanhedrin* (99a).

The inner point of this is that, in truth, the Torah is the wisdom and will of Hashem, but out of free kindness, it was given as a gift below. For were it not for this, even Moshe Rabbeinu would have forgotten it, even though he learned it from the mouth of Hashem on the mountain, where there was no connection to materiality or even physicality, for he ate no bread and drank no water. Consequently, the greatest and the smallest are equal in this. This is similar to what is explained in many places: that in relation to the Infinite, one and a thousand thousands and myriads of myriads are truly equal.

With blessings for success to you in all the above, and for long years and good days.

P.S.
As is my custom, and for the sake of affection for the matter, I will at least offer a few comments on this book of yours:

Regarding the beginning of the book, and repeated on page 60, concerning the discussion in *Maseches Kiddushin* 16a, it should be noted:

1) In *Sefer Ha’Ittur*, which is also cited in *Otzar HaGeonim* on the spot, it brings the language of the Gemara, which implies that it does not include the words "or in the presence of a Beis Din, go."

2) Regarding the conclusion of your discussion there, one should note *Nedarim* 45a, so that one may be a *zocheh* and two may testify, for in the case at hand, it is a statement in the presence of two. See also *Gittin* 33a and 40a.

3) Regarding the opinion of the *Noda B’Yehuda* as to whether a *get* requires a Beis Din, see *Shu"t Tzemach Tzedek*, Responsum 162.

4) There, in the *Tosafos* to *Maseches Sotah* 78a, s.v. *B’Matnisen*, and in the tenth chapter of *Chumash HaPekudim* regarding what you wrote about the *Tosafos Yeshanim*: One could say regarding the matter of *Krias HaTorah* that there are two categories: a) An obligation of the community, not an individual obligation, as per the opinion of the *Milchamos* in *Megillah*, Chapter 1, s.v. *Ve’od Amar*. See also the *Tzafnas Paneach* of the Rogatchover Gaon on the Rambam, *Hilchos Tefillah*, Chapter 12, Halacha 5. Since this is a communal obligation, it is analogous to the giving of the Torah, which was given to the entire Jewish people. Therefore, "things that were given in writing, you are not permitted to recite by heart," etc., because it must be as it was given (see *Shu"t Radbaz*, Part IV, Responsum 1105). Category b) That this is part of the *tefillah*, similar to "we will render the prayers of our lips" or an addition to the offering of a sacrifice. This is the intent of the *Tosafos Yeshanim*—that it is a necessity of the service—and it is from the *Yerushalmi*. Consequently, it is not analogous to the giving of the Torah to the entire Jewish people, and therefore the law of "things that were given in writing, you are not permitted to recite by heart" does not apply to it. This is the case for all the readings of the sacrifices on Yom Tov, Rosh Hashanah, and Yom Kippur, which are distinct from other *Krias HaTorah*. See *Tosafos Megillah* 30b, and also the Rambam, *Hilchos Tefillah*, who divides the subject of *Krias HaTorah* into two halachos. For your purposes, this summary should suffice.

At the end of the book, in the explanation of the Sages' words, "Nowadays, many have trampled upon it," you ask quite rightly in what manner the situation of "many have trampled upon it" came to be. You wish to explain that this was during the time of the decree against the mitzvah of *bris milah*, and they were unable to wait for a clear day, because that was precisely when they were watched more closely; therefore, they did it specifically on a cloudy day—that is, at a time when they were not accustomed to performing *bris milah*. However, it is difficult to accept this, for since there is danger involved, how could they circumcise their sons? The very incident itself provides proof to the contrary, for regarding the generation of the desert, after they knew of the decree that they would be in the desert for forty years—and consequently, the Clouds of Glory would be present for forty years and the north wind would not blow—they still did not circumcise their sons. How much more so in the case of a decree, which is destined to be nullified, should they not have circumcised their sons and endangered them.

What seems to me to be the case is that it is similar to the explanation of the *Tosafos* regarding a similar, perhaps even more difficult, question: that the letters *MNZP"CH* were forgotten (*Megillah* 2b), which occurred after Haman burned the Torah. Similarly, one can explain the case at hand: that "many have trampled upon it" occurred in Bavel, which was a "valley" in many matters. When Rav descended there, and likewise the other Amoraim, he found the situation that "many have trampled upon it." This is also the case regarding bloodletting on Friday (*Shabbos* 129b). See also the *Iggeres Rav Sherira Gaon* regarding the situation in Bavel before Rav descended there.

## 2792

...Regarding what you wrote, that during a farbrengen there is an awakening, but afterwards, when you do not see success, you feel a bit discouraged and lack joy: such an attitude has no basis whatsoever. ## 2,793

B"H, 29 Iyar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from last week, and I was pleased to read that in the yeshiva where you are a guide, there is "everything necessary regarding room, board, and spiritual education." Surely such a responsible statement is made after observing the situation in the yeshiva and what is required—most importantly, the education of *avreichim* in our current times. This is especially true since you write that you are the spiritual guide and the one responsible for the *bochurim’s* diligence in our holy Torah. If, as our Sages of blessed memory stated (*Shabbos* 31a), this applies in all times—that if the fear of Hashem is one’s treasure, then it is well, but if not, it is better that one had not ascended—then in this orphaned generation, we have seen and continue to see, even with our physical eyes, the immediate truth of their verdict.

Therefore, it was surprising to me to read the conclusion of your letter, in which you write that the *avreichim* are studying Gemara, Chumash, and *dinim*, yet you make no mention of the study of *Chovos HaLevavos*.

My hope is that this is merely an omission in your writing, rather than a deficiency in practice. As is well known, in matters of education, a deficiency—even for a short duration—can result in that which is crooked that cannot be made straight, and that which is lacking that cannot be numbered. Surely you have also seen in a tangible way that if, in years past, it might have crossed one’s mind to say that one could suffice with the study of *mussar*, life and actual experience have proven that for *avreichim* who possess intellect and understanding, it is essential that their study also include the study of *Chovos HaLevavos* in an intellectual manner. And how much better it is when done through the path of increasing light, rather than through the contemplation of the darkness of gloom—which is the path of the teachings of Chassidus. Since you write that you have studied Chassidus, I trust that even these few lines, small in quantity, clarify the matter sufficiently. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success in raising your students to be truly G-d-fearing, for then their wisdom will endure.

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 2934

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

... I was pleased to read in your letter that you study a shiur in Tanya every day. It is well known what the Nasi of Chabad said regarding the Tanya: that even the greatest of the great cannot fully fathom the entire depth of the Tanya, yet at the same time, every Yid can take something from it. For the intention of the Baal HaTanya was that this should be a sefer for all Yidden to study, and *tzaddik gozer v'HaKadosh Baruch Hu mekayem* (a tzaddik decrees and Hashem fulfills). It is indeed known that *yagata umatzasa* (you have labored and you have found)—that the more one exerts oneself in it, the more one absorbs and understands the matters discussed there in the Tanya.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, in good health.

## 2898

2898

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, engaged in the needs of the community, Rabbi Nissan Nemanov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 25 Iyar. It is a pity that there is such a delay in receiving good news, for there is no "good" other than Torah and a Chassidishe farbrengen, which is a double good—for people and for Heaven, as explained in Kiddushin 40a. See also the letter of the Rebbe (Rashab) n.e., printed in Kuntres 61. It is understood that my intent here is regarding the Lag B'Omer farbrengen about which you write. If in all times people yearned to receive good news, both physically and spiritually, how much more so in our generation, the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, when "there is no day..."

Surely you will increase your efforts in the campaign regarding the vacation period; whoever increases and exerts themselves in this is praiseworthy. The precision of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, on this matter is already known and printed in Hayom Yom, 17 Nissan.

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

P.S.

Please be so kind as to publicize among Anash regarding the study during the upcoming days of the festival of Shavuos: the suggestion I offer is to study the maamarim for the festival of Shavuos 5704, which were published some time ago in copy and are also being printed now.

## 2,399

Brooklyn.

## 2800

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter of 22 Iyar, in which you write regarding your son, may he live and be well, that you would like to see him settled in life, both materially and regarding marriage—matters which are interconnected. You therefore ask for my opinion as to whether he should immediately begin learning a trade.

Your son, may he live and be well, is learning among many bochurim of his age or even a few years older. Therefore, it is my opinion that he should conduct himself in this regard just as his peers do. In general, the standard practice is that at his age, it is still too early to focus on "settling down." Regarding the example you cite in your letter, aside from the fact that the individual in question is much older than your son, there are other specific reasons that apply to him. However, regarding your son, it would be a pity to tear him away now from his learning, in which he is successful and has a desire to engage.

Currently, the diamond-cutting trade is very weak, and learning that trade takes only two or three months if one has the connections to learn it. Therefore, there is still plenty of time. It is certain that in his time, Hashem will grant him success with a good arrangement, both regarding parnassah and a good shidduch. In the meantime, he would be better off utilizing his time to acquire more knowledge in learning, which will serve him for his entire life, both materially and spiritually.

In accordance with the above, he should not be disturbed now with thoughts of "settling down" and shidduchim, which are only relevant a few years from now. He should continue his learning with success.

In accordance with your request, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the improvement of your health and also for parnassah.

May the merit of having raised a son who learns the Torah of Hashem with hasmadah and conducts himself according to its—Torah—instructions, stand by you in all that you need.

With blessings.

## B'Tisa

B"H, 2 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned man, engaged in communal needs, R' Elchanan HaKohen, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through Mr. Nissan Mindel, who also told me about your influence on a bochur, encouraging him to begin wearing tefillin again after he had not done so for a time.

The magnitude of this matter is beyond measure. As is explained in your tefillin booklet, this aligns the head with the heart. This is as the Shulchan Aruch states, which is also cited in Tanya, Chapter 41 (page 2): "to nullify and include the aspect of his chochmah and binah, etc., and likewise to nullify and include the aspect of da'as within his soul, etc., to subjugate the heart and the brain, etc."

The days preceding Matan Torah are days of special success for taking upon oneself the matter of ahavas Yisrael, to bring others closer to Torah and mitzvos. May this be realized in practice, in a good and joyful manner.

With blessings in the style of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and with best regards to Mrs. Cohen, may she live, and to your children and grandchildren, may they live.

## 2,702

B"H, 2 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, the illustrious and G-d-fearing, scion of noble lineage, branch of the tree of the patriarchs, etc., etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Shimon Zev, shlita

Peace and blessing!

After a long interval, it was a pleasure to receive your letter, dated the 30th of the month of Bnei Yisrael, bringing good tidings that all is well with you. May Hashem grant each of us the merit to bring one another tidings of only good—and there is no "good" other than Torah, which is called *Toras Chaim*, meaning that it is connected and unified with life in the literal and plain sense, which obviously includes the life of this world as well. This is especially so according to what is explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 36, and it is necessitated by the ruling of our Sages that the Torah is not in heaven, but specifically in this physical world.

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding your daily study of the *Tanya Kadisha* (the text of the *haskamah* of the *Tanya*, Zolkiew edition, even though it was located far from the residence of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, and by rabbis who had not seen the author). It is already well-known what the original approvers of the *Tanya* wrote—the great disciples of the Maggid of Mezeritch whose approbations are printed at the beginning of the *Tanya*—and that which is famous requires no explanation. Surely, you have also seen the list of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of saintly memory, which is printed at the end of the *Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya*.

Thank you, thank you, for mentioning me at the holy sites. Surely, for one of your stature, it is superfluous to point out what is explained regarding these matters in the *maamar* of the Mitteler Rebbe, son of our Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya*, titled *Lehavin Inyan HaHishtatchus*, and additional explanation on this in the *maamarim* regarding *hishtatchus* by the esteemed Chossid, R. Hillel of Paritch, of blessed memory.

As you requested, I will mention you and your entire household, may they live, when I am at the holy *tziyun* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of saintly memory.

And last but not least, regarding your good news that a daughter was born to you, *mazal tov*, and you have named her Sima Leah: May it be the will of Hashem that you raise her to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds, and may you and your wife, may they live, derive from her and from all your offspring, may they live, an abundance of Chassidishe *nachas* for long, good years.

With a blessing in the style of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 2,753

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Regarding what you wrote about the studies in the village, it is surprising that you do not mention the study of the halachos concerning the mitzvos that are dependent on the Land [of Israel]. I hope that this is merely an omission in your writing and not in practice, for it is well known that our Sages ruled that it is not the study that is the main thing, but the action...

Regarding what you wrote about the weakness in concentration, one of the known pieces of advice for this is that when one becomes tired, one should switch the study to a different subject that one’s heart desires, rather than forcing the power of thought to continue specifically on the matter in which one has become fatigued.

And regarding your notification of your birthday... may it be the will of Hashem that for long days and good years—good with all the interpretations—you should increase your strength in Torah and its mitzvos, and permeate your surroundings as well with Torah, mitzvos, and the light within them, which is the teachings of Chassidus. And in his days and in our days, the prophecy will be fulfilled: "And all the horns of the wicked I will cut off; the horns of the righteous shall be exalted" (Tehillim 75:11). As Rashi explains there, this speaks of the true and complete Geulah, the wiping out of Amalek, and the exaltation of the horns of the Tzaddik of the world. You should also awaken the light of the Torah from our Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, in his *Drushei Chanukah* (p. 600).

With blessings in the style of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 2404

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Iyar, in which you write regarding your daughter, may she live.

For a Jewish person—of whom it is said, "One nation on earth," and as the Alter Rebbe emphasizes (Iggeres HaKodesh, ch. 9) that even in worldly matters they are not separated from the One of Truth—it is necessary, alongside action and effort in the natural way, to also do something in the corresponding spiritual matters, which generally includes an increase in Torah and mitzvos.

You do not write in your letter what the doctors are doing for your daughter, may she live, aside from the advice of changing the climate and the medications they are using here for her health condition as you mention in your letter (although, of course, it is impossible to know the situation clearly from the two words you mention in your letter). Have they used cortisone?

My intention in saying that one must do something in spiritual matters is, first, to clarify whether your daughter was born in purity—that is, whether you observed the laws of taharas hamishpachah in a mikveh at that time. I hope you will not take offense at this remark, for since I do not know you, and in a matter concerning the health of a Jewish soul, there is no place for misplaced shame. That is to say, regarding the knowledge of the aforementioned: if, G-d forbid, it was not so, then you and your wife, may they live, must, in addition to being precise in observing the mitzvah of taharah from here on, increase your efforts in advocacy regarding this matter, especially since this is, at the very least, a partial rectification of the aforementioned.

In any case, it is appropriate that your wife set aside a few coins for tzedakah before lighting the candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, as well as on Monday and Thursday mornings. You should do the same before davening every Monday and Thursday morning, and after Shacharis, you should recite the portion of Tehillim as divided for the days of the month. Also, check the mezuzos in your home to ensure they are all kosher.

May Hashem grant you the merit to bring good news regarding all of the above, and especially regarding the improvement of your daughter's health, may she live.

With a blessing to utilize your influence as an official in the Religious Council to raise the banner of our ancestral Judaism in your surroundings and locality without compromises, and whoever increases in this, they increase for him from Above with what he and his household, may they live, require.

With a blessing for good tidings.

## 2,755

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Iyar, in which you write about the pain in your right leg: Beyond what you are doing through natural means by following the instructions of the doctors in this field, it is explained in many places that *tzedakah* is the aspect of the "leg" in the spiritual stature of a person. The concept of *tzedakah* includes both *tzedakah* with one’s money and *tzedakah* with one’s body—meaning the exertion of the body in matters of *ahavas Yisrael*. You should therefore increase your efforts in both of these areas, and may Hashem add His blessing regarding your health, in spirituality and especially in physicality.

I await good news, and with blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

P.S.
It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your *shiurim* in *nigleh* and *Chassidus*.

## 2,656

B"H, 5 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, R' Avraham Chaim, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Iyar, as you requested, the *Kuntres* of 19 Kislev is being sent to you in a separate package.

Regarding what you wrote about pronouncing the *lamed* in *lazman* with a *chirik*, this is indeed the custom of all *anash*. I believe it is **clear** that I heard the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, pronounce it this way. My question was whether you, in your greatness, were aware of any source or tradition regarding this. As for the objections raised based on the rules of grammar, which you also included in your letter, those rules apply when the definite article *hei* is elided. However, if the word *zman* is used from the outset without the definite article *hei*, then the *lamed* can indeed take a *chirik* according to the rules of grammar as well. Nevertheless, I am still looking for a source for this, though as of now, I have not found one.

As we approach the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah and its reception, may it come upon us for good, I hereby express my blessing in the phrasing of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory: that you may receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 2757

B"H, 5 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs in faith,
Mr. A. Shklovsky, may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

In due time I received your letter—undated—in which you describe the situation at the Chabad shul in Petach Tikvah. I was pleased to receive the additional information that the situation is improving, and I hope that it will continue to go from strength to strength.

It goes without saying that for everything, Hashem demands that we also act through natural means (*b'derech hateva*). In matters concerning a shul and *beis medrash*, this depends on the *gabbaim*. When one takes action, one can be certain that the blessing of Hashem will follow, as is His promise: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do."

This is especially true when it concerns *l'zachos es harabim* (meriting the public), and specifically when it concerns a Chabad shul—for which our *Nesi'im* sacrificed themselves for *anash*—that these Chabad shuls should continue to grow and expand. They should serve according to the statement of our Sages as a *mikdash me'at* (a miniature sanctuary), from which light and warmth should spread into the homes of those who frequent the shul.

The merit of one who is chosen from Heaven to be a *gabbai* in such a shul is great, as it allows one to fulfill the will of our *Nasi* regarding the aforementioned. I hope to hear good news from you in this regard.

In these days before *Matan Torah*, when the *Midrash* tells us that all six hundred thousand Jews had to be present—and had even one been missing, it would have been an impediment to the giving of the holy Torah—you should strengthen yourself in all forms of *hishtadlus* (effort) to bring closer whomever can be brought closer to Torah and *mitzvos*. Through this, one acquires both the Torah and the Giver of the Torah. This is in accordance with the statement of our Sages that the **beginning** of *Matan Torah* is the commandment "Anochi" (I am), which are the *rashei teivos* (acronym) for: "I have written and given My soul" (*Shabbos 105a*, *Tanya, Chapter 47*).

With a blessing—in the style of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, for you and for all the congregants of the Chabad shul.

I await good news.

## 2758

B"H, 5 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, engaged in communal needs, R' Chaim, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

Some time ago I received your letter confirming receipt of the seforim sent from here. It is surprising that you do not mention whether these seforim are being used to strengthen and disseminate Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos.

It is understood that while you are correct in what you wrote—that if there were a spiritual leader from among the residents themselves, it would be much easier to influence and lead them—one must not wait until then. Time is a loss that cannot be recovered, and the youth are growing up, as our Sages of blessed memory have said (Kiddushin 34a). Consequently, it is incumbent upon you and your colleagues to do as much as you can in this regard, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

Surely you are aware that when the refugees from Russia and Poland arrived in Paris, they began to work in the field of proper education for the Jewish children of France. At first, they had no common language and had to rely on hand gestures, etc., as well as the few words of Lashon HaKodesh from the Chumash, etc., which were known to the aforementioned children because they had heard them in shul and the like. Gradually, their work flourished and succeeded on an increasingly wider scale, and scores of boys and girls are already learning and understanding well. Furthermore, they have even influenced their parents’ homes, bringing them closer to Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos.

If you follow this path in your location now, you will surely succeed—not only according to the teaching of our Sages that one who sustains a single soul of Yisroel is as if he sustained an entire world, but you will certainly sustain many, many souls.

Approaching the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah and its acceptance, may it come upon us for good, I hereby express my blessing in the phrasing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: that you may receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

#### ***2758***

**R' Chaim:** Herman, Asmara.

## 2519

B"H, 5 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly individual, engaged in communal needs, R' Shmuel Menachem Mendel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Rosh Chodesh Sivan, in which you write about your activities among the *shochtim*, who are gradually advancing toward the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs. Certainly, if you continue in this with ways of pleasantness and ways of peace—which are the very ways of the Torah—you will succeed in this even more.

Regarding what you write about *farbrengens*, and that it is appropriate to read from the *sichos* at the gatherings of the Agudas Neshei U’Bnos Chabad: While it is true that reading external books is damaging and harmful, etc., it is well known that, in general, one must proceed from the easy to the difficult. This is especially true regarding outreach among women, as our Sages have said regarding the Giving of the Torah—a point noted in Rashi’s commentary there: "Thus shall you say to the house of Jacob," implying that for women, the approach must be one of "gentle speech."

Similarly, regarding the aforementioned, the emphasis should be placed more on the addition of "do good"—namely, reading the *sichos*, etc. Then, in the course of time, the ruling that "a little light pushes away much darkness" will be fulfilled, and all the more so with "much light." It is understood that my intention here is not to grant approval for them to read the aforementioned external books, but rather that for the time being, the emphasis should be on the aspect of "do good."

At a time of favor, I will mention all those whose names you have written while I am at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May Hashem grant them success so that they may go from strength to strength.

You write that you are teaching *Tanya* to young *bochurim*. I am sure that on the next occasion you will inform me whether they are from the *yeshiva* or if they are still from the outside. May Hashem grant you success in all of the above.

Approaching the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah and its reception, I hereby express my blessing in the formula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: that you may receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

With blessing.

## 2510

B"H, 5 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, who toils in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer Hakohen, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Your letters have been received.

Regarding your inquiry concerning Rashi (Sotah 39b, s.v. *min*), which states that once the final "Amen" is concluded, the Kohanim turn their faces and the Shaliach Tzibbur begins *Sim Shalom*, and the Kohanim pray "Ribono shel Olam," etc.—yet the Gemara states that the Kohanim may not turn their faces until the Shaliach Tzibbur begins *Sim Shalom* (Chavas Yair on the Rif, end of Megillah), and no Rishonim are found to support Rashi in this:

One could explain that Rashi’s interpretation is necessitated by logic (see Tosafot, s.v. *iba'it*, Shevuot 22b, bottom; Sdei Chemed, Klalim, Ma'arechet Sevara) and by the Gemara itself.

From the Gemara: Since it says that the Kohanim are not permitted to begin another blessing until the "Amen" is concluded, it implies that immediately thereafter they are permitted to do so. One could say that according to Rashi, this refers to the "Ribono shel Olam" prayer, similar to what is written in the Beit Yosef; see also Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim, 128, end of section 19.

From logic:

a) The Kohanim’s prayer, "Ribono shel Olam," is a continuation of the Birchas Kohanim; therefore, it must be adjacent to it (this is in addition to the matter discussed in section 19, paragraph 7). Before this, they must turn their faces so that they pray toward the direction where the Shechinah resides.

b) Even though one should connect the recitation of "Ribono shel Olam" with *Sim Shalom*—as they are one subject—what is the reason for the Kohanim and the people to turn their faces after the conclusion of the final "Amen," when the matter of Birchas Kohanim **has been completed**?

And as for what you say—that all the Poskim, including the Alter Rebbe, have ruled otherwise:

Regarding what the Gemara says, that they are not permitted to turn until the Shaliach Tzibbur begins *Sim Shalom*, Rashi would interpret it according to the explanation of the Maharshal, which you cite in your letter. It can be reconciled by noting that the Gemara uses this phrasing, which is not entirely precise, because of the latter part—**"until he finishes"**—which is the main point of its novelty.

***

Since Tosafot (Sotah 39a, bottom) cites Rashi without commenting on it, it implies that they agree with him.

As for what is written in the Levush (128:15), that they turn their faces when saying "and it is good in Your eyes," etc.—this has already been questioned in the sefer *Koh Tevarachu*, Ma'arechet Tefillah. It is also in need of further study from the language of the Levush himself in section 16 there. Time does not permit an elaboration.

Approaching the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah and its reception, may it be His will, I hereby express my blessing, in the phrasing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory:

To receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

With blessing.

B"H, Erev Chag HaShavuos, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished and exalted Rabbi, a man of stature, of noble lineage, great among men, G-d-fearing, who contemplates matters of goodness, etc.,

And since the inner dimension of Torah, in the language of the holy Zohar, is the "soul of the Torah," I am confident that the study of Chassidus will bring and draw vitality into the "body of the Torah"—which is the revealed dimension of Torah—and that both together will bring vitality also into the physical, into the creatures and the body, for among the Children of Israel, physicality and spirituality walk together.

## 2512

B"H, 8 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you raise concerning the communal activities of the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and noble, involved in the needs of the community, etc., Rabbi...

[You suggest] that this naturally might hinder him from applying himself to Torah study as required. It is known, however, that the Alter Rebbe rules (in the beginning of Torah Or) that through the performance of tzedakah (and tzedakah for the many, all the more so), one’s mind and heart become refined a thousand times over. From the glosses of Admur the Tzemach Tzedek on this discourse, which is printed in Likutei Torah for the three parshiyos, it is understood that the number "a thousand" is precise and not an exaggeration. Consequently, involvement in communal needs cannot hinder him; on the contrary, it assists him.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2513

2513

B.H., 8 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letters from Rosh Chodesh and the 5th of Sivan, I was distressed to see in your letters that it appears the relations in your home have still not improved. It is a known principle that even a "bad" peace is better than even a "slight and good" quarrel, and it is certainly understood that a "good" peace is better still. After all that you write in your letters, I do not see any substantial matter that should serve as a cause for a rift between hearts in your home. Consequently, I stand by my opinion from when I spoke with you when you visited me.

However, since the current situation is difficult to bear, perhaps it is possible—as per the suggestion of your husband, the Rabbi, may he live—albeit with some modification, that you both present your arguments before one or two individuals who are friends of both you and your husband, may they live. Sometimes, one standing on the sidelines clarifies the situation and reveals a path to straighten the crookedness in the heart, even when those involved in the matter cannot see it due to agitation and personal involvement.

May the Ribono shel Olam continue the blessing in your home with an abundance of peace, and may you share good news regarding this soon.

With blessings.

## 2515

B"H, 8 Sivan, 5714

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 27 Iyar, as well as the Haggadah and the book *Toldos Yosef*. Thank you very much.

Regarding what you write about establishing a regular study of Chassidus: this Torah has already been printed in many books and *kuntreisim*. You should turn in this matter to the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Shlomo Matusof, who is involved in communal needs—his address is below—as he also has books and *kuntreisim* in this part of our holy Torah.

It is already known what the holy Shelah explains regarding the verse "I have sinned, for I did not know"—that even a lack of knowledge is considered a sin, especially in this generation, regarding which the holy Arizal ruled that it is a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom.

It is understood that one does not fulfill one's obligation merely by speaking about it—although even speaking of it is a *segulah* for many, many matters—for the study of Torah must also be with *havanah* and *hasagah*. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

With blessings for success in all of the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

P.S.
Certainly, if you are able to obtain manuscripts or books on *chochmas ha'emes*, please inform me of this. If I do not have them, it will surely be possible to exchange them for books from our publishing house. It would be appropriate to discuss this as well with R' Shlomo Matusof, as he is aware of the books already located here.

## 2517

B"H, 8 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...It surprises me that you are overthinking your health, when the Creator, blessed be He, says, "Lift up your eyes on high and see who created these." When one looks at what is happening around them with open eyes, one sees that Hashem Yisbarach leads the entire world. Therefore, any person with intellect must come to the conclusion that since Hashem Yisbarach is the true and only Master of the entire world, and He is the essence of goodness, everything will certainly be conducted for the good. When one has such a good Master, there is no need to overthink, for there is no doubt that He—blessed be He—knows what is good and what is even better.

It is also understandable that at times the yetzer hara interferes and confuses a person’s thoughts, but why be impressed by this, and why believe the "old and foolish king"?

May Hashem Yisbarach help you to fulfill the instruction, "Serve Hashem with joy." When one does this in truth, one sees—even with physical eyes—that there is much to be satisfied and happy about.

And may Hashem Yisbarach grant you success, so that in good health and happiness, you may be able to engage in matters of Torah and mitzvos with peace of mind.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2-518

B"H, 8 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Iyar: You should increase your study of the letters of Torah and tefillah, and endeavor to memorize at least a few chapters of Mishnayos and a few chapters of Tanya, as well as the maamar entitled *Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken* in Likutei Torah, at the end of Parshas Kedoshim. Furthermore, every Monday and Thursday before morning davening, set aside a coin or two for tzedakah, and strive as much as possible to influence the youth, to draw their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven. In addition to all this—and this is the most important thing—you should divert your thoughts from the sin and even from its rectification. For all the aforementioned is a segulah and a rectification; once you serve Hashem with joy, you will gradually feel an improvement in your situation. May it be His will that you begin this soon.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you to keep the three daily study portions established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the well-known portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya.

With blessings for success in all your affairs.

## 2,559

B"H, 8 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter of 5/2 has been received, in which you write about the places where you have been until now, and that this led to not observing [the laws of family purity], etc.

It is absolutely necessary that from now on, the laws of Taharas HaMishpachah be observed according to the requirements of our holy Torah, which is also a Torah of **life**—bringing life and joy to Yidden in their homes.

And, at the very least, to rectify to a certain extent that which was not as it should have been, you should give a few coins once a week to be used for the maintenance of a mikveh in one of the cities in our holy land, may it be built and established. On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita.

## 2520

2520

B”H, 9 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned man, involved in communal needs, Rabbi Menachem Shmuel Dovid Halevi Reitzes, who also informed me that you have purchased a lot and are planning to build there. May Hashem Yisborach help that it should be with success, and in accordance with the expression of Rabbeinu HaZaken, may Hashem Yisborach grant you abundant gashmius (material means), and may you transform that gashmius into ruchnius (converting it into participation in and support of matters of Torah and mitzvos), and may you do so in good health and with joy.

Rabbi Reitzes also informed me that you are a doctor. I am therefore certain that it is unnecessary to point out to you that for a person, the health of the body—the guf—is connected to the health of the neshamah. Consequently, you do not require any special explanation as to how important it is for a Yid that his neshamah should receive what it requires—which are the matters of Torah and mitzvos—for only then can his body be healthy. This is also one of the hints—the allusions—of the mitzvah of wearing tefillin, which one places upon the head where the brain is located, and upon the arm opposite the heart. For with the brain, all the nerves of the entire body are connected, and from the heart, blood is distributed throughout the entire body. In tefillin, there are four parshiyos of Torah, and the beginning of them is the verse, “Shema Yisrael Hashem Elokeinu Hashem Echad,” which is the call to every Yid to hear and remember that Hashem Yisborach is the sole Master of everything and over everything, and by extension, in **his** private life as well. When this knowledge permeates and penetrates his brain and heart, then his entire body—his guf—and his entire neshamah are healthy.

I hope that these few lines convey in brief strokes one of the important hints—remazim—of the mitzvah of tefillin, in its connection to daily life.

I will be pleased to hear from you from time to time, and I wish you success in all that was mentioned above.

## 2561

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a hiatus, it was pleasant to receive your letter from 3 Sivan, and most importantly, to read in it that you are being offered a distinguished match for your daughter... Regarding what you write—that the young man's parents are not asking for a dowry and wish to take upon themselves the entire arrangement of an apartment, furniture, and other expenses, etc.—while on one hand I was pleased by this as a testament to the merit of your daughter, may she live, on the other hand, a Jewish man and woman in general, and parents in particular, *darfen velen az zeyere kinder zolen zey kasten trucha b'gufam b'nishmasam v'afilu b'mamonam* (must want their children to cost them effort in their bodies, in their souls, and even in their finances). It is known from the holy Zohar (Vol. II, 128a) that in matters of holiness, there should not be the element of "free of charge." This is all the more so regarding the marriage of a daughter, where not only should one be involved in the expenses, but one should not be stingy with them. Certainly, this is included in the matters of a person that are allotted to him during the ten days between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, *un az men shtelt zich breit git Hashem oich mit a breitkeit* (and when one conducts oneself with breadth, Hashem also gives with breadth)...

With blessings, awaiting good news,

P.S.

In general, the order should be that a chassan looks up to his father-in-law. If the chassan has fixed shiurim in Tanya, then all the more so must the father-in-law have fixed shiurim, not only in Tanya but also in Likutei Torah, maamarim, etc. May Hashem grant you the merit to share good news regarding this as well.

## 2262

B.H., 9 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

...Among other things, your husband, may he live and be well, also told me about the law in your country, that after the age of seventy, every citizen receives a certain pension from the government, and that you are considering whether or not you should accept it.

Everything that happens in the world, and especially among Jews, occurs through Hashgacha Pratis, and contains a specific meaning and content. When a Jew has the opportunity to increase their share in matters of Torah and mitzvos—and certainly when this opportunity comes without any extra effort on the person's part—it should be accepted as a hint from Above that it can surely be utilized in a positive way, that is, in accordance with the guidance of our holy Torah. If a person is situated such that they do not need the money for their own living expenses, it is certain that through this money, they can increase their share in giving tzedakah, or more accurately, give the entire amount to tzedakah—especially tzedakah that is connected to bringing Jewish hearts closer to our Father in Heaven.

Therefore, I am of the opinion that in your case as well, since the general law entitles you to a certain sum each month, it would be nothing more than right, and also a zechus for you, to utilize this right in good health. Through this, you can increase, to a significant degree, the participation of yourself and your husband, may they live and be well, in the tzedakah that is dedicated to educating Jewish children to make them even more Jewish and to be Jews as our holy Torah requires. May Hashem Yisbarach help you that, together with your husband, for many long and good years, you should give tzedakah with a broad and full hand, in good health and with joy.

With blessings.

## 2,563

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Iyar and the one preceding it: regarding what you wrote about your sister-in-law—your wife’s sister, *tichyeh*—and her *shidduch* with the *avreich*... you yourself list and count all the merits of the matter, yet worry is apparent between the lines because, in your opinion, they lack the necessary means to rent an apartment, etc. Consider the matter for yourself: our Sages of blessed memory stated that matching couples is as difficult as the splitting of the Red Sea, yet she has found her suitable *shidduch*, both materially and spiritually. If such a miracle has occurred, are you worried about what will be with a kitchen, furniture, etc.?! At a time when, as a relative, you should be thanking and praising Hashem for providing her with an *avreich* who is a *yirei Elokim* and studies Torah, etc. (as you write in your letter), and that even though he is not a man of wealth, she has given her consent to this wholeheartedly. May you only report good news of this nature from here on.

Regarding your own situation and personal arrangements: my words have long been spoken based on the well-known principle of our holy Rebbes, starting from the Baal Shem Tov and the *Nesi'im* who followed him, up to and including my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*: black melancholy and sadness must be banished entirely from the camp of Yisrael, whatever the cause may be. It brings no benefit; on the contrary, it is a cause and a breeding ground for all matters of destruction. This applies to your situation as well—it is a pity to waste your thoughts on such things. You should dedicate yourself to work in proper *chinuch*, despite the various arguments you present for not engaging in it. Then, ultimately, you will find spiritual satisfaction and realize that there was no basis for your hesitations and doubts. May Hashem grant you success so that this happens soon.

With blessings for success in all the above, and awaiting good news regarding the above, as well as regarding the health of your son, *sheyichyeh*.

## 2724

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was surprised to learn that you are not careful about maintaining your health. This is contrary to what is explained in Chassidus in several places—and which was also cited in the maamar of 10 Shevat 5713—regarding how one must be careful in this matter. Furthermore, the ruling of the Rambam is already well-known, that this is one of the ways of Hashem.

It is understood that there is no contradiction between this and maintaining the yeshiva’s schedule and setting additional times for Torah and tefillah, etc., for it is impossible for one mitzvah to contradict another. This is especially true for a student of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, which was founded and is guided by our Rebbeim, the Nesi'im, may their merit protect us. A student must maintain the yeshiva’s schedule while also keeping his body and soul healthy and whole, so that he can serve Hashem without distractions.

Therefore, at the very least, from this point forward, you must maintain a schedule of eating, drinking, and sleeping as is necessary and required for your physical constitution, for not everyone is the same in this regard. Through this care and caution, you will also gain more in your understanding and retention of your studies and in your fulfillment of mitzvos. The ruling of our Sages is already well-known: "You have labored and you have found."

I await good news regarding all of the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2525

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter (which arrived with some delay), in which you write regarding your son, the distinguished avreich, who is engaged in communal work, a man of fine character, and a man of many accomplishments in bringing the hearts of the Jewish people closer to our Father in Heaven, etc., [Name]—may he live and be well. You write regarding the explanations [offered] in the place where he is to seek his appropriate match, and you, sir, are concerned about what people might say, etc.—that he is, G-d forbid, not listening to his father, who insists that he travel specifically to a certain country for this matter, and that people might conclude that the influence of Chassidus on your son is to dissuade him from fulfilling the mitzvah of honoring one’s father, etc.

In truth, I do not know if the above requires a response, for everyone knows that the teachings of Chassidus and its guidance draw a person’s heart closer to the service of the Creator, and consequently to the fulfillment of His mitzvos, and not, G-d forbid, the opposite.

I was startled to read in your letter of such a concern. My defense of you is that a person is not held accountable for what he says in his distress, and since it seems to you, sir, that it would be better for him to travel [to the place you suggest], it is akin to what is said regarding Moshe Rabbeinu—that when he came to a state of anger, he forgot the halacha. Especially since the ruling of our holy Torah is well-known, found in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, Laws of Honoring One’s Father, at the end of section 240: that a student who wishes to go to a place where he is certain he will see a sign of blessing in his studies, and his father objects because he is worried—having heard rumors that this involves a matter of danger to life—he is not required to listen to his father in this. Similarly, if a father objects to a son marrying a woman whom the son desires, he is not required to listen to the father. See the commentaries on the Shulchan Aruch there.

Now, this halachic ruling applies even if the father has clear evidence and a clear reason—as mentioned above, that the non-Jews are making false accusations, or that the father has already seen the woman the son desires or her family members and objects to the marriage. But in the present case, where there are no such proofs or evidence at all, how much more so is the aforementioned halachic ruling in full force.

Furthermore—and this is the main point—it is not at all understood why you, sir, need to place your distinguished son—may he live—in such a trial, when it is in your hands not to command him to travel specifically to a certain place. In doing so, the entire issue of honoring one’s father in this matter would be removed. The Torah’s ruling on this is well-known, and it is also there in the Shulchan Aruch, paragraph 19, etc.

My hope is strong that you, sir, will encourage the spirit of your son—may he live—and strengthen his hand in his work, the holy work, and lift his spirits to continue in it with added courage. The Holy One, blessed be He, is certain to pay the reward for this great mitzvah from His full and generous hand. May it be the will of Hashem that you, sir, experience an abundance of Chassidic delight from all your descendants—may they live.

I would appreciate it if you would inform me that all the aforementioned matters have been resolved in the best possible way.

With blessings.

## 2726

B.H., 10 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter, in which you write regarding what was conveyed to you in my name, and you respond that there are details you agree with and details you do not wish to accept, and that consequently, it would only be a matter of coercion, etc.

Now, this entire approach is incorrect and inappropriate. When one approaches the beginning of a life path—and it is clear that everyone wants their life to be happy, and happiness in life depends, **specifically**, in quality and quantity, on the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He—the question is not what the **person** wants or does not want. Rather, the approach must be: upon what does a person’s happiness depend, in whom is it invested, and under what conditions can one hope for happiness to be realized in practice?

I told [the groom] when he was here that a person’s wife can be a help to him or a hindrance. And although it is difficult to foresee and know with absolute, one-hundred-percent certainty how the relationship will be over the course of decades, a known and important criterion in this is the relationship between the young couple and the consideration they show for each other’s perspective before the wedding. He must clarify this (as must every man and woman who wishes to enter into the covenant of marriage) as much as possible.

Regarding him, he should not hide anything from her concerning his current outlook on life, and he should ask her to tell him clearly what her stance is toward his outlook. If she acts as she did in her letter—arranging her life according to her own desires without regard for the opinion of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and the instructions He has given to every man and woman of the Jewish people—then one must reflect very carefully on the question of the marriage and the *shidduch* in its entirety.

Since [the groom] wanted to know my opinion on this, as well as my consent—and, as he expressed it, my blessing—I, for my part, can only consent with a whole heart when I see the maximum possible hope that their lives will be happy. This depends on them arranging their lives on the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos* as they are stated in the *Shulchan Aruch*, and not according to the interpretation of each individual, where one agrees to a certain detail and does not agree to others. For the Holy One, Blessed be He, says that walking in the ways He has instructed guarantees a life of blessing and success, whereas walking in other ways does not. I cannot take upon myself the responsibility of participating in such a matter when one of the parties approaches the whole thing [saying] that they do not want it, that they do not promise it, and that they are being coerced against their will, etc.

If someone says that they cannot concede and walk specifically with their head covered by a *mitpachat* or a *sheitel*, and it makes no difference to them if, by doing so, they jeopardize their happiness and the happiness of the other party in their life together for decades, then such a person has no sense of responsibility, nor any appropriate appreciation or knowledge of what a shared life is, and how worthwhile it is to concede even on more important matters, provided that the life is unified and happy. And as mentioned above, this is impossible in the life of a Jewish man and woman except through Torah and *mitzvos*.

May the Holy One, Blessed be He, grant her the merit to recognize her path in life and to decide what is good for her—the true good, which is good both materially and spiritually, and [to realize] that, in truth, one is impossible without the other.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, Shlita,

Secretary

## 2727

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent worker for the needs of the community, R' Yehoshua Shneur Zalman, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

...I will repeat and reiterate once again what I have written many times: it is imperative that you expand the yeshiva as much as possible, both in quantity and in quality. The Ribono shel Olam does not deal unjustly with His creatures, and certainly, the aforementioned is within your capabilities. It is only that "if one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him." You must remove the matters of concealment and obstruction regarding any avodah, especially avodah in the field of proper chinuch in a country where this is in the stage of inception. And yet, it is very distressing that for several months now, you are the only ones working on this, because... you have seen tangible, outstanding success regarding the building and the positive attitude from several people who, at first, did not hope for this. Despite this, you are still calculating calculations, etc., etc.

As for all the explanations you write—that you do not have a great lamdan who knows the language of the country, etc.—the reality of Chabad avodah in various countries refutes all these excuses. In general, what is the use of excuses when it is clear that there must be a Tomchei Temimim yeshiva in actual practice in Australia as well? The greatest proof of this is that if not for this matter, it is not understood at all why the Ribono shel Olam brought you there, as there is no apparent material gain nor spiritual gain. I believe I have already written to you the saying of the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory, who said: "A Litvak does not believe until he counts it over," but one should not fail to believe even after it has been counted...

Regarding what you wrote, that the yeshiva will have a library of Nigleh and Chassidus: this is correct. I believe you already have a library of books from Kehot Publication Society... and when you send a list of the books you already have, they will complete what is missing for you.

With blessings for success in all the above, and awaiting good tidings.

## 2768

B”H, 10 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 6th of Sivan and thereafter, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein. I will read them at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and he will surely arouse Divine mercy for all those mentioned in them, for each according to their needs in both material and spiritual matters.

Regarding what you wrote about your class—that for several reasons they have been unable to study for some time—it is a known ruling of our Sages: "You have labored and you have found." This is all the more true in this work, which is *meleches shamayim* (heavenly work); consequently, the assistance from Above is in the greatest measure. However, as with all matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, it is required that the approach be one of joy and confidence in the success of the work. When one does so, both the *mashpia* and the recipients see clearly how the success grows and continues to increase. This is in addition to the fact that in such a manner, the effect on the health of the *mashpia* is for the good, and adds to their health in the literal sense as well.

Regarding what you wrote about the *avreich*... who is delaying the matter of his examination due to the questions involved: the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is well known in this regard: "For such a matter, it is worth sacrificing one's life." However, within these very examinations there are several aspects and methods, and it is understood that it is worthwhile to begin with the method where the concern according to *halacha* is minimal. May Hashem grant him success in bringing good tidings regarding all of the above, and soon.

With blessings for success,

P.S.
It is surprising that in all your letters you do not mention anything regarding your participation in *farbrengens* of *Chassidus*, etc.
