## 2729

B"H, 12 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated to communal needs,
Rabbi Avraham Dreizin
and Rabbi Ephraim Wolf

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your three letters from the 14th, 17th, and 29th of Iyar, regarding the vocational school...

It goes without saying that I cannot change the Lubavitcher path, nor do I have any desire to do so—even if the Ministry of Labor, together with the Joint, were to demand it. I spoke clearly with Rabbi Young when the initial discussions regarding the vocational school took place: it must be in the spirit of Lubavitch, for if not, my hands are removed from it, and I will not even begin. He was also surprised at the very notion that they might interfere in such matters. It is understood that my perspective on this has not changed in the interim. Consequently, what is essential and cannot be compromised is that the time dedicated to *limudei kodesh* must be **more** than the time allotted for vocational training (it would be best if two-thirds of the time were for *tefillah* and *limudei kodesh*, and one-third for vocational training).

2) It is essential that the *limudei kodesh* schedule take place before the vocational training schedule, and also after the work—a study session at night.

3) It is also essential that the study of *Chassidus* take place both in the morning and in the evening.

4) The primary point of the vocational school is that the vocational training is secondary to the *limudei kodesh*, and not, *chas v'shalom*, the other way around...

6) It appears that during the past winter, you sent letters requesting assistance for the vocational school to the United States, and perhaps to other places as well. I am interested to know if the income exceeded the expenses, and by approximately how much.

7) Although this point concerns the *Tomchei Temimim* in Lod more than the vocational school, since it also affects the vocational school, I am including this matter in my current letter: it appears from letters received here that there is a trend among the students of *Tomchei Temimim* in Lod to run off to the vocational school.

As the Sages have already said, "It is not the mouse that is the thief, but the hole [that provides the opportunity]." This must be combated in good time, through appropriate means, by establishing certain restrictions and regulations regarding who is accepted into the vocational school. It would be best if one of the conditions for acceptance were that the student must first study for a certain period in one of the Chabad *yeshivos* in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and only then be accepted into the vocational school.

8) It is good that for the time being, you are not accepting additional students beyond those you already have. Until things are settled, it is better that the vocational school contain only those students who are already known, who have already spent time in a Chabad educational institution.

9) Regarding the expenses of the vocational school, it was discussed that once the building is established, the Joint would take upon itself the maintenance of the teachers, students, etc. It is understood that before the matter is put into practice, they could not detail the specifics, and it is surprising that they do not mention in the letter if they have been told anything about this now. In any case, the idea of linking the vocational school with the Committee, etc., is not the case, as I wrote at the beginning of the discussion regarding the vocational school—this is a separate matter entirely, etc.

10) I will address the other matters another time, as I do not wish to delay this letter in order to establish firm guidelines on the essential matters of the vocational school. The most essential point of all is that this is a school for the education of Jewish youth in the spirit of our ancestors, with the addition that they also learn a trade there—which clarifies several of the points mentioned above.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**Rabbi Ephraim Wolf:** Additional letters to him appear above, Vol. 5, p. 336, and in the notes indicated there.

**Limudei Kodesh:** See also above, Vol. 8, letter 2776, section 14. Below, 2840.

**From letters received:** See also above, letters 2660, 2677.

## 2730

15 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of 10 Sivan, in which you ask for my opinion on whether you should travel to Morocco for a period of three or four months so that it might be possible for you to save money for the travel expenses to the United States, etc.

It is well known, both in the revealed Torah and in the hidden Torah, the greatness of the matter of Torah study, to which even "matters of Heaven" cannot be compared. However, according to the ruling of our Sages (Shabbos 31a), Torah study must be conducted specifically with *yiras shamayim*, for then "the fear of Hashem is His treasure," and there is endurance for the Torah study, as hinted in the verse, "And the faith of your times shall be... wisdom and knowledge."

Since Hashem has granted you success and placed you in a place of light—the *Tomchei Temimim* Yeshiva, which was founded and is directed by the *tzaddikim*, the Rebbe Rashab and his son, my father-in-law, the Rebbe—it is incumbent upon you to cherish every moment, and all the more so days, weeks, and months, to remain within its four cubits and to toil in the study of the revealed Torah and the hidden Torah with true *mesiras nefesh*.

Consequently, any thought that disrupts this possibility, even if it seems on the face of it to come from the *yetzer hatov*, is nothing but one of the ways of the *yetzer hara*. It is said of him that he is an "expert" (Shabbos 108b) in his work, and he approaches each and every person with such temptations, hoping they will listen to his incitement and his efforts to remove a person from the path that ascends to the house of Hashem.

The same applies to your situation: you must decide for yourselves with a true resolution that you will study with *mesiras nefesh* in the place where you are now, and you must not listen to the arguments that come from the "left," which incite you by saying, "When I am free, I will study." It is well known what the *Mishnah* says (Avos 2:4): "Do not say, 'When I am free, I will study,' for perhaps you will never be free."

In particular, every single member of *Bnei Yisrael* believes and hopes for the coming of *Moshiach Tzidkeinu* speedily in our days. The preface and preparation for this—as the *Melech HaMoshiach* said to our master, the Baal Shem Tov—is that his "wellsprings will spread outward." Therefore, you must utilize every opportunity in time to absorb the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, which are explained thoroughly in the *Torah* of *Chassidus*—*Chochma, Binah, Da'as*—so that you may be able to stand at the forefront of those who will merit to greet *Moshiach Tzidkeinu* in the near future.

"The study is not the main thing, but the action"—that is, the study **in practice**, with diligence and *mesiras nefesh*, from a place of pure *yiras shamayim*, which comes through the *avodah* of *tefillah*, and is also evident in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*.

I look forward to receiving good news from you that you are persevering in your studies of the revealed Torah and *Chassidus* more and more, and that you are ascending in holiness from time to time, and that as for all the thoughts regarding traveling here—in a state of *ratzo v'shov*, etc.—you will, for the time being, set them aside.

With blessings for success in the study of Torah, in the *avodah* of *tefillah*, and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*.

P.S.
It is understood that all of the above applies also to your friends, and I authorize you to publicize the content of this letter of mine in the classes where you study. Certainly, the *mashpia*, the esteemed *chossid*, a man of action whose work is the work of Heaven, a man of character and energy, Rabbi Nissan Nemanov, may he live, will be able to add for you explanation and understanding regarding all of the above, as it is impossible to explain the details of these matters in writing.

## 2731

B"H, 16 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

Since my last letter, I have received your letters dated 20, 24, and 26 Nissan, 17 and 29 Iyar, and 5 Sivan, along with their enclosures. I am writing to respond to the first, etc.

1) Surely, as time has passed, it has become even clearer how necessary it is to ensure that the Yeshiva does not lack students in the future, especially since the immigration of youth has decreased so significantly, etc.

In the current situation, this can only be secured by accepting students—even if in separate classes—without **excessive** stringency. Although it is self-understood that one must be careful not to lower the reputation of the Yeshiva thereby, etc.

2) It is also understood that, in addition to the above, this is one of the intentions and goals of the Reshet schools: that the older students in them should be able to transition to Lod.

3) In connection with this, regarding the establishment of Tomchei Temimim branches in other cities in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily: I do not see any additional benefit in this (aside from the question of expenses, for it is impossible to hold both ends of the rope—to report in every single letter that the financial situation is dire, etc., and on the other hand, to increase expenses as mentioned above without benefit or necessity). If there is a possibility to open a yeshiva as a preparatory school for Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod, then this should be incorporated into the Reshet program, and for **several** reasons...

4) In connection with this, regarding the question of purchasing the Yeshiva buildings: you do not write where the funds would come from, given that even the regular budget is difficult to fulfill, etc. Furthermore, you do not write what the practice of other yeshivos is in this regard, as surely a significant portion of them do not own their buildings but rather rent them.

Moreover—and this is the main point—what is the benefit in transitioning the buildings from a state of renting to a state of ownership?

Surely you will write regarding this at the next opportunity...

## 2732

2732

By the Grace of Hashem, 17 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I am surprised that I have not heard from you all this time. I would like to hope that this is a good sign, indicating that everything is going as it should. Nevertheless, I would be pleased to read an explanation of this in your letter, and may Hashem Yisbarach help that it should be to the fullest extent.

It is surely unnecessary to point out to you that the conduct of a home in general, and the relationship between a husband and wife, depends to a greater and larger extent on the wife than on the husband. This is as the expression in Tanach states: "The wisdom of women builds her house" — the construction and maintenance of the home depends on the wisdom of the woman. Especially in American life, where the work of men is associated with much nervous tension and haste, it is the duty of the wife all the more so to ensure that there is a maximum of shalom between them, through a maximum of understanding on the part of the wife.

And even when it seems—and perhaps partially with justification—that the husband could have been more of a *baal maalah*, one must take into account that this *shidduch* was already determined long ago by Hashem Yisbarach. When one sees a deficiency in **oneself**, the advice is not to cause oneself pain, but rather to seek ways that are not associated with pain to rectify it.

This is true, and to an even greater extent, regarding the relationship between husband and wife. For at the end of the day, it is difficult to know what the other person is experiencing and the difficulties they have had in years past. When a husband sees softness from his wife and a feeling of strong *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach, he naturally views the whole world differently. He sees that Hashem Yisbarach is the *Baal HaBayis* of the entire world, and specifically of his own home and surroundings. This adds even more good-naturedness and joy, and one then sees for oneself that it was well worth it **for one’s own sake**, because it brings warmth and tranquility—far more than the effort it cost to yield and forgive.

Hopefully, regarding you and your husband *shichyu*, this entire reflection is not needed, and it is as a Chassidishe home should be: permeated with *ahavas Yisrael*, for which our holy Rebbes sacrificed themselves to see in Chassidishe homes in particular. However, since there is no limit to what is good, I therefore calculate that these written lines will have the effect that there should be even more and better mutual good shalom and understanding in your relationship, which should also spread to your surroundings as a model of shalom and light. And may Hashem Yisbarach bring you happiness.

With blessings,

## 2733

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...And in these days following the receiving of the Torah, which is called the Torah of life and the eternal Torah—one of the interpretations of which is that it infuses life even into worldly matters—may it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of us should see this within our own four cubits and those of our households, may they live, and may we see this also in the literal sense, that you should have a lively, healthy, and happy summer, and a healthy and happy [life] always.

With blessings.

## 2734

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding the practical application, it is explained in many places in Chassidus that after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, all things and matters are a mixture of good and evil. The avodah according to the path of Chassidus is to engage in strengthening the side of good and light. This is why it can be done with great joy (unlike the path of Mussar, which emphasizes the line of "turn from evil" primarily, which leads to sadness, etc.). Furthermore, in relation to people, one must utilize their good qualities and talents as much as possible; then, either automatically or through slight effort, the not-good matters are nullified.

The same applies to everyone participating in one of the activities of the institutions of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. One must provide the opportunity for each of the other workers to utilize their talents, to arouse them and encourage them in this, so that little by little, the undesirable matters are nullified, even if they existed beforehand.

...I have already written at length in *Kerem Chabad*, and it is sufficient to provide each person with satisfaction in this, and with how to utilize their talents to their fullest without touching the imagined honor of their fellow, and certainly not the true honor of their fellow. Rather, the vessel that holds blessing in all the aforementioned matters is peace and the drawing together of hearts.

It is understood that I have not come in this letter to preach Mussar, but rather to arouse and encourage once again that in each and every one... there are great powers that have not yet been utilized at all... for trivial reasons. And when everyone "throws themselves" (*arayvarfen*) with *mesiras nefesh* into this holy work, I am certain that within a short time they will be amazed at themselves, wondering how they did not see the simple fact that by adding strength, everyone **together** could have increased and magnified the work of... many times over. In this way, their personal satisfaction and *hiskashrus* to the *ilana d'chayei* (Tree of Life) would also grow, as would the additional blessing in the matters of... and the personal affairs of each and every one and their families, may they live.

And it is understood—it goes without saying—that it is completely absurd to distance anyone from this holy work, for aside from the distancing of a *ben Yisrael* from the *ilana d'chayei*, this will cause damage to the work of... and further elaboration on this is entirely superfluous...

With blessings.

## 2736

B"H, 19 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Yehuda Zev, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the telegram regarding the esteemed Chossid, etc., Rabbi... regarding what you wrote concerning the permission for the aforementioned to daven and learn, etc., and you conclude that perhaps it should be permitted through *hirhur* (mental contemplation). Regarding learning, it is possible that one can suffice with learning through *hirhur*, as that is the essence. However, regarding davening, one must endeavor to find a way to permit him to daven with speech as well, and to arrange the vessels in his room in an appropriate manner, etc.*.

... It will surely interest you to see the excerpt of the *sicha* enclosed herewith, and you should act with a generous eye regarding others as well.

With blessings for success in his holy work and in his personal matters.

#### ***2736***

**Rabbi Yehuda Zev:** Segal. Additional letters to him — see above, Vol. 8, 2621, and the references in the notes there.

**The permission for the aforementioned to daven:** Regarding *mei raglayim* (urine) that is flowing from him via a vessel. Following this — see below, 2905.

*) It is not my practice to issue halachic rulings. Nevertheless, I will note here a few points: a) One could argue that this does not have the status of *mei raglayim*, since it comes directly from the bladder (via a catheter) and not from the organ, and there is doubt whether they have the status of *mei raglayim* immediately upon exiting the kidneys. b) Even *mei raglayim* (and even if it is flowing — *Magen Avraham*, end of Siman 76) is only a Rabbinic prohibition, and it does not override a Torah prohibition, nor does it override davening and *tefillin* (*Shulchan Aruch HaRav*, end of Siman 76). c) The prevention of davening and *Talmud Torah*, etc., will certainly cause distress, and consequently, a weakening of the patient's health, and many matters have been permitted for this reason (see *Choshen Mishpat* 254).

## 2737

B"H, 20 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, may they live,

Shalom and blessing!

...It is understood that one must utilize all appropriate strengths in the work of the Reshet. Regarding what I wrote—that the teachers should be from Anash—this concerns only the law of priority, as our Sages of blessed memory said, "The poor of your city come first." This is especially true since the work of the Reshet sometimes demands dedication beyond the ordinary, and it is easier to demand, expect, and hope for this from Anash than from others.

It is also understood, conversely, that it is a pity for the appropriate strengths of Anash to work in other vineyards, especially if there is room to expand the activities of the Reshet. For one must prepare the suitable workers for this in advance, rather than having to search for them at the last minute, which would necessitate taking whoever happens to be available...

It seems that nothing will come of the idea of organizing a study day for teachers, lectures, and so on. There is no point in crying over the past; in any case, they should organize such an event now. It would be best if it were done with appropriate publicity, etc. The benefit of this, both internally and externally, requires no explanation...

I await confirmation of the receipt of this letter as soon as possible, and, if possible, a response to it as well. With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 2739

2739

B.H., 21 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Agudas Chassidei Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

...I have written previously regarding the status of the Chabad shuls in the Holy Land and what is being done with them. I am writing now because if you already have information regarding this, it is worthwhile to inform me in good time, as this relates specifically to the upcoming 12 Tammuz. This is the only *yoma depagra* throughout the year that belongs uniquely to Chabad (for even 19 Kislev is celebrated by some of the Chassidim of Poland as well). Therefore, it should be utilized within the Chabad sphere in a special way, through appropriate publicity at the proper time beforehand. It is understood that in this, one must utilize the possibilities of the Chabad shuls. This is in addition to the primary question, which is the necessity of maintaining the character of these shuls and developing them—namely, to increase their influence on the surrounding environment and also on the congregants of the shul, which to a large extent depends on the shul’s administration and their Rav or *magid shiur*.

Therefore, along with general information, there must also be information regarding the nature of the aforementioned individuals. I await detailed reports, as well as a proposal from your side regarding the activities of Agudas Chassidei Chabad that are possible in these shuls in connection with the above.

3) I was astonished to learn that not long ago, several *bichelech* of *D'Chassidus* were brought from the Holy Land to London, and also here, for sale. It is a great wonder that either they were not aware of this at all, or they were aware and paid no heed—for there is room to say that on the spot in the Holy Land, it would have been possible to purchase these *bichelech* more cheaply, and most importantly, to safeguard them so they would not fall into the hands of strangers (in this context, and who knows, perhaps even strangers in the literal sense). One does not cry over the past, but in any case, I am writing to urge caution for the future. My astonishment is even greater, given that for some **years** I have requested to publicize, ask, and search for *bichelech* of *D'Chassidus* and send them here—and if it is not possible otherwise, then with the intent of returning them. Yet throughout all these **years**, only from one person were some *bichelech* received in exchange...

4) In continuation of the above—it has come to my attention that the grandchildren of the *tzaddik* and *chossid*, etc., Moreinu Harav Shneur Zalman, of blessed memory, of Babruysk, possess several *bichelech*—of *D'Chassidus*, and perhaps also of *Nigleh*—of our *Nesi'im*, namely the Tzemach Tzedek and his sons, and some say also from the Alter Rebbe and the Mitteler Rebbe. From those who told me, I could not clarify whether these are original manuscripts in their holy handwriting or copies. But in any case, please, I urge you to visit the aforementioned (I do not know clearly with which of the grandchildren these are located) and ask them in my name to permit one of the *avreichim* to make an index of these *bichelech* in order to send it to me. And if they contain matters that are not in my possession—especially those pertaining to the subjects currently being printed—that I might receive these *bichelech*, at the very least as a loan for a period of time. This request also includes *D'Chassidus* from R' Hillel Paritcher and R' Yitzchak Isaac Epstein of Homil, of blessed memory...

With a blessing for success, I await good news regarding all of the above.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2542

Brooklyn.

As is already known from the ruling in the holy Tanya, Iggeres HaKodesh, Chapter 22, that when one contemplates this, etc., then "Hashem will also grant that which is good" and will shine His countenance upon him in a manner of revealed love, and [the harsh judgments] will be sweetened, etc., and nullified, etc. May Hashem grant you the merit to share good news soon.

## 2-5743

B”H, 24 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...As he mentioned to me... his father studied in Lubavitch. It is a well-known ruling of the Mishnah that a father merits his son with *chochma*, which is defined as straight, logical reasoning, as explained by the commentators on the Mishnah there. And there is no reasoning more straight than this: to recognize the absolute necessity in these generations of ours to study this wisdom (see *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, page 142b). This influences every standing and situation of a person, especially for those whose parents have already entered the vineyard of *pnimiyus haTorah*. For them, the command of our Sages (Shabbos 31a, end) — "If the fear of Hashem is his treasure, then he has it..." — is absolute and urgent. May the Ribono shel Olam merit him to also be a conduit through whom this study will spread to his peers and his surroundings as well.

With blessings of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov.

## 2,484

B”H, 24 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 19 Sivan... It seems that the matter of N’shei U’Bnos Chabad has become stagnant, etc. It is puzzling that after all they have witnessed regarding Hashgacha Pratis, it appears that the realization has still not penetrated their inner beings that this is not merely a matter of external propaganda. Rather, it is **primarily** relevant to the women and girls of Chabad and their own homes, and not only regarding matters of *hiddur* (embellishment) alone. The situation is not comparable to how it was in our country in the past, where the choice was only between two extremes: either *mesiras nefesh* for the right, or total abandonment to the left. This is not the case in the current situation, and to the wise, a word is sufficient.

Since it is said that "women are of a light mind," there is all the more reason to demand that this be organized by the men. May it be His will that the verse "and he shall rule over you" be fulfilled in matters of Heaven—which will come about once the matter becomes as relevant to them as it ought to be. It is understood that all of the above is written for all *Anash*, and you have the permission, and indeed the merit, to publicize it in an appropriate manner.

With blessings,

P.S.
Regarding the *kabbalos* (resolutions), I am sure it will be arranged by the offices.

## 2745

B.H., 24 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs,
R’ Avraham Chaim, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 8th of Sivan, and subsequently, the book *Teshuvos Beis Hillel*. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success in fulfilling your portion and role in increasing and glorifying Torah, which is dependent upon maintaining pure *yiras shamayim*. As our Sages of blessed memory state (*Shabbos 31a*), when the fear of Hashem is one’s treasure, then "the faith of your times is a strength of salvations, wisdom, and knowledge" is fulfilled. In our days, this is only possible through fulfilling the directive of the Arizal (see *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe—the authority on the *nistar* of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the authority on the *nigleh* of Torah)—that in these generations, it is permitted and a **mitzvah** to reveal this wisdom. See the introduction of his student, Rav Chaim Vital, to *Shaar HaHakdamos*, where he discusses this at length using awesome and startling expressions.

It is also a known ruling of the *Shulchan Aruch* (*Orach Chaim*, beginning of *Siman* 98) that before *davening*, one must contemplate the greatness of the Almighty, etc. It is understood and simple that one cannot contemplate this without knowledge of it. To elaborate further would be superfluous. How great is the concealment and hiding that, even though all the above is understood simply, it is still necessary to explain the necessity of this study.

Enclosed is a check for your personal expenses. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success.

With blessings,

P.S.
Regarding what you transcribed in your letter concerning the two names of *Havayah*, etc.: You did not explain the matters sufficiently. 

1) Regarding the words of the Rosh: Since the thought of *avodah zarah* is joined [to the deed], it is not considered "before" one has sinned. 

2) Regarding the interpretation of "Hashem is One," which explains that there will no longer be a need for more than one name: How is it possible to say that in the future there will not be the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* (thirteen attributes of mercy), which, according to many of the *Rishonim*, begin from the first name of *Havayah*? On the contrary, it is precisely accurate from the language of our Sages, "I am He before one sins." 

The explanation of this in brief: 
a) Based on what is written in *Tanya*, *Perek* 16, regarding the precision of the language "joins it"—it should have said "it is accounted to him as if he had performed it." See there in *Korban Nesanel*. 
b) The matter is not that one name of *Havayah* will be nullified, G-d forbid, from the two names of *Havayah*. Rather, it refers to the cessation of the *ta'amim* (cantillation marks) between them, such that in the future, the two names of *Havayah* will be in unity.

See *Zohar* Vol. III, 138a; *Likutei Torah*, *Devarim*, *Nasoh*.

***

**R’ Avraham Chaim:** Levinson, of Jerusalem.

**What he transcribed in his letter:** In the book of the holy Gaon, one of the early ones, our Master of Munkatch, *zy"a*, in the name of the holy Gaon R’ M.L. of Sasov, *zy"a*: Our Sages of blessed memory state in *Maseches Rosh Hashanah* 17 regarding the thirteen attributes, "Hashem, Hashem, I am Hashem before one sins," and "Hashem" after one sins. The Rosh asks there: Why is the attribute of mercy needed before one sins? He answers that it speaks of the thought of *avodah zarah*, which is "before one has sinned," and although generally a bad thought is not joined to the deed, regarding *avodah zarah* it is joined, as it is written, "in order to capture the House of Israel in their hearts." These are the words of the Rosh, *z"l*. According to this, two names are needed only because of *avodah zarah*. In the future, may it be speedily, when "idols will be removed from the earth and the idols will be utterly cut off," there will be no thought of *avodah zarah* at all. Therefore, in truth, there will be no need for two names, only one name—the attribute of mercy in its entirety, without which one cannot exist. May the Ribono shel Olam merit us soon that "Hashem will be One" through the King Moshiach, the speaker of his nation, speedily in our days, *kein yehi ratzon*.

It is understood that this must be done without worry and without becoming completely immersed in it, yet on the other hand, without lacking the actual effort. May Hashem grant you success.

## 2,748

B"H, 26 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Sivan, in which you ask about your son... *shiy*, who is not diligent in his studies, etc., and you ask for my opinion on the matter.

I do not see room for the question. It is already known that our Sages of blessed memory ruled, "Until your own [child] is at your neck," etc., which begins from the age of sixteen—the age of your son, *shiy*, whom you mention in your letter. Consequently, the onus is upon you to take the necessary steps and pleasant approaches so that he will study with dedication and personal commitment, and then he will succeed.

Regarding what you wrote about the affairs of the yeshiva, it is surprising, for since you are also one of the *Roshei Yeshiva* and *mashgichim* of the yeshiva, the responsibility for the administration as a whole rests upon you as well. As is the case with all communal matters, this does not mean that the individual is exempt from them, as is well known. Every *Rosh Yeshiva* and *mashgiach* who engages in his specific area with dedication and sincerity will inevitably influence the rest of the yeshiva’s administration and the manner of work of the other *Roshei Yeshiva* and *mashgichim*. All of the above is in addition to the halachic ruling (Kiddushin 40b, cited in Rambam) that a person should always view himself as if he is balanced [on a scale], and with one action of his, he tips the scale for himself and for the entire world toward the side of merit, or the opposite. I look forward to your letter detailing how you are increasing your efforts in the areas under your jurisdiction—increasing as much as possible—as well as detailed proposals regarding improving the situation in the matters and areas under the administration of others. It is understood that the more detailed, the better.

With blessings.

## 2,789

B"H, 26 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your inquiry regarding whether your parents should move from their current location to settle in a *kibbutz chofshi* (secular kibbutz) in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established: I am surprised that such a thought even crossed your mind. You should examine closely the language of the Rambam in *Hilchos Deios*, beginning of Chapter 6: "A person must associate and dwell with the wise... and distance himself from the wicked... he should go to a place where the people are righteous... and if they are wicked and sinful... he should go out to caves, thickets, and deserts."

How much more so is this true when one is currently in a place where the customs are based on Torah and *mitzvos*; it is impossible to even contemplate moving to a *kibbutz chofshi*. He who guards His people Yisrael at all times and in all places, who "neither slumbers nor sleeps," will guard your parents among all of Yisrael, specifically in an environment of *yiras shamayim*, Torah, and *mitzvos*, where the *Shechinah* dwells. For his part, he can contribute to this by increasing his diligence, dedication, and commitment to the study of the revealed Torah and the *Toras HaChassidus*, and by performing *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, all of which must be founded upon pure *yiras shamayim*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2550

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 1 Korach, in which you write regarding the three types of ways to obtain sustenance for one’s home: It is already well-known that the instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory, which applies to every person (with the exception of unique individuals), is that one must create a vessel to receive the blessing, as the verse states: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you **do**." The reason for this is also explained in many places in the teachings of Chassidus, including in *Likutei Torah* by our Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya* (who is the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah) and the *Shulchan Aruch* (the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah), *Parshas Tetzei*, page 37b.

Even though a person’s sustenance is as difficult as the splitting of the Red Sea—which is one of the greatest **miracles**—one must nevertheless create a vessel in the ways of nature, as explained in *Likutei Torah* there. However, in order to increase the blessings of Hashem, one must be strong in *bitachon* and increase one’s courage in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, for these are the very channels and vessels for the drawing down and receiving of Hashem’s blessings as needed.

May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 2551

## 2552

B"H, 27 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Menachem Nachum Yitzchak Isaac, may he live.

I was pleased to receive your letter of 21 Sivan, in which you bring good news that your daughter, Sterna Freida, has given birth to a son, may it be for good fortune. May it be the will of Hashem that his parents, may they live, bring him into the covenant of Avraham Avinu at a good and auspicious time. Regarding what you wrote asking for advice on what to name the newborn boy, may he live:

It is well known that the response of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in such matters is that he does not intervene. This is understood based on what is written in the writings of the Arizal (Shaar HaGilgulim, ch. 23; see also there, Shaar 1, end of ch. 4), which is also brought in Ohr HaTorah at the end of Parshas Bereishis (and in Likutei Amarim of the Maggid of Mezritch), that from Above, the idea is placed into the parents' minds as to how to choose the name for the son or daughter being born—a name that belongs to that soul. This is explained in many places in Chassidus; see also Likutei Torah, Behar (41c), that the letters of the name belong to the vitality of the soul and the body.

With the blessing of Mazal Tov.

## 2753

B"H, 28 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding what you wrote about the ship: This is a matter of Jewish ownership, and naturally, this applies even if the workers there are not Jewish. Since it is being done with such great publicity, it requires deep study (*tzarich iyun*), as it is possible that there is a prohibition involved, whether *d'oraisa* or *d'rabanan*, and this is all the more so if the workers are Jewish. As for what they said—that everything is done automatically—this is certainly impossible, as is known to those who belong to this profession. With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 2,755

## 2,256

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 19 Sivan, in which you write about the various concealments and obstructions you are experiencing, detailing them point by point: All the points you list have a single source—the incitement of the *sitra achra*, which hinders a person in every way to prevent them from serving their Creator. Since the cause is singular, the remedy must be a single, fundamental change: total dedication and commitment to the study of *Nigleh* and the study of *Chassidus*, without any excuses.

When you truly decide, *aliba d'nafshi*, to do this, and you recognize the truth that this affects your entire standing and situation in life—not only in spiritual matters but in material life as well—you will see the success of Hashem. It is already a known ruling that even a little light dispels much darkness. However, in order to increase *siyata d'shmaya*, one must keep the three daily *shiurim* that are incumbent upon every soul, as established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevg"m, zya* (in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*), which are well known. Furthermore, increase in *tzedakah* with others—that is, bringing them closer to the Torah of Hashem and His service—for *tzedakah*, even in spiritual matters, "exalts a nation," as explained in *Torah Or* by the Alter Rebbe at the beginning of the work.

The conclusion from the above is: study with diligence and total dedication in *Nigleh* and in *Chassidus*; increase your resolve in the *avodah* of *tefillah* and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*; and influence others to bring them closer to the "Tree of Life." Then the prophecy will be fulfilled: "Little by little I will drive them out." And you will be able to share good news regarding all the matters you touched upon in your letter.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe *shlita*,

Secretary: A. Quint

The same applies to the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the head and Nasi of Yisrael; may it be the will of Hashem that very soon, the body will follow after him, so that even the "heels" (see Nazir 51a and Responsa Tzafnas Paneach by the Rogatchover Gaon, Vol. 1, 34) are included in this, in the true and complete redemption.

With blessings.

## 2558

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the congregants of Beis Yosef
in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom Rav and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter, in which you write regarding the celebration of your anniversary, as well as the farbrengens held in the days following, including the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah. I was especially pleased to read in the letter about the shiurim being studied, both in the revealed Torah and in the teachings of Chassidus.

May Hashem grant you success, that your house may be a house of prayer and a house of study, in accordance with the words of our Sages regarding the verse, "Hashem loves the gates of Zion more than all the dwellings of Jacob"—and perhaps this refers to Beis Yosef ("Yosef Hashem li ben acher"—"May Hashem add another son for me"). It is explained in the teachings of Chassidus that one "makes" a son when one transforms darkness into light. This is achieved through the intellectual soul’s contemplation of the greatness of Hashem, etc., until even the animal soul agrees to this. Then, the "advantage of light from darkness" becomes a true advantage, when the darkness itself is transformed into light. Through this, an infinite addition of light is drawn down even Above, as all this is explained at length in the maamar entitled *Ben Poras Yosef* by the Tzemach Tzedek (printed in *Ohr HaTorah*, p. 386b). The attribute of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "measure for measure," only that it is "measure for measure" in a way that adds light (which is the general term for the illuminations and influences from Above) without end, also below, in whatever is needed for all those who engage in the aforementioned, both for themselves and their households, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for the upcoming Festival of Redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, which I am certain you will celebrate in an appropriate manner in your synagogue, and may it be His will that it be with extraordinary success regarding the practical application.

## 2760

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...It appears from your letter that you have a set routine of **beginning** the davening on Shabbos morning at midday! I do not agree with such a routine at all (even though you surely recite Krias Shema before then, and likewise hear Barchu, etc.). It is different if one begins early and extends the davening. It is much better to begin approximately with the tzibbur, and [to recite] Kabbalas Shabbos and onwards after the conclusion of the tzibbur’s davening.

## 2763

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Sunday of this week, and I was pleased to read therein that your sons are being praised for their Torah studies. May it be the will of Hashem that this be realized in practice, in accordance with the words of our Sages, "It is not the study that is the essential thing, but the deed"—that their learning should lead to the fulfillment of mitzvos with *hiddur*. It is understood that it is essential that they also study Chassidus, for then the concept of "the fear of Hashem is His treasure" is fulfilled, through which the study of Torah is also preserved, as explained by our Sages (Shabbos 31a). It is certainly obvious that in order for these paths to be accepted by your sons, *sheyichyu*, you must also have a fixed *shiur* in the **study** of Chassidus. I emphasize "study," not merely reading or occasional perusal, for the verdict is well known: "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him." Further elaboration is unnecessary.

With blessings to hear good news regarding all of the above.

P.S.

Regarding what you wrote about a good and suitable position for yourself, you are surely aware of the situation regarding such positions in cities like New York and the like, where the number of those seeking positions is far greater than the number of positions available.

And as for changing your current position for a position in a small town, on the face of it, what is the benefit in that?

## 2,764

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Sivan: While it is true that prior to the giving of the Torah, the fact that the Jewish people were "a hasty nation" was considered a virtue, as explained by our Sages (Shabbos 89a), nevertheless, in general, after the giving of the Torah—and this refers also to every single day, as explained in Chassidic thought regarding the precise wording of the blessing on the Torah in the morning prayers, "Who gives the Torah" (in the present tense)—and especially in one's ongoing avodah, things must be orderly and without haste.

Consequently, you should occupy yourself with your livelihood matters now, with the appropriate level of effort, without allowing your mind to be distracted by thoughts of entering into yeshiva work while you are in the midst of doing so. When the situation in the yeshiva improves, as you wrote in your letter, that will be the time to consider the details and methods of work there, as well as to make a decision in a general sense.

May Hashem strengthen you in maintaining your *kavius itim* (fixed times) for the study of both the revealed Torah and Chassidus, as this, too, will add blessing and success to your livelihood matters.

With blessings,

## B'Tashsa

## 2766

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished avreich, who is involved in communal needs,
R' Yaakov Eliezer, may he live.

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 9 Sivan, and I thank you for the good news regarding the yeshiva. I appreciate your gratitude for the past and your request for the future to continue in this manner, and may Hashem grant you success.

2) Regarding your question as to whether the yeshiva administration should act firmly in every matter with the students and their parents: It is not possible to provide general instructions on this, as it is understood that the matter depends on the specific case under discussion. If it is a fundamental issue, one must not compromise on it; however, even then, one must proceed with pleasantness and peace, for then it is much easier *צו אויספירען* (to carry out). It is superfluous to add that in a place where there is a concern of *hezek harabim* (harm to the many), this overrides the consideration of the benefit of the individual. As experience in other places has shown, when the members of a school’s administration consult among themselves, in the vast majority of cases they find the appropriate words to explain to the parents and students the necessity of a specific directive or instruction, and how it is for the benefit of the collective and the benefit of the individual...

With blessings for success in communal matters and in your personal affairs.

#### ***2766***

**R' Yaakov Eliezer:** Herzog, Melbourne.

May Hashem grant you success.

## 2759

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in the needs of the community,
Rabbi Chaim Shaul, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 22 Sivan. May Hashem grant that in your next letter you will be able to share good news that things are going from good to even better, both in your personal affairs and in general matters—to increase Torah and make it glorious. I have already written to someone else that this verse is cited regarding the two extremes of *Talmud Torah*: both in the teaching of young children (Rambam, *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, end of Chapter 2) and in the study of Torah that is entirely above even the matter of *mitzvos* (*Chullin* 86b). This means that it is not merely "from one extreme to the other"—which would imply that because it is limited by two extremes, it is called "small," as is said regarding Yaakov, "he who passes from one extreme to the other—for he is small"—but rather that it is above all extremes and above any measurement or limitation whatsoever, as is explained in *Chassidus* in many places.

With blessings for success in all of the above, I await good news.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2751

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you write, that you find it difficult to strengthen your power of thought, speech, and action as we are commanded in His holy Torah—the Torah of life and the eternal Torah—and you ask where to turn and where to flee: You do not need to flee. As the Tanya Kadisha states in Chapter 41: Hashem stands over him, the whole earth is full of His glory, and He looks upon him, examining his kidneys and heart to see if he is serving Him as is fitting. This in itself provides the strength to stand in the war against the yetzer and to conquer it. Even a slight contemplation of this is sufficient.

To increase the *siyata d'shmaya* in this, you should have engraved in your mind and memory several chapters of Mishnayos and several chapters of Tanya, as well as the *maamar* in *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Parshas Kedoshim*, *d'h* "Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken." This is in addition to the fact that you should carry a Tanya in your pocket—wherever it is permitted, of course—and from time to time, during your free moments, study a few lines from it. If you do all of the above *aliba d'nafshi* (sincerely and personally) and remind yourself of the constant commandment, "I have set Hashem before me always," you will slowly but surely drive away the evil and increase the light within your *daled amos*.

I trust that you are reporting your spiritual state from time to time to the *mashpia* with whom you study *Chassidus*, and that you are acting according to his instructions. I look forward to hearing good news.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2712

B.H., 29 Sivan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs, Rabbi Yehoshua Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 10 Sivan. Surely, in the meantime, you have received my letter in which you will find answers to several of your questions. The beginning of this letter addresses a general point: the vast majority of your letters are filled with the content of how difficult, and almost impossible, it is to organize a yeshiva in your location, etc., as you wrote in your previous letter. This is despite the fact that you have witnessed open miracles, seeing how in all matters that were not dependent on the *bechirah* (free choice) of the Bnei Yisrael, you saw tremendous success. If there were difficulties, they were only in those points where the hand of the Bnei Yisrael—and specifically *anash*—who possess *bechirah chofshis*, was involved. Since they are in the likeness of Above (where that is the only place of true *bechirah*, as explained in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Emor* 38b, in the explanation of the verse, "Behold, the man has become as one of us"), it is there that *he'lem* and *hester* (concealment and hiding) were found, etc.

Regarding your question as to whether to establish a *Talmud Torah* for the young children or to suffice only with the day school: it is simple that you must establish a *Talmud Torah* for the young children as well. This is especially so given that it is doubtful whether the number of students in the day school can be sufficient unless you first draw the youth closer through their education in a *Talmud Torah* and *chedarim*.

Regarding cooperation with *avreichim* from another yeshiva or with people from another circle with whom you have acted with *ratzon* and *shalom* until now: although the established conduct is that one must accept everyone with *sever panim yafos* and must utilize the strengths of each and every one in the vineyard of Chabad as much as possible—even from those who are not from Chabad—nevertheless, regarding the creation of a full partnership, which inherently gives the partners a full say and at times even a decisive say, one must be extremely cautious. This is especially true in a country [...] where this also involves the *kiddush* of Lubavitch, etc. It is understood that all of the above does not apply to the matter of accepting students from those circles as well; this is only said regarding those who will have a say in the decision-making.

It is understood that one should not introduce matters of any party, whatever it may be, into the yeshiva building. Although, on the other hand, it is not your concern to check those who come to daven or learn to see if they belong to a party, the building and all matters connected to it are, of course, **above** party lines.

The same applies regarding the *nusach*. It is simple that in a yeshiva building named after *kudsha brich hu* and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h nbg"m zi"e*, the *nusach* of the davening must be his *nusach*. There is **no** offense to anyone’s honor in this, for everyone understands the concept of "even to conquer the queen with me in the house." Since the building and the yeshiva are named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, it must be appropriate to him. But on the other hand, you are not obligated to check every individual as to which *nusach* they daven in, etc. Consequently, it is also understood that if, on a temporary basis, someone goes before the *amud* and davens in a different *nusach*, this is not a matter for conflict.

As mentioned above, I reiterate once again that you must accept students into the yeshiva even if you fear that the students will remain only temporarily. For in addition to the fact that if you influence the students as you ought, at least the majority of them will remain permanently, it is also worthwhile for the sake of even temporary influence in pure *yiras shamayim*.

Regarding the conclusion of your letter, that the pain of *anash* is very great because they see that it is possible to succeed, and the deficiency is that there are no people suitable for it: since *Hashgacha Elyona* brought specifically you to [Australia] and not others, and showed you open miracles... it is **clear** that the ability lies in the hands of *anash* who are in [Australia] to do everything necessary. May it be the will of *Hashem* that you bring this ability from potential into action, and may it be done quickly and easily.

With blessings for success, awaiting good news, and regards to all *anash*.

For the heart of every Yid is awake to Hashem, His Torah, and His mitzvos, and to the Geulah, as explained in the Midrash Shir HaShirim Rabbah on the verse, "I sleep (in exile), but my heart is awake."

May Hashem grant you success, so that just as you write in your letter that you are increasing your study of Chassidus—with the intention that this be for yourself—you should also endeavor with all your ability to ensure that this study increases in the shul as well, in a public Talmud Torah. May the manner of study be one of "engraving," the virtue of which is explained in many places; see the Shelah on this parsha, and its explanation in Likutei Torah in our parsha, as well as in Parshas Bechukosai.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2744

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your two letters from 5 Sivan in due time. Regarding what you wrote about the kashrus of the shmurah [matzah] you purchased, and you even enclosed a certificate of kashrus: It is surprising, as it seems you have grasped the entire matter **not at all** according to my intent. I did not speak a word regarding the kashrus of the shmurah, but rather about the matter of hiskashrus, which depends on the manner of one’s emunah in our Nasi, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory.

The story of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, is already well known: when our Alter Rebbe was imprisoned, he said that he had practiced mesiras nefesh in actual deed so as not to be separated from the Baal Shem Tov **in movement**, even for a brief moment, and even only in appearance (see at length in the letter printed in the pamphlet *HaTamim*, Part 2, page 56). And although who is he and where is he who would dare to approach or attain even one-thousandth of the level of the Alter Rebbe, nevertheless, according to what is brought in *Tanya*, Chapter 44, a small edge and a trace of his goodness and light shines upon the totality of the Chassidim and anash.

And one must conclude with what is stated in the letter of the Rebbe, my father-in-law (ibid., end of Chapter 2), that if in matters such as these there must be such dveikus, then regarding the "food of faith" and the "food of healing" and the "night of watching" [the Seder night], which was revealed to each and every one of the sons and daughters of Yisrael in His glory and essence, how much more so!

It is my hope that at least now it is understood to what extent everything you write regarding the kashrus of the shmurah, as well as the proceedings of how the shmurah came into your possession, etc., etc., is completely irrelevant to such a matter, and further elaboration on this is merely superfluous.

With blessings.

## 2756

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, R' Shmuel, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive the news that this coming Shabbos is the Bris Milah of your grandson, the son of your daughter, Chana Etel, may she live. May it be the will of Hashem that his parents merit to bring him into the covenant of Avraham Avinu at a good and auspicious time, and just as they bring him into the covenant, so too may they bring him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to maasim tovim.

It is already known that this is the ruling of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya (who rules in the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who rules in the revealed aspects of Torah), in his pure Shulchan Aruch, second edition, end of section 4, that the mitzvah of milah is the beginning of the entry of the holy neshamah into the Jewish body.

It is also known from the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that as is known, the neshamah is called by five names: nefesh, ru'ach, neshamah, chayah, and yechidah. When one performs the matter of Torah and mitzvos in the world below, in this world—the world of Asiyah—it is likewise accomplished in the ru'ach, neshamah, and chayah in the worlds of Yetzirah, Beriah, and Atzilus. And this all resonates in the yechidah as it exists in the worlds of the Ein Sof above Atzilus. Even if a person does not know the entirety of the matter, nonetheless, the matter takes place in all the worlds, etc. Regarding this it is said, "And His righteousness endures forever"—that he has capital in the higher worlds, and in time he will come to know of this as well (Sichos, 19 Kislev 5693, section 17).

May it be the will of Hashem that you and your wife, may you live, derive from them and from all your descendants, may they live, an abundance of Chassidishe nachas for long, good years.

With blessings of Mazal Tov.

## 2757

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and dedicated to communal needs, R' Avraham, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letters of 21 and 27 Sivan (as well as the previous ones from 30 Nissan, 4, 19, and 24 Iyar, and 5 Sivan, though I believe I have already acknowledged their receipt), regarding the matters of the Reshet and the affairs of the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod—surely you have already received my letters of response to them and have read them. In general, I am astonished that in matters that are simple and clear, there are times when one errs from one extreme to the other, contrary to the approach of Lubavitch throughout all these years. May it be the will of Hashem that, at the very least, from here on out, things will change.

It causes me great distress that, apparently, the seforim sent from here are not being distributed as they should be, and some say that there is no effort being made to distribute them at all. What the end result of such conduct will be is difficult for me to fathom. From time to time, I am reminded of the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that soon the time will come—"days in which you have no pleasure," which refers to the days of Moshiach—*un men vet zich chappen farn kop* (and one will grab one’s head in regret), realizing that there was just now a time when one could have accomplished so much, *un men hot dos durchgelozn aza zman* (and one let such a time slip by). I believe that you were also present at that farbrengen...

I have written to Aguch in Tel Aviv, as I heard that there are manuscripts (and perhaps even the original handwriting) in the possession of the grandchildren of the Rashan, of blessed memory, of Bobruisk, as well as the grandchildren of the Shezaban, may his soul rest in Eden. I requested that if it turns out to be true, and these manuscripts contain matters that have not yet been printed, they should acquire them and send them here. And if it is not possible otherwise, then at least for a period of time...

Since you do not mention anything regarding your health or the health of your family—may they live—I assume that each of you is in good health. Nevertheless, I will await explicit good news.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 2758

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...And in these days of preparation for the *yimei hageulah* of *K’vod Kedushas Moreinu V’Rabbeinu Nasi Doreinu*, it is as was discussed at the *farbrengen* of *Shabbos Mevarchim* the month of Tammuz: When one needs to free someone from a pit of captivity, one first frees the head, and all the limbs connected to the head follow along. So too, in the *kumah sheleimah*, although *basar reisha gufa azil* (the body follows the head), one must nevertheless be strongly connected—and this is through *neileich bederech yesharah asher horanu midrachav venaleich beorchotav netzach selah va’ed* (we shall walk in the straight path that he has taught us, and we shall walk in his ways forever). This brings about the reality that *tzaddik d’itpatar ishtachach bechulehu almin yatir mibachvahi* (a *tzaddik* who has departed is found in all worlds more than during his lifetime)—meaning, also in this *Olam HaMaaseh*, as is explained in *Iggeret HaKodesh* of *Rabeinu HaZaken*, Chapter 27, and its commentary.

With blessings for *nachas chassidishi* from all his children, may they live, to him and his wife, may they live.

## 2,759

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Sivan, in which you write regarding your situation until now, the changes therein, and your current state, which requires rectification in several areas:

It is a well-known ruling of our Sages: "If one says, 'I have labored but not found,' do not believe him; 'I have not labored but I have found,' do not believe him." In your case, the choice is in your hands to walk the straight and good path, both materially and spiritually, through dedication and commitment to the study of the revealed Torah and Chassidus, and the fulfillment of mitzvos. A primary element in this is the avodah of tefillah with hiddur. As for all the matters that distract you, which you mention in your letter, we see tangibly that every person is given the strength to overcome and nullify those things within their own "four cubits" that conceal and obscure their true desire and will—which is to fulfill the will of the Creator.

It is understood that for everything one needs siyata d'shmaya, and one merits this also by keeping the three daily shiurim that are equal for every soul, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: the well-known portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya; giving tzedakah, both spiritually and materially; and being careful regarding tevilas Ezra, etc.

This is especially true since you have merited to study in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, which was founded and is directed by the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and his son, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—who invested and continue to invest their strengths into the Yeshivah, with outstanding success in the Yeshivah and its students.

The conclusion from all the above: divert your mind from the self-questioning thoughts regarding your situation, etc., and study the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus with dedication and commitment. Be strong in your trust in Hashem, that when you labor in all the above, you will find what you seek—and more than that, you will also be successful.

Regarding what you write about experiencing a weakening of your memory, and that sometimes even simple things slip your mind: in general, this is also connected to your aforementioned self-questioning thoughts. When you fulfill the instruction to divert your mind from that self-questioning, these details will also improve. Do not force your memory to study specifically the subject that is causing you strain; when you feel a weakness, switch your study to a different subject, one that your heart desires, and afterwards, try again.

With blessings for success in all the above.

## 2780

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Sivan, in which you write regarding the various changes you have experienced over time until now, and regarding your current situation—which, although improved compared to the past, still requires correction in several points and matters.

You should rejoice in the merit and success of being in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, which was founded and is directed by the Rebbe and my father-in-law, the Rebbe—may the merit of the righteous protect us. They invested their own strengths into it with mesiras nefesh; consequently, anyone who is within it with all their 248 limbs and 365 sinews, both physical and spiritual, is a vessel for receiving their blessings. You will succeed in all that is necessary, according to your ability, to learn, to daven, and to be meticulous in the performance of mitzvos with simcha. For if a little light pushes away much darkness, then how much more so does a great deal of light, and how much more so does the "source of light"—which is Chassidus, its teachings, its guidance, and its customs.

It is well known that the path of fasts, and even self-affliction, is not the path of the Baal Shem Tov, as is explained in many places, including the maamar of 10 Shevat 5713, *Basi L'Gani*. This is especially so according to what is brought in the book *Toldos Maharash*, that the "fast" of a Chossid means delaying, even for a few moments, something that he desires, etc. See also Tanya, Chapter 27 (page 34b). In the aforementioned maamar, it is also explained that it is necessary to maintain one's health, as this diminishes the disturbances of the body.

When you increase all of the above and take action in this direction, the assistance from Above will also increase, so that all of the above will come into actual practice in your daily life.

Regarding what you wrote about "corrections," etc.: increase your engagement with the letters of Torah and the letters of tefillah. Surely, you have committed to memory several chapters of Mishnayos, several chapters of Tanya, and maamarim of Chassidus—among them the maamar *Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken* in *Likutei Torah*, at the end of Parshas Kedoshim.

With blessings for success in Torah, avodah, and gemilus chasadim, which are the three pillars upon which the great world—and the small world, which is man—stand.

## 2781

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your letter dated Thursday, Parshas Korach, in which you describe what you have experienced since arriving in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. Your distress is evident at the end of your letter, where you write about the situation in the place where you served in the rabbinate for many years and have now left. You are already familiar with the response given to Yirmiyahu by Baruch ben Neriah when he sought prophecy at the time of the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash and the exile of Yisrael (for in a spiritual sense, when they were exiled to Edom, the Shechinah went with them, and the Shechinah is also in exile).

It is also well known what the Tzemach Tzedek replied to one of the great Chassidim—a story we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—regarding his request to move to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. The Tzemach Tzedek said: "Reb Hillel, Eretz Yisrael does not lack you; you lack Eretz Yisrael. Make Eretz Yisrael here." Seemingly, the conclusion, "Make Eretz Yisrael here," and its connection to the beginning of the statement, is not understood. The interpretation is that the yearning for Eretz Yisrael must first and foremost be expressed by "making it here"—that is, in one's place of residence—Eretz Yisrael.

I do not wish to dwell on a painful subject, especially since you are already in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and one can find merit in the fact that even before you moved to the Holy Land, you were in Eretz Yisrael, and from there you came to... In any event, may it be the will of Hashem that while you are in Eretz Yisrael, you make your surroundings Eretz Yisrael. This is in accordance with the inner interpretation brought in many places in Chassidic discourse: *Eretz* (land) refers to one who wanted to do the will of its Creator (*ratzah*); *Yisrael* refers to "straight to G-d" (*yashar-el*), "for you have struggled with G-d and with men." An even deeper inner content is that *Yisrael* means "Yisrael is my head" (*li rosh*); see Likutei Torah, Parshas Shelach (48b and onwards).

With blessings for true health for you and your wife, the Rabbanit, and for success in all the above with peace of mind.

P.S.
I am sure you participate in Chassidic farbrengens and also encourage and remind others about this from time to time. May Hashem grant you success.

## 2882

B”H, 3 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Wednesday regarding the rationale for men and women sitting together without a kosher *mechitzah*.

In such a matter, since the *Agudas HaRabbanim* has already published [statements] in the press, and I believe that for some time now there has been something similar from Young Israel and other rabbinical associations, you should obtain clippings of these publications. (You can surely find out where to obtain them from the administration of the *Agudas HaRabbanim*, and perhaps through the esteemed Rabbi Dr. Weiss at Young Israel). Once you publish these newspaper clippings among your congregants—and who can say what will happen when they see the clippings printed in English (perhaps it was in the *Jewish Life* magazine)—it will make the discussion and debate on this matter easier for you.

As for the idea of immediately looking for another position: aside from the scarcity of suitable positions, even if you find one, it is impossible to know in advance whether there won’t be matters there that are even more painful.

Furthermore, regarding your specific situation, one must consider the truth of our Sages’ teaching: "Whoever acts with flattery toward his fellow will eventually fall into his hand." For the fact that in certain matters your outward appearance does not match your inner conviction—which is a form of "flattery," as you want to conform and specifically appear in such a way that outsiders will not recognize that you are a student of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, since this is not because you truly believe in this conduct, but rather as a form of flattery toward the environment—you will eventually fall into their hands. They will argue that since the Rabbi, the *mara d’asra*, wants to conform to his environment, why and on what basis should they not want to conform to their environment in their own affairs? And the argument that this is a matter of *derabbanan* and that there are even those who permit it entirely—to this, the answer is ready: in matters of *maris ayin*, one must consider the observer, not the excuse of the person involved.

I also know the excuse for this, that the vast majority of young rabbis also conduct themselves in this manner. However: a) they, too, have many troubles, etc.; and b) lately, a movement has begun to improve the external appearance as well, even where one might find a "hechsher" for it. And whoever is a pioneer in this, the merit of the many depends upon him.

As is your custom, you do not mention in your letter the status of your *shiurim* in *Nigleh* and *Chassidus*, the diminution of which is also somewhat of an excuse for the aforementioned.

With blessings for the lessening of the *he'elem v'hester* (concealments) that you are experiencing, and for the easing of your *avodah* as a *Chossid*, as a Rabbi, and as a G-d-fearing man.

## 2783

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I am **extremely** distressed by the lack of attention... regarding the education of girls, and by extension, regarding Agudas N'shei U'bnos Chabad as well. For in this generation and in these days, this is not a matter of embellishment or work for others, but a **vital** question concerning the girls and women, and consequently, the men as well... It is distressing that it had to take six years in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) until the results of this lack of attention are already visible. Would that they "emerge" with the results seen thus far, and immediately work with the greatest energy and in the pleasant ways—which are the ways of our Torah, the Torah of life—to improve the situation and rectify it as much as possible. May Hashem grant them success to bring good tidings soon.

With blessings.

## 2784
