## 2785

B.H., 4 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal needs, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Nissan, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, in which you raise a question regarding what is written in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Shelach* (42b), which states: "For a *niddah* and a *zavah*, their purification is in *mayim chayim* (living waters)." You ask for the source of this, noting that it is the opinion of the *poskim*, both early and late, that a *niddah* does not require *mayim chayim*.

It should be understood that *Likutei Torah* is not a book of *piskei dinim* (halachic rulings). Furthermore, it is understood that according to the *nistar* (the hidden dimension) of Torah, one must explain not only the opinion that is accepted as *halacha*, but also other opinions, for "these and those are the words of the Living G-d."

- See, for example: *Likutei Torah, Nitzavim* 45, bottom of column a: "The shofar of Rosh Hashanah is of a wild goat, straight." And it is obvious that there is no difficulty from *Derech Mitzvosecha*, end of *Mitzvas Aseh*, to discuss the back-and-forth of the debate. -

Regarding the statement that a *niddah* is purified in *mayim chayim*—this is the position of the *Tikkunei Zohar* at its end (end of *Tikkunei HaZohar*): "Like a *niddah*, etc., to purify her with the waters of Torah, **living waters** that do not cease."

By the way: Regarding what you noted in the book *Taharas Mayim* (p. 46) concerning the opinions that hold a *zavah* requires *mayim chayim*, one should add to them the opinion of Rav Nachshon (and see *Otzar HaGeonim* to *Shabbos* 64) and the *Zohar*, Vol. III, 97b (in addition to the *Tikkunei Zohar*, which arrives at this *kal v'chomer* from a *niddah*).

In *Sheilos U’Teshuvos Shem Shimon* by Rabbi Shimon Pollak—First Edition, *Yoreh Deah*, Section 19—he points out from the aforementioned *Tikkunei Zohar* that it holds a *zavah* requires *mayim chayim* (via a *kal v'chomer* from a *niddah*). It is surprising that he did not also cite the aforementioned *Zohar*, Vol. III. Perhaps it could be said that in the *Zohar*, Vol. III, the *Ramak* explains (as cited in *Or HaChama* there) that *mayim chayim* are required because she counts seven weeks and not seven days, unlike a regular *zavah*. However, regarding the *Tikkunei Zohar*, this cannot be said.

With respect and blessing.

#### ***2785***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 22, p. 305, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

**Moreinu HaRav Nissan:** Telushkin. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 7, 1888, and in the references in the footnotes there.

**Regarding what is written in *Likutei Torah*:** See also *He'aros V'Tziyunim* to *Likutei Torah* there.

## 2785

B"H, 4 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs,
Rabbi Y.D. [Moskowitz] shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 1 Korach, along with the pamphlet regarding the possibility and necessity of establishing an Eiruv in Manhattan.

There is already a pamphlet titled "Proposal for the Establishment of an Eiruv" by the esteemed Rabbi Zvi Eisenstadt shlita, which is detailed and includes references to the matters you wrote about, as well as **additions** to them.

It is surprising that in all the halachic analysis in the pamphlet you sent me, you did not mention the issue of the seeds [or grains] found in the city, which, according to many Rishonim and Acharonim, invalidate the partitions. Furthermore, you did not touch upon the fact that part of Manhattan is surrounded by the sea, and even the part called the "river" is a matter of great doubt as to whether it qualifies as a river according to Halacha. I will not elaborate here; see the aforementioned pamphlet by Rabbi Eisenstadt. See also Mikvaos, Chapter 5, Mishnah 4; Makkos 4a, and elsewhere. See also Responsa Tzafnas Paneach by the Gaon of Rogatchov, Siman 58-59, regarding the definition of a river according to law. Additionally, as explained in that pamphlet, there are several places that were not enclosed, in addition to the issue that parts of the partitions were not constructed for residential purposes.

Regarding your note on the dispute among the Rishonim as to whether there must be six hundred thousand people traversing [the area], this is how Rabbeinu HaZaken ruled in his Shulchan Aruch, Siman 345, Seif 11. See also Responsa Beis Av, Part 2, Siman 5, where he lists thirty opinions among the Rishonim who hold this view.

Regarding your comment on the words of the Rav of Buchach—that there is no proof that non-Jews are not included in the count of six hundred thousand, and you are seeking proofs for this—in many places among the Acharonim, it is implied that non-Jews are indeed included in the count of six hundred thousand.

The basis for this can be explained by the fact that the commandment of Shabbos was given at Marah (see Tosafos, s.v. *Atchumin*, Shabbos 87b), at which time they were still under the laws of Bnei Noach (as is known to be the opinion of most Rishonim on this). Furthermore, even afterwards, at the Giving of the Torah, the laws of Shabbos were defined **"as He commanded you"** (at Marah).

Regarding the matter of the mitzvah to establish an Eiruv, in addition to what you mention in your letter, see Shita Mekubetzes to Beitzah 16b; Responsa HaRosh, Klal 21; Tashbetz, Part 2, Siman 37; Chasam Sofer, Orach Chaim, Siman 99; and Responsa Beis Av, Part 2, Siman 1.

With blessing.

## 2787

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, in which you ask for the interpretation of the event where you and your friend stood for an examination to receive a position as a Rabbi, and your friend succeeded while you did not, and that you were told you could be examined again at the end of the month of Marcheshvan.

Indeed, none of us knows with certainty the intent of Divine Providence. However, there is reason to suggest that since: a) all matters of holiness, regardless of how good the current situation may be, always have room to be improved and enhanced further, for holiness is *Ein Sof*; and b) since in the study of Torah there must be "fear of Hashem is His treasure," and likewise in the fulfillment of *mitzvos*—as the language of our Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya* (who is the authority in the hidden dimensions of Torah) and the author of the *Shulchan Aruch* (who is the authority in the revealed dimensions of Torah), in his holy *Tanya*, beginning of Chapter 41, states that the beginning, the essence, and the root of *avodah* is *yirah*—especially for one who wishes to be a Rabbi and leader of a holy community, this is an indication that he must dedicate special attention to further increasing the level of *yiras shamayim*. As is explained in the holy *Tanya*, there are many levels to this, explained thoroughly. See also on this matter in the holy *Zohar*, Part I, 13, end of side b.

And with this, it is also understood why they postponed the examinations until after the month of Tishrei, which is the month of *yirah*. The path that leads to fear of Hashem is explained in the *Tanya* and in the teachings of Chassidus in general in many places, and you will certainly discuss this with the Rav and Chossid, etc., etc... And may Hashem grant you success and bring you good tidings in all the above.

With blessings.

## 2890

B"H, 6 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn

To the Administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok
Lubavitch in the Holy Land, may they live,
Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of the letters from the 13th and 15th of Sivan—two letters—and from the 28th—two letters. In the meantime, you have surely received my response to your previous letter, which also contains answers to several of the questions in your aforementioned letters. It appears that my telegram regarding Cholon did not arrive, which is very surprising (it was sent to the address of Rabbi Chanzin, shlita).

2) The proposal to organize intensive courses for teacher training and to utilize the vacation days for this is very correct, even without the concern that next year they will strictly demand certification from every single teacher. You are surely working on this with the greatest energy. It might be worthwhile that even those who are already certified participate in at least part of the courses in order to review what they have learned, for a beis medrash cannot exist without innovation. Regarding the rationale for the summer camp (kaitana), this request was received from the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok school in Yafo, and they suggest holding it in the Kfar. In any case, this is also a correct proposal, and perhaps even a necessary one.

3) I do not know the expenses involved in the above, but there is certainly room to request special assistance from the appropriate offices, and for the rest, you must endeavor to find [funding]. After all, there is already a significant deficit in the Reshet, and the liras that will be added for the two aforementioned expenses will not change the situation. Surely anash will endeavor to provide the means for this.

4) In continuation of this, and according to my policy that all matters of the schools must be conducted by the General Administration, I am answering the school in Yafo that the partial assistance they requested will be provided to them by their applying to the General Administration, and primarily to provide it to them as soon as possible and to encourage and strengthen them to conduct the summer camp.

5) Since the summer camp will be in Kfar Chabad, there may be room for students from other schools to be hosted there as well—meaning not only from Yafo, but also from other Oholei Yosef Yitzchok schools. It is possible that through this, it will be easier to obtain assistance from the various offices, since by concentrating all the students in one place, expenses will be reduced, and what is even more important, the supervision will be better.

6) Regarding the proposal to establish Oholei Yosef Yitzchok schools in the most distant places, such as the Negev, etc.: given the current situation in the General Administration, I do not see how they could supervise them. There is only room to think about such proposals if people are found on-site who can be trusted one hundred percent.

7) The idea that every person suitable for it should teach a class in addition to their work in the General Administration of the Reshet is very correct. This is not only because of the lack of funds, but also for spiritual reasons, including bringing the teachers closer to the administration by having them recognize that they, too, are participating in their work through these activities.

8) It goes without saying that one must not concede on the principle that the selection of teachers for the Reshet must be done exclusively by the administration, and not by anyone from the outside. This was one of the **first** conditions during the negotiations regarding the entry into the state religious education system (although even in this, one should not act through conflict; experience has already shown that through pleasant ways one accomplishes much more and more easily)...

9) It is my hope that even though the 12th and 13th of Tammuz are vacation days, you will nevertheless utilize these days to tell the students about the significance of the holiday in some way.

10) It would be appropriate for the people suitable for this to meet with Mr. Shazar, shlita, since he was the mediator and also knows about the promise regarding the appointment of teachers, and he still has influence now, and also on...

Shlita.

With a blessing for success in your holy work, and especially in these days of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in whose name the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok schools were founded, and in whose spirit they must be conducted and expanded. I await good news.

## 2792

The analogy is understood.

I look forward to detailed letters, and I conclude with a blessing for success in all the above.

## 2,793

## 2795

B”H, 7 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs and possesses noble character traits, a scion of noble ancestors, etc., R’ Sh.Z. (may he live),

Peace and blessing!

I hope that your return trip was pleasant and successful. As is the way of every person upon returning home from a long and active journey—when one summarizes the events and actions that occurred during their travels—I hope that you are satisfied with the summary of your trip in general, and your visit to New York in particular. And most importantly, as is the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: this spiritual satisfaction is not of the type that leads to "resting on one's laurels." On the contrary, it awakens the desire and appetite for further activities with even greater courage and energy, by way of a *kal v’chomer*: "If, with the effort invested until now—which was tied to a beginning, and it is known that 'all beginnings are difficult'—I nevertheless succeeded, thank G-d, then how much more so, if I increase my efforts, will I surely succeed with even greater, manifold success..."

It is surely unnecessary to remind you once again regarding assistance for all our matters, the matters of Chabad, which are in truth the matters of all Israel, and which are close to your spirit in any case. I have written only to fulfill the teaching of our Sages, "One only encourages the already diligent." This is especially true in these coming days, days of gathering and a *sha'as ratzon* (time of favor) in honor of the *Chag HaGeulah* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—12-13 Tammuz—which are especially auspicious for spiritual awakening and for drawing down blessing and success from the *Baal HaSimcha*, may his merit protect us.

I wish you much success in this in advance.

With respect and blessing, and looking forward to hearing good news.

## 2,796

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you and your family through your wife, Mrs. [Name]—may she live and be well. Most importantly, I was pleased to hear that you have merited that your children are studying the Torah of Hashem, which is called the Torah of Life and brings content and vitality into daily life, and that your children are studying with enthusiasm. If in all times parents were required to ensure that their children study the Torah of Hashem, then in our times—and especially in the United States—parents must do so to an even greater degree and with even more hitlahavus.

It is also self-understood that since Hashem Yisbarach leads the world and provides for Jews and all people in general what they need—for He, blessed be He, is the sole Provider and Sustainer of all—it cannot be that conducting oneself according to the will of the Creator, such as ensuring children study Torah, would be an obstacle to parnassah. On the contrary: when one strengthens oneself and acts according to the will of the Creator, even if it seems to be connected with difficulties, one merits the fulfillment of the promise of Hashem: "If you walk in My statutes" (Rashi explains that this means you should be toiling in Torah—that Torah study comes through hard work), "then the land will give its produce," etc.—meaning that Hakadosh Baruch Hu provides parnassah with great abundance.

I am certain that these lines will be sufficient to instill in you an increase in your bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach and an increase in your desire to educate your children and strengthen them in their Torah study. May Hashem Yisbarach help that this should be with good health and good parnassah.

With blessings,

## 2997

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Thursday, Parshas Beha'aloscha, in which you write the main points of your life history, what you have experienced, and your current situation.

It is already known that the instruction of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is that one who serves Hashem as is proper must not err regarding his own essence—neither to the right nor to the left. That is to say, one should not belittle oneself more than is appropriate, and certainly one should not elevate oneself more than is appropriate. Consequently, what you write—that you see that you do not belong at all to the "service of the heart"—is clearly an assumption that is **utterly** incorrect. Every single one of the children of Israel belongs to this, since the holy Torah demands it of everyone, and the Holy One, blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures. However, even regarding this, the ruling of our Sages applies: "If one says, 'I have not labored and yet I have found,' do not believe him." On the contrary, this applies even more to [avodah] than to the study of Torah, as is understood from what is written in the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*—that in these days, the primary opposition of the *sitra achra* is directed toward the matter of *tefillah*, even more so than toward the matter of Torah, as is explained there. I was pleased by what you wrote, that you influence your peers and, in general, those you meet, to bring them closer to *avodah* in practice and to *yiras shamayim*. The merit of this matter is great, and it will surely influence for you an addition of blessing and success in all that you need, both materially and spiritually.

Regarding what you wrote about the respectable offers being presented to you... in my opinion, you should also take interest in other offers. In time, you will see and discern, and consequently, your second question—what you should do after the wedding and how to settle down—there is still time to discuss this. After all, the matter of marriage is an eternal thing, and one should not rush into it or snatch the first offer.

Regarding what you wrote about the spiritual state of your parents, may they live and be well, you should endeavor to have them recognized in their place of residence by G-d-fearing people—and how much better if they are *anash*—and ask those G-d-fearing individuals to look for an opportunity to influence your parents and bring them closer to our Father in Heaven.

Surely you are aware of the customs for a birthday: receiving an *aliyah* to the Torah, giving *tzedakah* before *Shacharis* and *Mincha* (if the birthday falls on Shabbos, then on the day before), and adding a *shiur* in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of *Chassidus*. May Hashem grant that this year be a year of success for you in the study of *nigleh* and *Chassidus*, and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*.

With blessings for success in all of the above.

**M. Schneerson**

***

**Customs for a birthday:** See also above, letter 2770, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 2798

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, occupied with communal needs and the needs of the community,
Rabbi Sh. Y. [Shlomo Yosef Zevin]

Shalom u’Bracha!

I have received your letter from the beginning of the month of Tammuz, and I thank you. Regarding what you wrote—that my interpretation of "Eileh HaMishpatim" is not accepted—on the contrary, the other interpretations of such matters serve as proof and evidence for my own. It is understood that even though it is stated in Sanhedrin 19a, "An incident occurred involving the slave of Yannai... at that moment they said...", this does not constitute proof according to logic against the *binyan av* (foundational principle) that I am deriving, as I have explained at length in the discussion regarding my interpretation.

I was pleased to hear that you were at the opening of the Agudas Yisrael conference. It is a pity that you are not present at the other main sessions as well. My hope is that if they propose you as a member of their Council of Torah Sages, you will agree to it. After all, when any individual participates in a party, he does not necessarily agree with every detail and action of that party, for their opinions are not identical. Consequently, in a case like this, it should not be a contradiction to join the Council.

Mazal Tov on the appearance of your book, *HaMoadim B'Halacha*, in a new edition. I would certainly be happy to hear that you are compiling a collection of printed Chassidic sichos, the sayings of our Rebbes, etc., with the sources indicated. This is something that has needed to be published for a long time, and in this area, there are fewer workers than in other fields. It is closer to the category of a *mitzvah* that cannot be performed by others. I trust that the *Talmudic Encyclopedia* is also progressing as it should, and may Hashem be his help.

As we approach the days of redemption—the redemption of the leader of the Jewish people, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—may it be the will of the Almighty that "the body follows the head," and may we merit, speedily in our days, the true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu. Surely these days will be marked by *hisorerus* and appropriate resolutions.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Since you do not mention anything regarding your health, I assume everything is peaceful and in order. Enclosed is the continuation of the *Reshimas HaMaasar* (Prison Diary) which was published in connection with the upcoming days of *Chag HaGeulah*, 12-13 Tammuz.

## 2798*

*[Beginning of Tammuz 5714]*

*[To the Great Assembly of Agudas Yisrael]*

"In response to your letter: In our generation, where those who 'put darkness for light and light for darkness' are breaking forth, and who use light to increase the darkness—where the falsifiers of the values of our holy Torah have multiplied—may it be the will of Hashem that your assembly succeeds in emphasizing the distinction and the opposition between compromise and truth, and in raising the horn of the elder Israel through an absolute demonstration that only through the Torah, and within the Torah, is the existence of the Jewish people. And may we merit the true Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu."

With respect.

## 2,799

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 1 Tammuz, in which you write that your entire family and your wife’s family are in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established), and that your parents also wish to move there and are suggesting that you do the same, and that your wife (may she live and be well) also desires this.

You must ensure that you will be able to settle upon your arrival in the Holy Land in an environment of people who are G-d-fearing, who study His Torah and fulfill His mitzvos. If you are certain of this, you should take upon yourself (naturally, without a vow) an increase in your study of Nigleh and Chassidus, as well as an increase in the performance of mitzvos with hiddur. This will serve as preparation for your move to the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are at all times, from the beginning of the year until the end of the year. May it be His will that you succeed in all of this and be able to share good news.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2800

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in the needs of the community,
Rabbi Shmuel Abba, may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your two letters dated the 4th of Tammuz, in which you write regarding the antique Sefer Torah found in the large beis medrash where you daven. You note that during the Torah reading of Parshas Beha'aloscha, it was observed that the inverted *nuns* between the sections are missing. Instead, the *nun* of *binso'a* and the **second** *nun* of *kemit'onenim* are decorated with dots. Furthermore, there is an unusually large number of *osiyos rabrasin* (large letters) in this Sefer Torah—it is said that the entire aleph-beis in large letters is present therein—and you ask for my opinion on this matter.

Regarding the opinion that the dotted *nun* should be the second *nun* of *kemit'onenim*, I have not yet found this anywhere (the various opinions are collected in the sefer *Meir Einei Sofrim*, siman 14; see also *Mishnas Avraham*, siman 24).

As for what you wrote in your letter that this is according to the Maharshal: the Maharshal—as cited in the aforementioned *Meir Einei Sofrim*—refers only to the first *nun* of *kemit'onenim*, not the second. Since these must be corrected, they should be corrected as they ought to be written *lechatchilah*—that is, by placing the inverted *nuns* in the space between the sections, while the other *nuns* should be written in their standard form, according to our current custom. Furthermore, since other deviations were found in this Sefer Torah, such as the aforementioned *osiyos rabrasin*, one should, in accordance with what is written in *Shaarei Ephraim* (Shaar 5, se'if 18), check for other errors, as the custom of the scribes has been altered.

I will read the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed in your letter at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Enclosed is the continuation of the *maamar* published for the *Chag HaGeulah*, 12-13 Tammuz, which is approaching. During these auspicious days—the days of the liberation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the head of the Jewish people—may Hashem grant that each and every one of us follows the principle that "the body follows the head." May the obstacles to the work of spreading Yiddishkeit in general, and to the strengthening and expansion of the matters and institutions for which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, labored and toiled in particular, be diminished and nullified from here on, and may we walk in his paths, *netzach selah va'ed*.

With blessing.

## 2811

B.H., 11 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Tammuz with the two versions of the tombstone inscription: you may combine the titles from both versions. However, in my opinion, it is more correct and common for the inscription to be written not in the first person, but in the third person; consequently, the words "our father," etc., "our glory," should be omitted. The versions are returned herewith.

It is surprising that, as is your custom, you again make no mention of your activities in your current location regarding matters of Yiddishkeit and Chassidus in particular. Although you have become accustomed to this, and I have consequently become accustomed to it as well, this does not rectify the matter. It has been a long time since the time arrived when, wherever you go, you should remember that you studied in the Yeshiva of Tomchei Temimim of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Consequently, your impression must be evident—not only on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur and the like, and not only when you are within your own private four cubits, but at all times and in every place you go, and with influence upon your surroundings as well. When one truly wants to accomplish the above, one finds the means and the ways; all excuses in this regard come from the "side of the opposite," as is understood.

With blessings for a healthy and happy summer, both materially and spiritually, for you and for all your household members, may they live.

## 2802

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in communal affairs,
Rabbi Yissachar Dov, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter from Erev Shabbos, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed within, which I will read at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote about the conduct during the vacation period, where they grant approximately two months of freedom during which the students return to their parents' homes: In general, the vacation time should be shortened, as is known from our Sages, of blessed memory: "[If] you abandon Me for one day, I will abandon you for two days." However, since they have already been accustomed to the aforementioned schedule for several years—as is apparent from your letter—one must act pleasantly and diplomatically. Nevertheless, my hope is that for a significant portion of the students, you will be able to effect this change, so that at the very least, the vacation time will be shortened. Perhaps it is possible to arrange that they do not all leave at once; consequently, the students who are on vacation will always be in the company of those who remain as permanent students. In accordance with this, the manner and timing of the examinations should be arranged. It is certainly not far-fetched to also cancel the vacation time for the *Beis Rivkah* students in the middle of the summer, and it is possible to schedule the vacation time during the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* or similar periods, when in any case they do not study as they should. During the summer days, one should only adjust the study schedule to suit the type of students—that is, whether to switch to lighter, more engaging studies, or also to shorten the time. Regarding matters such as these, one must decide on the spot, and you should certainly consult with *anash* who know the situation there, for "victory is found in the multitude of counselors."

And approaching the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz—the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the head of Israel—may it be the will of Hashem that "the body follows the head," such that Hashem will grant success to each and every one of the Chassidim who are *mekushar* to him, or who are connected to him, to succeed in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in general, and in the dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus in particular, with proper health, ample livelihood, and peace of mind.

With blessing.

## 2804

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5714

Greetings and Blessings!

I hope that you are strengthening yourself in your path in life, a life according to the Torah—the Torah of life—as it is explained in the teachings of Chassidus, which is called the "Tree of Life." Just as in physical life we see that every birth, growth, and development is connected with labor, difficulties, and the removal of concealments and hiddenness, my hope is strong that your ascent on the path leading to "Beis-El" will not be deterred by the difficulties in your way, and that you will succeed in this with extraordinary success. Certainly, from time to time, your hiskashrus to this path—which is, in truth, the path of every Jewish person—will strengthen; it is only that not everyone merits to find it, because not everyone merits that the inner dimension of their soul and heart be revealed in all its beauty and splendor, and influence their day-to-day life.

## 2515

B"H, 12 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and diligent in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchok, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter has been received.

During these auspicious days—the days of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the leader of Israel—may Hashem grant success to each and every one of us, that we may follow the principle that "the body follows the head."

May it be that from here on, the obstacles in the work of spreading Yiddishkeit in general, and in maintaining and expanding the matters and institutions for which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, labored and toiled in particular, will be diminished and nullified, and may we walk in his paths, as he has paved for us.

With blessings.

a) Regarding what you wrote—that perhaps this does not have the status of *mei raglayim* (urine) because it is taken via a catheter from the bladder, and consequently: 1) it does not remain in the bladder as is natural, and perhaps its quality has not yet been finalized; 2) it does not exit through the organ (for it is obvious that the law would be the same even if the catheter went **directly** from the bladder to the outside)—one can bring support for this from the law of *ha-hofchi* (the one who reverses) in *Machshirin* (Chapter 4, Mishnah 7), even though they emerge clean.

See there.

And let it be known that even without the above, there is room to permit it, as noted in my previous letter regarding the *Pri Megadim*, etc.

It is surprising that you write that it was simple for them to rule it forbidden. After writing my letter, I found in the *Sefer Melamed Leho'il*—a responsa by Rabbi Hoffmann of Berlin—in *Orach Chaim* 67, that he permits it as stated above, although he does not address my first reasoning at all, as he does not mention it.

b) The explanation of the statement in *Zohar* Vol. I (4a), "Who among you, etc."—in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 10—is based on the precision of the word *mahapchan* (reverses them), meaning that the evil itself is transformed, etc., and this is *is'hapcha* (transformation).

The explanation of the negation in that statement, "who does not reverse, etc."—in *Likutei Torah*, *Chukas* (61d)—is based on the commentary of the *Remaz* there (as noted in *Likutei Torah* there), that it is the sweetening of the *kellipah nogah*, etc., through Torah and mitzvos, etc., which is relevant and **essential** for every person, as is understood. See also *Torah Or*, *Miketz* 42a, and in the *drushim* in *Sefer Derech Mitzvotecha*, **Vol. II**, for *Shemos*, *Parshas Mishpatim*.

## 2,559

B"H, 12 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the venerable Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Avraham Yaakov, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Your letter of 15 Sivan has been received.

In these auspicious days—the days of the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the head of Israel:

May Hashem grant success to each and every one of us, that we may follow the head, for the body follows the head.

May it be that from here on, the obstacles to the work of spreading Yiddishkeit in general, and to the support and expansion of the matters and institutions for which my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, labored and toiled in particular, will diminish and be nullified, and may we walk in his paths, may his merit protect us.

With blessing.

P.S.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the content of the prohibition "Do not bear false witness against your neighbor," which you discuss in your book, section 4 and 5, and regarding what you found in the Ramban on the Torah, Parshas Devarim 5:12, that this applies even when one does not obligate [the neighbor] in anything in Beis Din, and [this is] unlike the difficulty raised against him in Minchas Chinuch, Mitzvah 37.

Behold, this is proven even more strongly in the Chizkuni there, that even though in every place where it is said "witness," it means two—yet even with one witness, this prohibition exists. Now, the Ramban on the Torah and likewise the Chizkuni are commentators and not codifiers, but this opinion is implied in Teshuvos Geonim Kadmonim, section 3 (and similarly in Shu"t Shaarei Tzedek, Gate 7, section 48; Shu"t HaRi Ibn Migash, section 166), and not like the Sefer Yereim, section 640; Sefer Mitzvos Gadol (Semag), Negative Commandments 216; Sefer Mitzvos Katan (Semak), section 235 (and this is also implied in Milchemos of the Ramban, end of Sanhedrin—and not like his commentary on the Torah); Tumim, Klalei Miggo, end of section 52—and as **he elaborated** on all this in the commentary of the Ri"f Perla to the Sefer HaMitzvos of the Rasag, Negative Commandment 34. See there. It is also worth noting the Yerushalmi, Sanhedrin, at its end—cited in the aforementioned commentary—which implies there that "Do not bear false witness against your neighbor" also applies to the Holy One, Blessed be He.

According to my explanation regarding the matter of *yoma d'shuta* (the day of conversation), the expression **in the Gemara** "ha'idna" (nowadays)—meaning the time of the Amoraim—is also precise.

**R' Avraham Yaakov:** Neimark. Additional letters to him—above 2,889, and in the references in the notes there.

**According to my explanation:** Above, there.

## 2807

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 7 Tammuz, in which you write that you have become engaged to [the young woman]—may she live and be well. It is my prayer to Hashem that this be in a good and auspicious hour, for the building of an everlasting edifice upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus.

Regarding your question asking for my opinion concerning the proposal that after the wedding—in a good and auspicious hour—you reside in a room you have in a courtyard, where the kitchen is located outside and far from your room: this is not in keeping with the ways of *tzniyus* for a daughter of Israel—may she live and be well.

In matters such as these, and in accordance with the verse, "The entire glory of the king's daughter is within," one must take her opinion into account and seek out a suitable apartment. The One who provides for all other expenses will surely provide for this as well, since this is to fulfill His will regarding the matter of *tzniyus*, and all the more so when it concerns the daughters of Israel.

You should certainly establish a *shiur* in the study of Chassidus—the inner dimension of Torah, which is called in the holy Zohar the "soul of the Torah"—for then an added vitality will also be infused into your study of the *nigleh* (revealed) aspect of Torah. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings of *mazal tov*.

## 2808

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Shlomo Schneur Zalman, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 10 Tammuz, along with the list of names that I read at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on the auspicious day of 12 Tammuz—the day of his birth and the beginning of his redemption, which is also our redemption, for the body follows the head.

Regarding what you wrote about expanding the work of the N’shei U’Bnos Chabad organization by opening another branch in your city, near where they live: This should only be done if it does not diminish the activities of the existing N’shei U’Bnos Chabad branch. Even then, the meetings should be held on different days so that it does not serve as even a pretext [for friction]. One must be extremely careful about this, in accordance with the teaching, "The beginning of strife is like letting out water." It is my hope that you will ensure this (guarantee it), for if so, it is certainly worthwhile to increase the number of branches, as this will also increase the number of participants. Perhaps it would be diplomatically advisable to provide a special branch for young women and a separate one for those who are already in their mature years, etc., since sitting together with older women sometimes discourages the younger ones from attending the meetings. It is understood that this must be done diplomatically, without any friction whatsoever, and the wise will understand.

Regarding what you wrote about distributing *pushkes*: Since your letter was received on the auspicious day of 12 Tammuz—at which time a collection is made for the institutions of *Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch*—then in addition to the *pushke* for *Kolel Chabad*, for which you are surely already making efforts, you should also distribute *pushkes* for the aforementioned institutions. May Hashem grant you success.

If you do not have *pushkes* ready, it is understood that you can take any *pushke* available and affix a label with the name of the aforementioned institutions, in which case the issue of "not changing from one charity to another" does not apply.

With blessings for success, awaiting good news.

*[Letter from the Secretariat regarding the above]*

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash, in every place:
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and blessing!

At the *farbrengen* of 12-13 Tammuz this year, the Rebbe *shlita* explained, among other things, how important it is on this day—the birthday and *Chag HaGeulah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—that everyone who is connected to the *Baal HaSimcha* and wishes to strengthen that connection can achieve this by bringing *nachas ruach* to the *Baal HaSimcha* through a concrete action.

Therefore, at the *farbrengen*, the Rebbe *shlita* proposed maintaining the custom established on this day: to participate with a special contribution for the benefit of the educational institutions that bear the name of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the *yeshivos*, *talmud-torahs*, etc., in Eretz Yisrael, Africa, and elsewhere, which bear the name "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch."

Naturally, all those present at the *farbrengen* immediately carried out the Rebbe’s proposal, each person submitting their contribution in a sealed envelope for this special 12 Tammuz collection.

In order to give the opportunity to those who could not be present to also have the merit of participating in this custom, we feel it is our duty to inform you of this.

Although ideally, the Rebbe *shlita* noted, it would be better for the sake of the cause if everyone sent in their commitment within eight days—from the birthday until the day of the *bris*, i.e., until 19 Tammuz—those who did not have the opportunity to do so can still do it later, though at the very least, the sooner the better.

We hope that all those who receive this letter will not only merit this for themselves but will also encourage others to maintain and strengthen their connection to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and through this, draw down upon themselves and their households the Divine blessings and influences in all that is needed, with children, life, and ample sustenance, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing,

**The Secretariat of the Rebbe**
**shlita**

Please note the aforementioned contribution as "12 Tammuz."

## 2809

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Sivan: I was astonished by the content of your letter, which is long for the circumstances. With every page I read, my bewilderment grew, for you surely believe in Hashem, and consequently, you know that Torah and mitzvos are the channels and vessels for receiving Hashem’s blessing in all that a person and his family—may they live—require. When the Creator of the world has granted you success and placed you in a beautiful position where your material livelihood is also provided through engagement in chinuch al taharas hakodesh—that is, drawing the hearts of Jewish boys and girls closer—you should be thanking Him for this every single day. Yet, instead of this, you view the entire matter as if you are doing a favor... as if this is their private affair, or as if the students are their own children and their sole responsibility. Consequently, you feel that if, and only if, your salary is provided on time and in full (and you do not wish to know from where or how—as if that makes any difference to you), then, in your great kindness, you will deign to grant their request and teach the students.

Regarding what you wrote about friction among the board members—whether it exists or not, it is entirely irrelevant to the above. Since drawing your students closer to our Father in Heaven until now is **your merit and your success**, both materially and spiritually, as well as the success of your family—may they live—if you were not in need of a livelihood, it would not even be clear who should be paying whom: whether you should be paying the administration for the opportunity they provide you to participate in an institution named after my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, which prepares the way for the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu by increasing light in the world through the breath of the mouths of school children, or whether they should be paying you. It seems that if you were not in need of a livelihood, it is doubtful you would be engaged in this work at all. Thus, the Masevav HaSibos (the Cause of all causes) has orchestrated that you provide your time and energy, and they serve as the intermediaries between the Holy One, Blessed be He—who feeds and sustains all—and you and your family. And I still do not know if you would find better intermediaries, more G-d-fearing and more devoted to the word of Hashem, etc.

It is already known how my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, interpreted the verse, "Relief and deliverance will arise for the Jews from another place, but you and your father's house will perish"—that is, the merit of this mitzvah will be lost to you. So too in the present case: I am certain regarding my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that his institutions will succeed and develop, and the children will continue to receive a chareidi education. The only question is whether the merit will be yours, or whether you have not yet merited this, and Hashem will provide in your stead a person who is good in His eyes to merit the salvation of the souls of the Jewish people and to connect to the "Tree of Life," to fulfill, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today."

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2510

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn

To the Administration of the Vocational School in Kfar Chabad
May Hashem preserve them and keep them alive

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 3 Tammuz. Regarding what you wrote concerning secular studies: the point here is that it is not the role of Chabad to establish schools for secular studies, not even as a secondary subject. The exception to this (and this is only under duress) is along the lines of what is done in the United States, with the knowledge of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Until the age at which mandatory government education applies, they learn the minimum of secular studies required by law, because without this, the *chedarim* and lower grades could not exist. This serves as a precedent for the *Reshet* schools, the *Talmud Torah* of the village, *Beis Rivkah*, etc. This is not the case, however, regarding a vocational school, and generally regarding classes that have already passed the age of mandatory education. If there are parents, or a movement among some people close to Chabad, who want them to learn secular studies as well, this is a change that must not be agreed to.

It is understood that this applies to secular studies in general. However, that which serves as a supplement to the trade being learned in the vocational school is not a separate study, but rather an extension of the vocational training.

The same applies regarding the curriculum of the vocational school; it does not matter what anyone calls it—a "high school"—because what I discussed here with Rabbi Young is the establishment of a vocational school, not a high school for secular studies, or even for secular and holy studies combined. From this, it is understood that there is room to learn matters pertaining to the work, as you write in your letter, but there is no place in this school for learning subjects so that the students can receive a high school diploma or the like.

Certainly, even in this, one must begin with a peaceful opening and in pleasant ways, even though one cannot compromise on the matter.

2) I was pleased by what you wrote, that holy studies and *davening* occupy much more time than the study of the work and what pertains to it, and surely you will maintain this...

It is surely unnecessary to awaken you once again to ensure that the vocational school does not become a place of escape from the *Tomchei Temimim* Yeshiva in Lod, and furthermore, that in general, admission there should be after a period of study in the *Tomchei Temimim* Yeshiva in Lod, and only in exceptional cases should other students be accepted...

With blessings for success in your holy work.

#### ***2510***

**Much more time:** See above, letter 2629.

**Should not become a place of escape:** See also above, 2660, and the references in the notes there.

## 2,811

2,811

B”H, 15 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter from Friday, Parshas Chukas, in which you share the good news that your son, Yosef, may he live, has entered into the covenant of the mitzvos, and that he also delivered a discourse on the holy Torah regarding the themes of the day and from the holy Zohar. May it be the will of Hashem that from being thirteen for the mitzvos, he should reach fifteen for Gemara, and so on, in accordance with the ruling of our holy Torah, and may you and your wife, may you live, derive much nachas from him and from all your children.

It is somewhat surprising that you do not mention in your letter whether the Bar Mitzvah included in his discourse any words of Chassidus, even though you are surely aware of what is written in the letter of the holy Baal Shem Tov, that on Rosh Hashanah 5707 he ascended to the chamber of Moshiach and asked, "When will the Master come?" and Moshiach Tzidkeinu replied, "When your wellsprings spread outward"—which refers to the teachings of Chassidus, as explained at length in the sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on Simchas Torah 5690.

With blessings to hear good news regarding all the above, and with best wishes for a Mazal Tov.

## 2,812

2,812

B”H, 15 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Tammuz, in which you write that the plan to settle in... has not materialized for the time being, and you ask for my opinion regarding how to proceed and how to seek a suitable position.

Surely you are aware of the organizations through which one seeks respectable rabbinical or educational positions, such as the Agudas HaRabbonim, Torah Umesorah, and the like. You surely have acquaintances among the members of these organizations who could expedite your request in this matter. However, on the other hand—and I believe I mentioned this to you when you were here—you should endeavor to improve the situation where you are now. Regarding the fact that the situation there has deteriorated in terms of Yiddishkeit over time, it is well known that in times of war, when the battle intensifies, the advice is not to flee to a place of rest; rather, on the contrary, one must increase one’s courage in the place where one is stationed, in accordance with the situation that has deteriorated. The analogy is understood.

May Hashem guide you on the path that is straight and good for you, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2,813

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of 4 Tammuz, in which you write that you are studying in... and that there are those who hinder you, claiming that you need to help support the household.

It is well known that the ruling of our holy Torah is that the way for a Jewish man to receive his livelihood—which depends **only** on Hashem, who sustains and provides for all—comes about as it is written: "If you walk in My statutes," which Rashi explains to mean that you must be **toiling** in Torah. Consequently, it is understood that by studying Torah with the necessary dedication and self-sacrifice—in the language of our Sages, that you be **toiling** in Torah—it is precisely through this that the promise of the Holy One, blessed be He, will be fulfilled: "And the land will yield its produce," etc., and the blessing of Hashem will be upon everything a person and his family requires.

It is not as they say—that by stopping his Torah study, Heaven forbid, the Holy One, who gives the Torah, will increase his livelihood. The lengthiness of this explanation is unnecessary. You may show this letter of mine to the Yeshiva administration, and surely they, too, will be able to influence your parents—may they live—in the direction mentioned above. May Hashem grant you success and bring you good tidings regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2,414

B"H, 18 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter from the end of Sivan, I was alarmed to read about your strange plans regarding your future, following the various "conflicts" you have had with the administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. This whole matter is perplexing. Just as it is the duty of an administrator to manage the yeshiva to the best of his ability with dedication and self-sacrifice, so too is it the duty of the yeshiva students to apply themselves to their studies to the best of their ability with dedication and self-sacrifice. It is specifically through the combined efforts of both that a yeshiva is built.

It appears from your letter that you and several of your friends are interfering in the administration of the yeshiva. Aside from the well-known dictum of our Sages, "The destruction of the elderly is a building, and the building of the youth is a destruction," it is impossible for your interference in any matter not to distract your attention from your studies. If so, it is surely almost certain—even in your own eyes—that this entire matter of your interference in administrative affairs is one of the tactics of the Yetzer Hara to disconnect you from your studies, and surely, to the extent possible, from your avodah of tefillah as well. As is evident from your letter, you yourselves have experienced this tangibly, since you conclude your letter by stating that you came home from the yeshiva, which implies, with near certainty, that you interrupted your studies, etc., etc. If so, the source of the entire matter is **clear**.

If you will listen to my opinion, you will return to the yeshiva immediately and dedicate yourself to the study of Nigleh and Chassidus to the best of your ability. You should know clearly that all the excuses—that you have no study partner, that you lack diligence, that you have no taste for learning, etc.—are, as the word *am-tla* (excuse) implies, *emes-lo* (truth-no, i.e., not the truth). This comes from the side of the Yetzer, who has evidently succeeded in enticing you until now. Nevertheless, every single Jew is promised that in one hour and one moment, he can transform himself from one extreme to the other. This is especially true since you have had the merit of studying for some time in the yeshiva of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, who invested his own soul-powers into it—powers which are eternal and, consequently, continue to exert their influence upon all those who studied within the walls of his yeshiva. May Hashem grant you success so that this happens for you as soon as possible, and that you return to your studies in a way that you will, at least in part, rectify the past (to the extent that this is possible regarding the matter of Talmud Torah, where one is obligated for every single moment in its own right).

Awaiting good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2815

B"H, 18 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Tammuz, in which you write that you will soon turn nineteen, and immediately following this, you continue with your dispute with the Yeshiva administration, stating that you cannot fulfill their requirement to study in accordance with the Yeshiva’s schedule, etc. Surely you yourself understand that this is a contradiction from the beginning to the end. For if you are soon to turn nineteen, it is certainly impossible for you to possess the experience in education and methods of conduct of a person who has lived for several decades. Consequently, it is understood that your decisions regarding what is "impossible" and what is "necessary," etc., are prone to error—especially when those who have been engaged in education for many years, and who have no personal stake in the matter, say the opposite of your own conclusion. Furthermore, since the result of your decision is that you have neglected your studies, left the Yeshiva, and abandoned its discipline, etc., it is surely highly probable, even in your own eyes, that these are the machinations and enticements of the *yetzer hara*. The *yetzer hara* plots in every possible way to disconnect a person from the *avodah* of the Creator, and it approaches him with arguments of *yiras shamayim*, honor for one's mother, or by finding various faults in the Yeshiva administration, etc.

If you will listen to my opinion, you will return to the Yeshiva to study there with *mesiras nefesh*. You will then succeed. Regarding your health, when you consult with a specialist physician, he will certainly arrange your studies so that your *neshamah* remains healthy and your body remains healthy as well. The matter depends solely on you—that you truly decide to engage in the Torah of Hashem for at least some time longer and to walk in His ways; then you will succeed.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2717

2717

By the Grace of Hashem, 19 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished individual, a man of many deeds and knowledge, scion of a noble lineage, etc., R. Gad, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter in due time, as well as the two books you sent: the *Mejelle* and the volume *Mivchar Kitvei Yisrael* by Dov Frumkin, edited by G. Kressel. Many thanks for them, and I request that you continue to favor me with such items in the future.

In connection with the Chag HaGeulah of 12-13 Tammuz of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, from his imprisonment in 5727, the third part of his *Reshimah* on this matter has been published, which I am enclosing here. May the merit of the *Baal HaSimcha* stand for each and every one of us to spread the light of the teachings of Chassidus and its *maayanos*—and also—outward.

With respect and blessing.

It is a wondrous thing that in the laws and penal code of our holy Torah, there is a fundamental distinction from the legal systems of other nations: in our Torah, there is no such thing as a **punishment** of imprisonment (the case of one who was placed in a *keipah*—*Sanhedrin* 9, 5—was not a matter of a punitive sentence of imprisonment, as explained in the Mishnah there). In this, we also clearly see the Torah’s perspective on the immense value of actual deed and the preciousness of life. As the verse states, "Days were fashioned, and not one of them [was lacking]," implying that every moment of a person’s life is counted. Since punishment according to the Torah is not a matter of vengeance but of *tikkun*, there is no place to deprive a person of the possibility of action, even for the sake of the *tikkun* of the many—which is the purpose of imprisonment—except for one who is not fit to fulfill his role at all, whose punishment is death.

From this, we learn three fundamental points: 1. As mentioned, the immense value of every single moment of a person’s life; 2. The immense value of the individual; 3. Even though a person has sinned, he still has a special role to fulfill in his mission from the Creator of the world.

And this is not the place to elaborate.

***

**R. Gad:** Frumkin. Another letter to him—above, Vol. 8, 2393.

**Mejelle:** The Ottoman Civil Code, translated by Gad Frumkin.

**It is a wondrous thing:** See *Likkutei Sichos* Vol. 25, p. 215, note 17, and the references cited there.

## 2,818

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long hiatus, your letter was received on the day of the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—and our own redemption, for the body follows the head. Regarding what you write—that you do not write because you have nothing to report—this is more puzzling and difficult to accept than the lack of correspondence itself. When you are in a city where thousands upon thousands of Bnei Yisrael reside, regardless of the state of Yiddishkeit, there is always something to improve. This is a common denominator in all places and at all times, from after the sin of the Golden Calf until the spirit of impurity is removed from the earth. It is therefore understood that there is always material ready to be written, unless there is a lack of desire to act and improve, or a lack of desire to write about it.

As for what you wrote—that the place is such that "no man shall lift his hand," etc.—this should be viewed *kal v'chomer*: this is a place where no man can lift his hand without the Holy One, Blessed be He, who is the King of Kings. Furthermore, even according to human logic, and even according to the logic of the *nefesh habehamis*, the matters of authority and control only apply to external appearances. The actions themselves do not cause confusion, and consequently, they will not be hindered. Since the internal matters are not affected—only the external actions, authority, and control—there is certainly room for action, and the authority does not affect any of the aforementioned.

To summarize the calculation in other words:

Regardless of all the suggestions, explanations, and justifications that you have told me orally and written in your letters, even if they are correct, they will not add a **single** action in the dissemination of Torah in general, and the dissemination of the wellsprings in particular. This is in contrast to when you begin to act. It is a known ruling of our holy Nasi that "propaganda" (outreach) never returns empty, and one action is better than a thousand sighs. This is especially true since we do not know what the results of an action in holiness might be; it can bring forth fruit and the fruit of fruit until the end of the world—or, as our Sages explain, until the end of the concealment and hiddenness.

With blessings.

## 2,819

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...It is certainly permissible to remind him of what is explained in the Gemara in many places regarding the obligation and the merit of a Rav toward the people of his community. It is also well-known how our Alter Rebbe emphasized the title *Rav Mara D’Asra*, for in truth, he is the "master" (*ba’al*) of his place. Since the Ribono shel Olam does not deal unjustly with His creatures and only demands according to their capacity, it is certain that the Rav has been granted the powers to fulfill this role—though he must bring them from potential into action. And for one who comes to purify himself, he is assisted. It is understood that I am not writing this as a sermon, but rather regarding the practical application, and most importantly, the infusion of the performance of practical mitzvos into daily life—and there is a presumption that such efforts (*ta'amulah*) will not return empty.

With blessings for success in all the above.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Tammuz: It is surprising that you do not mention anywhere in your letter that this is the day of the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the Nasi of Israel. In general, they consist of studying the teachings of Chassidus, following and conducting oneself according to its guidance and customs, and influencing your friends and surroundings in this direction. For ahavas Yisrael is the vessel for "you shall love Hashem your G-d," which is the foundation of the entire Torah. It is not the study that is the essential thing, but the action: to establish, from this point forward, daily shiurim in the study of Chassidus—some of them before davening—and especially on Shabbos, and to be meticulous in the performance of mitzvos, as explained at length in the sefarim of Chassidus and in the maamarim. Our Sages have already ruled: "If one says, 'I have not labored and yet I have found,' do not believe him; [if one says,] 'I have labored and found,' believe him."

With blessings,

## 2821

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter—which does not indicate when it was written—in which you write about the distribution of plots in the village [Kfar Chabad] by lottery, and you express bitterness that you received an unsuitable plot, and consequently, you complain about the village administration who cast the lots, suspecting that they did not treat you as they should have, etc., etc.

Surely you are aware of the words of our Sages that a Torah scholar who offers an opinion after the fact is not to be trusted. If, before the lottery was cast, there was room to discuss how the distribution should be conducted, after the fact I see no room for this—especially since, by your own admission, you are an interested party. Furthermore, there is **absolutely no room** to stir up controversy regarding this matter. Who is to say that the entire lottery should be nullified, thereby causing a dispute, Heaven forbid, the end of which is baseless hatred, etc.? If in the Diaspora one must guard against all of this, then how much more so in the Holy Land, upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year. You did not travel there out of necessity, but by free choice; that is, of your own good will, you took upon yourself the responsibility to live in the King’s palace. Even with a slight amount of contemplation, it is easy to realize that one must be meticulous in all matters. This is especially true since the calculations you are making are accompanied by an excess of emotional agitation. It seems to me that you have already realized over the years that you have been in the Holy Land (may it be built and established) that the separation of hearts and the "snatching" from one another—the snatchers gained nothing; on the contrary.

The conclusion from all of the above is that if you can exchange your plot for another in peace and pleasantness, without stirring up a commotion and certainly without causing a separation of hearts, etc., etc., then **perhaps** it is worth trying to do so. However, if the matter is likely to lead to what is written, "The beginning of strife is like letting out water," then you must not do this at all. The One who sustains and provides for all has already made known His conduct: "The Holy One, blessed be He, did not find a vessel that holds blessing other than peace." Further elaboration on this is entirely superfluous.

With blessings,
