## 2824

B"H, 21 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and dedicated to communal needs, Rabbi Nissan Nemanov, may he be well.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 15 Tammuz with pleasure, in which you write regarding the farbrengens and their content. I was also pleased to hear that additional students have joined for the summer period, and that the hope is already beginning to be fulfilled that some of them will remain to study in the yeshiva. Regarding this, as I wrote to someone else in recent days, one should make a *kal v'chomer* (a fortiori argument): If the efforts made until now have already yielded visible fruits, then how much more so when one exerts oneself with greater energy and vigor—there is no doubt that the fruits will be multiplied accordingly. In matters of holiness, an increase in quantity ultimately leads to an increase in quality as well. Surely, elaborating on this is unnecessary, and these lines are sufficient to express my opinion. May it be His will that this continues in a practical manner, that dozens of students simply arrive—and this is not beyond the reach of the Almighty.

On this occasion, I will repeat once again what I have written and hinted at in this letter several times, which is:

Surely you are aware of the history of the work in Georgia, where they began the work with Sephardim in a new way, and so on. Over the course of a few years, hundreds of *avreichim*, *bochurim*, and also laymen were added. There is no doubt that even now there are fruits there, and the fruits of their fruits, until the end of the world (when, ultimately, the concealment and hiddenness will cease). It is incumbent upon you and all those assisting you to look at the work with the *bochurim* from Morocco with the same approach—meaning, it depends on you to conquer the entire country of Morocco, and through this, also their brethren in Tunisia, and so on, to make them students of the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe. This can be done by transforming the tens of students currently with you into proper Chassidei Chabad, and consequently, they will become "moist enough to moisten others" (*tofeach al menas lehatfiach*)—influential *mashpi'im* when they return to their surroundings. When they realize that in our generation they have the power to make three hundred thousand Jews into Chassidei Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe, there is no doubt that they will be filled not only with desire and effort, but also with an outpouring of ideas and methods on how to bring this from potential into reality. Especially since, as it appears, it is difficult to transform the aforementioned individuals into the desired form when they are in close proximity to their parents; it is specifically when they are exiled from their place [that this is achieved], as is evident in practice. You should strive to increase the number of students coming from Morocco, and the main thing is to bring them in a short time to illuminate them with the light of Chassidus and to instill in them the necessary *hislahavus* (enthusiasm) that prepares a person to be a *mashpia* among the Sephardim with greater intensity and strength, due to their warm nature for emotional matters and things that come from the heart.

I hope that you will surely find the appropriate words to elaborate on this matter and to influence all the *Roshei Yeshiva* and *Ramim* of Tomchei Temimim in France, so that all of them together will act on this matter as shluchim of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his father, the Rebbe—may the merit of the righteous protect us. Then, one can hope that in the near future, hundreds and thousands and more will be added to the camp of Chassidei Chabad, and the merit of the many depends on them.

With a blessing for success in your holy work.

## 2825

21 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Yaakov HaKohen

Greetings and Blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 3rd of this month. Please accept my sincerest apologies for the delay in my response, which was due to the pressure of many preoccupations, particularly during the days preceding and following the days of liberation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. These are days of *hisorerus* and *farbrengens*, following in his footsteps to increase our efforts in the path he taught us, so that "we may walk in his ways" (the expression of the Alter Rebbe in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, ch. 27).

You remarked in your letter regarding the *maamar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, from the first day of Rosh Hashanah 5703, where he writes: "We must say that when Rosh Hashanah falls on Shabbos, the obligation of the mitzvah of *shofar* does not exist, and it is not that it was merely deferred." You raise a difficulty based on *Yevamos* 90a, where Rashi (*s.v. shomer*) writes that we nullify the *shofar* blowing on Shabbos **by Rabbinic decree**. This implies that the mitzvah of *shofar* does indeed exist on Shabbos.

I must question your premise. Why look so far afield? In this very *sugya*—which is where my father-in-law, the Rebbe, begins his *maamar* (referencing *Rosh Hashanah* 29b)—it is stated that it is **by Rabbinic decree** that they forbade *shofar* on Shabbos. (Perhaps you are precise because in *Rosh Hashanah* the language used is "by Torah law it is permitted," whereas in Rashi in *Yevamos* the term is "mitzvah of *aseh*." However, even in Rashi it does not say "mitzvah of *aseh* on Shabbos," and consequently, it can be explained there too that on Shabbos it is merely permitted.)

This *maamar* is based on the *maamar* of the Alter Rebbe in *Likutei Torah*, *Devarim* 56a, and the *maamar* of his son, the Mitteler Rebbe, in *Siddur Shaar HaTkias* (as I noted in my annotations to the *maamar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe). According to the rule of our Sages that "words of Torah are... enriched in another place," we should add an explanation to the *maamar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, based on what is explained there. It states (*Likutei Torah*, loc. cit., beginning of 56b): "On Shabbos, [the light] is drawn down from the *mitzvah of aseh*... consequently, it is not **needed** for the *shofar*... and therefore the *mitzvah of aseh* of *shofar* is deferred on Shabbos."

It is explained even more clearly in the *Siddur* (*Shaar HaTkias*, 27, beginning of page 4): "By Torah law, the mitzvah of *shofar* is not nullified even on Shabbos, but [only] by Rabbinic decree."

From all this, it is proven that even in these *maamarim*, the intention is not that there is **no** *mitzvah of aseh* of *shofar* at all on Shabbos, but rather that the **necessity** for it is not the same as when it falls during the week. On Shabbos, the matters are drawn down even without the *shofar* blowing; therefore, were it not for the decree, or prior to the decree, they would have blown the *shofar* on Shabbos as well, and the Rabbinic decree was able to nullify this.

It should be known that even according to the *nigleh* (revealed Torah), the decree of Rabbah—"lest he carry it"—alone would not have been enough to nullify *shofar* on Shabbos, as explained in *Tosafos* in *Rosh Hashanah* there. See also the precise language of the Rambam, *Hilchos Shofar*, ch. 2, law 6: "Even though the blowing... and why do we not blow..." Seemingly, this is an unnecessary length of text, but it is understood according to the view of *Tosafos*, and likewise from what the Alter Rebbe wrote in *Shulchan Aruch*, ch. 588, sec. 4. See also *Machatzis HaShekel* and the places cited there.

I have your books on *Maseches Rosh Hashanah* and *Makkos*. If you would honor me with your other published books, I would be very grateful. It is understood that you may also exchange them for books published by Kehot, for which a catalog will be sent to you separately.

With respect and blessing.

***

Since I have your aforementioned letter in hand, and for the sake of affection, I went through the pages of your book on *Maseches Rosh Hashanah*. I did so cursorily, as time permitted, not in depth. Based on the words of our Sages (*Bava Metzia* 84a), "he raises difficulties... and consequently the *shemaita* (the subject matter) becomes clear," I have noted a few comments:

**Page 1a:** You are in doubt regarding a document that lists its date according to the kings, not from Nisan—as per the ruling of the *Mishnah* at the beginning of *Rosh Hashanah*—whether it is invalid *bedieved* (after the fact). You resolve your doubt from what the *Baal HaMaor* writes there, that it is invalid.

It is obvious that there is no room for doubt that the document is invalid as a **legal document**, as is explicitly stated in the *Shas* **on the spot** in this context, that this is the law of the *Mishnah*: "Promissory notes that are antedated are invalid." Consequently, the proof from the *Baal HaMaor* is irrelevant, as he is speaking only of the aforementioned (he only comes to negate Rashi's interpretation, and he also explains the intent of Rabbeinu Chananel at the end, "as the *Mishnah* states promissory notes..." after he already explained for what purpose this is—that it refers to documents).

The doubt is whether the document is invalidated entirely, even as evidence that a loan took place, etc. This doubt can be resolved from *Bava Metzia* (72a), where according to *Tosafos* one cannot collect with it at all, and according to Rashi, one can collect from unencumbered property.

Alternatively, to avoid increasing the number of disputes, even according to *Tosafos*, the document is not nullified entirely. Promissory notes are different, as we issue a decree lest he collect from the first date (and not because he did not write the date according to the *takanas chachamim*). This is also indicated by the plain reading of the *sugya* in *Bava Metzia*.

**Section 108:** Reading of the Torah is by Torah law. This is puzzling, as it is a decree of the Prophets (*Bava Kamma* 82a; in the *Yerushalmi* and Rambam—from Moshe Rabbeinu)—except for the portion of *Zachor* (and *Parah*). What is written in *Magen Avraham* at the end of ch. 685 is irrelevant to this case, as is understood.

**At the end of Part 1 (65d):** You resolve the difficulty of the *Tiferes Yisrael*. According to the view of Rabban Gamliel (*Berachos* 2a), it is forbidden to recite *Krias Shema* after midnight if one has not yet prayed *Maariv*, because it is like reading from the Torah, and it is forbidden to study before prayer (according to Rashi, *Berachos* 5b, and not like *Tosafos* there; see also *Likutei Torah* of the Alter Rebbe, *Parshas Bracha* 96b). While this is a fine point, it is difficult to say there is a decree "lest he forget to pray **while studying like this**," since his entire purpose was only for the order of prayer. This is preferable to the case in *Berachos* (31a): "from a definitive ruling." It is similar to what our Sages said (*Pesachim* 11a), "he himself..." Therefore, the *Tosafos* (*s.v. ella*, *Berachos* 5b) did not raise a difficulty against Rashi from the aforementioned *Berachos* (31a).

**Responsa Section A:** Regarding prostate surgery—(a) I have always wondered why one is not required to ask a *chacham* (a sage) before undergoing this surgery, since it involves a matter of castration (at the very least, a close concern). (b) Although the essence of the *shichvas zera* (semen) originates from the testicles, many substances are added to it from the prostate. If so, it is a matter of inquiry whether, without these substances—due to prostate surgery—the fluid that is emitted has the legal status of *shichvas zera* according to Torah law. (c) The aforementioned surgery negates the concept of "shooting like an arrow," to a large extent at least, but not the emission of the *shichvas zera* (if we assume that the law of *shichvas zera* applies to it). After clarifying with doctors (and how the surgery is **actually performed now**, as there are changes in this as well), the question should be decided.

**Responsa Section 22:** The view of the Rambam is that eating *terumah* is an *avodah* (service), as he writes explicitly in *Hilchos Terumos* at the end. See there in *Yad Eisan*.

**Ibid., Chiddushim, Section 1:** See *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe, *Orach Chaim*, ch. 328, sec. 3: that Shabbos is deferred entirely and there is no desecration here at all. And there in sec. 16—the reason of the *Raavad*, even though the Rebbe rules that Shabbos is deferred and not permitted. See there that he combines it with the reason of the *Ran*. I will not elaborate.

**Ibid., Section 7:** It is the custom of Israel **not** to marry during the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* (this is not difficult from *Yoma*, as when it is certainly possible, it is different). Many opinions hold that one should "pass over" a mitzvah to perform it in the most optimal way (*min hamuvchar*): *Terumas HaDeshen*, *Maharil*, *Chacham Tzvi*, *Tur Shulchan Aruch*, *Rema*, *Divrei Malkiel*, and others. This is also **an everyday occurrence**: walking to a further *shul*, receiving the sixth *aliyah* or *Maftir* (for those who hold they have an advantage over the previous ones), etc. Especially in this case, where preparation is needed (and great preparation at that), according to many *Acharonim*, the law of "passing over a mitzvah" does not apply at all (the opinions are collected in *Sdei Chemed*, *Pe'as HaSadeh*, *Klallim* 1, 47). Heaven forbid to nullify, because of pilpulistic difficulties and resolutions, many of the customs of Israel, the content of which is to fulfill the mitzvah of Hashem in the most optimal way, as it is written, "All the fat is for Hashem" (see Rambam, end of *Hilchos Issurei Mizbe'ach*). Regarding this it is said (*Midrash HaGadol, Bereishis* 4:4): "Because he brought his sacrifice from the choicest, with a good eye, his sacrifice was pleasing to the Holy One, blessed be He, and of him it says: 'Then the offering of Yehudah and Yerushalayim will be pleasant to Hashem, as in the days of old and as in ancient years.'"

## 2826

24 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, who is engaged in the work of Tzedakah and Chessed,
Rabbi Binyamin Eliyahu Gorodetzky, may he live and be well,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the Fast of the Fourth Month—may it soon be transformed into joy—and the letter that followed it. The telegram regarding your trip to Tunisia was also received, and I assume this also includes the island of Djerba...

I was very pleased to hear that you found someone to translate the *sichos* from Yiddish into French. However, regarding your suggestion that they send all the booklets for the coming year: you are surely aware that the booklet here is published at the beginning of the month, meaning it is only finished being written in the final days of the month. It is therefore self-evident that in such a manner, the French booklets will never appear on time. Since time is also needed for translation, one would be lucky if they appeared even after the following month. Therefore, this should be done using the booklets from previous years; aside from the *parshiyos* or *haftaros*, the booklets are relevant for all years.

...Regarding the *seforim*: if the sale of the *seforim* is handed over to a stranger, there is a great concern that until a significant quantity of the *seforim* he receives is sold, he will not agree in any way to bring in new *seforim*. He will simply state that the lack of sales is proof that there is no demand for them, etc. Therefore, and for other reasons as well, one should not hand this over to or involve a stranger from the outside. Among *anash*, I do not know of anyone to whom this matter can be entrusted **officially**, other than Rabbi Yehuda Leib Schmotkin, may he live. However, in practical terms, one should utilize the young people—the energetic individuals—who can exert themselves in sales and distribution to the maximum extent. It is understood that if the person handling this requires a salary, it is worth it, etc., for after all, who knows what he will do with the *seforim*? Perhaps it would be worthwhile to set the salary as a percentage rather than a fixed wage, so that the incentive is increased, etc. You will surely be able to see on the spot which of the young people to involve in this. In any case, one must also obligate the various Chabad organizations to participate in the distribution, in accordance with their general mandate of spreading the *maayanos* outward. In this regard, the young people of Agudas Chabad are more suitable, as they are the ones who travel and visit the villages and settlements, and consequently, they have familiarity with the people on the spot...

For some time now, there has been a discussion regarding the printing of the *sichos* in Lashon HaKodesh in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. Rabbi Shalom Haskind, may he live, has taken this upon himself. It is understood that, as with all Chabad matters, the question of funding immediately arises, and thus the matter is currently quiet. Since I anticipated this delay, I spoke about this in general terms with Mr. Shazar, may he live, and I told him that it is my intention to pursue this matter—namely, the printing of a monthly journal in Lashon HaKodesh in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established...

I also spoke with him about finding the means for a group of students from Tomchei Temimim here to travel for a few months to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, on the condition that they would also be under the auspices of Tomchei Temimim there—though, of course, they would also tour the land, but under the supervision of the aforementioned, and not under the supervision of the Jewish Agency...

You are surely aware of the Rav Kook Institute, which prints *seforim*, and is also connected to the publication of the monthly journal *Sinai*, most of which is dedicated to matters of Halacha and Aggada. When Mr. Mindel, may he live, visited Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, last year, I asked him to get in touch with the management of the aforementioned institute and arrange for them to send the items they publish to my library, and primarily, also what they have published until now, since the library here is a matter for the public. It is understood that there is no fund to pay for the *seforim*, and it is also understood that they should be sent *seforim* from the Kehot publication house if and when they request them. To my regret, Mr. Mindel, may he live, did not succeed in this, even though he met with some of the management, who told him that it is not their custom and that there is no way other than to purchase from them, etc. It is worthwhile that during your stay in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, you find out upon whom this depends, for there is no doubt that with the appropriate explanation, they will agree to the above. It is understood that the shipping costs for their previous publications, which will surely amount to a significant sum, should be taken on the account of Agudas Chabad, and the like.

In the same vein, one should propose this to other publishers in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, especially the Tarbitz publishing house (which publishes scientific *seforim*), the publications of the University, etc...

I believe I told you when you were here about our conversation with Mr. Shazar, may he live, regarding the possibility of founding a second Kfar Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and also his conclusion that for the time being, they should develop the first Kfar Chabad.

Nevertheless, it is worth your while to clarify his perspective on this for the future, after the aforementioned matter is concluded, etc...

Rabbi Menachem Lipsker, may he live, writes to me that he was informed of a proposal to establish a yeshiva in proximity to the Ohel of the late Rabbi Amram, may his merit protect us, where people come twice a year, etc., and the location is between Fez and Meknes. I will await your opinion on this as well.

With blessings for success in your holy work in all the above, and awaiting good news.

## 2827

B"H, 24 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter of the 20th of Tammuz, along with the enclosure. You need not be concerned at all, for I open all letters addressed to me personally. It goes without saying that if the writer does not wish for anyone other than me to see the letter, that is how it is handled. This is also the case regarding your letter, and you can be completely certain and at ease.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter we discussed here—giving a certain sum to the yeshivos—you write that you do not yet know when, and that you are waiting for an answer regarding your application.

Hopefully, my letter to your wife, tichyeh, arrived in due time. As for your connecting this to your application, it seems to me that in our conversation I drew your attention to the fact that these should not be linked. At the very most, this might apply only to the funds from the application, but the remainder should be taken care of as soon as possible.

According to the instruction of Rabbeinu HaZaken in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 21, where he writes—in substance—the following: The Akeidah is constantly mentioned as a basis for Hashem Yisbarach to provide all Jews with what they need. We recite the Parshas HaAkeidah every day before davening, and before and after it we recite a prayer that Hashem Yisbarach should treat us with kindness and mercy in the merit of the Akeidah. Furthermore, the Parshas HaAkeidah is one of the blessings and requests in the Musaf of Rosh Hashanah, and it is also read on Rosh Hashanah. The Alter Rebbe explains in Iggeres HaKodesh that the novelty here is not the Akeidah itself—which was not such a great test for Avraham Avinu—but rather the innovation is that Avraham Avinu performed it with *zerizus* (alacrity), thereby demonstrating his desire to fulfill the will of Hashem Yisbarach with joy. The merit of this **haste** protects and stands by Jews in all generations, as per the expression of Rabbeinu HaZaken, "**for us and for our children forever.**" And Rabbeinu HaZaken adds, "And this is especially relevant to the act of tzedakah, to hasten it **as much as possible**."

Certainly, when writing to a Chabad Chossid, it is unnecessary to bring proofs to reinforce the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken. Therefore, I am confident that after looking into the aforementioned Iggeres HaKodesh, you will see the need to hasten the matter we spoke about, in accordance with the expression of Rabbeinu HaZaken—the *posek* in the *nistar* of Torah and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the *posek* in the *nigleh* of Torah—**"as much as possible."** May Hashem Yisbarach help, and He will help, that you should do this with joy and a desire to fulfill the will of your Creator and to provide *nachas ruach* to your Maker. May this merit stand by you in this world as well, as the Alter Rebbe writes there, for you, your wife, and all your family, for long, good days and years.

With blessings.

## 2828

2828

B"H, 24 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

An inquiry has reached me in your name from the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, active in communal needs, a man of many accomplishments and fine character, R' Shalom DovBer Gordon, regarding the matter of your daughter. She became engaged, and now she is distancing herself, saying that her feelings have not yet crystallized, and you are asking whether you should pressure her.

In my opinion, it would be more diplomatic and also easier to influence your daughter if you were to ask one of her friends to speak with her about this. You yourself should only do so from time to time, so that your daughter does not get the impression that you are trying to boss her around. I believe that the reason your daughter’s feelings regarding this matter have changed is because they conducted themselves in a way that is not permitted for Jews to conduct themselves before marriage. This has now brought about the opposite result, causing her to distance herself from him. If mothers, and parents in general, would take an interest in the upbringing of their children while they are still young, as the **holy Torah** demands, they would avoid much heartache and trouble for themselves, and even more so for their children.

It goes without saying that I am not writing this to cause you pain, but rather to draw your attention to the fact that, at the very least, from now on, just as you are pressuring your daughter regarding this shidduch in general, you should also influence her—and **even more so**—to take upon herself that when she marries, she will conduct a Jewish home as a Jewish daughter should, with Taharas HaMishpacha, a kosher kitchen, keeping Shabbos, and so on. For only with such conduct can there be a happy life among Jews. May Hashem help you to begin acting on this in an appropriate manner immediately and repeatedly, for in the end, one eventually succeeds. May you be able to report good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2829

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5714

Especially since, according to the assumption, it was said that the institution in Sefrou would be akin to a yeshiva, and not a Talmud Torah. You write in your aforementioned letter that "double beds" will soon be finished. I do not know your intent in this. But if the matter is as it sounds—meaning that two people sleep in one large bed—this is highly questionable, and I demand that this be absolutely avoided... Perhaps **this is not your intent** with the word "double."

With a blessing that you will be able to share good news... soon, and that you will succeed in your holy work, which will consequently bring an increase in blessing and success in your personal matters and those of your entire household, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2830

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about [those] who do not wish to pay their debts: In such a case, the example brought in Chassidic discourse is well-known—that one must arrange for the debts to be paid over a period of time, paying them little by little. If, along with this, the necessity of paying debts is explained publicly at a meeting, there is hope that this, too, will improve, at least to some extent...

Regarding the high school for girls: The main point is missing from your letter, which is: what is the curriculum? It is surely unnecessary to elaborate that it is not the role of Chabad activists to engage in the dissemination of secular studies, especially among the daughters of anash, and particularly when there are those who are already preoccupied with this far too much. If the intention of the high school is to enable the girls to continue their kodesh studies on the spot, then this is **very, very** correct. This is not the case if the intention is for secular studies; it is not comparable to Beis Rivkah, where, due to the young age of the students, the compulsory education law applies to them, which includes secular studies in its curriculum. This is not the case for the age of high school students, who are exempt from this. If only they would invest their energy and talents in kodesh studies appropriate for girls! It is obvious that one must not breach the fence by establishing a high school in Kfar Chabad for both secular and kodesh studies together... The summary of the above is: it is very, very correct—if there are suitable students and suitable administration—to organize in the Kfar itself a continuation of kodesh studies for those who have already completed the Beis Rivkah curriculum. But one must not establish a high school in the Kfar for secular and kodesh studies.

With blessings for success in your work, and awaiting good news regarding all of the above.

**Regarding the high school for girls:** See the continuation—below, 2895.

## 2,831

B"H, 26 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Many thanks for your letter with the good news regarding the improvement in your physical health, and that you are also traveling for the sake of your livelihood. May it be the will of Hashem that you also share good news regarding your spiritual health, that it may be as it should be, and that as you travel for your physical livelihood, you may also gain an increase in spiritual livelihood.

According to the statement of the Baal Shem Tov, brought at the end of the *He'aros* to *Likutei Torah* (Kehot publication), a Yid, through the simple *emunah* in his heart, exerts an influence in the places he visits, purifying the atmosphere, and so on. This is all the more so when there is also actual *maaseh b'fo'al* (tangible action). And although it is explained there in the context of *chutz la'aretz* (the Diaspora), one should learn from this a *binyan av* (a foundational principle) regarding the increase of *kedushah* in Eretz Yisrael.

With blessings for success and livelihood,

## 2832

2832

By the Grace of Hashem, 26 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his holy work,
Rabbi Chaim Moshe, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 17 Tammuz (may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness)... I was pleased to hear what you wrote regarding the activities observed among the students who study in the afternoon—although you did not specify which schools they come from, this will surely be filled in at the next opportunity. Certainly, you will not be satisfied with what has been accomplished thus far; on the contrary, you should apply the principle of *kal v'chomer*: if the efforts made until now have already yielded fruit, then how much more so will the fruit multiply in both quantity and quality—fruit and the fruit of fruit—until the end of the world. And as interpreted in *Chassidus*, this means until there is an end to the *he'elem* (concealment) and *hester* (hiding).

Regarding your observation concerning the statement in *Chassidus* that Moshiach possesses a level that is greater than Moshe Rabbeinu—see also *Likutei Torah*, Vayikra 17a; *Bamidbar* 89b-c; and at the end of *Shir HaShirim* 49c and onward. This is also mentioned in the commentary of *Tanchuma*, Toldos 20, which on the face of it contradicts the well-known fact that "there arose no prophet since in Yisrael like Moshe."

There are several distinctions to be made here, namely regarding the matters of prophecy, kingship, knowledge of Torah, etc.

The fact that "there arose no prophet like Moshe" is agreed upon regarding the level of prophecy, as is also brought in Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah* 9:2. See also *Rosh Hashanah* 21b. However, regarding kingship, one did arise [who was greater], and certainly regarding the level of the *neshamah*. See the aforementioned *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Shir HaShirim*, where it states that the level of Moshiach is greater. Consequently, there is no contradiction, as this applies also to the study of Torah. This is especially true regarding the "Torah of Moshiach," which is the concept of "let him kiss me with the kisses of his mouth"—the *pnimiyus* (inner dimension) of Torah, the *yechidah* of Torah. This corresponds to the connection of Moshiach to the *yechidah* of the collective soul, whereas Moshe’s connection is to the level of *chayah*, as brought in *Shaar HaPesukim*, Parshas Vayechi, and elsewhere. See also *Menachos* 29b, "that he did not know what they were saying."

Regarding your query as to whether a *chazzan* who is a *bochur* should wear a *tallis*: Regarding *Mincha* and *Maariv*, it is surely known to you—and it is also recorded in *Hayom Yom*—that we go before the *amud* without a *tallis*, according to the Lubavitch custom. Regarding *Shacharis*, we are also not particular about this here in the *Yeshiva*, and I believe that they were not particular about this in Rostov, Otwock, etc. Since there is no such custom, why wear a *tallis*? It enters the category of a potential unnecessary blessing, etc. On the other hand, if this is considered strange according to the customs of Jerusalem, it is not worth inciting controversy by having the *chazzan* wear a *tallis* during *Shacharis*. However, if there is no controversy about the matter, it is worthwhile to maintain the aforementioned custom. See *Sukkah* 32, bottom of page b...

Regarding your observation on what is written in *Ohr HaChaim* (Vayeshev 37:21) that a person with free choice can kill even someone who has not been decreed death by Heaven—which is the opposite of what is written in *Iggeres HaKodesh* by the Alter Rebbe, section 265—one is pitting one great authority against another. However, on the face of it, it is difficult to reconcile with what is written in *Zohar Chadash* (185a, there) and what is written in Scripture (II Samuel 24:14). It may be explained as being similar to one who stands in a place of danger (*Shabbos* 32a), where, nevertheless, it depends only on the verdict from Above. The danger is greater than [the power of] a person with free choice, unlike the case of people—and especially the Jewish people—whose choice is truly free (see there in the commentaries on the *Zohar*). One can force this interpretation also on the language of the *Ohr HaChaim* and the commentary of the *Ritva* to *Chagigah* 5a. This requires further study in the words of our Sages (*Arachin* 15b), "the third killer," and what is written about this in *Hayom Yom*, 13 Cheshvan.

## 2833

B”H, 26 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the interval, I was pleased to receive your handwritten letter. Surely the ruling of our Sages, "Whoever is treated with kindness [is rewarded]," will be fulfilled in your case (Bava Basra 12b). You are certainly aware of our perspective on matters such as these, based on the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov (which, in truth, was also agreed upon by the Jewish philosophers who preceded him): that every single detail of human life, and of the inanimate, vegetative, and animal realms in general, is directed toward a specific purpose.

As the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, goes in one of his *maamarim* on *Chassidus*: it completes the Divine intent.

According to one of the fundamental principles of our faith—that of free choice—every matter contains a portion of good, to the extent that even *chashocha* (darkness)—which according to Torah is darkness—can be transformed into *nahora* (light), and bitterness into sweetness. Since you have found yourself in the hospital, you must utilize this opportunity to influence those who are there, by drawing their hearts closer to Torah and Yiddishkeit in general, and to Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs in particular.

The sooner you hasten to do this, the sooner your mission in that place will be completed, and consequently, you will be discharged from there in health, peace, and success. And the *zerizin* (the diligent) act quickly. Especially as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "Chassidim are clever, and do not put off until tomorrow what can be accomplished today." May it be the will of Hashem that from here on, you complete all your affairs in ways that are only good and kindness, in a good that is revealed and manifest.

With blessings for a complete and speedy recovery.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2834

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in communal affairs,

It is obvious that there is no prohibition in wearing galoshes, but it is an external sign of what is happening on the inside, and a word to the wise is sufficient...

## 2,835

B"H, 28 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Today I received the news that your health condition is not as it should be. Through Hashgacha Pratis, this news was received today, just before my departure to the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. I mentioned you there for a speedy recovery, and surely my father-in-law, the Rebbe, will awaken Divine mercy for the improvement of your health. I am confident that you will be able to bring me good news that your condition is steadily improving.

According to the teaching of our Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya (who is the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah)—which is transcribed in the Sefer HaMitzvos of the Tzemach Tzedek, page 114b, and is also found in his letters as noted in the annotations there—that according to the progression of the holy supernal attributes and their order, namely Chesed, Gevurah, and Rachamim, it follows that after the attribute of Gevurah (judgment), the attribute of Rachamim (mercy) is awakened. This attribute is greater than the attribute of Chesed that preceded it, as is known, for it is the attribute of Yaakov, "an inheritance without boundaries," "a bar reaching from one end to the other," etc. May your news, therefore, be in accordance with the above.

With respect and blessings, awaiting good tidings.

## 2,836

B"H, 28 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 8 Tammuz, in which you briefly describe what you have been through and that you are now studying at a vocational school, and you add that you are being pressured to move to a kibbutz.

Behold, every member of Bnei Yisrael believes that the Ribono shel Olam is the One who sustains and provides for everyone with kindness and mercy. It is He who wrote in His Torah that "if you follow My statutes"—which our Sages explained, and is also brought in Rashi’s commentary there, to mean that you must be toiling in Torah—then "I will provide your rains in their time, and the land will yield its produce," etc., and all the blessings written in that parsha. From this, it is understood quite simply that if one truly desires that Hashem provide his livelihood when he needs it, he must fulfill the condition of being toiling in Torah. This is especially true at your age, as you are seventeen years old, when you must dedicate yourself to the study of Toras Hashem with total commitment. Hashem is certain to provide you, at the appropriate time, with a good arrangement in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

On the contrary, you should also explain to your brother, who is eighteen years old, that he too should study Toras Hashem for the majority of the day. For if not now, it is impossible to know if he will have the ability to understand and grasp our Torah—the Torah of life and the Torah of truth. As the Mishnah rules: "Do not say, 'When I am free I will study,' for perhaps you will never be free." Furthermore, regarding anyone who studies the revealed Torah and the pnimiyus haTorah, which leads to yiras Hashem and His love, our Sages have said that his assets will succeed.

These lines will surely suffice to inspire you to increase your diligence and perseverance in your studies, and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2837

B"H, 28 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, R' Avraham Sender, may he live and be well,

Shalom u'Bracha!

It was a pleasure to receive the news that you and your wife, may they live and be well, have found a place of rest in New Haven. Surely, even there, you are seeking opportunities to illuminate the light of Torah, the candle of mitzvah, and the light of the Torah—its guidance and customs—within the surrounding environment. As is well known, the interpretation of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the expression of our Sages, "engaged in Torah" (*osek b'Torah*) rather than "learning Torah" (*lomed Torah*): just as in a business in the literal sense, one strives to conduct it in a place where there is much foot traffic, and one does not sit closed away in a room within a room, waiting for someone to perhaps come and propose a business matter, but rather one runs after it—so too must be the engagement in Torah. Further elaboration on this is superfluous.

Surely, since you are striving in the aforementioned manner, you will succeed, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages: "You have labored and you have found."

With blessings for a healthy and happy summer, and that all the aforementioned matters be "well explained" (*be'er heitev*). As the hint is brought down, the word *heitev* in the "preceding numbering" (*mispar kadmi*) equals 70—meaning that it is explained to all seventy nations that this is the nature of the *birurim* (refinements) of each and every person, and that ultimately, it affects all seventy nations. This is in accordance with the ruling of our Sages, brought down in the Rambam, that a person must view themselves as perfectly balanced, such that with one action they are about to perform, they tip the scales for themselves and for the entire world toward the side of merit.

With blessings,

## 2838

2838

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Dovid Meir
Shlita

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Tammuz, in which you raise a point regarding the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek (cited in Hayom Yom, 24 Tammuz), which states: "The inner meaning is that asking for a blessing for avodah is 'they will look to their vanities' (Yeshayahu 2:6), and it must be that 'the work be heavy upon the men' (Shemos 5:9)." Specifically, the phrasing: "a blessing for avodah, etc."

The precise meaning of "a blessing for **avodah**" is understood based on what is explained in many places in Chassidus, including in Tanya, Chapter 15, regarding what is called an *oved* (as opposed to a tzaddik, or one for whom it has become habit and nature). It is specifically one who struggles with his nature and the yetzer, etc. See also Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Mishpatim, in the explanation of the concept of avodah, which is related to the term *oros avudim* (tanned hides)—and one can add, by way of wit and allusion, that the tanning of hides is done with dog excrement, etc. From this, it is understood that one who still requires avodah and asks for a blessing for it—since a blessing is a concept of *hamshacha* (drawing down), as is known, and comes from the term *mavrich* (grafting/bending down) from above to below—this is the opposite of the concept of avodah, which is by way of from below to above, through the **"men."**

As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they need in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings that Hashem will speedily transform these days into joy and gladness with the complete and true Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

#### ***2838***

**R' Dovid Meir:** Shulman. Additional letters to him: see above, Vol. 7, 1935, and the references in the notes there.

## 2839

2839

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter requesting a blessing for Mr. [Name] and his family has been received. I will mention him for whatever he needs when I am at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding your question as to whether they should move to another country: It is already known what our master and teacher, the head of all the Diaspora, the Rambam, ruled in his Yad HaChazakah, Hilchos De’os, beginning of chapter six: A person must attach himself to tzaddikim and sit with the wise always, etc., and distance himself from the wicked who walk in darkness so that he does not learn from their deeds, etc. And if... he cannot go to a country where the customs are good, etc., he should sit alone by himself, etc., and go out to caves, crevices, and deserts.

It is therefore understood that if there is room to say—as you write in your letter—that by moving to a new place they will be in the environment or under the influence of the aforementioned types of people, then it is clearly better to sit alone or go to the desert than to move there. May Hashem, who feeds and sustains all, provide them with their livelihood in a kosher and tranquil manner, and may they be able to increase their strength in the study of our holy Torah and in the performance of His mitzvos with hiddur.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2840

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Tammuz, in which you write that you have drawn somewhat closer to the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, etc. Since you yourself emphasize "somewhat," it is understood that you recognize this is not sufficient. According to the words of our Sages, "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him," the matter depends on you to increase your efforts in the aforementioned according to your ability. This is what is expected of you: to study the teachings of Chassidus—in addition to your study of the revealed Torah—with true dedication and diligence. For the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, the *neshamta d'oraysa* (the soul of the Torah), adds vitality to one’s study of the revealed Torah and the performance of *mitzvos*.

Regarding the notification of your brother’s Bar Mitzvah on Tisha B’Av—may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness—surely your brother will begin the study of the holy *Tanya*. This will be a preparation and a good beginning for *avodas Hashem* in a way that will fulfill in him, "The matter is very close to you, in your mouth and in your heart, to perform it," upon which the *Tanya* is founded, as per the language of *Rabbeinu HaZaken* in the *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*.

Surely you are keeping the three *shiurim* that are appropriate for every soul, established by *Kvod Kedushas Moreinu V'Rabbeinu Admur* [the Rayatz], *ztzukulleh"h nbg"m zya*—namely, the well-known *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—and you are endeavoring that your friends keep them as well, for the merit of the many depends upon you.

With blessings,

On behalf of *Kvod Kedushas Admur Shlita*

## 2842

B”H, 3 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished,
Rabbi Yaakov, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

Regarding your letter of 26 Tammuz: The reason I did not cite the Yerushalmi in Rosh Hashanah (Chapter 4, Halacha 1) concerning what is stated in the maamar of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, from Rosh Hashanah 5703, is because according to the Yerushalmi, the fact that we do not blow the shofar on Rosh Hashanah that falls on Shabbos is a matter of Torah law, not Rabbinic law. This aligns with the initial thought (*k’salka da’atach*) of Rav Chama bar Chanina in the Babylonian Talmud. See also the Sifra, Parshas Behar (this teaching is also cited in the Yerushalmi there). Even though many commentators on the Sifra suggest that in the Sifra it is merely an *asmachta* (a scriptural allusion), and see also the Pnei Yehoshua on Rosh Hashanah 4:1 regarding this—in any event, the Yerushalmi is not relevant to the maamar of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

As for your suggestion that the Yerushalmi does not hold by the decree of Rabbah, and that it follows the opinion of Ben Azzai—as cited in the Yerushalmi in Shabbos and also transcribed in Tosafos (Shabbos 5b)—this cannot be said. For the decree of Rabbah is also the rationale for the laws of Megillah and Lulav, and there, there is no derivation from a verse. Furthermore, even according to the Yerushalmi, it is held to be forbidden, as per the anonymous Mishnah. Regarding the fact that the Rif would blow the shofar on Rosh Hashanah that fell on Shabbos, his reasoning is explained: in his opinion, **nowadays** we blow the shofar in any place that has a distinguished Beis Din, even if they are not *semuchim* (ordained). See the Ran, the Ritva, and the Milhamos on Rosh Hashanah there.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the prostate surgery—that since it comes about due to illness, it is "in the hands of Heaven," etc.: Aside from the fact that in such a case, while the beginning is in the hands of Heaven, the end is in the hands of man—the actual surgery, regarding which there are several opinions (cited in Otzar HaPoskim to Even HaEzer, siman 5, see there)—the procedure in **this case** has no connection to the loss of the ability to procreate. For in the vast majority of cases, this surgery is performed because the prostate begins to press on the passages, and consequently, the semen and urine are released slowly. It is understood that this is not a matter of castration at all.

Likewise, regarding what you wrote that he is elderly and not capable of procreating, etc.: It is puzzling how one can determine, and who is it that can determine, if he is still capable of procreating. I have never heard that doctors act in such a manner, other than based on a **mere** conjecture that from a certain age, most people do not have children. Furthermore, what you wrote to be lenient because the surgery is not on the testicles but near the penis—I also did not understand the practical difference (*nafka mina*), for the Gemara states (Yevamos 75b) that "a crushed one" refers to all of them.

With respect and blessing.

## 2843

B"H, 3 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—in which you write that although you are satisfied with the transfer to..., for the time being, your salary is not sufficient for your needs, and this is affecting your state of mind.

It is surprising that after you have seen with your own eyes the kindness of Hashem toward you, you do not have sufficient faith in His ability to certainly continue to guide you with His kindness in the future and lead you out of your straits. Even if, for reasons not understood by us, the matter is delayed, only the Creator of the world, who knows the future and what is truly good, has the ability to decide in what manner it is best to bring a person and his family to their true happiness, both materially and spiritually. If this is true even regarding people whose situation has diminished compared to what it was previously, and is also lesser in relation to their surroundings and acquaintances, then it is certainly clear regarding those whose situation has improved compared to the past. In these difficult months, your situation is certainly better in relation to many in your surroundings who, nevertheless, do not despair, G-d forbid. Certainly, you and your wife, may she live, should not lose heart, G-d forbid, or become saddened. We have already seen and witnessed in practice that the more a person’s level of *bitachon* grows, and the more they view their future with **simcha**, the sooner the realization of these matters will be brought about in practice.

I hope that soon you will gladden me with good news regarding all of the above, both regarding yourself and regarding your wife, may she live.

With blessings.

## 2844

2844

B"H, 3 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To Anash and the residents of Kfar Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom Rav and blessings without end!

Your *pan* was received, which I read before the *Rosh Chodesh* of Menachem Av at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*, our *Nasi* and the *Nasi* of Yisrael. It surely awakens *rachamei shamayim* for each and every one of you regarding whatever you may need, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

My words have already been said many times, based on what is explained in many places in *Chassidus*: that the *hemshech* from the source must be drawn down specifically here below, in this world, which is precisely the *dirah lo yisbarach*. This is accomplished through the act of *tzedakah*, as is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* in various chapters. The vessel for this is the concept of *shalom*, as it concludes our Torah in *Shas*: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, found no vessel to hold blessing for Yisrael other than *shalom*." The declaration of the *Tzemach Tzedek* is already well known: *Aleph-Beis*—*ahavah* (love) and *berachah* (blessing). To the extent that they increase in the *Aleph*, the Holy One, Blessed be He, is guaranteed to increase in the *Beis*. Further elaboration for you is surely unnecessary.

In these days, which, as our prophets foretold, will soon be transformed into joy and gladness, the cause of this—the cause of our final *galus*, as our Sages of blessed memory state in *Yoma* 9b—will also be rectified. And in the rectification of *d'is-hapecha* from one extreme to the other—darkness to light and bitterness to sweetness—there will be a multiplication of *shalom*, a multiplication of *ahavah*, and consequently, a multiplication of *hashpa'ah*, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

I await good tidings in all the aforementioned categories, for one is dependent upon the other.

## 2846

2846

B"H, 3 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from 4 Menachem Av, and as you requested, I am answering it out of turn.

The content is that a shidduch is being proposed to you where all the details are suitable, and it appears that this is the case from both sides, except that from the place where you come, there were people who were careful not to enter into a shidduch with a divorcee.

Regarding this, despite what is brought on this matter in several seforim, even in those times they were only careful about the aforementioned in specific, exceptional cases. Especially in our times, and specifically when the woman is a kosher woman, etc., in my opinion, you should move forward with the matter. Since our Sages of blessed memory have said that a second marriage is according to one’s deeds, you must increase your study of Torah—both in the revealed aspects of Torah and in the inner dimensions of Torah, which is the teachings of Chassidus—and in the performance of mitzvos with hiddur. Furthermore, until after the wedding—may it be in a good and auspicious hour—you should give a few coins to tzedakah each weekday before davening. May Hashem grant you success in building your home as an everlasting edifice, a Jewish, Chassidishe home. It is well known the story of our Sages of blessed memory (Bereishis Rabbah, end of Chapter 17) regarding the chassidah (stork) that was divorced and subsequently remarried, etc., which teaches that even for such a case—Heaven forbid—He made him a tzaddik.

With blessings.

## 2851

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, R' Nissan, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 27 Tammuz: Thank you for the good news regarding the increase in the number of male and female students. Surely, there is an increase in quality as well.

What concerns me is that it appears from your letter that the age of the students is only up to thirteen. It is understood that you must make the greatest effort to ensure that at least a significant portion remain to study even after that age. Even if this is contrary to the local custom until now, you must nevertheless endeavor to explain that the profession of a teacher, shochet, and the like, is also a matter of livelihood—and, on the contrary, a livelihood that provides both material and spiritual sustenance together. Surely you will consult among yourselves to find the appropriate explanation and the suitable manner of presenting it; there is salvation in a multitude of counselors.

You conclude your letter by mentioning that a number of students will be traveling to the colony vacation. Surely, in addition to the teachers who will be with them permanently, you yourselves will visit there at the beginning and from time to time. The virtue of "entering and exiting" is well known—that even the mere possibility of this alone also brings rectification.

With blessings for success in your holy work and in your personal affairs.

#### ***2851***

**R' Nissan, may he live:** Pinson, Casablanca.

## 2852

B"H, 10 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt speedily), Lod Branch,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of 27 Tammuz, in which you write regarding the founding of your branch and the election of the committee.

May it be the will of Hashem that the "desire of Hashem" [chafetz Hashem] should succeed in their hands to disseminate the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs—in their immediate surroundings and in their wider surroundings as well. This dissemination will bring additional light, strength, and vitality to the study of the revealed Torah and the performance of mitzvos with hiddur. This is, of course, based on the language of the holy Zohar (Vol. III, 152a), which calls this [Chassidus] the "soul of the Torah"—for the more the existence of the soul is emphasized and becomes visible, the more it adds to the vitality of the body as a whole, and to the vitality of every single limb within it.

The analogy is understood.

And according to the words of our Sages, "It is not the study that is the essential thing, but the deed," you will surely continue all of the above through actual practice—that is, the actual dissemination regarding others, and the drawing down of Chassidus for yourselves, in actual deed.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the precise phrasing **"the desire of Hashem" [chafetz Hashem]**—for the desire of Hashem is the inwardness of the will; taanug—your involvement will also be with an inner desire, for actions performed out of true delight are the most successful.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 23, p. 430, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

## 2852

B.H., 10 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To my dear friend, the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who occupies himself with communal needs,
R' Azriel Zelig, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

With some delay, I learned of the passing of his sister—may she live a long and good life—Feiga, a"h. May Hashem comfort him among the other mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim, and may he know no further sorrow or distress, G-d forbid.

I was also deeply shaken just now by the news of the passing of the brilliant Gaon and distinguished Chossid, who served the community with self-sacrifice, etc., etc., R' Avraham Chaim Naeh, a"h. Surely you will provide the details regarding how and what happened. It is also worthwhile to take precautions (bavarenen) in a timely manner regarding the manuscripts and seforim that he left behind. That is to say, regarding the manuscripts that remain, you should make every possible effort to have them printed. In particular, he wrote to me some time ago that he was occupied with printing a portion of Ketzos HaShulchan. Furthermore, if there are any Chassidic manuscripts or valuable seforim in his possession, perhaps it is possible to exchange them for Kehot publications or handle them in another way and send them here. It is understood that this applies to both manuscripts and seforim that are not already here. I thank you in advance for your efforts in this matter, and it is understood that "the sooner, the better."

Regarding the suggestion to send [students] to study here: based on what I have observed regarding the influence of the atmosphere of the United States on the avreichim who have come from Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, in the majority of cases it has not been successful thus far. Although the salvation of Hashem can come in the blink of an eye, and since the Torah speaks of the majority, I am doubtful whether this is the right path—to send students here immediately without first attempting the approach I wrote to you about previously (which I am certain you have received in the meantime).

In recent days, I learned that in the Ministry of Torah Education, one of the officials is Dr. Lifshitz, who was previously in Moscow and observed Torah and mitzvos with mesiras nefesh. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, involved him in several activities and assisted him in his affairs. Surely, if one were to stir the chords of his hiskashrus to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and explain to him that these are the very same activities and the very same matters, he would certainly assist with all his might. I will await good news regarding this. If you only find the appropriate approach to the aforementioned individual, you will certainly succeed. You have my permission to tell him that I prompted you regarding this, or even to tell him that the initiative came from me, adding my bewilderment that until now I have not found his name among those involved in the vineyard of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, knowing as I do his attitude toward the affairs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, at a time when it involved actual danger.

I was pleased by what you wrote, that it is your intention to join R' Z.S. and R' M. Weber, may they live, and that the main focus of their work is the rescue of the youth in Eretz Yisrael within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. This is a very, very correct matter. It is understood that whatever requires correction should be corrected, but the work and the matters themselves are internal, Chassidic matters.

With blessings for Chassidic nachas from all your children, may they live, in good health and with peace of mind.

## 2853

B"H, 10 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs,
Rabbi Yisroel Noach, may he live.

... I derive pleasure from the stories of Tzaddikim that you transcribe in your letter, and surely you will continue to do so in the future, and thank you in advance.

He said that the Tzaddik of Shpola told the Alter Rebbe, "You have begun to write a 'Sefer of Tzaddikim,' and the world cannot bear it. Accusations were aroused Above, and it was decreed that it be burned, and I will ascend to Heaven in that very flame." And so it was; at the time of the fire, the holy Tzaddik, the Saba of Shpola, passed away.

Blessings for a healthy and happy summer, and may you have good tidings.

## 2854

2854

B"H, 11 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned Rabbi Menachem Zev, may he live, HaLevi,

Shalom u’Bracha!

... Thank you for beginning to work on the matter of the form of the letters. Surely, when you have any new findings regarding this, you will inform me. It is understood that you may write to those you mentioned that you are gathering information on this at my request.

... I am surprised that, apparently, the author in all his books avoids mentioning anything from Chabad **sefarim**, even though he mentioned the Tzemach Tzedek himself once. It should be explained to him that it is a simple and absolute matter for all of Klal Yisrael that this is a part of our holy Torah. It is well known: (a) The ruling of the Alter Rebbe in Hilchos Talmud Torah (2:10) that a Jewish person must, during the course of his life, study the entire Torah at least [once]; (b) The teaching of our Sages, "Whoever says this teaching is pleasant, this teaching is not..." (Eruvin 64a); (c) To inform him and explain the crux of the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, Nasi of Israel, in the *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*, regarding the rejection of the opinion of those who exempt themselves from this study; (d) The condition of the precedence of *na’aseh* to *nishma*—that it was specifically through this that Bnei Yisrael received the Torah. This prerequisite was necessary not only on the 6th of Sivan in the year 2448 from the creation of the world, but also from then on, every single day (since every day we receive the Torah, as the language of the blessing of *Birchas HaTorah* is "**gives**" [in the present tense]). And if this prerequisite is necessary for the *Pshat, Remez, Drush,* and *Sod* of the Torah (Zohar Vol. III, 202b), even though it is closer to the *neshamah* as it is in the body, then all the more so is it necessary regarding the *neshamta d’oraysa* (the soul of the Torah).

It is possible that the above is too sharp for the aforementioned author. You may change some of the wording, but in any case, not the content—and perhaps that will suffice. You may begin your letter to him with a request for a great pardon, etc., etc., and by citing the saying of the wise man (also brought in the letter of the Tzemach Tzedek written to Mandelstam, I believe) that truth is loved above all else.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 2855

B"H, 12 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker,
Rabbi Shlomo Chaim, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what I have written previously concerning vacation time: my perspective on this is well known. The point is that the custom of some to leave the walls of the yeshivah during the days of Selichos and the majority of the month of Tishrei to be at home is, in all yeshivos in general—and certainly in a yeshivah whose purpose is Torah study with yiras shamayim specifically—completely contrary to logic, as is understood.

Even if, for whatever reason, it is necessary to grant a vacation during those weeks, one must strive to the utmost that the students spend the majority of those days, and specifically the most essential ones, within the walls of the yeshivah. From this, it is also understood and necessary that it is the duty and the privilege of the *rebbeim* and *roshei yeshivah* who are concerned with the students' benefit in this direction to also be within the walls of the yeshivah during these days. Even though it is possible, and even likely, that their families may not be entirely satisfied with such an arrangement, the merit of the many depends upon them, and to elaborate further on this would be superfluous...

## 2855

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs, Rabbi Nissan Nemanov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote about the young man who touched his beard: one should have gathered friends to speak to him about this, especially since his older brother conducts himself as is proper.

You should also explain to him, based on what is brought in *Sefer Derech Mitzvosecha*, Part II, in the entry *V'hu Rachum*, that the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* (rectifications of the beard) correspond to the thirteen attributes of mercy. Since all those who cannot claim their needs from Hashem through the attribute of *din* (judgment) must rely instead on the attribute of *chesed* and *rachamim* (kindness and mercy), then—as a matter of *middah kineged middah* (measure for measure)—they must leave the *tikkunei dikna* intact. See there at length. It is therefore understood that a young man who needs to arrange his livelihood, a good *shidduch*, etc., and who is in need of the *rachamim* of Hashem in general, must be meticulous regarding the thirteen *tikkunei dikna*. You will surely find the appropriate words to convey this to him.

Regarding your question about your acquaintance... since there is a doctor who says that surgery is not necessary, and that he only needs to be careful with his eating and drinking, etc., he should conduct himself in accordance with this instruction and strengthen his *bitachon* (trust) in Hashem, who heals all flesh and performs wonders. Peace of mind is one of the most effective remedies for ailments such as these.

Regarding the same person’s question about the fact that he cannot find buyers for the house he purchased for his livelihood: he should take Hashem as a partner by pledging to charity a little more than a *maaser* (tithe) of the **profit**—and it is even better to approach a *chomesh* (fifth)—and the aforementioned Partner is guaranteed to bring blessing and success, in accordance with the teaching, "Tithe so that you may become wealthy."

Once he sees *hashgacha pratis* (Divine providence) in this, it would be worthwhile for him to continue engaging in the purchase of houses for livelihood in this manner, in addition to engaging in his work—with *an impet* (momentum)—and with the necessary intervals of rest.

With blessing.

## 2,857

2,857

B”H, 12 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 4th of Parshas Matos, in which you write regarding the state of your livelihood, which is not as it should be, and that you are, G-d forbid, in debt, etc.

The conclusion of your letter, regarding your lack of joy, stands in contradiction to the beginning of the letter, where you describe what you have been through—in your own words, that you were miraculously left among the *she'eris hapleitah* and have built a family, etc.

You should draw an *a fortiori* inference (*kal v’chomer*) for yourself: If it was within the power of the *Ribono shel Olam* to save you from the events of the past years and to grant you success in building a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*, then how much more so will He, who feeds and sustains all, provide you with your livelihood and the livelihood of your household. This depends solely on *bitachon* and the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*. Absolute *bitachon*—that the *Ribono shel Olam* will provide you with what you and your household need—is effective *klapai shamaya* (in the Heavenly realms), especially when combined with *tzedakah*, regarding which the *Kadosh Baruch Hu* asks, "Test Me now with this," so that you may become wealthy.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success, and may you bring good news regarding all of the above.

You are surely aware of the *takanah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zia*, which is applicable to everyone: to recite *Tehillim* every day after *davening* Shacharis—according to the division of *Tehillim* for the days of the month—and likewise to study each day a few verses of *Chumash* with the commentary of Rashi from the weekly *parsha*.

With blessings for livelihood in both material and spiritual matters, with peace of mind.

## 2858

2858

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5714

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is incumbent upon each and every one of us, both those in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) and those abroad, to know the clear truth: that one’s personal participation in the affairs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is the same now as it was then. Just as during his time in this world my father-in-law, the Rebbe, stood and served to bestow upon those who participated—both them and their households—everything they required in body and soul, so too now, in accordance with the custom of the faithful shepherds of Yisrael, he stands and serves on high to bestow upon those who participate in his affairs—both them and their households—everything they require in body and soul. Indeed, this is even more so than during his lifetime, as is brought in the Zohar and explained in the Iggeres HaKodesh of our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 27, and its commentary.

These influences that he arouses are not merely a salary for work, like a check recorded from the appropriate institution; rather, their essence is in children, life, and proper health, and that one’s livelihood should be with blessing, etc. Further elaboration is unnecessary.

With blessings for success in your holy work and in your personal affairs.

## 2859

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your two letters from the 18th of Tammuz and the 4th of Menachem Av, in which you ask my opinion regarding changing your channel of parnassah.

Having worked all these years in the holy Yeshivah Tomchei Temimim and seeing that this has brought you hatzlacha in your affairs, one should, chas v'shalom, not abandon this channel and vessel. Therefore, it appears to me that you should remain in your holy position; on the contrary, if possible, you should increase your efforts in this work. One should hope that the yeshivah will grow, for which you should also exert yourself, and this will presumably also bring an increase in salary and parnassah.

It goes without saying that if there can be an additional matter of parnassah in a way that would not interfere by even a hair’s breadth with your holy work, it does not matter, but only with that condition.

May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the pregnancy of your wife, tichyeh, and may she complete her days in the proper manner and give birth to living and enduring offspring.

With blessings.

## 2861

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Refael Nachman, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from Motzaei Shabbos Korach, 19 Tammuz, and the *pidyon nefesh* which I will read at an auspicious time at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May Hashem grant you success and may you have good news to report regarding all that is written therein.

Thank you for writing, at least briefly, regarding the *farbrengens*. I am certain that you will continue to do so in the future, and with more detail and length, and I thank you in advance.

Regarding what you write—that there are two opinions concerning someone who was awake all night: whether to *daven* and then go to rest, or to sleep for a few hours first and then *daven*—

It is impossible to establish general rules for this, as it depends on the clarity of mind of each individual. There are times when one’s *davening* will be more settled if one sleeps in the interim, and there are times when, on the contrary, if one sleeps for only a few hours—not as much as one requires—one’s *davening* will become confused afterward. Since *miltah d'levushai yakira* (the matter is of great importance), I once heard from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that sometimes his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, would sleep for a period of time on the morning after the night of Shavuos and then *daven*. Whether this was his constant practice or only on occasion, I did not hear.

Regarding what you write about the story of R' Yaakov Meshullam, it seems to me that it is printed in the book *Sipurim Yekarim* by R' Y. Kaydaner, but the book is not currently at hand for me to check.

It is surely unnecessary to urge you to bring the esteemed [name], who is G-d-fearing, etc., closer, since he has several challenges and is struggling intensely. We must fulfill the commandment to "walk in His ways" (and some say this is a Torah-level obligation). Just as the Holy One, blessed be He—according to what is explained in the Midrash—occupies Himself with the deer that comes to His flock, with special attention and care for its needs, just as He does with the sheep and lambs in the flock, so too must we walk in this path, as is understood.

With blessings for proper health and to report good news, both generally and specifically.

***

**2861**

**The story of R' Yaakov Meshullam:** See *Sefer HaSichos Kayitz 5700*, p. 96. *Shmuos V'Sipurim*, Vol. 1 (new edition, pp. 49-51).

## 2862

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your request for a blessing for your son who is in the army has been received. I will mention him at a time of favor at the Tziyun, that Hashem should protect him wherever he may be and that he should return home in peace at the proper time.

Surely you will explain to your son, may he live, that in order to draw down and receive the blessings of Hashem, one must create channels and vessels for this, which is the conduct according to the Torah and its mitzvos. This is possible even while in the army, in accordance with the democratic system of this country. Listed below are articles on this subject which it would be worthwhile for your son, may he live, to read.

In particular, you must engrave upon the tablet of your son’s heart the obligation to put on tefillin every day, which requires only a few moments. If it is impossible to do so in the morning, the time for it is all day long. Beyond the personal obligation (*chovas gavra*) involved, the mitzvah of tefillin is a *segulah* to protect our Jewish brethren in the army. This is known to us from the last war, where all those who turned to my father-in-law, the Rebbe [of saintly memory], for a blessing and followed his instruction to put on tefillin every day, returned home in peace.

With blessings,
