## 2863

2863

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letters of the 10th and 7th of Menachem Av, along with the enclosure. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you the merit and success to continue this matter further, following the good start you have made, just as we discussed when you were here.

It is a well-known statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that when a person opens their heart to the Ribono shel Olam even to the size of the eye of a needle, the Ribono shel Olam opens up paths of blessing and success like the *Pesach HaUlam* (the entrance to the Sanctuary) that existed in the Beis HaMikdash. It is further explained in Chassidus regarding the concept of the *Pesach HaUlam*: all the entrances to the Beis HaMikdash had doors, and consequently, they were sometimes open and sometimes closed. However, the entrance to the *Ulam* had no door and was always open to those who were already standing in the *Ezrah*. This is the promise of the Ribono shel Olam: when one makes a start, even to the size of the eye of a needle, the blessing and success from the Ribono shel Olam is always open, like the *Pesach HaUlam*.

The *kabbalos* will be sent once they are received from the relevant offices.

With blessings for long, good years for you and your wife *tichyeh*, and may you quickly, with alacrity, **and with joy**, continue the fulfillment of your promise and the desires of your hearts for the good.

#### ***2863***

In continuation of letter 2827 above.

## 2864

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Menachem Av, I am surprised by your writing that the difference between last year and this year is "beyond the natural order," and judging by the tone of your letter, you do not mean this in a positive sense.

In my opinion, if you recall the situation regarding health and take into account that your wife, may she live and be well, is expecting in a good and auspicious hour, it is clear that it is indeed "beyond the natural order," thank G-d, but in a positive direction.

And the fact that for a short while there is less in the bank account balances is not a deficiency in practical matters, and certainly not in matters of *banai, chayei, u’mezonei* (children, life, and sustenance).

It is a known statement of our Sages (Sotah 48b) that one who has enough for the day's expenses and worries about tomorrow is among those of "little faith." If one is, thank G-d, provided with cash not only for the day but for the month as well—let alone for several years—yet one worries about what will be many years from now, and when the bank deposit shrinks, the worry grows even more for the years ahead, and one forgets in the process that this has no value and is not in the same category as the improvement of health and the fulfillment of one’s heart's desires for good—this is a very great *helem v’hester* (concealment).

Self-evidently, I do not mean this as a lecture. It is simply a pity and a source of pain when a Yid who has every reason to be in *simcha*—not only in spiritual matters but even in physical matters, meaning that the *simcha* is not only from the *neshamah* but also from the body, from both the *nefesh elokis* and the *nefesh habahamis*—is instead worried and distressed about what the One who sustains and provides for all with kindness and mercy will do in several years regarding his livelihood and the livelihood of his household.

As we are already in the joyous days, and according to the expression in the Zohar (Yisro 78b) that from the tenth of Av, *Eisav* is lost and not found, so too should all these concealments and enticements that come from *Eisav's* side be lost and not found. Then will be fulfilled "with all your heart," *b'levav shalem*—with two *beis*s—"serve Hashem with *simcha*."

With blessings.

## 2865

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your question about those teachers who are suspected of being unsuitable for their positions: it is already a known ruling of our Torah that in the education of students, one must consider the benefit of the students, and in general, the benefit of the many overrides the benefit of the individual. However, in this matter, one must take into account that education involves not only knowledge but also dedication. Therefore, when deliberating regarding a specific teacher, one must weigh both factors together and only then make a decision.

Regarding an increase in teaching hours on the part of the teachers, it is correct and necessary...

## 2886

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I confirm receipt of your letters... Upon receiving them, I was reminded of the Sages' teaching: "Tobiah sinned and Zigud was lashed," which echoes the content of your letter. Even if one were to say that you are one hundred percent correct in your claims... in any event, the conclusion you draw—that because of this you do not cooperate with them or do not work with the necessary vigor—is that the ones who suffer are the students and the teachers; that is to say, the affairs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Where is the sound logic in that?

As in the aforementioned teaching of our Sages, the intention here is not to justify Tobiah, but to clarify the matter: while one must endeavor, to the extent possible, to ensure that Tobiah ceases to sin, it is **obvious** that there is no place to lash Zigud. The analogy is understood...

I wish only to emphasize the point... that I am certain that, in the end, all debts will be cleared. And while I understand that it is difficult to wait, I repeat what I wrote then: Yisrael—who are believers, the children of believers, in Hashem and in Moshe His servant, and in the *atpashtuta d'Moshe* (the extension of Moshe) in every generation, which in our generation is my father-in-law, the Rebbe, whose institutions these are—know that the compensation for one's labor is not merely the check... which will also be paid eventually, but also *bnei, chayei, u'mezoni revichei* (children, life, and abundant sustenance). This means that blessing will rest upon one's sustenance, which is worth many times more than the value of the check. Further elaboration is surely superfluous...

## 2868

2868

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Menachem Av and those preceding it,

I was pleased to read what you write regarding your care in davening with a minyan, your efforts to influence others, and your reviewing of Torah by heart while walking to work. The matter of the "purification of the atmosphere" achieved through this is beyond description, as is brought down in the *kruz* of *hisorerus* from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the review of Mishnayos by heart. It would be appropriate for you to memorize several chapters of *Tanya* and review them by heart as well, while going to and from work.

Regarding your question as to how to distribute the *maaser* that you set aside for *tzedakah*: I answered someone else who asked a similar question that if he wishes, he may send half to be distributed at my discretion, and distribute the other half himself—allocating half of that to the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), and the other half as he sees fit. And in accordance with the warning of our Sages, of blessed memory, not to be overly meticulous with *tzedakah*, one should set aside at least some amount beyond the *maaser*.

With blessings to the above effect.

#### ***2868***

**By heart... purification of the atmosphere:** See at length above, Vol. 1, Letter 132. The words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on this matter are transcribed there as well.

## 2869

2869

B"H, 20 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, [Name of] Branch, may Hashem protect them,
May they live.

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive a report of your work, and surely you are already beginning to organize the preparations for the month of Elul and for the time following the summer. This should also influence your entire future program, keeping in mind that the month of Elul is the month of *cheshbon* (accounting) for the entire year, as well as the month of mercy. It positions a Yid so that he may subsequently, on Rosh Hashanah and throughout the month of Tishrei, merit a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for himself and all his household.

This preparation must encompass both aspects of human conduct, as human deeds are categorized: the obligations of man to the Ribono shel Olam (*bein adam laMakom*) and the obligations of man to his fellow (*bein adam lachaveiro*).

This is also the indication found in the name of the month — *Elul* — as explained in *sefarim*: it is an acronym for (a) *"Ani l'dodi v'dodi li"* ("I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me"), which encompasses all matters of *bein adam laMakom*, and (b) *"Ish l're'eihu u'matanos l'evyonim"* ("A man to his friend and gifts to the poor"), which are the matters between man and man.

When one makes a proper accounting in both these areas of human life, the Borei Olam helps one to establish oneself with good resolutions for the days, weeks, and months that are to come, and they then arrive for good and for blessing, for us and for all Yisrael.

With blessings for success in expanding your work with breadth and with joy, and, needless to say, also increasing the number of members as much as possible, as is known the instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory, that whoever sustains one soul of Yisrael is as if he sustained an entire world.

#### ***2869***

A similar version was sent to several branches throughout the world. It was sent at the end of Menachem Av and the beginning of Elul. One of these versions is printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 14, p. 274.

2870

And may Hashem join them together, and through this, may they be elevated from a pure place to one that is holier, as is explained in *Tanya* that through an *is'arusa d'lesata* comes an *is'arusa d'le'eila* to a place that is higher and more exalted. Consequently, the *hashpaos* will arrive without obstacles or delays, in the manner explained in *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Parshas Korach*.

## 2871

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...The essence of my intention regarding him—specifically concerning his *yiras shamayim*—is that he should have a full beard. For even if you were to say that he maintains in his heart (and I am doubtful of this) that the *halacha* follows the opinion of those who permit [shaving] and not the opinion of Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, nevertheless, as a rabbi and a spiritual leader who must serve as an example of what a *yirei shamayim* looks like—and from whom others consequently learn in this matter as well—he is causing others to stumble and transgress, *chas v'shalom*, five Torah prohibitions. This is explained in the *sicha* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, zy"a*, printed in the *Kuntres* of the Chicago visit.

And since he is already married—may he have long, good years—the question of a *shidduch* is no longer an obstacle. The only explanation I have for why he does not conduct himself in this manner is simply the impulse of "giving in to the world." This is like the complaint of the prophet already in the time of the First Temple, that many of the Children of Israel declared, "We shall be like all the nations." How much more so is this impulse prevalent in the era of *ikvesa d'Meshicha*. The reason I emphasized that he is a "Lubavitcher *chanich*" is for the simple reason that only Lubavitcher *chanichim* born in America are particular about this and similar matters...

With blessings for success in your general and personal affairs.

## 2872

## 2774

B”H, 26 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write that the matter of forgetfulness has intensified for you, etc.: generally, this depends on two factors. 

a) When one studies without desire or interest, the study does not stem from the inner core of the will, and consequently, this causes forgetfulness, as is hinted at in the Iggeres HaKodesh of our Alter Rebbe in the Kuntres Acharon, in the discourse beginning *Dovid Zemiros*, and at length in the *Reshimah* on *Eichah* by the Tzemach Tzedek. 

b) A lack of caution regarding *kedushas habris*. 

When you strengthen your resolve in these two areas—and this is appropriate for the *parsha* of the week, "Behold, I set before you today a blessing, that you will listen, etc." (and the precision is well-known, that in the blessing it is written simply "that you will listen," and there is no doubt in this, unlike the conclusion of the verse—"if"—and the prerequisite for this is essential)—then the matter of memory will also improve, and you will succeed in your studies in both *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2875

B"H, 26 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter in which you write regarding your order of study and conclude that foreign thoughts distract you from the exertion in the avodah of tefillah: It is already well-known that guarding the holiness of the bris and the tongue diminishes foreign thoughts. Furthermore, one should have a sefer or a Siddur open before him, so that the letters shine and drive away thoughts that are not of their subject matter. According to what is explained in Likutei Torah at the end of Parshas Kedoshim, when the letters of Torah in general—and specifically the letters of the pnimiyus haTorah—are engraved in one’s mind, this gradually diminishes the letters of thought that oppose this. May Hashem grant you success, and may you have good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2876

B.H., 27 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, distinguished scholar, etc., Rabbi Yaakov, may he live, Hakohen.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter, and I waited to reply until the arrival of your sefer, *Responsa Beis Yaakov*, which you mentioned in your letter that you were sending. It has recently arrived, and I offer you my heartfelt thanks for this gift.

Regarding what you wrote—that it is proven in a *maamar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that when Rosh Hashanah falls on Shabbos there is no *tiki'as shofar* from the Torah, in accordance with the opinion of the Yerushalmi—I have already noted that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, writes explicitly that this is only *miderabanan*. The Admurim who preceded him in this matter write the same, as does the Alter Rebbe. Furthermore, in the *maamar* printed in the *Siddur*, it is also explained why we blow the shofar from the Torah, and that it is only the *Rabbanan* who issued a decree regarding this; see there.

As for my suggestion to examine the *Pnei Yehoshua* at the beginning of *daf* 4 of Rosh Hashanah, it is because there is a remarkable point there. It seems he holds that even according to the *Shas Bavli*, there is room to explain that there is no *tiki'as shofar* on Shabbos even from the Torah—a position for which I have not yet found a parallel.

Regarding the matter of the prostate, which you describe as a form of castration caused by illness: the illness of the prostate is a condition that does not affect procreation at all. As is well known, the illness is an enlargement of the prostate, which consequently narrows the urinary tract. Similarly, regarding the matter of an elderly man who is no longer capable of procreating: it is obvious that according to *din*, such a category exists, and it is relevant to the appointment of the Sanhedrin and to several other matters. However, it requires study to find a criterion that would be absolute according to the law of the **Torah**—that a certain individual is unfit to procreate due to his old age—since it is obvious that this does not depend on age. And this is simple.

With respect and blessings.

As is my custom, out of affection for the subject, I looked through your sefer, though due to the pressures of the days, only in passing. As a sign, I noted at least three points:

**Responsa, Section 6, 91a:** "Even though there is no need for the feather..."—so writes the Rambam. The source of this requires study. In all the editions I have seen, **it is not there.** In any case, it is puzzling to explain his intent as referring to a case where one needs the feathers themselves, for if so, what is he teaching us? And in such a case, what difference does it make in general whether one needs the feather?

Regarding what you wrote at the end, that the law regarding cutting nails according to the opinion of the Rivash requires study: see the *Magen Avraham* there, who cites him, and in the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, there—for an explanation of the Rivash's opinion, see *Responsa Tzemach Tzedek*, *Shaar HaMiluim*, *Chiddushim L'Shabbos*, 94b.

**Beginning of Section 24:** Note the *Tzofnas Paneach* (by the Gaon of Rogatchov) on the Rambam, *Hilchos Ma'achalos Assuros*, Chapter 4, Halacha 8; *Hilchos Shechitah*, beginning of Chapter 5; and in many other places.

**End of Section 54:** Citing the Ra'avad of Ponevezh that we do not find [a prohibition], etc., and it is kosher without question. Based on this, one should be able to write this even *l'chatchilah*! And what great strength is required to reject the opinion of the *Pischei Teshuvah* in the name of the *Ginas Veradim*—in actual practice! And it is forbidden to act contrary to the *Pischei Teshuvah* and the *Ginas Veradim*, who merited that the Jewish people accepted their ruling. See also *Sdei Chemed*, *Asifas Dinim*, *Ma'areches Get*, Section 17, subsection 37.

**Regarding what you wrote there about *Birkas Hamazon*:** The obligation of *Birkas Hamazon* and *Zimun* begins and is established at the time of eating; if so, there is no difference between the nights of Pesach and the rest of the year. And one does not respond to a witticism.

## 2,777

B"H, 27 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding your work against the mission, may it be the will of Hashem that this be with outstanding success, in accordance with the words of our Sages, "Whoever sustains one soul of Israel, it is as if he sustained an entire world."

Regarding what you wrote, that you have changed the knot of your tefillin to the Chabad knot: surely you have also changed the inner aspects of the matter. For it is brought in the Zohar, and at greater length in the teachings of Chabad, that tefillin are a matter of the *mochin*. Therefore, when putting them on, one must intend to subjugate the heart and the brain (*mochin d'nukvah* and *mochin d'za*). May you have changed in a manner that is appropriate, such that you immerse (*toivel*—the letters of *bitul*) your mind in the study of *Chochma, Binah,* and *Da'as*—in the teachings of Chassidus Chabad, its guidance, and its customs. May Hashem grant you success in all of the above.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2878

B"H, 27 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your question regarding your brother, who has asked you to study Chassidus with him, and your doubt in this matter since the mikveh is far from the neighborhood where he lives and he only immerses on Erev Yom Kippur—you ask whether or not you should study the aforementioned subject with him.

Now, one detail does not affect the other, for it is understood that the fact that he only immerses on Erev Yom Kippur is entirely unacceptable. This concerns not only the study of Chassidus, but the purity of the body and an increase in the strengthening of faith in general (see Rambam, end of Hilchos Mikvaos), the indwelling of Elokus, etc. This is especially true when we are speaking of youth and those who are in the land upon which the eyes of Hashem are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year. Therefore, you must endeavor to influence your brother to immerse more frequently, as much as possible. At the very least, he should observe the immersion of *Tevilas Ezra*. In place of an immersion for **additional purity** (and not the aforementioned), he should study some Mishnayos from Seder Taharos—it is best to study Maseches Mikvaos—so that in cases of unavoidable circumstances or the like, this replaces the matter of the mikveh as an **additional purity** (and not an immersion from impurity to purity).

Furthermore, it is self-understood that you must study with him, even before his aforementioned conduct changes for the better. The study of Chassidus, which is the *neshamah* of Torah—the *penimiyus* of Torah, the *ilana d'chayei*—is essential in these final generations for the proper fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos, as explained in *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*. For this study draws vitality into the *nefesh elokis*, to the point that through it, the *nefesh habahamis* and the body are also brought to true life through *dveikus* to the *Eitz Chaim*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2,882

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter in which you write that you feel yourself in a low state, even though you are in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim:

It is already known from our Sages, of blessed memory, "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him." Labor is not the same for every individual; it is measured specifically according to the strength one has been given and according to the needs of one’s body and animal soul. Consequently, you should learn with true dedication and self-surrender, and then you will succeed in your studies of both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus.

It is superfluous to add that every individual requires *siyatta d’shmaya* (Heavenly assistance). This is why we say in our *avodah* of *tefillah*, in the first of the blessings where we request our needs: "Grant us from Yourself wisdom, understanding, and knowledge." Therefore, the *avodah* of *tefillah* is essential.

With blessings for success in Torah study with *yiras shamayim*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2883

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in the needs of the community and the needs of the heavens, etc.,
Rabbi R. Sh. Y. (may he live)

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos and the one preceding it: I was pleased with the content of your conversation with Rabbi Kasher (may he live), as my opinion is the same—namely, a negative stance regarding the proposal to make a trip here. Surely you are aware of the cheap publicity that is customary in this country, which, to our great sorrow, has also penetrated the "tent of Torah," etc., and not only in matters of *tomchei d’oraysa*, but also, etc. Happy is the man who is able to avoid this, even if it means "sit and do nothing," and all the more so for one who can redirect the energy and time that would be spent on the aforementioned toward matters of public benefit, especially in the "tent of Torah," which is your beautiful portion, for which you have been privileged from Heaven. Even if they promise that they will refrain from excessive forms of publicity, in the vast majority of cases it is impossible to keep such a promise, for "when you come to a city, follow its customs," and if even angels—literally—ate [in the home of Avraham] for this reason, then all the more so human beings, etc. This is an additional reason, beyond the waste of energy, time, health, and nerves—*nerven*—to a great degree, as we see clearly in those who visit here on missions of any kind. And there are several other reasons for my aforementioned opinion regarding the proposal, and the material **benefit** for the Talmudic Encyclopedia and the like—which cannot be achieved by those who are already here and the many offices—is, in my opinion, extremely doubtful...

With blessings for success in your holy work, with tranquility and peace of mind.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
For a certain reason, the sending of this letter was delayed, and last night Rabbi Gold (may he live) visited me. I was pleased with the way he spoke about you. Naturally, he spoke about the question of your trip here as an aside, saying that it is not a partisan matter but rather for the honor of the Torah, etc. I answered him with a story that occurred a year or more ago, when the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva here wanted to invite you for a visit of several months, and my opinion was negative, because it is not suitable for your health. He replied that in that case, they should ask for a doctor's opinion, and I reiterated my words and my opinion.

## 2885

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks a date—in which you write about what you and your household have been experiencing, and that you do not see success in your affairs, etc., and you conclude by saying that in your soul you are a Jew who wants to fulfill the mitzvos of our Torah, but that you are not observant and do not keep Shabbos, etc.

Now, just as regarding the life of the body: if a person were to speak day and night about how he believes in the benefit of food and wants to receive it and eat it, as long as he does not actually eat, his words will be of no benefit to his body. From time to time he will grow weaker, until eventually he will not even have the strength to speak about the benefit of food. It is exactly the same regarding the life of the neshamah. Even if one speaks frequently about wanting to fulfill the mitzvos and about the benefit of the mitzvos and the like, as long as one does not do so in practice, the neshamah is not strengthened. Since it lacks its necessities, it weakens over time, just as discussed above regarding the body. Consequently, there is no need to search for further reasons for the lack of success in your affairs, for the lack of fulfillment of mitzvos is sufficient to explain the lack of success. And even though we see many people who do not fulfill mitzvos and yet are successful, we do not know the calculations of Hashem Yisbarach, to whom He pays the reward early and to whom He pays the reward later, or the reason for the difference in this. Since you write in your letter that you believe in the Torah, it is already written in the Torah, in the Ten Commandments, regarding the necessity of keeping Shabbos and the reward associated with it, and likewise regarding the other practical mitzvos, even though you do not mention them in your letter.

If you will listen to my advice, then immediately and without delay, have all the mezuzos in your home checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law. Begin to put on tefillin every weekday according to the law, and pray at least the Krias Shema and the Shemoneh Esrei. Immediately institute kosher food in your home, and all of this is in addition to keeping Shabbos. Since you mention the esteemed R' Yona Eidelkop in your letter, he will surely assist you in all the aforementioned matters, and also show you how to put on tefillin, etc. I am confident that when you do this, within a short time you will see success in your affairs.

Awaiting good news and with blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2886

2886

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, as well as the one preceding it. It goes without saying that there was no *kapida* on my part; my inquiry was prompted solely by my desire to know to what extent one can be certain that one is walking on the straight and good path.

It is surely superfluous to remind you of the verse, “And do not hide yourself from your own flesh,” but my intent is this: even though one who is occupied with communal needs is exempt from other obligations, this very work—which requires *siyatta d’shmaya* to the greatest possible degree—necessitates several matters that a private individual is not necessarily obligated in. Among the primary matters brought in various seforim, and also transmitted orally, are: regarding the aspect of *gemillus chasadim*—"one should give a *prutah* to a pauper and then pray"; regarding the aspect of *avodah*—since the *Beis Hamikdash* was destroyed, "prayers were instituted in place of sacrifices"—namely, *tefillah* with *meitinus* (deliberation) and purity. This, at the very least, refers to the caution regarding *tevilas Ezra*. See the Rif and his student, Rabbeinu Yonah, in the first chapter of *Berachos*, in the name of Rav Hai Gaon, that the requirement for *tevilah* was not nullified for *tefillah*, only for Torah study. Even though we do not rule accordingly, everyone agrees that *tefillah* is more readily accepted when accompanied by *tevilah*. This is especially so given what is already known regarding the Rambam: that even though the requirement for *tevilas Ezra* was nullified, he himself never ceased this *tevilah*.

Regarding the aspect of Torah: a fixed study schedule—meaning a fixed time and a fixed commitment of the soul—in the portion of Torah called the "soul of the Torah" (*Zohar*, Vol. III, p. 142a), which is *pnimiyus haTorah*. Just as the revelation of the vitality of a person’s soul is felt and adds vitality to the person’s body, so too is it with the soul and body of the Torah. This is especially true in our generation, *ikvesa d’Meshicha*, where it is known from various sources that the lack of study of *pnimiyus haTorah* prolongs the *galus*. See the introduction of the R’ch”u to *Shaar HaHakdamos*; this is a point agreed upon by all types of Bnei Yisrael, not only among Chassidim, as is also written by the Gra (in his book *Even Shleimah*, if I recall correctly).

With respect and with the blessing of *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah*.

#### ***2886***

**As is also written by the Gra:** See regarding this *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 10, p. 252.

## 2887

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you ask about what is explained in many places in Chassidic teachings regarding matters Above by way of analogy to the human soul—and [you raise the difficulty that] "no thought can grasp Him, etc.," and all the more so for us, who have no business with hidden things.

This is explained at length in the *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*, which is a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, answering someone who asked him the same question as you. You will find the matters explained there as they should be. The main point is that just as in the fulfillment of all mitzvos, it is impossible to succeed except by prioritizing *naaseh* (doing) over *nishma* (understanding—for if *nishma* meant literal hearing, it would be impossible to do before hearing what one is required to do), so too regarding the mitzvah of Torah study in particular, which is equivalent to all the mitzvos, the *naaseh* must precede the *nishma*. That is, one must study in practice, even if for the time being he does not **understand** the necessity of the study, etc. I emphasize the word "understand," because it is certainly **known** to everyone that the study of the inner dimension of Torah—which is the teaching of Chassidus—is a necessity. This is especially true in our generation, where, in addition to what is written in the Zohar (Vol. III, p. 124b) that through this study "the Jewish people will emerge from exile with mercy," it is explained in the introduction of Rav Chaim Vital to *Shaar HaHakdamos* that the lack of study—and consequently, the diminishing of study—prolongs the exile. This refers not only to the exile of the Jewish people, but also to the matter of the *Shechinah* in exile. When each one of us contemplates that by diminishing the study of the inner dimension of Torah, he is, Heaven forbid, keeping the *Shechinah*, the *Knesses Yisrael*, and consequently the Jewish people—souls in bodies—even **one** moment longer in exile and in double and redoubled darkness, the hair on his head will stand on end at the responsibility placed upon him and the matters that depend on the study of the inner dimension of Torah. As for all the questions one may have about this, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well known: the *Yetzer Hara* is an expert at his craft and approaches each person according to his nature; there are those to whom he comes dressed in a silk coat. The test for this is that if one's rationalizations prevent actual *avodah*, their source is the *sitra achra*.

As you requested, I will mention you and your wife, may they live, at the holy gravesite. The *pidyon nefesh* has been received.

Enclosed is an excerpt from the *sicha* of Shabbos Mevarchim, 8 Elul 5751, the content of which is timely for all years and throughout the entire year, and surely you will publicize it in an appropriate manner.

With the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

## 2889

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and involved in communal needs, R' Yaakov, may he live, Shochet and Bodek

Greetings and blessings,

Thank you for the books you mentioned in your letter, which I assume you have already sent. It is understood that you should inform my secretariat regarding the shipping costs, as well as the expenses for your travel concerning these matters. The story told by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding such situations is already well-known: if one does not wish to accept such expenses and desires to "take it upon himself" [to cover them], it ultimately hinders the *avodah*, because the *yetzer hara* has an argument to make. Therefore, you should act according to the verse, "Do not be overly righteous," and inform us of the expenses so they may be settled, along with our thanks.

With blessings for a successful arrangement in both material and spiritual matters, and for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 2891

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 4th of Menachem Av. I am surprised by you, for you have been involved in *Tzivos Hashem* for several years now, yet every time you encounter *he'elem v'hester* (concealment and hiddenness)—to use your own words in your letter—you become discouraged. This is despite the fact that for over eighteen hundred years, the *Shechinah* has been in *galus*, and with Her, the *Knesses Yisrael* and the Jewish people. As the Ramban writes in his letter, "Everything that is holier is more desolate."

It is understood that my intention here is not to justify *he'elem v'hester*, but only to emphasize and recall what is known in any case: just as in previous years there were *he'elem v'hester*, and yet people engaged in Torah and *mitzvos* in general, and in the matters of *Chassidus* in particular, so too must we conduct ourselves in such a manner. Even if we do not always understand through our intellect what the benefit is in the *he'elem v'hester*, in the vast majority of cases, the debate and argumentation—whether there is a benefit in the *he'elem v'hester* or not—hinder the actual *avodah*, or at the very least diminish it. This is proof that the source of this debate is from the *sitra achra*. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, once answered someone who asked a question of this nature: "Are you also questioning why the way of the wicked prospers?" He elaborated in that letter that one should abandon all such inquiry and dedicate oneself to the *avodah* in practice...

With blessings for a *ksiva v'chasima tova* and for success.

## 2892

B"H, 1 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was distressed to hear that your health is not as it should be, and primarily that you are experiencing a certain decline in spirit. It is astonishing—regarding you, and indeed regarding every individual of our generation, whom Hashem has protected and who remain as "brands plucked from the fire"—that after having witnessed such Hashgacha Pratis with their own eyes, there is still doubt within them. This is not, G-d forbid, regarding the power of faith in a **general** sense, but rather regarding the feeling of the heart: whether it is truly the case that Hashem, who is the Essence of Good and whose nature is to do good, orchestrates the life of a person down to its details and the details of those details. For if this faith and understanding were to penetrate the person’s feelings as well, they would certainly be happy with their lot, and consequently, their health would also be as it should be. They would then add strength to their avodah in fulfilling the mission of the Supreme Master in this world.

Although in every matter one must maintain a grasp on the ways of nature, as it is written, "in all that you do" (the reason for this is explained in many places, including in *Kuntres U'Maayan* near its end), and therefore one must be careful to follow the instructions of the doctors, the conduct in this must be without a "divided heart," as is well known.

If you will listen to my advice, you should take a vacation for a week or two in order to calm your state of mind, and through this cessation and rest, strengthen your health. After this break, and with a firm resolution to serve Hashem with joy, you will be able to continue your affairs and activities in good health and with success.

With blessings for good tidings, both from yourself and from your family, may they live, and for a *Kesiva V'Chasima Tova*.

## 2893

B"H, 1 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Although it is unpleasant for me to write about this, since it concerns the welfare of a fellow Jew, I do not have the right to remain silent. I must express my disappointment, for I had hoped that after the struggle your son—may he live—has gone through, both within himself and with his environment, especially regarding his outward appearance, the first thing his parents—may they live—and especially his mother—may she live—should have done was to encourage and strengthen him in this path, which is full of trials. As the common expression goes, a "merciful mother." Especially since the matter of outward appearance is, **by everyone’s admission**, not a matter of substance in and of itself; it has no intrinsic importance whatsoever. It is merely a matter of convention. Consequently, its only "importance" is the desire to find favor in the eyes of observers, to remove the question of "what will people say." And these are not the kind of people who have an appreciation for the inner content of life—for when such people see a man or woman standing firmly by their convictions and swimming **against** the current, it evokes in them a sense of respect. Rather, it concerns those people who have no interest in looking at what is inside the vessel, as long as everyone follows the **crowd**. On the other hand, this shakes the inner confidence that a person possesses when, in their daily life, they conduct themselves according to what their own conscience dictates, rather than being forced to go against their own judgment. It is precisely in this instance that I was disappointed.

I am sure you will forgive me for these lines, and it is understood that it is not pleasant for me to write about this (especially since you, too, conduct yourself according to the Ashkenazic ways of *yiras shamayim* regarding the aforementioned matter). But as I wrote in one of my previous letters, this is not a question of the *mitzvah* of growing a beard, but a question of an **appropriate** attitude when one sees a close relative—and especially a son or daughter—struggling to arrange their life according to their own convictions, and one weakens their resolve because of the argument of "what will 'the people' say" (*Tanya*, Chapter 32)...

With blessings for true health and for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*.

## 2894

B"H, 1 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Menachem Av, stating that in approximately two weeks you will be moving into your new home: surely, the very first things you should bring into the house are a Chumash, Tehillim, a Siddur, and a Tanya. May it be the will of Hashem that this change of place brings a change of fortune for the good and for blessing, both materially and spiritually.

Regarding what you write about your son, may he live and be well, in connection with the question of studying secular subjects: it is clear that this should be rejected in his current situation. Since Hashem has granted him success and he is diligent in his studies at the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim, he must hold fast to Hashem’s blessing and success and utilize them to the fullest extent. He should not listen to the incitement of the Yetzer Hara, which seeks out justifications; its intention is to confuse people in general, and the youth in particular, and divert them from walking in the ways of Hashem. Knowing that if it were to reveal its true intent, it would not be listened to, the Yetzer Hara disguises itself in the cloak of "practical considerations" and the like. As is known from our Sages, this is the craft of the Yetzer Hara: today it tells him this, and tomorrow it tells him that. Fortunate is his portion that your son is found within the four cubits of Torah and Yiras Shamayim, which protect against the strange winds currently blowing in the world at large, and in the Land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year in particular. The necessity for great caution for those who are in the King’s palace is self-evident.

I hope that these few lines, small in quantity, will suffice—not only for him, but that he will also utilize his influence on his surroundings in this direction. Great is the merit of one who assists those who are rising in general, and in matters of Yiras Shamayim in particular; may it draw down upon him blessing and success in all that he and his household, may they live, require.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

## 2995

B"H, 1 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Menachem Av, in which you write that there are parents who are approaching you with requests to teach their daughters mathematics, physics, and so on.

For surely you will endeavor to utilize your influence over them to strengthen them in *yiras shamayim*.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant success to you and your wife—may you both live in good health—and may you share good news in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for a good and sweet year.

## 2898

B"H, 2 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your previous inquiry regarding *tikkun*.

The beginning of this *avodah* is a firm, absolute decision to abandon the improper behaviors of the past and to engrave this within one’s mind and heart—meaning, it must touch one’s feelings, not merely one’s intellect.

The *hisbonenus* required for this is simple: one must take into account the damage and destruction that these behaviors cause, both to the life of the body and, *a fortiori*, to the life of the *neshamah*, as explained in the *sefarim*—both in the general *sifrei mussar* and in *sifrei Chassidus*. To rectify the past, one must increase the "letters" of *Torah* and *tefillah*. This means davening the entire *tefillah* without resorting to "permissions" to skip parts, etc. (After all, one can arrive at the beginning of *tefillah*, or even earlier, at which point there is no room for any such "permissions"). Regarding the "letters" of *Torah*, this means, simply, learning, and also ensuring that one has committed to memory at least several chapters of *Mishnayos* and several chapters of *Tanya*, reviewing them while walking on the road, etc. It is also worthwhile to know by heart the *maamar* "Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken" from the end of *Parshas Kedoshim* in *Likutei Torah*. Since light pushes away darkness, keeping the letters of *Torah* and *tefillah* in one’s memory will, little by little, drive out the contrary letters.

I trust you have a fixed *shiur* in the study of *Chassidus*, and that you recite the daily *Tehillim*—according to the division of *Tehillim* for the days of the month—each day after *davening*. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success.

With the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 2899

B"H, 3 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your inquiry in your letter of 23 Menachem Av regarding the methods of studying the laws and the methods of learning the craft of *shechitah*, and how to divide the time between them: You should consult with the elders of *anash* who are present in your location and are familiar with the local conditions and your personal talents. However, in accordance with what is brought in the *poskim*, in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe, and in the *She'eilos U'Teshuvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, a *shochet* must be exceptionally *yirei shamayim*. Furthermore, you must increase your study of *Chassidus Chabad*, which leads to the fear of Hashem—both *yirah tata'ah* and *yirah ila'ah*—which is rooted in the *chochmah* of the soul, as explained in *Tanya* in many places. The prerequisite and the vessel for receiving the aforementioned is through the *avodah* of *tefillah* as it ought to be performed. And if you truly desire it, you will succeed.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 2,802

B"H, 3 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 28th of Menachem Av, and I was distressed to perceive between the lines that the financial hardship you believe you are experiencing has caused you spiritual distress. It is most astonishing that a ben Torah and one raised in a Chassidic home would feel themselves in a spiritual strait because of a financial difficulty—which, quite apart from the doubt as to whether it is truly significant, is in any case a passing matter. It is already known from our Sages, of blessed memory, that the world is a revolving wheel, and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, explained that on a wheel, when one finds oneself at the lowest point, G-d forbid, this is absolute proof that an ascent is imminent, as can be seen in the analogy of a physical wheel; and the analogies of the Torah are precise in every detail to the matter they represent. Even though one who merely imagines that they lack something—even if only a physical thing—should pray to Hashem that He fill the lack, for this is the essence of the mitzvah of tefillah according to many Rishonim, nevertheless, G-d forbid, one must never be disheartened by this, for it is impossible not to be distracted by such a decline from the avodah to the Creator of the world as is required of him.

It is my hope that these few lines will suffice. In these days, as the Alter Rebbe writes in Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh, page 32b, the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, allows anyone who wishes to go out to greet Him, and He receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all, as it is written, "Hashem will shine His countenance upon you." May it be the will of Hashem that you find your livelihood in a kosher manner, with tranquility and peace of mind, and may you bring good tidings that you are increasing your strength in influencing your surroundings to bring them closer to Chassidus through the dissemination of the wellsprings outward.

With blessings for a *ksiva v'chasima tova* and for good tidings.

## 2903

2903

B"H, 3 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Elul, with the *pan* enclosed, which I will read at an opportune time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in which you write regarding the state of your health.

I have already written to several people who have asked about such matters, that while on one hand, one must follow the instructions of the doctors—as is explained in many places and is also brought as a halachic ruling in *Shulchan Aruch* regarding the laws of Shabbos, *milah*, etc.—on the other hand, this applies only to the actual, practical actions. However, the power of thought should not be occupied at all with delving into one’s physical health, etc., since this is not one’s profession—meaning, one is not the doctor for this specific individual, and no benefit will come to the individual from this. Consequently, for him, this falls into the category of "thought without purpose," and as such, it is distracting, as it occupies the power of thought and prevents it from being invested in what it ought to be thinking about. Anything beyond what is necessary is considered as if it were not there. Therefore, regarding yourself, you should fulfill the instructions of the doctors regarding the practical actions, and place your trust in Hashem, that He will send His word and heal you.

With blessings for the fulfillment of your requests in the aforementioned *pan*, and for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah* in particular.

#### ***2903***

**I have already written:** See above, Vol. 6, letter 1619, and the references in the notes there.

## 2804

B"H, 3 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter: regarding the general matter about which you write, the cause is often a lack of guarding the holiness of speech (*kedushas halashon*). At other times, it is physical weakness, and sometimes it is that the *tefillin* or *mezuzos* require checking and replacement. You should rectify all of the above and increase your strength in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, in the *avodah* of *tefillah*, and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. ## 2805

B"H, 4 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Vaad of Kfar Chabad, may they live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 18 Menachem Av regarding the inquiry about the high school, where you explain that your intention is to enable the girls to continue their studies within the village itself in an appropriate environment, and that the purpose is not to disseminate secular studies:

In such a case, it should certainly be arranged that the school you establish will include *limudei kodesh*. As for those who are studying secular subjects in any case, this should be arranged by traveling once or twice a week to an appropriate institution—naturally with *yiras shamayim*—in Tel Aviv or the like.

It is self-understood that the education at Beis Rivkah must be organized properly—that is, it must begin at the required hours, as is standard in other educational institutions. For there can be no proper education if it is not conducted with a fixed and firm structure. This must be taken into account from the outset, as it is a fundamental matter. While it is true that "the Merciful One exempts one who is under duress," the students do not receive their education through such an exemption, and consequently, it is lacking.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*.

## 2,907

B"H, 4 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 27 Menachem Av, which gave me great pleasure to read. It was a pleasure to learn that you had the opportunity to influence groups of students, as well as a group of young people who are themselves counselors; by influencing them, you impact the way they guide those who come to them.

However, I am surprised that among the subjects you studied with them, there is no mention of *limudei Yahadus* (Jewish studies). While it is true that there may not be specific textbooks for this, no Jewish education can exist without this foundation. In the "old country," one might have absorbed this naturally from the *beis knesses*, from the home, and even from the street. But in our time, the responsibility to instill *Yahadus* lies entirely with the *madrikh* (counselor) and *mashpia*. The street is often a contradiction to it, and the home is sometimes one way and sometimes another; in any event, one cannot rely on those sources.

I would like to hope that this was merely an omission in your writing, and that in practice, *limudei Yahadus* was included. Please write to me about this at the next opportunity. Hopefully, you will maintain your connection with these groups and increase your influence upon them in matters of *Yahadus*, for "this is the whole person." Knowledge of Torah must be imparted to a living human being, and a Jewish life exists when there is "you who cleave to Hashem your G-d—are all alive today." *Dveikus* in the *Ribono shel Olam* comes through Torah knowledge, feeling, and vitality in *Yahadus*.

I hope that the *sifrei Chassidus* and *kuntresim* you possess provide nearly ready-made material to explain these concepts in their own language. There is no need for me to elaborate on the greatness of this *zechus*. May the *midah* of the *Ribono shel Olam* be *midah k'neged midah*, and may He grant you much *nachas*—Jewish *nachas* and Chassidic *nachas*—from all your descendants, together with your wife, *shichyu*.

With blessings for success in all the above and in your personal matters, and with wishes for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 2,908

2,908

B"H, 4 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month, regarding what you wrote about your state of health and the weakness in your avodah: I have already written to you about this many times, and it is surely well-known that the intention in the avodah of Hashem is not to wear out the body (except in exceptional cases), but rather to wear out the nefesh habehamis. For in our generation, when one wears out the body, it becomes weakened, and consequently, this confuses the grasp of the intellect and the feelings of the heart. This is in addition to what is explained in the maamar "Basi LeGani" 5713 regarding this, and further elaboration is unnecessary.

There is enough time during the day for lengthy tefillah, for learning properly—both nigleh and nistar—and for the performance of mitzvos with hiddur. All of this can be done without compromising physical health regarding eating, drinking, sleeping, etc., as is necessary for your specific body (for not every person is the same in this regard). Consequently, there is no room to complain or to search for far-fetched reasons. When you do all of the above in an orderly fashion, things will be in order...

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2819

B"H, 4 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you briefly describe your biography and conclude that in order to supplement and perfect your knowledge in Yiddishkeit you would like to study at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim and receive the necessary information and explanations from the bochurim. You also write that you have studied a little Chumash, Tehillim, etc., and it appears that you can also read Yiddish, not only English, and you wish to do something for the Klal Yisrael.

In my opinion, since the Yeshiva has its own set schedules for the bochurim to study, and they are occupied with this almost the entire day, I do not see how you will be able to learn from them what you require, unless it were no more than half an hour a day, which is what one of them might be able to give you. Furthermore, I do not know how comfortable you would feel spending all your time among young bochurim, and consequently, the learning would not be successful.

Therefore, in my opinion, you should participate in the shiurim that are taught publicly in the shuls, such as Ein Yaakov, Chumash, Kitzur Shulchan Aruch, and the like, and find an older talmid chacham who would study with you for an hour or two each day, either entirely for free or for a small fee. During that time, he could also explain to you what was not understood when you studied on your own.

If your residence is not far from the Yeshiva or a similar yeshiva, you could daven together with the bochurim and also spend time with them during their free time, especially on Shabbos and Yom Tov. All of this together would give you the possibility to reach your aforementioned goal.

I hope that, as you write that you wish to do something for the Klal Yisrael, you will not postpone this to a later time, but rather act on it now by influencing relatives, friends, and acquaintances to bring them closer to Yiddishkeit in general and to the fulfillment of mitzvos in particular. When one speaks heartfelt words, in the end, it influences everyone.

I hope to hear good news from you regarding all of the above, and according to the custom of Yisrael, I wish you a Kesiva V’chasima Tova.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2819

B"H, 5 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter regarding the situation in your family, and specifically concerning kashrus: it is well known that first and foremost, one must "call for peace"—that is, to proceed in ways of pleasantness and clarify to them that the Torah and mitzvos in general are for the benefit of the person, both regarding the soul and the body, and both in this world and in the World to Come. This is especially true regarding the kashrus of food and drink. As our Alter Rebbe states in the holy Tanya, since food becomes the blood and flesh of one's own flesh, a Jewish body cannot tolerate non-kosher food. Even if it sometimes takes a long time until negative results appear, Heaven forbid, it is understood that normal people with sound minds would not do anything that would severely damage their physical health, even if the damage would only manifest after several years. When you add that this is not intended to frighten them, but rather stems from ahavas Yisrael in general, and love for a relative and son in particular—that one is compelled to protect loved ones from any harm, Heaven forbid—then words that come from the heart will enter the heart. May it be the will of Hashem that this happens easily and soon.

Regarding the receipt of your visa, it is surprising that you write that the matter must take a long time, given that the request comes from a well-known educational institution. My hope is strong that when you exert effort in the manner you describe in your letter on behalf of the institution, Hashem will grant success.

Regarding what you write about setting the date of your wedding for the 13th, the eve of the 14th of the month of redemption, the month of Kislev, may it be the will of Hashem that it be in a good and auspicious hour. You may write "14 Kislev" on the invitation, but do not use the term "night"; rather, use "the eve of the 14th" (*or l'Yud-Daled*), as our Sages taught in the language of the Mishnah.

Enclosed is a segment of the sicha from Shabbos Mevarchim, 8 Elul 5711, the content of which is relevant for all years and throughout the entire year. I am certain you will utilize it in the appropriate manner.

With blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 2811

B"H, 5 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Vocational School, may they live,

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter of 25 Menachem Av, and the previous ones—13 Sivan and 7 Tammuz—regarding the question of accepting such-and-such a student into the vocational school: It is understood that this depends on the character of the student and his ultimate intention in entering the vocational school. Consequently, you must consult on this with the administration of the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod, where the aforementioned students have studied until now, and decide in accordance with the information obtained from both sides. It is understood that you must maintain the point I have written previously: that one must be careful that the vocational school does not become a place of refuge and escape for those who wish to exempt themselves from proper study.

Regarding the acceptance of new students for the upcoming term: In general, this is a necessity, as it is the only outward sign of the growth of an educational institution. However, the number of new students depends on the ability to accommodate them, etc., and the expenses involved. According to the instruction of our Rebbes, when one "sets oneself up broadly" (takes on the responsibility), Hashem provides with expansion.

Regarding the question of whether to accept students from the Reshet schools: You did not detail the pros and cons of this in your letter. Furthermore, on the face of it, this contradicts the logic that before entering the vocational school, students should study in the Yeshiva for a period of time. Even if there are those who are incapable, for whatever reason, of Yeshiva studies, surely everyone can adapt to it for a year or half a year. And if one is capable but unwilling, it is doubtful whether he is suitable for the vocational school either.

As for the opinion of the vocational instructor that those who have not adapted to the work should be sent away: It is understood that determining that one is incapable requires time, and it is impossible to decide based on a few weeks, especially in a place that is new for the students and in a new environment. In particular, dismissal from the vocational school will also cause them to leave an environment that is suitable for the student [although, on the other hand, it is understood that teaching those who bring **no** benefit at all has no place (perhaps it is possible to find some other matter for those students who are incapable of vocational study, so that they might still remain in the village or in the Chabad environment in some service role, etc.?)].

The pictures—two copies—were received.

With a blessing for success in your holy work and for a *Kesiva V’chasima Tova*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 2813

B"H, 5 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, I was pleased to hear that you are seeing success in your study of Chassidus with the students of the vocational school. Regarding what you wrote—that you have not had much success in your own studies—this is the opposite of the words of our Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya—the arbiter of the hidden dimensions of Torah—and the Shulchan Aruch—the arbiter of the revealed dimensions of Torah—who writes at the beginning of his book *Torah Or* that through the act of tzedakah, one’s mind and heart become refined a thousand times over.

(Although, from this very phrasing, it is understood that this only means that the mind and heart have been refined, and in a wondrous manner—namely, a thousand times over. According to the explanation of the Tzemach Tzedek and the glosses to *Likutei Torah* on the three parshiyos there, this is not merely an increase in quantity, but also in quality, and is incomparable, as it elevates one from the world of Asiyah to the world of Atzilus. However, after this, it is still only a refinement, which means that if one studies for an hour afterward, one will succeed as if one had studied for a thousand hours; but in any case, that hour must be studied. And "study" means *aliba denafshei*—for one’s own self—and subsequently also *lishmah*, as all the levels of this are explained in Chassidus.)

May Hashem grant you success in all the above, and may you see the effect in such a way that no room remains for the incitement of the *sitra achra*.

With blessings for success, for a *kesivah vachasimah tovah*, and to hear good news regarding the improvement of your father’s health.

P.S.

Regarding what you wrote—that there is a rationale for you to be at home during the upcoming Rosh Hashanah, even though many of the students of Tomchei Temimim will be within the walls of the yeshivah during these auspicious days, and the reason for this is that your father’s health is not as it should be—I am astonished and dismayed by such a lack of bitachon in Hashem. At the end of Menachem Av, you are already determining and are certain, Heaven forbid, that your father’s health will not be as it should be a month later, and consequently, you accept the rationale that you need to diminish your *avodah* of tefillah, etc. It would be far better and more in line with the instruction of our Nasi—*tracht gut, vet zein gut* (think good, and it will be good)—to be confident that your father’s health will certainly improve, and that you will certainly be able to increase your *avodah*—the *avodah* of the heart—as much as is necessary.

## 2814

B”H, 5 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the 1st of the month, in which you write that you participate in Chassidus shiurim on Shabbos but are extremely busy throughout the rest of the week: it is understood that this is not sufficient at all. Furthermore, it is essential that chapters of Mishnayos and chapters of Tanya be engraved in your memory, so that even when you are busy, you will be able to review them by heart.

May Hashem cause your wife’s (tichyeh) pregnancy to be completed properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child at the proper time, in a healthy manner and with ease.

## 2,915

2,915

B"H, 7 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write that you do not feel vitality in your study of Chassidus and ask for advice regarding this.

Surely you are aware of the teaching of our Sages that the receiving of the Torah was specifically through the precedence of *naaseh* to *nishma*—which means understanding and vitality (for if it were taken literally, it would be impossible to perform before hearing what is to be done). Consequently, one should not be discouraged if one is tested in this as well, and G-d forbid, one should not slacken in one's study because of this, for every matter of trial is as it is said, "to know whether you love Hashem your G-d."

Be careful regarding *tevilas Ezra*, and recite the daily *Tehillim* after *davening*—according to the division of *Tehillim* for the days of the month—as instituted by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Before *davening*, set aside a *prutah* for *tzedakah*, and perform *tzedakah* in your surroundings by influencing others to draw their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven. This will surely assist you in removing the concealments and obstructions, until you will feel—and not merely know—the "good light" that is hidden in Torah in general, and in the teachings of Chassidus in particular.

Awaiting good news, and with blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah*.

On behalf of the Rebbe,

Secretary

## 2,916

B"H, 7 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter: first and foremost, you must divert your thoughts from matters such as these. You should be careful regarding *tevilas Ezra*, and study a daily *shiur* in *penimiyus haTorah*, which is called the *ilana d'chayei*. As explained in *Zohar* Vol. 3, page 124b, the "other side" has no hold upon it, as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe—the *posek* in the *nistar* of Torah and author of the *Shulchan Aruch*, the *posek* in the *nigleh* of Torah. You should know by heart several chapters of *Mishnayos* and several chapters of *Tanya*, and study the *maamar* in *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Parshas Kedoshim*, *d.h. Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken*. Furthermore, we are already sworn and standing from Mount Sinai to guard and sanctify our speech, which is one of the well-known *segulos* for these matters.

It is also well known that one must guard the health of the body, the refinement and purification of which in these days is achieved through *tzedakah*, being careful with the aforementioned, and similar practices, rather than through fasts and *sigufim*. Our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, elaborated on this in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*. If you conduct yourself in this manner, you will surely be able to share good news regarding an improvement in your situation.

May it be the will of Hashem that your writing—that you have become closely connected to Chabad—will not, Heaven forbid, be labor in vain (which is also one of the hints regarding your situation, as they are one and the same). Rather, may this manifest in practice through your conduct: in studying *Toras HaChassidus* and following its ways and customs in your daily life. There is nothing that can stand before the will.

Awaiting good news and with blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2818

B"H, 8 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the long hiatus, it was a pleasure to receive your letter from the 5th of Menachem Av, in which you share the good news that you have already accepted the rabbinic position... and that, little by little, the other matters are also being arranged. It is well known from our Sages (Bava Basra 12b) that "all who are kind to him..." [are blessed].

As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they may need, as you have written.

Regarding your question asking for my opinion on participating in a Torah publication: this depends on the nature of the publication. That is to say, if it is intended to legitimize various matters—as is well known to be the approach in certain circles that have adopted the Sages' teaching that "the power of leniency is preferable" as their slogan—then we are already distressed by the initial [problems], and we should not add to them. However, if it is a matter of "magnifying Torah and making it glorious," then it is understood that the decision changes accordingly. In most cases, this can only be clarified through close acquaintance with those who are at the helm and those who determine the direction of the publication; in the vast majority of cases, this only becomes clear after the first issue has been published, at the very least.

May Hashem guide you on the straight and good path—and there is no "good" other than the perfect Torah, combined with fear of Heaven.

It is surprising that you do not write regarding the scheduling of the wedding date; it is a pity that it continues to be delayed.

With blessings for success in the above and for a good and sweet inscription [for the New Year].

## 2819

B"H, 8 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Meir Shalom, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 6th of Menachem Av, in which you write about your meeting with Mr. [Name], may he live, and the details thereof, and you ask for my opinion on how to bring the aforementioned closer, and specifically to Chabad.

It is difficult, from a distance and based on a letter, to even point out specific approaches, especially since, as it appears from your letter, he is an emotional person. If in matters that depend on the intellect alone it is difficult to gauge what is happening in another person’s soul, this is certainly true regarding the emotions of the heart and *hispaalus*. This is all the more so based on what is written in the introduction to the Tanya, that even the *hispaalus* of the intellect is not the same from one person to another.

Nevertheless, based on your letter, it seems you should speak to him *on the hands*—that is, to tell him that nothing is ever lost, and "no one is cast away from Him." Even though one does not cry over the past—over the time that has been lost—from this point forward, every moment should be precious to him. When he contemplates the inner depths of his soul, he will see that, in truth, he has always yearned to return to his source and his origin, which is Torah and *mitzvos*. Through this, the lack of spiritual satisfaction he has felt in his activities until now can be understood.

Furthermore, as is understood even by human reason, there is one who acquires his world in a single hour. Especially since he is a person of influence within a circle of many of our fellow Jews, he can, to a great extent, rectify the past. As for his lack of understanding regarding what has happened to him over the past years, "Why concern yourself with the hidden ways of the Merciful One?"

I await good news from you regarding all of the above, as well as regarding the matters of the network and its details.

With blessings for success and a *kesivah vachasimah tovah*.

#### ***2819***

**Rabbi Meir Shalom, may he live:** Belizinsky. Another letter to him—see above, Vol. 5, 1559.

## 2920

2920

B”H, 8 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, occupied with communal needs, R’ Yehoshua [Schneur Zalman]—may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

It is surprising that I have not received any letters from you for some time. This is especially so since I received good news from the avreich Herzog—may he live—that in the days before he traveled, a shift for the better was noticeable in the affairs of the yeshiva. You will surely write with the details.

Regarding what you wrote about the rationale for bringing older students there from Paris and Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt speedily—beyond the very large financial expenditures involved, one must consider how these individuals will influence the children [of Australia] who do not speak English. Furthermore, there would be a gap between the level of knowledge of the students who would arrive and those who are already on-site.

Do not let your spirits fall because (since the Shechinah is in galus, and Knesses Yisrael is in galus, and consequently) Bnei Yisrael are in galus, and the holier something is, the more the galus conceals it. For ultimately, "ours will be the victory," even if "little by little I will drive them out," as this matter has been explained in many places, and as you have also seen tangibly in those lands where you have already been. However, as with all matters of holiness, "one hour earlier is better," especially since one must fill the time and utilize it for as long as the individuals are in such an educational environment, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Regarding the matter of R’ Y.D. [Gruner]—may he live—remaining there, this is certainly the correct course of action. However, since he is connected with the department of the yeshiva here in the city of Buffalo—and apparently, before his departure, he promised them a continuation of the work there—he must discuss this with the central office of Tomchei Temimim here. Only then will it be possible to make an effort in this matter. If it is found possible for the yeshiva department to continue without him, there will be prospects for Rabbi [Gruner]—may he live—to remain in your camp for a period of time. It might be worthwhile, in order for the proposal to be better received, to link this with a matter of income for the central yeshiva.

With blessings for outstanding success in all of the above, in good health, and for a kesivah v’chasimah tovah,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***2920***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 23, p. 504; completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**R’ Yehoshua Schneur Zalman:** Serbranski. Additional letters to him appear above, 2881, and in the references noted there.

**The Yeshiva:** In Melbourne.

## 2921

B"H, 9 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your recent letter, it was a pleasure to read that the matter of studying Tanya in public has been arranged in your shiurim. Regarding what you wrote—that there is still a need for more hislahavus—it is well known that all Bnei Yisrael constitute a single complete stature (*komah shleimah*). Consequently, when vitality and hislahavus are added to any limb of that stature, it is **inevitable** that hislahavus will also be added to the others, even if the beginning of this process is in the limb that hears rather than the limb that speaks. It is understood that I do not mean by this that the speaker should rely on the listener; however, on the other hand, the listener himself must also act upon the aforementioned, and Hashem illuminates the eyes of both.

Regarding what you wrote about... and the place of study for the upcoming time: in matters such as these, one must consult with his teachers and mentors who meet with him day after day, and take their instructions into account. They are the ones who see the boy during his studies and while he is with his peers, and they see things without bias. This is not the case with parents, who are suspected—due to the love parents have for their children—of viewing matters and seeing them not as they truly are. Since the parents' will and desire is for the boy’s true and long-term benefit, and not for a temporary benefit, it is understood that it is worthwhile to accept a temporary shortcoming in the boy's affairs, provided that he walks on the straight path and they will derive pleasure from him for long days and years...

As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and may Hashem grant them success to share good news soon.

With blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah* and livelihood in particular.

## 2922

B"H, 9 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh: one should not be affected by the times and dates mentioned by the doctor who examined you. As is well known, the saying of our holy Nasi is that the Torah grants the physician permission to heal, but G-d forbid, not to make the heart heavy. Consequently, one must fulfill their instructions while knowing that they are merely an axe in the hand of the Healer of all flesh, who performs wonders, and who will send His word and heal you speedily. The channel and vessels for this, in general and specifically for a young man from the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva, are the increase in the study of Torah—Torah of life—and its mitzvos, and the foundation for this: the avodah of tefillah.

And in these days, as expressed by our Alter Rebbe in Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh, page 32b, the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, allows anyone who wishes to go out to greet Him, and He receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all, as it is written, "May Hashem shine His face upon you." May it be the will of Hashem that He send His word and heal you as before.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.
