## 2923

B"H, 10 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you suffer from the fact that your speech precedes your thought—meaning, that you lack composure.

It is already a well-known saying of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe—the authority on the *nistar* (hidden) aspects of Torah, as well as the *Shulchan Aruch*, the authority on the *nigleh* (revealed) aspects of Torah—regarding the verse, "And you shall perish quickly from off the good land which Hashem gives you" (*Devarim* 11:17). The desire and enthusiasm for *avodas Hashem* (in general, and the study of Torah in particular) is the "good land," and the instruction "you shall perish quickly" means that one must destroy the haste and impulsivity in this, and instead study with pleasantness, to delight the *neshamah* with the sweetness of Hashem—see *Sefer HaSichos* 5700, page 59. When you contemplate this a few times, it will certainly become easier for you to rectify the aforementioned issue and to study with composure.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you the desire to study with *mesiras nefesh*, both in the *nigleh* of Torah and in the teachings of Chassidus, to fulfill the *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, and to begin the *avodah* of *tefillah*.

With blessings for success and a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2924

B"H, 11 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal needs,
Rabbi Shlomo Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

My previous letter was surely received in due time, and I hereby confirm receipt of your letter dated 12 Menachem Av.

It seems that among the students, a competition has begun as to who can write more letters to me. Consequently, they are writing about matters that should be discussed with their Rosh Yeshiva, their Mashpia, and the like. It would be worthwhile, at an appropriate time, to explain to them that this is not the path to spiritual elevation, nor even to hiskashrus. On the contrary, when they delude themselves into thinking they have fulfilled their duty in this regard simply by writing a letter, it weakens their attention to the essential matters. Hiskashrus and rising from level to level are achieved through matters of **actual deed**, meaning an increase in action, speech, and thought. You will surely find the appropriate words to convey this.

Regarding the reasoning in your letter concerning the travel of some of the students to the United States, my opinion on this is well known, as I have written many times. It is based on what we **see** in the young men who have already come from there to here. Since they continue to press the matter despite this—and it is surprising that you do not find the appropriate words to explain to them that this inclination contains a mixture of [self-interest]—those who nevertheless persist and prepare papers on their own initiative should be arranged to travel first for six months or more to study at Tomchei Temimim in France, where the discipline is strong. After this trial period, it will be decided whether they will continue their travel here or to Canada, or if they will return to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

With the blessing of a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 2926

B"H, 11 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter of 5 Elul was received, in which you begin by stating that you are of Chabad descent and wish to correspond, and that you also want to have a share in this.

Now, following such an opening, logic would dictate that you continue by expressing your perspective on how you might participate in the Chabad community. Instead, your letter contains two matters... the questions you have regarding the conduct of Chabad. It is well known that the holy Zohar states (Vol. 3, p. 124b) that from the side of the Tree of Life, there is no such thing—neither a question from the side of evil, nor dispute from the spirit of impurity; this is explained at length in the Iggeres HaKodesh of our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 26.

If your desire is truly to succeed in the study of Torah in general, and in the study of Chassidus in particular, there is no other path than by prioritizing *naaseh* (we will do) before *nishma* (we will hear). It was in this manner that the general giving of the Torah took place, and it is in this manner that the giving of the Torah occurs every single day—as in the phrasing of the blessing, "Who **gives** the Torah," in the present tense. Regarding this it is said, "The integrity of the upright shall guide them," etc., and so on.

May Hashem remove from you the concealments and obstructions, so that you may be able to study Torah with pure *yiras shamayim*.

#### ***2926***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 10, p. 252; completed according to the secretariat's copy.

## 2927

B"H, 14 Elul, 5714

Greetings and blessings!

Foremost among these is the effort to increase the number of students—both those who study all day and those who study for only a few hours a day—and to elevate the importance of the Yeshiva and its affairs so that it becomes the city’s center for matters of Yiddishkeit on the basis of purity and holiness. This means that the congregants of the shul there should study regular daily shiurim there, and so on.

According to the adage of our holy Rebbes, "As one sets out, so it proceeds," it is of the utmost importance that the beginning be carried out with hidur (beauty/meticulousness) and hitpashtus (expansion).

And surely these few lines will suffice to awaken in you, and in all anash, and in each one of them individually—for you have permission to publicize the above among anash—the hidden powers, and even the latent powers, so that they may be brought into actual practice in building the affairs of Chabad in your country, now, until Mashiach Tzidkeinu comes and gathers the outcasts of Israel from the four corners of the earth, and "no longer will one teach his neighbor... for they shall all know Me," etc.

Awaiting good news soon, and with blessings for a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 2,930

B"H, 15 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter of 8 Elul, bringing the good news that you have arrived safely in the city... It is surprising that you delayed this notification for so long. In your letter, you write about the nature of the people there, and also what was told to you by those who previously attempted outreach in matters of Torah and mitzvos, and that the matter is dependent upon difficulties.

Surely you are aware of the story from a letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding how his grandfather, the Rebbe Maharash, wrote to someone who had traveled to a place where Jews lived who were not so close to Torah and mitzvos. He wrote that it is simple and certain that Hashem could have provided him with physical sustenance in his own place, in a place of Torah and yiras shamayim. Therefore, it must be that Hashem brought him to that remote corner for the sake of spiritual sustenance—namely, to exert influence in his new location.

And since we continue to add Elokus through an increase in the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos, it is no wonder that it is connected with difficulties. For the greater the benefit, the greater the effort of the *sitra achra* to prevent it. On the contrary, the magnitude of the concealment and hiddenness indicates the abundance of light that can be drawn down in that place. This is explained by the analogy of a stone situated at the top of a wall, which falls further than one situated in the middle of the wall. The matter depends solely on the shaliach who has been sent to a particular place to fulfill his role as required.

It is my hope that if you conduct yourselves with the local people with calmness and in ways of pleasantness, and begin by influencing them through their children—may they live—then even a little light dispels much darkness, and certainly a great deal of light. It is understood that in such matters, one must be careful not to arouse suspicion among the local residents that you view them as *amei ha'aretz*, and so on.

The point in this, as explained in Chapter 32 of Tanya, is to conduct oneself according to the attribute of Aharon: "Love the creatures, etc." It is understood that one should not demand that the aforementioned people change from one extreme to the other, but rather slowly, slowly. And it is a presumption that outreach does not return empty.

With blessings for success and for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*. Awaiting good news.

## 2,931

B"H, 16 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Elul, in which you ask whether you should continue your practice of occasionally davening at length and with hisbonenus in a topic from Toras HaChassidus, given that it does not seem to you to have an effect on your middos, and consequently, you ask whether to continue in this way.

This question is puzzling. For if, even when you conduct yourself in the aforementioned manner, you have not yet affected your middos, one can only imagine what will be if you abandon this path—for that is a daily occurrence. It is also understood through simple logic that davening at length and engaging in hisbonenus in a topic from Toras Chaim assists in the refinement of one’s middos, and eventually, leads not only to iskafya but also to is'hapcha.

You should have your tefillin checked, and also give a few coins to tzedakah every weekday before davening. After davening, you should recite the daily portion of Tehillim—as divided according to the days of the month—and I am certain that you will then see, with your physical eyes as well, the effect of this avodah of yours upon your middos.

Regarding your notification of the date set for your wedding with your bride, may she live and be well: May it be the will of Hashem that you live in good fortune—mazal tov, mazal tov—at a good and auspicious time. May you build a home in Yisrael, an everlasting edifice founded upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah"—which is Toras HaChassidus.

With blessings of mazal tov, mazal tov, and a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 2932

B"H, 16 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you write that you have taken upon yourself, without a vow, to organize a Talmud Torah for children in your place of residence—and surely your intention is for a Talmud Torah in the true sense of the word, our holy Torah—

May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in this and see good fruit for your labor. And in accordance with the ruling of our Rebbeim that the measure of Hashem is "measure for measure," may He grant the *siyata d'shmaya* that you and your wife, *shichyu*, will educate and raise your children, *shichyu*, for Torah, for the *chuppah*, and for *maasim tovim*.

And since for every matter and endeavor one requires *siyata d'shmaya*—especially in the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, where the responsibility is consequently greater—and since it is not in the power of a human being to demand, but only to request from Hashem as an act of free kindness, one must increase in *tzedakah* and kindness below, for then one increases *tzedakah* and kindness from above. Therefore, it is proper that every weekday you set aside a few coins for *tzedakah* before *davening*, and after *davening* each day, recite a few chapters of *Tehillim*. Furthermore, in this generation, the generation of the footsteps of *Moshiach*, it is a *mitzvah* and a privilege to establish a *shiur* in the *pnimiyus haTorah* that has been revealed and explained in the teachings of *Chassidus*. May Hashem grant you success in all of the above.

I will read your *pidyon nefesh* at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*, and awaiting good news regarding all of the above.

## 2933

2933

B”H, 16 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Parshas Shoftim, in which you write about the difficulties you are encountering in your path at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in... — or more accurately, that the order of the day there is unfamiliar to you, and the studies are new to you as well.

Surely you are aware of the teaching of our Sages (Sukkah 52a) that the yetzer hara of **every person** is constantly and perpetually engaged in its war, to the point that the holy Torah testifies that were it not for the Ribono shel Olam helping him, one could not overcome it. From this it is understood that when the subject is a young man who desires to be a yirei shamayim and wants to learn, if his yetzer hara sees that an opportunity has opened for this young man to ascend higher and higher, both in yiras shamayim and in the study of Torah, it seeks additional stratagems to obstruct him as much as possible from continuing on this new path. And even though it is called an "old and foolish king," this is because it incites to matters that are the opposite of true wisdom; however, in its methods of incitement and seduction, it is extremely cunning—its root is also in this, as it is written, "And the serpent was cunning," and therefore it is called an "expert," for **the Torah** testifies about it that it is a master craftsman in its work.

It is simple to understand that if it were to come to a young man as described and say to him, "Know that if you follow this path, there is a near-certain hope that you will become a greater yirei shamayim and succeed more in your Torah study," he would not only not be deterred from his path by this, but on the contrary, he would gain even more courage in it. Consequently, the yetzer hara has no choice but to cloak itself in the mantle of a yirei shamayim and a talmid chacham, and approach the young man with arguments from the opposite extreme: that if he follows this new path, he will not reach the goal that a young man who is a yirei shamayim yearns for. And since there is no such thing as perfection in the world and in creation—for there is none perfect except for One, the Ribono shel Olam—there is always room to find a point of imperfection in any matter whatsoever.

The test in all of the above, to know from which source the arguments and difficulties come, is like the story of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the holy tzaddik, the holy gaon, and the holy chossid, Moreinu Harav R. Nachum of Chernobyl (printed in the sicha of the festival of Pesach 5703). The point of it is that if the demand is to prioritize "we will hear" (understanding) over "we will do," this is the opposite of the manner of receiving the Torah. Furthermore, if the arguments hinder the actual performance of Torah, mitzvos, and the avodah of tefillah, they certainly come from the *sitra achra*.

When you contemplate, even for a brief moment, that "every river has its own course"—meaning that every yeshiva has its own ways—and certainly for a person for whom habit has become a second nature, it was understandable **beforehand** that you would find in Tomchei Temimim differences from your previous location, and that at first, this change would be associated with the difficulty of altering your second nature. If the aforementioned has taken the form of questions and demands for you, it surely comes from the *sitra achra* so that a person should overcome it and do the opposite of its will—that is, the opposite of the seduction and incitement—not only by not letting it weaken you regarding Torah and tefillah, but on the contrary, by dismissing it and adding both in diligence in Torah study and in the *hiddur* (beautification) of fulfilling the mitzvos. And there is nothing that can stand before the will. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success.

With the blessing of *Ksivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

## 2934

B"H, 18 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 17 Elul, which arrived on the auspicious day of 18 Elul. As the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, goes—in the name of the early Chassidim—"He brings vitality into Elul." It is self-understood that this vitality is the opposite of sadness, and to a certain extent, even the opposite of bitterness. For although it is explained in many places that a degree of bitterness also requires vitality, it is clear that this is not at all comparable to the vitality present in avodah performed with simcha, where the vitality is of an entirely different nature, as simcha breaks through barriers.

It is also understood that I do not intend this as a mussar lecture, but merely to awaken you regarding the content of your letter: there is no need to be bitter at all that your *kvius itim l’Torah* (fixed times for Torah study) is not yet consistent. This is within your control; at any given moment, you can establish it firmly, even in terms of time. According to the order of holiness—"little by little I will drive them out"—it is not advisable to take upon yourself a fixed time of several hours at the beginning of this change. Rather, start with a quarter or half an hour each day—and it is best if part of this is in the morning and part in the evening or at night. Although this, too, must be done *bli neder* (without a vow), as is the custom in these times, as explained in *Likutei Torah* at the beginning of *Parshas Matos* that one must say *bli neder*, on the other hand, one must be firm about that quarter-hour. Once you break through the path, it will eventually become a paved road, and you will be able to maintain the consistency not only in your soul but also increase the consistency in time. As our Sages have said, Hashem stands at the right hand of every Jew to assist him in his avodah; if a person opens an opening even as small as the eye of a needle, they open for him from Above an opening as wide as the entrance to the *Ulam* (the Temple hall). It is well-known that the entrance to the *Ulam* had no doors, and thus it was always open; all the avodah required is to enter the *Azarah* (courtyard), which is accomplished even by an opening the size of the eye of a needle.

Enclosed is a *Likut Elul*, which also contains my general letter. With blessings for the year, and it is understood that my intention includes you and your family, may they live, in what is written therein.

With blessings for the avodah of Hashem with simcha and from within simcha, and for a *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah*.

#### ***2934***

**As the saying goes:** See also above, Vol. 6, Letter 1851, and the references in the notes there.

## 2935

B"H, 18 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was distressed to hear that your health is not in a complete state. When I was today at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I mentioned you for an improvement in your health and for the service of Hashem with joy.

Since the Rambam, the Tur, and the Shulchan Aruch have already ruled—and it is brought in many places in Chassidus—the explanation of the verse "In all your ways know Him," that one serves Hashem even through the matter of eating, provided the eating is according to Torah, and likewise during time spent on outings, etc., and in all of a person’s affairs, it is self-understood that the commandment "Serve Hashem with joy" applies to these matters as well.

May Hashem grant you success so that you may immediately begin this with firm trust in Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, who sustains and provides for all with kindness and mercy. This is especially true as we are currently in the days of Elul, where, in the words of our Alter Rebbe in Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh, page 32b, the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, permits anyone who wishes to go out to greet Him, and He receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all, as it is written, "May Hashem shine His face upon you."

With blessings for a good and inscribed year.

## 2936

B"H, 18 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and pious, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yosef David, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter in response to what I wrote regarding my notes on the laws of Eiruvin.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the seeds—that you did not see seeds in Manhattan—it is surprising, as they are plentiful in many places there.

Likewise, regarding what you wrote about the rising of a sandbar—that in a case which is only Rabbinic in nature, we do not concern ourselves with the possibility of a sandbar rising—it must be said that this opinion has not been accepted. This is because, according to many Rishonim and many Acharonim as well, **in practice** there is no *reshus harabim* in our time, yet they still bring and discuss at length the concern of a sandbar rising even now.

And regarding what you wrote about my note that Shabbos is different because they were commanded about it at Marah, and you raise a difficulty from Tosafos, Shabbos 87b, s.v. *Techumin*: It seems clear to me that I also cited this Tosafos in my letter, for there it is implied that according to one opinion, they were commanded about *hotza'ah* (carrying) at Marah, and from that we learn for the second [opinion] as well, since that is not the point of their dispute. And regarding your attempt to compare this to *milah* (and your note from the Rambam’s commentary on the end of Chapter 7 of Chullin), I already hinted at this in my letter, where I noted that regarding Shabbos, **at Sinai** it was said to them, "As He commanded you at Marah," which is not the case for *milah*, and this is understood.

And I have written this now to wish you a *ksivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

With respect and blessing.

***

**2936**

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 384, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

## 2937

B"H, the bright day of 18 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letters from Thursday of Parshas Eikev and Thursday of Parshas Ki Seitzei, and I was pleased to read that your son, may he live, is already feeling well and has surely returned home in a good and auspicious hour.

I was also pleased to read that your business affairs have improved. According to the statement of our Sages (Bava Basra 12b) that "whoever is treated well [by Heaven] continues to be treated well," this is for a long time. May the Ribono shel Olam help that your business should go from good to better for many years, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

You need not be in a hurry to return the money I lent you from the fund of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, as I hope it will bring you blessing and success.

Regarding your question about visiting the gravesite of your father, of blessed memory, within the twelve months: in general, this depends on the local custom, as there are places where it is not done within the twelve months. However, if there is no established custom—and especially since we are in the days of Elul and Tishrei, which are days of favor—it does not matter if you do go.

You likely know the customs of how one conducts oneself when visiting a cemetery at the graves of ancestors: immersing in a mikveh that day, drinking before going, but not eating, etc.

Regarding a tikkun that you requested, and also a safeguard for the future: the first thing is that you must stop thinking about the matter, for the thinking itself leads to an impure occurrence. Regarding a tikkun, one should increase in the letters of Torah and tefillah, be careful with tevilas Ezra, give tzedakah frequently (without a vow), and act in an appropriate manner in the kosher chinuch of the sons and daughters of Yisrael. It is also a proper thing, if it has been a long time since your tefillin were checked, to have them checked.

I hope to hear good news from you regarding all of the above.

For the New Year, which is approaching for us and for all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I send you and your household, may they live, my blessing: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in body and soul.

With blessings.

## 2,938

B"H, 19 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter regarding Mrs. [Name]—may she live and be well—who is experiencing a lack of *shalom bayis*, and who attributes this to her mother-in-law, who causes distress by visiting their home too frequently, etc.:

It is highly probable that this is because the matters of *taharas hamishpachah* require rectification. Beyond all the other consequences that result from a lack of care in this area, the aforementioned issue is also included. As our Sages of blessed memory stated (*Niddah* 31b), "Why did the Torah say [that a menstruant woman is ritually impure]? So that she should be beloved to her husband." It is understood that this is in addition to the implications regarding the children, etc., etc.

It is my hope that you will find the words to explain all of the above to the aforementioned couple. Experience has already shown that the less there is of embarrassment—though, of course, it must be explained in ways of pleasantness—the more satisfied all parties will be afterward.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

## 2939

B"H, 19 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 18 Elul, and I was pleased to read in it that you remember your Chassidic heritage, and most importantly, that you maintain Yiddishkeit along with Chassidic customs here in America as well. As is well known, what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, said—that the logic and argument that "America is different from the old country" is a false argument, as is explained at length in the enclosed pamphlet.

Regarding what you write about *tefillah b'tzibur* (communal prayer), this is one of the fundamentals. It is self-evident that the mundane conversation you hear while *davening* is a great disturbance. However, the solution to this is not to *daven* alone at home; rather, on the contrary, you should utilize the *hashpa'ah* (influence) and the warmth that the *Ribono shel Olam* grants a person to influence your surroundings as well, so that they conduct themselves in *shul*—which is a *makom kadosh* (holy place)—as one ought to conduct oneself in a *makom kadosh*. When you speak with a fellow Jew—and every Jew’s *pintele Yid* is intact—if you speak to him from the heart, you will eventually be *po'el* (effect change), and in that moment, the *zechus harabim* (merit of the many) depends on you.

In accordance with your request, I will mention you and your children at the *tziyun hakadosh* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. However, you surely know the custom that one is mentioned by one’s Jewish name and the name of one’s mother. When you write the names to me, I will do so with pleasure.

As the New Year approaches, I wish you a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

P.S.
From the envelope, I see that you are the secretary of a *landsmanshaft*. I hope that you utilize your influence there for matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, and "whoever adds, they add to him."

#### ***2939***

**As is well known... said:** See *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe, Vol. 18, Letter 6313, and elsewhere.

## 2940

B"H, 21 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Tel Aviv, may they live,

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 10 Elul. I was distressed to read that the printing of the bulletin for Chai Elul did not come to fruition, even though it was your intention to do so, and the sole reason was a lack of funds. It is surprising that you are not seeking ways to secure the necessary means for the bulletin; surely, even as an internal publication, one should be able to obtain some funds from the people to whom it is sent, in addition to the support from the institutions. This is especially so since, if I recall correctly, a publication did appear last year for Chai Elul, and in matters such as these, one must increase and not decrease.

I was pleased to receive the report on the activities for 12-13 Tammuz, as well as the plans to broadcast on the radio in connection with Chai Elul, which I hope was carried out.

Regarding what you wrote—that you do not understand my intention regarding "public activism"—it is clear that this question cannot be answered from a distance, as it depends on local conditions. In Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, there is a vast field of opportunity. One branch of this is the establishment of Chassidus shiurim in places where they do not exist. (However, this should not be done in the way you describe, by having people come there from elsewhere for the sake of receiving a stipend. In such a case, there is great doubt whether it will have longevity, both in terms of the expense and the effort involved. In any event, in the initial stage, one should strive to organize shiurim in those places where a maggid shiur can be found locally. Then, even if he needs to be paid, the expense will be much smaller than for someone coming from a distant place.)

As my participation in the activities for the month of Tishrei, I am enclosing a check. However, as stated above, my participation is only symbolic, for my approach is that for regular and ongoing activities, the means must be found locally. This is a sign that it is an organization with a future and that there are those who are interested in its development.

The minutes from the joint meeting have been received.

Approaching the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, may it be the will of Hashem that success rest upon your holy work and your general work, which will surely bring additional blessing and success to each of the participants in their personal affairs.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 2941

B"H, 22 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

... I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the various shiurim that have been established, and most importantly, that the circle of students is growing. You should certainly exert yourselves in this even more. In truth, it is not even appropriate to say "even more," because no amount of effort is sufficient in proportion to the greatness of the matter—especially when taking into account the statement of the Alter Rebbe that the Torah of Chassidus is for all of the Jewish people. Consequently, anyone who acts in this direction is fulfilling the heart's desires of the Alter Rebbe, as more people are added to his community who have been brought closer to Chassidus, its teachings, its guidance, and its customs.

It is very appropriate that you have tasked all of anash with reviewing maamarim of Chassidus in turn. It would be excellent if the other branches would emulate this and implement the same practice in their own locations.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you that the shiurim you study should also include a shiur in the practical halachos required from Orach Chaim. This study has been neglected in many circles to such an extent that when a practical question arises, people do not know how to act, what they should do, and what they should not do—as experience testifies. It is already well-known how much our holy Rebbes warned about this study, as is also evident in the introduction to the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe.

As you requested, I will mention you and your family—may they live—at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings.

## 2942

B"H, 22 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the group of young women in..., may they live:

Blessings and peace!

I received your letter some time ago, and for several reasons, my response has been delayed.

On the threshold of the New Year, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for good and for blessing, I am writing this response—at least in brief, as the questions you raise in your letter are very difficult to answer in writing. It is my hope that Mrs.... will clarify the points in my response that require further explanation:

All of Israel are believers, the children of believers, that the Creator, may He be blessed, leads the world with Hashgacha Pratis. It is understood that there is no matter, thing, or detail that is in vain. This is all the more so regarding the human species, and even more so—many times over—regarding the Chosen People, where every single man and woman of Israel has a special role, which is not only for themselves but also for the collective as a whole.

It is easy for a person of understanding to know, and we also see it tangibly, that the purpose of life is not the attainment of pleasure from the fleeting delights of the world. Rather, "man is born to toil," and through his toil and exertion—in the eternal Torah and mitzvos—he attains spiritual satisfaction, especially when one acts and works for the benefit of others as well. This is the meaning of "Torah of life" in its literal sense—life even in this world.

It goes without saying that this does not mean a person is obligated to loathe the pleasures of the world to the point of engaging in self-affliction and suffering throughout their days. As is known, and especially in the teachings of Chassidus, the path of self-affliction is not the intention or the goal. However, one must know what is essential and what is secondary. The pleasures you emphasize in your letter, and from which it is so difficult for you to part, are not the purpose. One should not make a "golden calf" out of gold, or cinema, or the like—which I am sure you also recognize are secondary, or even entirely devoid of any real content.

All this applies even in normal years, and all the more so in our generation, when the emptiness, lack of content, and lack of taste in various "ideals" and false opinions are revealed before everyone—ideals where neither money nor power stood by a person in their time of need. In this generation, it is easier to see the simple truth and the pure avodah, since several of the veils and concealments of disillusioned opinions and the vanities of the world that confuse the clear mind have been removed.

Those of our people who remained as "brands plucked from the fire" after the terrible destruction—each and every one of us must see ourselves as a shaliach who must fulfill not only their own role, but also the role of all those who perished before their time.

Just as regarding the Jewish people as a whole, the parts that kept the Torah and mitzvos exist to this very day, while all those groups that strayed from the path either left no remnant or survivor, or are merely a few in number and are withering away like withered limbs—so too is it regarding the individual. By holding fast in their day-to-day life, and especially regarding speech and actual deed in the way of Torah, one acquires their world—this world as well—in that all their days are filled with content and satisfy their soul.

The fundamental point resulting from the above is that the Torah and mitzvos have preserved the Jewish people as a whole from annihilation, G-d forbid, despite the fact that they were the fewest of all peoples and in every generation stood against them to destroy them. The Torah and mitzvos are the scarlet thread that unites all generations of Israel from the time of the Giving of the Torah until now.

It is my prayer and my confidence that each and every one of you will walk in this path that our ancestors paved for us, and you will walk securely in their ways in a life that is happy in the physical sense, because it will be a life that is happy in the spiritual sense.

With blessings to utilize your strengths, talents, and the inheritance of the fathers within each of you in the battle to remain loyal to the eternity of Israel and its Torah, and to influence your surroundings in this direction as well.

And with the blessing of Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah.

## 2943

B.H., 22 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

It has been some time since I received your letter, in which you describe your state of mind as well as your work in the field of education, particularly with a group of young women in […]. I also received a letter from the group of young women, which also reflects your state of mind; as is well known, the character of the teacher is reflected in the student to a great degree.

In response to your letter: surely it is unnecessary to explain to a daughter of Israel such as yourself—especially one who comes from Russia and remembers the trials and tribulations she endured on her journey—that the world is not ownerless, and that the Ribono shel Olam manages it in every detail through Hashgacha Pratis. This is one of the foundations of our faith, which all sons and daughters of Israel are believers, children of believers, even if this faith is not always visibly apparent.

It is understood from the above that there is nothing in the world that is in vain, and every matter and thing has a specific purpose. It follows that if the desired purpose is not realized—and certainly if the opposite is done—the damage to oneself and to the entire world is understood.

This matter is even clearer to all those whom Divine Providence saved from the pit of destruction during the days of the decrees that were unleashed upon our people. Even with a slight contemplation, one can understand that they were not saved miraculously due to their own righteousness or merit, but for a specific purpose. At the very least, from here on, they must fulfill their role and their part in the world, and not, G-d forbid, destroy.

Anyone who has been gifted with special qualities that allow for influence must use these qualities for the benefit of their surroundings, for this is not a private matter. All the more so, one must recognize the responsibility toward the younger generation, which is beginning to find its way in life.

After this introduction, although it is unnecessary to elaborate on what follows from these words, for the sake of further clarity and so as not to leave room for any doubt, I will elaborate even where it would have been appropriate to be brief:

Since the Ribono shel Olam brought you out of confinement and saved you with signs and wonders that transcend the natural order, and brought you to a place where you can accomplish great things—and not even through mesiras nefesh, but merely through the surrender of the will—there is no doubt that you must relinquish your own "existence" and your ego for the sake of the truth. For it is understood that all the difficulty in this is only to prioritize *naaseh* (action) over *nishma* (which means understanding)—that is, the *kabalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke) involved in this.

And since the Ribono shel Olam also saved you, and gifted you with the power to influence your surroundings in general and the youth in particular, it is simple that you must recognize the privilege and the responsibility in this, and G-d forbid, you must not destroy.

It is your duty to use your talents to their fullest, and not just in part, to root simple faith among the sons and daughters of Israel, and especially among the youth, and not to leave room for any doubts in faith. And do not forget the simple truth: that what seems to you to be doubts in fundamental matters is nothing but an illusion stemming from the *ra* (evil) in the world, a part of which exists in every person (the *yetzer hara*), which obscures the light and the truth. And it is understood that **it** is also the one that incites you to say that you cannot influence in a specific direction as long as you yourself are in doubt.

But you are not the first to be in such a situation, nor will you be the last. Experience has already shown that all those who held fast to the path of their ancestors—the path of our Torah, *Toras Chaim* (the Torah of life), which is life even in this world—just as regarding the Jewish people as a whole, those parts that kept the Torah and mitzvos exist to this very day, while all those sects that strayed from the path either left no remnant or survivor, or are merely a few individuals who are gradually fading away—so too is it regarding the individual. By holding fast in one’s daily life, especially regarding speech and actual deed, to the path of Torah, all one’s days are meaningful and satisfying (when one makes an honest accounting of one’s soul), and one enjoys true *taanug* when seeing the results of one’s influence on others. This is not the case for all those who strayed from the path, who sowed doubts and consequently reaped disappointments, etc. It is painful to elaborate on such a distressing matter.

The conclusion from all the above: since the Ribono shel Olam has gifted you with talents of influence, and you have also merited to spend several years in an environment saturated with *yiras shamayim* and the performance of practical mitzvos, and a special merit has been added to you in that there is a circle of youth in your environment whom you can encourage and strengthen so that they are not at all impressed by undesirable influences that could cause damage, G-d forbid, in their lives—it is your duty and your privilege to utilize your aforementioned talents and merits to their fullest.

And even if your method is that the matter does not yet settle one hundred percent in your intellect, those you influence cannot wait until you reach perfection or until you banish all the thoughts that confuse you, for every passing day is a loss that cannot be retrieved.

As mentioned above, there is no doubt in my mind that this is your role in the world, for which the Ribono shel Olam saved you from all that you went through and brought you to your current place. And with the Almighty, one does not bargain.

With blessings for great success in all the above, and that the Ribono shel Olam should also grant you success in your personal life so that all this comes to you without excessive concealment and hiddenness, and with the blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*, awaiting good news.

## 2944

B"H, 23 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Upon receiving a letter from your son, Mr. ..., he also wrote to me regarding the accident that befell your older son, Mr. .... I will mention him at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, so that he may have a speedy recovery.

I hope that when you have good news regarding this, you will inform me. You may write to me in whichever language is more comfortable for you; having spent several years in Paris, I also read French.

With wishes for a good year.

On behalf of the Rebbe.

## 2945

B"H, 23 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I read with interest what you wrote regarding the summer camp in Kfar Chabad, and I was pleased that you finally took an active part in its organization. It is already a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that "one action is better than a thousand sighs," especially when the matter concerns chinuch, which brings forth fruit and the fruit of fruit until the end of the world.

Surely the Ribono shel Olam will fulfill His promise to reward measure for measure, by granting you increased success in your own learning and chinuch, for the period of a person's education is something that continues throughout his entire life, as it is written, "The multitude of years shall teach wisdom."

However, I was struck by what is evident between the lines of your letter: that the attitude of the counselors and teachers toward the administration of the Reshet is as if the matters belong to the administration, while the teachers and counselors merely hold a position in this or that area. I have already written in several of my letters to those participating in the Reshet that these matters are the responsibility of all participants, and consequently, to the merit of all participants. From this it is understood that those who are actively engaged in the primary task of the Reshet—namely, the educators in practice—have a much greater merit, and consequently, their attitude, desire, and energy in these activities must be much greater than those of the board members, who are nothing more than "supporters of the Torah."

It is simple, after even a slight amount of contemplation, that in any human endeavor, perfection is lacking. Therefore, even if it seems that the deficiency is greater than usual, this should serve as an additional factor for increased energy and interest in how to rectify matters. And the promise of the Ribono shel Olam is well known: "He who comes to purify himself is assisted."

May the Ribono shel Olam write and seal you for a good and sweet year, a year of success in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, and a year of success in influencing your surroundings, especially in the field of chinuch on the purity of holiness.

The *pidyon nefesh* was received.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 2945

B"H, 23 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent in communal affairs,
Rabbi Michael, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from 3 Tevo and the previous one, it is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, your situation has already improved, and consequently, without distractions, you will continue to strengthen your holy work. This is despite the custom of the country, which is contrary to sound reason—and even contrary to the reason of the *nefesh hasichlis*, let alone the reason of *kedushah*—where precisely at the end of Elul and in the month of Tishrei, one diminishes the work of *chinuch* on the basis of pure *kedushah*. And although, from the perspective of the students' senses, as per your letters and those of the esteemed Chossid Rabbi Shlomo Matusov, may he live, it is not possible to do this—it is known that while *ones rachmana patrei* (the Merciful One exempts one who is coerced), we do not say "it is as if he did it," and in the final analysis, the time regarding those being influenced is not being utilized. It is understood that my intention is not to offer rebuke, but to awaken contemplation once more; perhaps the time has come to improve the matter, at least to some extent.

It is my hope that even if I had not alerted you to this, those of your students who are immigrating to Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, would prompt you to do so, and would repeat and reiterate that they should connect there with *anash* and the Chabad institutions, and most importantly, the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Lod, where there are many students from the Sephardic communities. And how good it would be if, in addition to the letters that you surely give to the students, you would, for your part, write to the administration of the Yeshiva in Lod regarding the character of the students who have immigrated to Eretz Yisrael, as you have known them for some time.

Regarding what you wrote about the building and Bais Rivkah, surely in a few days Rabbi Binyamin Eliyahu Gorodetzky, may he live, will arrive here, and consequently I will ask him for the reasons for the refusal, since you, may you live, do not write them.

Regarding your visit to the United States, you write that it is possible to find a replacement for the duration of your time here. And it seems from your letter that the expenses are also not an obstacle. If so, you should begin the efforts, *ober on hispaalus* (but without emotional agitation), for in general, one must contemplate which time is more suitable—whether Yud-Tes Kislev or Yud Shevat—and it is possible that the manner in which the efforts succeed will serve as an instruction in this matter.

And approaching the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

## 2947

## 2948

B"H, 23 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 14 Elul and the one preceding it. As you requested, I will mention you at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good year, both materially and spiritually.

Regarding what you write about your current and past situation, it is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "One action is better than a thousand sighs." Furthermore, the instruction of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe—the *posek* of the *nistar* of Torah and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the *posek* of the *nigleh* of Torah—is that in our generation, one should not fast excessively. As he states in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 3, it is forbidden to multiply fasts. This is especially true when, in addition to the general weakness of the generation, one is under medical care. Even if one were to argue that there is ultimately a place for fasting, one should first attend to other matters, rather than something that weakens the body—the fast—which in any case also weakens one’s comprehension in learning and one’s *kavanah* in *tefillah*, as physical weakness is a distraction from these.

Therefore, in my opinion, you should increase your engagement with the letters of Torah and the letters of *tefillah*. You should find a way to be active in the field of chinuch for Jewish children on the basis of *taharas hakodesh*, whether by doing so yourself or by influencing others to do so. You should also establish a special, fixed *shiur*—fixed in time and fixed in the soul—in the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. In the language of the *Zohar*, this is called the "Tree of Life," where the *le'umas zeh* has no hold. This is especially one of the *tikkunim* for the known sin, as explained in several sefarim. And regarding anyone who adds to this, our Sages have ruled that they add to him, first and foremost in success in this very *avodah*.

With blessings for the improvement of your health, both materially and spiritually—for in the case of a Jewish man and woman, who are "one nation on earth," meaning they draw down unity into all their affairs, they surely walk together.

And with the blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

**2949**

## 2950

B"H, 24 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and diligent worker for the needs of the community,
Rabbi Chaim Dov, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

Due to circumstances, the confirmation of receipt of his book, *Sefer HaChinuch*, which he published with an introduction, notes, etc., was delayed, and I ask for his forgiveness.

May it be the will of Hashem to grant him the merit to increase and glorify Torah through activities such as these, in addition to his work in his community as a leader and *mashpia*—that it should befit the name given to the community of Israel from days of old, "a holy community" (*kehilla kedisha*), which depends on holiness in daily life and in actual practice. And since our Sages of blessed memory have said that Hashem only demands according to one's strength, surely he has been given the strength to fulfill this mission.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to him and to all that is his: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

P.S.
For the sake of affection, I went through the lines of notes and explanations and marked a few comments, which I am transcribing below.

On this occasion, I would also like to comment regarding his article about Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, in the English book regarding the leaders of Israel, in which there are several inaccuracies, etc. It is surprising that he did not turn to the office here, as it is surely known to him that we have printed many books regarding Chabad, its Torah, its founder, and his successor.

***

**Rabbi Chaim Dov:** Shevel.

**And I marked a few comments:** These did not reach us.

## 2951

B"H, 24 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, Rabbi Aharon, may he live.

Shalom and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the auspicious day of 18 Elul, in which you write that not only have you maintained the Yeshiva and Talmud Torah in Sefaria, but you have also introduced improvements to them. May it be the will of Hashem that you expand this holy institution in both quality and quantity; this is also the way to increase material income. As is explained in Chassidus, the distinction between a limb (*eiver*) and a vessel (*keli*): a vessel merely receives what is placed into it, whereas a limb also draws forth [sustenance]. Consequently, as the limb grows, the drawing forth also grows. At that point, *hishtadlus* (effort) is effective even through the ways of nature, since the matters are already prepared from above, and all that is lacking is the "garment" of nature.

Regarding what you wrote about the three students who, due to their age, are not suitable, etc., and there is a rationale to transfer them to the Tomchei Temimim in Lod—in matters such as these, you must consult together and decide in accordance with the specific details of each individual student.

As we approach the new year, may it be the will of Hashem to grant you immense success in your activities, so that your institution may be in accordance with the intent of our holy Rebbes, may their merits protect us.

Approaching the new year, which comes upon us and upon all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all who are yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

P.S.
Your *pidyon nefesh* has been received.

## 2952

B"H, 24 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 19 Elul, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein.

Regarding what you write—that you are unable to generate joy within yourself: Since the Torah commands this of every single person, it is clear that everyone has the ability to do so, and the matter depends solely on one’s will. As for your statement that you have nothing to be joyful about, this matter is explained in many places in *Tanya* and other writings, detailing the *hisbonenus* (contemplation) that leads to true joy. When you study these properly, you will surely find meaning in them, as well as points that are relevant to you.

I have already written to you that poor health and sadness also impair the very matter you are writing about. May Hashem grant you success in accomplishing all of the above, and as a result, your situation will improve—even if not all at once from one extreme to the other.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, and for success in the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim*.

## 2953

B"H, 24 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, who engages in communal needs, R' Yosef, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the first day of Selichos, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein. May it be the will of Hashem that you actualize the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that "one action is better than a thousand sighs." Since the Holy One, blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures, and *hashgacha pratis* has brought you specifically to your current location, it is certain that you have been granted the strengths to fulfill your portion specifically there in creating a "dwelling place for Him in the lower realms." As explained in *Chassidus*, the point of this is that, by way of analogy, a person is present in his own home with all his essence in a revealed manner. From this, it is understood that one cannot exist without the knowledge of *Elokus*; although "no thought can grasp Him at all," except when that thought is grasped and clothed in the *mitzvos*, it is understood that subsequently, there must also be the power of *Chabad* (Chochma, Binah, Da'as) filled with this through study, understanding, and deep contemplation in the knowledge of Hashem.

Approaching the New Year, which comes upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

P.S.
Surely you are aware that in Cincinnati there resides the son of one of the veteran Chassidim—who is mentioned in several places in the *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—whose name is Michael, known as Dr. Wilensky. His address is noted below. He possesses manuscripts that he wishes to send here, but due to his state of health, the effort is difficult for him. You would do well to visit him—naturally, after speaking with him regarding the time—and to take upon yourself, or through those who do your bidding, all the effort involved in this. It is understood that the financial expenses are at my account. Thank you in advance for the effort in this matter.

## 2,954

2,954

B"H, 25 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Monday, Parshas Nitzavim.

Regarding the fact that you feel your mother’s attitude is not as it should be: one must contemplate the pain of raising children that parents—and especially a mother—endure, from the days of pregnancy and birth, through care, education, and so on. When one considers this, it becomes much easier for children to overcome their own inclinations and restrain their feelings regarding any shortcomings they perceive in their parents—even if those shortcomings are real, and certainly if they are imagined or exaggerated.

However, bearing in mind that the mind cannot always rule over the heart, the recommended advice is that most of the time spent with parents should be in the presence of others. Generally, when in the company of others, people refrain from entering into conflicts, and consequently, they become accustomed to relations of peace, love, and friendship.

As for what you write regarding your mother’s level of yiras shamayim being somewhat lacking, this is irrelevant to the matter. While one should certainly strive as much as possible to influence this for the good, this is not the way to do it; it must be done only through pleasant, gentle methods.

With blessings for a *kesiva v’chasima tova* for a good and sweet year, for you and your family, *sheyichyu*.

## 2955

B"H, 25 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed avreich, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs, etc.,
Moreinu Machluf, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 19 Elul, along with the lists of students and your Pidyon Nefesh from the aforementioned date. Thank you for writing regarding the study schedules, the division of classes, and so on.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the ruling of our holy Torah—Toras Chaim and Toras Emes—that we must always ascend in matters of holiness. Certainly, you will not be satisfied with the situation as it currently stands, but will add to it, both in quantity and in quality—that is, in the number of students, both boys and girls, and in the level of their studies. It is self-understood that in order to increase the number of students, there must be an increase in the number of teachers, both men and women, and likewise in both quantity and quality—that is, in the quantity of their knowledge of Torah and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, and in the quality of their knowledge, meaning their depth of understanding and the performance of mitzvos with hiddur. And since the Ribono shel Olam demands this of us, surely the strength to do so has been granted, for "according to the camel is the burden."

May the Ribono shel Olam grace him with pure yiras shamayim for his own sake, through which there will be an increase in mitzvos in general, and in matters of chinuch in particular, with the success of the Ribono shel Olam.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and upon all Yisrael for good, may you be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year. May the Ribono shel Olam provide him with his proper zivug, both physically and spiritually.

With blessings.

## 2950

B"H, 25 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, who engages in communal needs, R' Yehoshua Schneur Zalman, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 19 Elul, along with the three *pidyonos nefesh* enclosed therein, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote—that the situation of the *yeshivah* is still unclear, etc.—in my opinion, this is not the case. It has been clear for some time that the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and their associated matters must be fulfilled through the directive of "spreading your wellsprings outward." Consequently, it is impossible for there to be any corner of the globe where members of the Jewish people are found that this Torah will not reach. And specifically, it must be in accordance with the will of the Baal Shem Tov and his successors, the *Nesi'im* of Chabad: that Torah and life should be one, meaning, within the context of daily life.

Since we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that we are in the *ikvesa d'meshicha*—that he is standing behind our wall and waiting only for the clarification of the final remaining details—it is a necessity that there be a study of *Chassidus* in Australia as well. This should not be limited to the *anash* from Russia who were sent there, but rather, it must permeate the residents of the land—the Jewish residents of Australia. And since this is a necessity, all that is required for this will certainly be found.

It is surely superfluous to point out that since the *yeshivah* building makes a good impression, one should strive for it to serve, in general, as a center for Chabad activities—a place for Torah, a place for *tefillah*, a place for *farbrengens*, meetings, and so on. It is understood that all of the above is meant in a way that does not contradict the studies, but there is certainly room and time for all these matters within this building. Experience has already shown that having these other matters take place there will certainly serve as an aid to the affairs of the *yeshivah*.

Approaching the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all who are yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 2,959

B"H, 28 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos and the *pidyon nefesh*. I was pleased to read in it of your activities in disseminating the teachings of Chabad.

Regarding what you wrote—that you do not find within yourself the courage to act in additional circles, etc.—see *Likutei Torah*, at the beginning of *Parshas Vayikra*, which explains that in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, the lower man is an emissary of the higher man; see there. Consequently, it is incomprehensible how one could lack the courage in such a matter.

In accordance with this, since you have been appointed as a lecturer, you should continue in this, and on the contrary, you should endeavor to speak not only before those who are religious, but also before those who, for the time being, do not know that they are religious. As mentioned above, you possess the strength and courage to influence them in an appropriate manner.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the activities of your wife, *tichyeh*, in strengthening and disseminating Yiddishkeit. I am certain you will fill this in your next letter.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessing.

## 2860

B"H, 28 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Elul, as you requested, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for a good inscription and sealing.

Regarding your question asking for my opinion on the matter of covering the hair, I am surprised by the question, especially in the form you describe—that she would wear a wig where the entire head is covered, with only two fingers' width left exposed in the front. It is incomprehensible whom one is trying to deceive with this; it is obvious that one cannot deceive the Almighty, nor even the world, but only oneself. What benefit is there in such a thing?

It is understood that this is only a minor point, for the law is explicitly stated in the Shulchan Aruch, and consequently, there is no room for question or doubt. I am confident that through pleasant words, spoken time and again, the person in question will agree to your desired view on this matter.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good, may you be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year, and may you utilize your influence in your surroundings among the *anshei chayil* to make them soldiers in the armies of Hashem.

With blessings.

## 2862

B"H, 28 Elul, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 4 Elul, in which you write regarding the state of your wife’s health—may she live and be well—and that the doctors have expressed the opinion that she should avoid pregnancy. You write that although they permitted you to take measures to prevent this, you have chosen to practice abstinence, especially since your wife has forgiven you [for not fulfilling the mitzvah of *onah*], and you ask for my opinion on this.

In general, I am not comfortable with stringencies such as these—namely, practicing abstinence. In our generation, only a select few are capable of guarding themselves from improper thoughts, and certainly from things beyond that. Who can say that their Torah study and *davening* will remain in a state of purity? Consequently, in the vast majority of cases, the loss outweighs the gain. This is especially true given that the Tzemach Tzedek permitted the use of a *moch* in such circumstances (see his *Responsa*, *Even HaEzer*, siman 89).

Furthermore, regarding the wife’s forgiveness in matters such as these, it is a subject of debate whether such forgiveness is even valid. Moreover, in many cases, the lack of *onah* has a negative impact on a woman’s health.

As you requested, I will mention you and your household—may they live—at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the improvement of health in both physical and spiritual matters. You should certainly also have regular *shiurim* in *Toras HaChassidus*, which is referred to in the holy *Zohar* as the "Tree of Life" and the "soul of the Torah."

May Hashem grant you success and bring you good news regarding all of the above.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'Chasimah Tovah*.

#### ***2862***

**The Tzemach Tzedek permitted:** See also above, Vol. 5, letter 1773, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 2863

2863

B"H, Days of Selichos, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brothers and sisters, the sons and daughters of Yisrael, wherever you may be, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessings!

Life, and especially spiritual life, requires that the transition from one year to the next be marked by an accounting and a summary of the past year, so that we may know how the new year should be structured.

One of the most significant moments of the year 5714 from the perspective of Jewish *cheshbon hanefesh* (soul-searching) is that this year, the conviction regarding the falsity of certain "ideals" and hopes—and the fact that Yidden cannot rely upon them—has become even more pronounced. These ideals, these "isms," and the groups that represent them, have once again brought bitter disappointment to those who placed their hopes in them.

The year 5714 has strengthened the conviction, even in alienated circles, that the existence of the Jewish people can be secured only by holding fast to the Torah and the way of life it prescribes.

The outgoing year has also demonstrated once again that the policy of compromise—the idea that Yidden should hold onto two or three equally important foundations, of which Torah is only one—serves merely as a bridge to lead Yidden from right to left, further distancing them from genuine and true Yiddishkeit, from *mitzvos maasiyos* (practical mitzvos) in daily life.

Yet, it is only this [Torah and mitzvos] that has sustained Yidden since they became a people at Mount Sinai by accepting the Torah.

It is a foolish and even more dangerous error to think that one can fulfill their duty with fine words and "speeches" while acting *k'chol hagoyim* (like all the nations), or that it is sufficient to receive "injections" of Yiddishkeit on certain days of the year or at certain moments in life.

For Torah and the Yiddishkeit of mitzvos is a way of life that must encompass and permeate daily life. Just as a healthy person is someone who is healthy at all times, and not merely healthy from time to time, for a few days a year, so too is the spiritually healthy Yid—the Yid who lives with Torah and mitzvos every day, all day, throughout the entire year, at all times.

Just as a person would not agree to compromise on their physical condition—to accept "fifty-fifty" health, half healthy and half not, *chas v'shalom*—so too, in spiritual life, a Yid cannot agree to a "fifty-fifty" Yiddishkeit.

And just as a healthy person must seek to be in a healthy environment and do everything possible to ensure that their surroundings are healthier, so too in spiritual life, every Yid has a duty to themselves, their family, and the environment around them—to spread the light and warmth of Torah and mitzvos and to make their surroundings healthier.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that the accounting we make at this time leads to a firm resolution and the realization of the truth: that our *Toras-chaim* (Torah of life) in daily, practical life is the only path of life for Yidden as individuals and for Yidden as a collective—and not only for life in the World to Come, but also, quite simply, for a happy life in this world.

And may this resolution and its implementation in life bring—and it will bring—to each and every one, a *kesiva v’chasima tova* for a good and sweet year.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 2864

2864

By the Grace of Hashem, Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5715

Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Aharon Eliyahu, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

Some time ago, I received your letters, both directly and through others, in which you write regarding the proposal to publish a book about the history of the persecution against Yiddishkeit in our country in the past, and you ask for my opinion on the matter.

It is difficult to express an opinion on such a matter without prior, specific knowledge regarding the content of the book—whether the intention is to add a chapter to the history of the Jewish people from that terrible era, or if there is an additional reason to emphasize matters of Kiddush Hashem, specifically concerning the Chareidi community.

In any event, whether it is the first approach, the second, or other approaches, the book must include precise information—namely, names, locations, dates, and so on. It requires careful consideration whether this poses a danger to the aforementioned relatives who are still behind the Iron Curtain, especially since there is no clear information from there regarding what is happening to them or the general attitude toward such matters. On the other hand, to write in general terms without mentioning names—it is questionable whether such a work would bring the desired benefit.

Regarding your question as to whether I have material on this: organized material certainly does not exist, especially since the writings and notes from the estate of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, have not yet been organized as they should be. It is highly probable that there is no such material in writing, and it would still need to be gathered from Anash who came from our country, based on what is preserved in their memories. I have not yet found anyone to undertake this task.

You are surely aware that from the German reparations, a large sum has been allocated for research into the history of the Jewish people in the recent period. However, their primary focus is regarding the country of Poland and the like, where these aforementioned concerns do not exist. Surely, in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, it is possible to clarify the details regarding this support through the appropriate offices and individuals.

Relying on the beginning of your letter, where you mention that you studied in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, etc.—the words of Tzaddikim and their actions endure forever, and this is also true of the strengths they invested in their students. It is therefore surprising that you do not mention your own good deeds in the vineyard of Chabad. The claim and the complaint are well known: "They made me a keeper of the vineyards" (meaning that these are also vineyards and must be guarded, and yet, "my own vineyard I have not kept")—this is a deficiency and provides room for a claim. And the main thing is not a claim from the outside, but a claim from the inner point of the soul. May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding this soon.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and all that is yours: a blessing of *Kesivah v’Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing,

P.S.

Regarding the booklet of polemics against... it is understood that the method of the polemic depends on the local conditions and the reaction of the readership. Nevertheless, the point is:

1) When speaking about an existing religion, and not about the creation of a new religion, it is understood that one must take into account the foundations of the religion.

2) It is also understood that a critic and thinker can only be someone whom the religion does not reject as a believer.

3) The verdict of who is a believer and who is a *kofer* is not a matter left to the discretion of just anyone; rather, it depends on the principles of the **existing** religion and its foundations.

As a result of all the above, the very approach of... is against the religion of Moshe and Yisrael. Consequently, all of his arguments—whether or not they have a basis in logic—are in any case irrelevant to our religion. It is also understood that if the aforementioned person intends to innovate a religion, one should not mislead the readers by saying the opposite. By clarifying these points in an appropriate manner, one saves much ink and paper.
